Report on the results of the parallel checks of the administration of value added tax between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic carried out in 2005
Introductory word
The presented material informs about the progress and results of the parallel checks carried out by the Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic and the Najvyšší Audit Office of the Slovak Republic, which were focused on the area of the administration of value added tax and the use of the information system VIES (Value Added Tax Information Exchange System).
In May 2004, the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic joined the European Union, so the revenue from value added tax affects not only the state budgets of both countries, but also the budget of the European Union as a whole.
The parallel control actions were aimed in particular at checking the procedure of the tax administrators when checking the amount of value added tax paid in commercial transactions carried out between individual Member States of the European Union.
The introduction of the VIES system enabled the electronic exchange of information on the registration of VAT payers in individual Member States of the European Union and on commercial transactions carried out by these payers.
The discrepancy between the data in the VIES system and the data in the tax return for value added tax submitted by the payer should alert the tax administrator to suspicious cases and allow the detection of tax evasion or fraud.
The benefit of the parallel audits was not only in the exchange of information on the procedure of financial or tax authorities in the administration of value added tax, but especially in the verification of the use of the VIES system when auditing the application of the right to exemption from value added tax on intra-community transactions.
The knowledge gained during the implementation of the parallel audits is beneficial for the development of mutual cooperation and will be used in the implementation of other parallel audits in cooperation with audit institutions of the Member States of the European Union.
Report on the results of the parallel audits of the Value Added Tax administration for the period from 1.5.2004 to 30.6.2005
Introduction
Audit number: (CZ) 05/19 (SK) 22/2005
Subject of the audit: (CZ) Value Added Tax Administration, (SK) Audit of the procedure of tax authorities in the administration, control and enforcement of Value Added Tax and the fulfilment of tasks within the VIES system for the exchange of information between EU Member States
The Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic (hereinafter referred to as “SAO, CR”) and the Supreme Audit Office of the Slovak Republic (hereinafter referred to as “SAO SR”) concluded on 12.9.2005 the Agreement on Cooperation in Audit Activities.
The subject of the Agreement was the cooperation in the performed parallel auditing operations “Value Added Tax Administration”, included in the audit plan of the SAO, CR for 2005 under No. 05/19 and “Audit of the procedure of tax authorities in the administration, control and enforcement of Value Added Tax and fulfilment of tasks within the VIES system on the exchange of information between EU Member Landscapes”, included in the audit plan of the SAO SR under No. 22/2005.
The parallel auditing operations had the character of a coordinated audit.
The result of the joint coordinated audit was prepared in the sense of the European Enforcement Regulation No. 31 for the INTOSAI auditing standards.
The cooperation consisted in the exchange of information to the extent stipulated by the concluded contract and in the preparation of a joint final report on the result of the parallel audits.
The purpose of the coordinated audit was to verify selected cases of delivery and acquisition of goods in suspicious commercial transactions between value added tax payers from the Czech Republic (hereinafter referred to as “the Czech Republic”) and the Slovak Republic (hereinafter referred to as “the Slovak Republic”).
Both parties contractually undertook to provide each other with information from public sources, from the VIES (Value Added Tax Information Exchange System) electronic system and data on received and sent requests to verify commercial transactions between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic.
The audits were carried out in parallel between June and December 2005.
In the territory of the Czech Republic, the audits were carried out by the State Budget Department and the territorial departments of Central Bohemia, North West Bohemia, South Bohemia, South Moravia, Central Moravia and North Moravia.
The audited bodies were the Ministry of Finance and 12 financial offices: the Financial Office in Mladá Boleslav, the Financial Office in Kolín, the Financial Office in Teplice, the Financial Office in Karlovy Vary, the Financial Office in Tábor, the Financial Office in Brno III, the Financial Office in Znojmo, the Financial Office in Zlín, the Financial Office in Šumperk, the Financial Office in Ostrava I, the Financial Office for Prague 7 and the Financial Office for Prague 9.
The audits in the territory of the Slovak Republic were carried out by the Financial and Tax Section of the SAO of the Slovak Republic in cooperation with the Expoziturami of the SAO of the Slovak Republic Banská Bystrica and Košice at 9 selected tax offices: the Tax Office of Bratislava I, the Tax Office of Komárno, the Tax Office of Trenčín, the Tax Office of Prievidza, the Tax Office of Zvolen, the Tax Office of Dolný Kubín, the Tax Office of Košice II, the Tax Office of Košice V and the Tax Office of Michalovce.
Objective of the audits:
The aim of the parallel audits was to examine the procedure of the financial and tax authorities in the administration of value added tax (hereinafter "VAT") after the integration of the Czech Republic and Slovakia into the single internal market of the European Union (hereinafter "EU") and to examine the use of the electronic information system VIES, in particular when checking the application of the VAT exemption.
The audited coordinated inspection period covered the period from 1.5.2004 to 30.6.2005.
Summary of results and evaluation of parallel control actions An electronic VIES system is in place in EU Member States to allow tax authorities to check whether the supplier has been authorised to exempt the taxable transaction from VAT and to check in the country of destination whether the purchaser has duly declared and taxed the acquired goods.
The VIES system is not centralised within the EU, with each Member State developing its own system.
The audit found differences in national VIES systems in the Czech Republic and Slovakia in the following areas:
The values of supplies of goods to other EU Member States are reported in the recapitulative statements, the values of services provided are not included in the recapitulative statements.
The data from the recapitulative statements submitted by Czech payers are processed in the Czech Republic at the level of the tax authorities, where they are compared with the data on supplies of goods to other EU Member States included in the VAT returns.
The tax authorities transmit the data from the recapitulative statements to the Ministry of Finance (CLO), which sends them to other EU Member States.
In the Slovak Republic, the data from the recapitulative statements submitted by Slovak payers to the tax authorities are only converted into electronic form and processed centrally at the Tax Directorate of the Slovak Republic (CLO).
In the Czech Republic, payers report the value of supplies of goods and the value of supplies of services to other EU Member States on separate lines of the VAT returns, which allows to compare the values stated in the recapitulative statements with the values of supplies of goods according to the VAT returns and to identify their possible differences.
In the SR, the values of supplies of goods and services to other EU Member States are reported summarily on a common line of VAT returns.
As a result, in the SR, the system does not make it possible to automatically identify the differences between the values of supplies of goods according to VAT returns and recapitulative statements.
Separate reporting of the values of supplies of goods in VAT returns makes it possible to use the results of data comparisons when checking the VAT exemption of supplies of goods to the EU.
The delivered data from recapitulative statements submitted by payers in other EU Member States are processed at the Customs and compared with the value of acquisitions of goods stated by payers from the Czech Republic and the SR in VAT returns.
In the SR, these data are sent to the tax authorities and the tax authorities themselves decide which cases of differences to check.
In the Czech Republic, the Ministry of Finance (CLO) determines which quantified differences between the values of supplies and acquisitions of goods must be checked by the tax authorities and transmits a list of these cases to the local tax authorities.
This ensures that for the most significant deviations, it will be checked whether the VAT was declared at the correct amount.
The audit also highlighted some problems in the VAT administration system complications caused by different reporting of intra-Community transactions (i.e. supplies and acquisitions of goods effected by payers from different EU Member States):
Summary reports are submitted in the EU for each calendar quarter and the maximum period for processing and sending the data to other EU Member States is set at 3 months from the end of the relevant quarter.
Reducing the period for which summary reports are submitted to one month together with the shortening of the period for processing them would allow earlier access to the data in the VIES system.
The tax administrators would thus be able to check more effectively whether the VAT was declared at the correct amount in intra-Community acquisitions.
At the same time, the submission of VAT returns and recapitulative statements for the same tax period (month) would allow faster verification of whether the payer has declared identical values of supplies of goods to the EU in both the recapitulative statement and the VAT return.
The differences between the values of supplies of goods declared by EU taxpayers and the values of acquisitions of goods declared by Czech and Slovak taxpayers were due, among other things, to the different reporting of data on intra-Community supplies and acquisitions in individual EU Member States.
These included, for example, the inclusion of received advances in the recapitulative statements, or the reporting of intra-Community supplies in the supplier's recapitulative statement in a different quarter than the intra-Community acquisitions in the tax return of the acquirer.
The unification of the conditions for reporting these data within the EU would lead to more effective control activities of the tax administrations of individual Member States.
The cooperation of the SAO, the Czech Republic and the SAO SR was also focused on the examination of selected intra-Community transactions carried out between the two countries.
Together, a total of 40 cases of commercial transactions carried out between 29 Czech and 32 Slovak tax entities were examined, where there were doubts about their realisation or suspicion of VAT evasion.
The SAO, the Czech Republic and the SAO of Slovakia found the following facts among others:
tax entities reported in their VAT returns the realisation of intra-Community transactions, which did not actually take place, in order to obtain an excessive VAT deduction;
tax entities reported intra-Community supplies within carousel shops, where there was a deliberate multiple reduction of the value of supplies in order to draw excessive VAT deductions;
suppliers reported in their VAT returns and recapitulative reports the intra-Community supplies of goods exempt from VAT to the acquirers, who were so-called "lost companies" and did not declare the tax on the acquired goods;
Suppliers made the intra-Community supply of goods exempt from VAT to tax subjects who were not registered for VAT in another Member State.
In these cases, the supply should not have been exempt from VAT and should have been subject to tax in the supplier's country;
Suppliers declared in their VAT returns the intra-Community supply at a higher value than the intra-Community acquisition declared by the acquirers, while in some cases the VAT was declared at an incorrect amount.
From the lessons learned in the audit operation, it emerged that the VIES system provides tax administrators with the information necessary to check the correct application of VAT in intra-Community transactions.
Tax administrators should pay particular attention to rigorous verification of differences between the data reported by VAT payers and the data in the VIES system and the use of all information in tax proceedings.
Value added tax issues after the accession of the Czech Republic and Slovakia to the EU
Value added tax
On 1 May 2004, the Czech Republic and Slovakia became members of the EU.
After the accession to the EU, internal borders and border controls on the movement of goods within the territory of the EU were abolished.
The VAT administrator was the competent financial or tax office until 30 April 2004, with the exception of the importation of goods and occasional bus transport in the Czech Republic, where the tax administrator was the customs office.
In connection with the adoption of the new Act No. 235/2004 Coll., on Value Added Tax (hereinafter referred to as “Act No. 235/2004 Coll.”), or Act No. 222/2004 Coll., on Value Added Tax (hereinafter referred to as “Act No. 222/2004 Coll.”), the administration of VAT on the acquisition of goods and services (formerly imports) from other EU member countries passed from the customs offices to the financial or tax offices.
The supply of goods in the Czech Republic according to the provisions of § 13 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll. means the transfer of the right to dispose of goods as owner.
The supply of goods from the Czech Republic to another EU member state is the supply of goods that have actually been dispatched or transported to another EU member state.
According to the provisions of § 64 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll. it is an exempt taxable transaction with the right to deduct VAT if the goods are supplied to a person registered for VAT in another EU Member State.
The supply of goods in the Slovak Republic according to the provisions of § 8 of Act No. 222/2004 Coll. means the supply of tangible property in which the ownership right is changed.
The transfer of goods that are owned by a taxable person from the Czech Republic to another Member State is also considered as a supply of goods if these goods are dispatched or transported by that person or on his behalf to another Member State for the purposes of his business.
According to the provisions of § 43 of Act No. 222/2004 Coll. the supply of goods from the Czech Republic to another Member State is exempt from VAT if the acquirer is a person identified for VAT in another Member State.
Acquisition of goods from another EU Member State in the Czech Republic according to the provisions of § 16 of Act No 235/2004 Coll. means the acquisition of the right to dispose as owner of goods that are sent or transported to the acquirer by a person registered for VAT in another EU Member State.
A Czech taxpayer purchases goods at a price without VAT and his obligation in the Czech Republic is to declare VAT according to the provisions of § 25 of Act No 235/2004 Coll., if he fulfils the conditions set out in § 73 of this Act he becomes entitled to deduct VAT.
Acquisition of goods in the territory of the country from another EU Member State in the Slovak Republic according to the provisions of § 11 of Act No 222/2004 Z. means the acquisition of the right to dispose as owner of movable tangible property sent or transported to the acquirer by the supplier or the acquirer or on their behalf to the territory of the country from another Member State.
Tax liability in the Slovak Republic arises for the taxpayer when acquiring goods in the territory of the country from another Member State according to the provisions of § 20 of Act No 222/2004 Z. z.
The payer can deduct VAT according to the provisions of § 49 of the Act No 222/2004 Z. z. if the tax is applied by him when acquiring goods in the Czech Republic from another Member State according to the provisions of §§ 11 and 11a of this Act.
Trilateral trade means according to the provisions of § 17 of the Act No 235/2004 Coll. or § 45 of the Act No 222/2004 Z. trade concluded between three persons registered for VAT in three different EU Member States, where the object of the trade is the supply of the same goods between these three persons.
Intracommunitary transactions means the supply and acquisition of goods effected between VAT payers from different EU Member States.
The total volumes of intracommunal transactions effected between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic are shown in the following table.
VIES system
In order to control the application of the right to exemption from VAT in intracommunal supplies of goods, a system of exchange of information in the field of VAT has been created within the EU.
It includes the VIES electronic system, which allows tax authorities of the EU Member States to check whether the supplier was entitled to exempt the taxable transaction from VAT and vice versa, whether the acquirer duly declared and taxed the acquired goods.
The VIES information system is not centralised within the EU.
Each Member State develops its own VIES system.
The national systems work on a common principle and are interconnected through a common EU communication network, the so-called CCN (Common Communication Network; see diagram below).
In the Czech Republic, the VIES system was interconnected with an automated tax information system (ADIS), in the Slovak Republic with the application software of the tax information system (APV DIS).
These systems are used by the financial and tax authorities as technical support for executive and management activities in the administration of taxes and fees.
International administrative cooperation
Through international administrative cooperation, the tax administration of each EU member country obtains information about tax entities that it would not be able to obtain on its own without this cooperation.
The main objective of international administrative cooperation is the fight against tax evasion and tax losses.
According to Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003, each Member State establishes within the internal organisational structure a central unit in the field of administrative cooperation between EU member states in the administration of VAT, the CLO (Central Liaison Office).
In the Czech Republic, the Ministry of Finance – Central Financial and Tax Directorate, where the Department of International Cooperation in the Administration of VAT (hereinafter referred to as "MF CLO") has been established, performs the duties of the CLO in the Slovak Republic.
The function of the CLO in the Slovak Republic is performed by the Tax Directorate of the Slovak Republic, the Department of International Administrative Cooperation (hereinafter referred to as "DR CLO").
These departments, among other things, communicate with foreign EU administrations, especially in the area of information exchange within the framework of the VIES system, spontaneous information exchange and information exchange upon request of EU tax administrations, coordination of multilateral (simultaneous) tax inspections, verification of tax identification numbers (hereinafter referred to as the “DIČ”) of persons registered for VAT in other EU Member States and communicate with the European Commission.
In order to verify a certain intra-community transaction or to obtain further information related to a particular tax entity, the financial and tax authorities send requests for information to the EU via the MF CLO or the DR CLO.
Through these requests, they obtain information from the requested Member States that they can use for the correct determination of VAT.
Requests for information are sent between the CLOs of EU Member States mostly in electronic form, using the SCAC standardized form.
Selected audit findings during verification of commercial transactions
The cooperation of the SAO, the Czech Republic and the SAO SR was focused mainly on the verification of selected intra-community transactions carried out between the two states and on the level of use of information obtained through international cooperation by financial or tax authorities.
The SAO, the Czech Republic, requested the SAO SR to verify in 30 cases commercial transactions carried out between 19 Czech and 25 Slovak tax entities.
The SAO SR requested the SAO, the Czech Republic to verify in 10 cases commercial transactions carried out between 7 Slovak and 10 Czech tax entities.
The verification of intra-community transactions revealed, among other things:
o
The SAO, the Czech Republic asked the SAO SR to verify the procedure of the tax administrator, to whom a reply to the request for information was sent.
The Slovak tax office requested through the form SCAC to verify the delivery of goods (footwear) in the 3rd quarter of 2004 from a Slovak payer in the value of 2 847 thousand CZK.
The tax office in the Czech Republic replied that the Czech payer stated the acquisition of goods in this amount only in the additional VAT return and delivered the same goods back to Slovak tax entities in the amount of 2 550 thousand CZK by the end of 2004.
Based on the international cooperation of the SAO, the Czech Republic and the SAO of the Slovak Republic, it was found that the locally competent tax office recognized the Slovak supplier in its entirety as entitled to an excessive VAT deduction incurred, among other things, on the basis of this supply.
The tax office did not provide information about the suspicion of re-export to the tax authorities of locally competent customers of goods imported back from the Czech payer.
These facts will be an incentive for further verification of commercial activities in connection with possible carousel fraud.
o
The Czech tax administrator asked through the SCAC form for verification of the supply of a technological line to the Slovak Republic in the amount of 4 850 thousand CZK in the 2nd quarter of 2004.
The tax proceedings conducted in the Slovak Republic revealed that only a part of the technological line was delivered, the components worth CZK 3,395,000 were not delivered.
The SAO of the Slovak Republic, when examining this case, found that the VAT on the effected taxable transaction was declared by the Slovak tax entity on the amount of CZK 4,850,000 in the VAT return (hereinafter referred to as "DAP") for the tax period 7/2004.
The SAO of the Czech Republic also found that the Czech tax payer declared an excess VAT deduction of CZK 655,000 in its DAP for the aforementioned quarter, which arose from the application of the VAT deduction on the purchase of this technological line from another domestic payer.
The Czech Tax Office concluded on the basis of the results of the investigation that the Czech and Slovak tax entities had established a business relationship for the purpose of obtaining an excess VAT deduction, questioned the realisation of the taxable transaction and did not recognise the Czech payer's part of the right to deduct the tax amounting to CZK 647,000.
o
In 2004, the Slovak Tax Administration applied through the SCAC form for verification of the supply of goods (copying machines) to the Czech payer amounting to SKK 24,246,000 effected in December 2002.
The Slovak payer purchased these goods in November 2002 in Slovakia from another tax entity amounting to SKK 29,667,000 and subsequently sold them to the Czech payer.
The Slovak tax entity claimed an excess VAT deduction for the relevant tax period.
In the tax investigation carried out in the Czech Republic, it was found that the Czech tax entity did not cooperate with the Tax Administration and did not submit a DAP for the 4th quarter of 2002 or for the following period.
The SAO found that the Slovak Tax Administration did not recognise the right to an excess deduction amounting to SKK 5,541,000 effected in the DAP for the month of 11/2002 and determined the tax liability amounting to SKK 1,750,000.
At the same time, the tax entity was not granted an exemption from VAT in respect of the export of goods in December 2002.
o
The Czech tax administrator received an order from the MF CLO to verify the value of the acquired goods for the 3rd quarter of 2004.
According to VIES data, the Czech payer was supposed to acquire goods (diluent) from the SR in the value of 3,767 thousand Sk.
This tax entity did not cooperate with the tax administrator, it did not submit the DAP and the VAT for the months of 7 to 12/2004 was charged to it ex officio in the amount of 0 CZK.
The Czech tax administrator asked through the SCAC form to verify whether deliveries of goods from the SR to the Czech Republic took place, in what amount and price (according to invoices).
The Slovak tax office with local jurisdiction sent a copy of the invoice, waybills and an invitation to pay the invoice.
The SAO SR found that the Slovak payer was granted an exemption with the right to deduct VAT on this delivery.
The SAO, Czech Republic found that the Czech tax administrator evaluated the reply to the request for information received from the SR as evidence that the company had acquired goods from another EU Member State.
Based on further investigation, the tax office in the Czech Republic will ask the superior authority to review the tax liability.
o
The Slovak company supplied goods (particle board products) to, among others, an American company that deposited these goods in the Czech Republic in a free customs zone.
The operator of this free customs zone was listed on the invoices as the recipient of the goods.
In 2004, the American company, for example, purchased from the Slovak payer particle board tiles worth 57 600 USD (at a unit price of 100 USD/piece), which it placed in a free customs zone.
Subsequently, the company transferred ownership rights to the goods to the Swiss company in the amount of 14 400 USD (a unit price of 25 USD/piece) and the goods were exported back to the Slovak Republic.
The goods were not unloaded in the Czech Republic, but left the area of the free customs zone on the same means of transport.
The Slovak tax administrator initiated tax inspections of the individual tax periods of 2004 and 2005 at the supplier of the goods on suspicion of carousel transactions.
The verification of the underlying transactions was requested from the Czech locally competent tax administrators through several SCAC forms.
Individual answers gradually created a picture of the transactions and confirmed the involvement of Slovak and Czech stakeholders in carousel transactions.
The SAO, the Czech Republic in cooperation with the SAO of the Slovak Republic found that in these commercial relations the value of the goods was deliberately gradually reduced several times.
The tax directorate of the Slovak Republic concluded on the basis of the information obtained that in this case of carousel trade it is free price formation (i.e. the import of undervalued goods and their overvaluation by domestic companies located in the chain between the importer and the exporter), which is not a violation of the VAT Act in the Slovak Republic.
Under the current legislation it is not possible to prevent the payment of excessive VAT deduction to export companies, as they meet all the conditions of the Act to exempt supplies from VAT.
o
On 12 July 2005, the Czech payer's VAT registration was cancelled.
On 27 October 2005, on the basis of a voluntarily submitted application for VAT registration, this entity became a tax payer again.
The Czech tax entity entered into the DAP for the month 8/2005 (i.e. the period when it was not a VAT payer) the value of the acquisition of goods (polygraphic printing press) from Slovakia in the amount of CZK 1,174,000 and claimed the right to deduct VAT.
This value corresponded to the delivery of goods from the Slovak payer in the amount of SKK 1,530,000, which the Slovak payer stated in the DAP as a delivery of goods to another EU Member State with the right to deduct VAT.
The Slovak tax administrator requested to verify the said delivery using the SCAC form, as the Slovak supplier did not prove how he acquired the goods delivered to the Czech Republic.
The SAO, CR found that the Czech payer did not cooperate with the tax administrator and did not reside at the address specified in the Commercial Register.
As part of the international exchange of information, a local investigation will be carried out in the CR by the locally competent tax administrator in order to verify the data.
o
The Slovak payer stated in the summary report for the 3rd quarter 2004 the delivery of goods in the amount of SKK 956,000 to the tax entity from the CR.
The VAT number of the Czech entity was marked as erroneous by the VIES system.
A verification in the database of payers revealed that such VAT identification number was never assigned in the Czech Republic.
According to invoices issued by the Slovak payer, it was the execution of electrical assembly works on real estate in the Czech Republic, it was not the delivery of goods from the Slovak Republic to the Czech Republic, but the provision of services.
The services were invoiced without VAT, as the Czech entity informed the Slovak entity that it was registered as a VAT payer in the Czech Republic.
The Slovak tax administrator requested to verify the above mentioned facts by means of the SCAC form.
The SAO, Czech Republic, inquired with the locally competent tax administrator in the Czech Republic that the tax entity stated on the invoices as a customer was never registered as a VAT payer in the Czech Republic, it did not declare the tax on received services from the Slovak entity, and it did not declare the tax on the acquisition of goods.
Neither the local investigation nor the tax inspection was carried out at the Czech entity, its current whereabouts are unknown.
Based on the international exchange of information, the Czech tax administrator learned that the Czech tax entity became a VAT payer by law by accepting the service.
A tax inspection will be carried out at the Slovak tax entity for the first to fourth quarters of 2004.
o
The Slovak tax payer stated in the recapitulative statement for the third quarter of 2004 the supply of goods in the value of 1 055 thous. to the Czech tax payer.
According to invoices issued by the Slovak tax payer, it was the execution of electrical assembly works on real estate in the Czech Republic.
It was not the delivery of goods from Slovakia to the Czech Republic, but the provision of services.
The Slovak tax administrator requested to verify the above mentioned facts by means of the SCAC form.
The SAO, the Czech Republic inquired at the locally competent tax administrator in the Czech Republic that the Czech entity was a VAT payer at the time of the delivery and a local investigation was carried out at the Czech entity in order to verify the acquisition of goods from other EU member states in the third quarter of 2004.
Based on this local investigation, it was found that the case was not really a purchase of goods, but a purchase of services, which the Czech entity also declared in the regular DAP.
The tax authority also found that the Czech entity did not pay the correct amount of VAT for the 3rd quarter of 2004 due to a bad procedure in the calculation of VAT.
The tax entity submits an additional DAP.
The SAO SR found out by a query with the locally competent tax authority that the Slovak payer misstated the provision of services in the summary report and a tax audit will be carried out on it for the 1st to 4th quarter of 2004.
o
The Czech tax entity voluntarily registered as a VAT payer from 10th March 2004.
For the 1st quarter of 2004 it submitted a DAP with a high turnover in both input and output.
The locally competent tax authority initiated tax proceedings, the entity did not cooperate with the tax authority, therefore it was charged VAT in the amount of CZK 0 due to a suspicion of involvement in carousel trade.
The other DAP was not submitted by this payer.
Due to a failure to comply with the obligations arising from the law, the registration for VAT was cancelled as of 4th January 2005.
According to data from the VIES system, this entity should have purchased goods from the Slovak payer in the 3rd and 4th quarter of 2004 in the amount of SKK 7,846,000.
In order to verify the realisation of these transactions, the Czech tax administrator sent two requests for information to the Slovak Republic.
The SAO of the Slovak Republic inquired with the locally competent tax office that the manager of the Czech company denied the realisation of the transactions examined in a witness statement and questioned the authenticity of his signature on invoices and other documents.
On the basis of the tax procedure carried out in the Slovak Republic, the intra-community delivery to the Czech Republic declared by the Slovak payer was questioned.
The payer will not be entitled to exemption from VAT and will be charged VAT on the above amount.
o
According to the VIES system data, the Czech payer should have purchased goods (working clothes) worth SKK 39,970,000 from the Slovak Republic in the 1st quarter of 2005.
The Czech payer declared the acquisition of goods from another EU Member State only in DAPs for the month of 3/2005, amounting to CZK 11,292,000.
The locally competent tax administrator carried out a local investigation with the entity in order to verify the data in this DAP.
As the company did not submit any documents or otherwise substantiate the realisation of taxable transactions, the tax administrator charged VAT of 0 CZK on 9 June 2005.
Due to doubts about the realisation of the acquisition of goods, the tax administrator sent two requests for information to SR in May 2005.
According to the reply to the requests for information, the tax administrator in SR had doubts about the realisation of business cases as well as about the realisation of the payment.
The SAO was informed that the Slovak tax administrator sent the DR CLO the initiative to carry out simultaneous inspections with the tax administration of the Czech Republic, which will be carried out at the participating entities.
At the time of the coordinated inspection, the locally competent tax administrator carried out another investigation concerning the Czech entity in the Czech Republic and at the same time an investigation by the Police of the Czech Republic was underway.
o
The following 2 cases concern companies suspected of involvement in carousel fraud.
Transactions with goods (work clothes) were realized between the Czech Republic and Slovakia in the 4th quarter of 2004 and the 1st quarter of 2005.
The Slovak payer No. 1 supplied goods to the Czech payer No. 2.
In the Czech Republic, the goods were then sold to the payer No. 3, who supplied them back to the Slovak payer No. 4 (see diagram No. 2).
A)
The Czech payer No. 2 was supposed to acquire goods (work clothes) worth CZK 4,847,000 from the Slovak payer No. 1 in the 4th quarter of 2004 and goods worth CZK 17,050,000 in the 1st quarter of 2005.
As the acquisition declared by the Czech payer in the DAP did not correspond to the data in the VIES system, the locally competent tax administrator sent a request for information to the Slovak Republic on 25 May 2005.
In reply, the Slovak tax administrator expressed doubts about the realisation of business cases as well as about the realisation of the payment.
On 8 June 2005, a request for information was received at the MF CLO from the Slovak Republic concerning goods worth SKK 16,575,000, which the Slovak payer No. 1 was supposed to deliver to the Czech payer No. 2 in December 2004.
The Slovak side requested to check whether the Czech payer No. 2 actually received the goods, declared in the DAP and paid the VAT.
The official record drawn up by the locally competent tax administrator in the Czech Republic shows that the Czech payer No. 2 no longer resides at the address registered in the Commercial Register.
Although he was a VAT payer with a monthly tax period, he submitted the DAP for the quarterly tax period.
Due to this fact, the Czech tax administrator could not assess the VAT.
The chargeable event between the Slovak payer No. 1 and the Czech payer No. 2 mentioned in the request in the amount of 16 575 thousand Sk could not be verified due to the above mentioned facts.
The Czech tax administrator suspected the involvement of both entities in the carousel business in order to draw an excessive VAT deduction.
B)
The Czech payer No. 3, dealing with the purchase and sale of passenger cars, submitted the DAP for the tax period of months 1 and 2/2005, in which he declared the delivery of goods (work clothes) to the Slovak payer No. 4 in the total value of 21 935 thousand CZK.
These work clothes were to be purchased by the Czech payer No. 3 from the Czech payer No. 2 in the period from December 2004 to January 2005.
The locally competent tax office sent a request for information to SR, the main purpose of which was to verify whether Slovak payer No. 4 purchased goods from Czech payer No. 3 in December 2004 in the value of CZK 1,025,000 and in the first quarter of 2005 in the value of CZK 21,935,000.
The response to this request for information received from SR showed that in the DAP for month 12/2004, Slovak payer No. 4 stated the zero value of the acquisition of goods from another EU Member State and in the DAP for months 1 and 2/2005 the value of the acquisition of goods from another EU Member State only in the amount of CZK 1,193,000.
The Slovak payer No. 4 did not respond to the request to submit tax documents for the tax period of months 10/2004 to 3/2005.
During a local investigation carried out in SR, it was found that the company was not located at the address listed in the Commercial Register.
The response also stated that this payer fulfilled all the characteristics of a so-called "lost company" and therefore there was a reasonable suspicion of carousel fraud.
The Slovak SAO was informed that the Slovak tax administrator sent the DR CLO the initiative to carry out simultaneous inspections with the tax administration of the Czech Republic, which will be carried out at the participating tax entities.
During the coordinated inspection, the Czech tax administrator collected documents that would confirm or disprove the existence of the goods.
VAT will be assessed according to the outcome of the investigation.
The case is also being dealt with by the Police of the Czech Republic.
Conduct of the auditing operation
As part of the preparation of the parallel auditing operations, in the first half of July 2005, a coordination meeting took place between representatives of the SAO, the Czech Republic and representatives of the SAO of the Slovak Republic.
The participants of this meeting became acquainted with the VAT legislation in both countries and with the integration of the VIES electronic system into the national databases.
The outcome of the meeting was the specification of the scope of cooperation and the setting of conditions for the selection of the auditing samples.
Both parties agreed that the cooperation will focus on the following areas: (a) verification of the validity and correctness of the VAT numbers of persons registered for VAT in the Czech Republic or Slovakia in intra-community supplies; (b) verification of data on intra-community acquisitions listed in the DAP by payers in the Czech Republic using information from the summary reports (hereinafter referred to as "SH") of payers from the Slovak Republic contained in the VIES system, and vice versa; (c) exchange of information between tax administrations in the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic on executed commercial transactions.
Furthermore, it was agreed that the selection of tax entities for inspection will be carried out in relation to the volume of intra-community supplies between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic and according to the number of requests for international cooperation sent and received between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic by means of the SCAC form.
5.1 Intra-community transactions
The procedure of information processing by tax administrations of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic in intra-community supplies and acquisitions of goods is illustrated by the following diagram.
5.1.1 Intra-community supplies
If the VAT payer makes an intra-community delivery, he is obliged to submit SH by the 25th day after the end of the calendar quarter.
The payer in the Czech Republic provides in the SH summary information on his/her deliveries of goods to another EU Member State exempt from VAT for the previous calendar quarter.
The payer in SR is obliged to enter in the SH the value of goods that were tax exempt and delivered from the territory of the country to other EU Member States for the period of the calendar quarter.
Data on the value of the goods supplied are always given in the SH in Czech or Slovak currency, broken down by individual tax entities with an indication of their VAT number under which they were registered in their country.
Data on services shall not be included in the SH.
If the payer in the Czech Republic finds out that he has given incorrect data in the SH, he is obliged to file a subsequent SH.
If the payer in SR finds that the data given in the SH were incomplete or incorrect, he shall file a corrective SH before the deadline for filing the SH, after the expiry of this deadline he shall file an additional SH.
The VIES system allows the exchange of information on the registration data of VAT-registered payers in the EU Member States.
Taxpayers from the Czech Republic or Slovakia can verify whether the tax ID of the respective acquirer is registered in the given EU Member State.
Data from the submitted SH are grouped on the MF CLO or DR CLO by the VIES system according to the individual tax ID of the acquirer.
The aggregate value of all deliveries for each tax ID of the acquirer and the code of the method of delivery from all its Czech or Slovak suppliers, the so-called L1QD files, are created.
Data from the L1QD files are sent to the respective EU Member States no later than three months after the end of the quarter to which the data relate.
The total value of intra-Community deliveries between the Czech Republic and Slovakia (from the L1QD files) is given in the following table.
If the VIES system in another Member State finds the erroneous tax ID of the acquirer in the sent L1QD files, it generates the so-called O_MCTL report, which contains all the erroneous tax ID with an indication of the type of error.
This report is then sent to the MF CLO or DR CLO.
The O_MCTL report may contain 4 types of errors: formally erroneous VAT numbers, the VAT numbers are not registered in the given state or have never been allocated, the acquirer with a specific VAT number was not a VAT payer in the given quarter, the registration for the VAT of the acquirer was terminated during the quarter.
In the CR, the MF CLO transmits the data from the received O_MCTL reports to the tax authorities.
If the erroneous VAT numbers of the EU payer are used in any of the sent SH lines or subsequent SH lines, the ADIS system generates the so-called "VAT ID Doubt Notice" at the relevant tax office.
The tax office checks whether the delivery to a VAT registered payer in another EU Member State actually took place and records the result of the verification in the system.
In the SR, the DR CLO processes all the O_MCTL reports in the VIES system and sends them electronically to the locally relevant tax authorities together with the identification of the tax payers who indicated the erroneous VAT numbers in their SH.
The tax authorities then invite the payer to submit the additional VAT number and indicate the valid VAT number, respectively the tax office verifies the supply of goods at the respective taxpayer when reporting the invalid VAT number in the submitted SH.
Data on the number of incorrect VAT numbers relating to intra-community transactions carried out between the Czech Republic and Slovakia are given in the following table.
Of the total number of 41,728 VAT numbers of Czech payers listed in the SH of Slovak payers in the period from the 2nd quarter of 2004 to the 1st quarter of 2005, 929 were incorrect VAT numbers, i.e. 2.23%.
Of the total number of 62,997 VAT numbers of Slovak payers listed in the SH of Czech payers in the same period, 416 were incorrect VAT numbers, i.e. 0.66%.
When reporting intra-community transactions carried out between the Czech Republic and Slovakia, Czech VAT payers reported on average less incorrect VAT numbers in their SH than Slovak payers.
When examining the activities of the financial or tax authorities, it was found that the VIES system did not provide up-to-date information on the validity of VAT registrations of tax entities in all cases.
E.g.:
- although the VIES system confirmed the validity of the tax entity's registration in the 4th quarter of 2004 at the request of the tax administration in the Czech Republic, the O_MCTL report was subsequently generated due to the termination of the payer's registration in that quarter.
The investigation revealed that the termination of the registration took place only on 1 January 2005;
- The SAO of the Slovak Republic further found that 6 tax entities submitted SHs in which the erroneous VAT numbers were stated, but the O_MCTL reports did not contain these VAT numbers.
In the Slovak Republic, the SH submitted to the tax authorities are converted into electronic form and the data from them are sent to the DR CLO.
After the subsequent processing of these data in the VIES system, the DR CLO sends to the relevant tax authorities the so-called SH error breakdowns submitted by tax entities for the respective quarters.
The SAO of the Slovak Republic compared the data on the occurrence of erroneous data in the SH as of 26 July 2005 (i.e. data processed before the start of the audit) and as of 2 February 2006 (i.e. data processed after the completion of the audit).
The following table contains the comparison of the data.
From the above data it is evident that the SAO SR's audit had an impact not only on the reduction of the number of SH with erroneous VAT numbers (on average by 199 SH per quarter) but also on the reduction of the number of uncorrected errors in the SH (on average by 431 errors per quarter).
In the Czech Republic, the value of intra-community deliveries stated by the payer in the respective DAP lines is compared with the value of intra-community deliveries stated by the payer in the quarterly SH.
The ADIS system automatically indicates the differences between these values.
The tax administrator should check the differences, remove any ambiguities and use the obtained data when determining the tax liability.
The SAO, Czech Republic, found that the audited tax authorities did not verify these differences in 27 cases.
The total difference between the values stated in the SH and DAP in these cases amounted to 537,231 thousand CZK.
From the 3rd quarter of 2004, the ADIS system allowed the tax administrator in the Czech Republic to consider the difference between the values stated in the SH and DAP of up to 0.5% of the total value of intra-community deliveries according to the SH as a match and set it in the ADIS system.
For payers with a large volume of intra-community deliveries for one quarter, 0.5% of the value represents a non-negligible amount, therefore tax administrators should not set the SH and DAP match in these cases without explaining the reasons for the differences.
For example, the tax administrator set the match without verification in the case of a difference in values of CZK 1,561,000.
The fact that the SH for each calendar quarter was filed by payers within 25 days after the end of this quarter complicated the verification of the differences in the Czech Republic and Slovakia.
Tax administrators could not compare the values of intra-community deliveries given in these DAPs with the values according to SH for the first two months of the calendar quarter for payers with a monthly tax period at the time of filing the DAPs.
In these cases, tax administrators only found out about the possible inconsistency of the data in the DAPs and SHPs at the time the tax liability or excess VAT deduction was assessed or refunded.
5.1.2 Intra-Community acquisitions
The VIES system provides information on the values of intra-community transactions carried out within EU Member States.
Acquisition of goods in the Czech Republic
In the Czech Republic, the delivered SH data submitted by payers from other EU Member States (delivered L1QD) are processed by MF CLO.
During processing, the data are converted at the minimum and maximum daily exchange rates of the Czech National Bank for the respective period and then compared with the acquisition value stated by Czech payers in the DAP for the respective quarter.
The value of acquisitions of goods reported by payers in the DAP should be in the range of the minimum and maximum converted L1QD values (values L1min and L1max).
If the value reported in the DAP is lower than the value L1min, a so-called verification order is generated for payers with the most significant irregularities.
The orders for verification of acquisitions of goods are a warning of problematic tax entities and are transmitted to the locally relevant financial authorities, which must investigate the transmitted data.
The number of verification orders related to audited financial authorities in the Czech Republic is shown in the following table.
The SAO, CR found that in 33 cases the audited tax authorities did not verify irregularities in the values of intra-community acquisitions, which were indicated by the received verification orders.
The total difference between the values stated in the SH of payers from other EU Member States and the DAP of Czech payers in these cases amounted to at least CZK 148,319,000.
The SAO, CR selected for the audit 533 files of tax entities for which the audited tax authorities received a verification order from the Ministry of Finance.
The audit found the following most frequent causes of differences between the values stated in the DAP of the acquirer and in the SH of the supplier: on the side of the acquirer (Czech payer) in 263 cases the acquirer did not state the acquisition of goods in the regular DAP, in 93 cases the payer declared the acquisition of goods in a different tax period than in which it was obliged to declare the tax, in 6 cases the acquirer stated the value of the acquired goods in the incorrect DAP line, on the side of the supplier (EU payer) in 88 cases the EU payers included in their SH the values of the provided services to the Czech payer, of which in 54 cases the Slovak payer was involved, in 39 cases the suppliers included in the SH the delivery of goods in a different tax period than the Czech acquirers in their DAP, in 22 cases the suppliers stated in the SH the incorrect VAT number of the Czech payer, in 16 cases the suppliers stated in the SH the wrong values of the delivery of goods, in 12 cases the suppliers included in the SH the value of goods delivered to the CR before 1.5.2004, in 5 cases the suppliers included in the SH the value of received advances.
On the side of the payers from the Slovak Republic, the value of provided services was included in the SH most frequently.
In the audited financial offices, 54 such cases were found.
For example, when investigating the verification order, it was found that the difference in the value of CZK 10,974,000 arose from the fact that the Slovak payer included in the SH the provision of services (construction works and supplies of goods including assembly on the territory of the Czech Republic) for the 1st quarter of 2005.
Another reason for the differences was the inclusion in the SH of the values of received advances, e.g. 2 Slovak payers included in the SH received advances from Czech payers, as a result of which the verification order for the difference of CZK 3,580,000 was generated.
The verification orders for acquired goods are generated only once per quarter.
In cases where there is subsequently a change in the data from the SH in the EU Member States, such as a change in the purchaser of goods in the Czech Republic or an increased value of the supply of goods to the Czech Republic, the new verification orders are not generated.
As the VIES system does not automatically warn of these changes, the locally competent tax authority of the purchaser of goods may not know about the facts decisive for correctly determining the tax liability of the acquired goods without any other incentive and there is a high probability of VAT evasion.
An audit by the SAO of the Czech Republic found that this situation occurred e.g. in the following cases:
The Slovak payer stated in the SH for the 2nd quarter of 2004 the value of the delivery of goods to the Czech payer in the amount of 1,504 thousand Sk.
On 1 February 2005, the tax office of the locally competent Czech payer sent a request for information to the Slovak Republic because the Czech payer declared the acquisition of goods in the amount of only 425 thousand CZK.
On the basis of the tax procedure, the Slovak payer filed an additional SH on 1 March 2005 in which he corrected the data on the delivery of goods to the Czech Republic by reducing the value of the delivery for the originally mentioned Czech payer to 538 thousand Sk and by increasing the value of the delivered goods for another Czech payer from the amount of 194 thousand Sk to the value of 1,160 thousand Sk.
Four Slovak payers reported in their SH for the 2nd quarter of 2004 intra-community delivery to payers from the Czech Republic for a total amount of SKK 10,240,000 (i.e. CZK 8,183,000).
However, the Czech acquirers did not declare intra-community acquisition in the DAP.
Based on the international exchange of information, it was found that the goods were delivered in all cases to another Czech payer, which was not mentioned in the SH filed by the Slovak payers.
During the 1st quarter of 2005, the Slovak payers increased the value of intra-community deliveries for this Czech payer by a total of SKK 10,240,000 in the additional SH related to the 2nd quarter of 2004.
In view of the above, the locally competent tax administrator in the Czech Republic could not have doubts about the accuracy of the data in the submitted DAP for the 2nd quarter of 2004, even though the actual acquirer did not fulfil the obligation to declare intra-community acquisition for this quarter.
The SAO, Czech Republic found that on the basis of the international exchange of information between tax administrations, the above-mentioned Czech tax payer was additionally charged VAT for the tax periods 5 and 6/2004 amounting to CZK 3,640,000 and for the 3rd quarter of 2004 amounting to CZK 3,305,000 on the acquired goods in these periods.
From the above mentioned facts, it is evident that tax authorities had to examine in tax proceedings not only differences arising from errors in the acquirer's DAP, but also differences caused by different reporting of data on intra-community delivery and acquisitions in individual EU Member States.
The unification of the conditions for reporting these data would lead to more effective control activities of tax authorities.
Acquisition of goods in the Slovak Republic
In the Slovak Republic, the APV DIS system allows comparing data on the value of the acquired goods obtained through the VIES system from other EU Member States with the data listed in the Slovak acquirers' DAP.
The method by which the data are compared is called the "MIN-MAX method".
Using this method, the values of supplies of goods listed in the SH of payers from other EU Member States are converted at the minimum and maximum exchange rates for the respective quarter.
The MIN-MAX interval is created, which is used for comparison with the values of acquisitions of goods listed in the DAP of Slovak payers.
The DR CLO sends the tax administrators information on the values of intra-community acquisitions listed in the DAP and the values of supplies from the EU in the VIES system.
The tax administrator decides which persons registered for VAT will be checked for the difference, taking also into account other risk analysis criteria.
On the basis of the data provided by the DR CLO, the SAO SR selected 57 files of Slovak acquirers of goods from the audited tax authorities, of which 25 payers acquired goods from the Czech Republic, where the highest differences between the acquisition values obtained from the VIES system and the values declared in the DAP were found.
The SAO SR's audit confirmed the fact that the tax administrators did not consistently verify the differences obtained using the MIN-MAX method and did not check the accuracy of the data stated in the DAP of Slovak acquirers.
As part of the audit, the SAO SR asked the tax authorities to carry out 47 local investigations at specific tax entities.
During the SAO SR's audit at the tax offices, 31 local investigations were completed.
Among other things, the following facts were found for Slovak companies, where the VIES system showed significant differences in the MIN-MAX values when acquiring goods from EU member countries:
In the DAP for the 4th quarter of 2004, the Slovak payer did not state the value of the acquisition of goods from the EU.
The tax office found that the company from the Czech Republic had mistakenly stated the VAT number of this payer in the SH for the 4th quarter of 2004, while the goods worth CZK 19,184,000 were in fact delivered to another Slovak payer.
According to the VIES system, the Slovak company should have purchased goods from the Czech Republic, Poland, Hungary and Austria in the value of MIN 682,692 thousand. Sk and MAX 715,105 thousand. Sk in the 4th quarter of 2004.
This company filed DAPs for the given periods, in which it stated the value of the EU acquisition of goods in the amount of only 480,599,000. Sk.
The Tax Office carried out a local investigation, which found that the tax entity had purchased electricity from the Czech Republic, Poland, Hungary and Austria.
Suppliers to SH and DAP did not mention intra-community supplies according to the invoice issue date, but according to the delivery date.
Due to other irregularities in the acquisition of goods from these EU countries, the Tax Office requests verification of the value of the delivered goods by means of SCAC forms.
The Slovak payer did not mention the acquisition of goods from EU member countries in the 4th quarter of 2004 in the DAP.
According to the VIES system, this payer should have purchased goods worth MIN 11,286,000. Sk and MAX 11,845,000. Sk.
The Tax Office carried out a local investigation, which revealed that the tax entity had not purchased any goods from EU member countries in the 4th quarter of 2004.
The SAO recommended that the Tax Office request verification of the delivery of goods from EU member countries by means of the SCAC form.
In the VIES system, the delivery of goods to a Slovak customer worth MIN 557 thousand Sk and MAX 565 thousand Sk was reported.
In the DAP for the tax period of months 10 to 12/2004, the payer did not declare any acquisition of goods.
The local investigation of the Tax Administration found that the tax entity had received an invoice from a supplier from the Czech Republic for materials consumed during the repair of a hydraulic loader on 10th December 2004.
The SAO recommended to carry out a tax audit of the payer.
During the audit of the SAO SR in 16 cases, the Tax Authorities did not terminate the local investigation.
In 10 cases, the SAO asked the Tax Administration to carry out a tax audit of the tax entities.
Reports on the results of the local investigations and tax audits will be submitted by the Tax Authorities after their execution to the SAO SR.
Examples of these cases were:
The Slovak acquirer did not declare in the DAP for the 4th quarter of 2004 any acquisition of goods from EU member countries and for the tax period of months 10 to 12/2004 did not declare any tax and claimed a claim for refund of excess VAT deduction totalling 1 236 thousand Sk.
The tax administrator carried out a local investigation, which showed that the tax entity acquired goods from the Czech Republic in the value of 683 thousand Euros (approx. 27,080 thousand Sk).
The goods were transported from the Czech Republic by the Czech supplier to the customs office in Čiernej nad Tisou, from where the transport proceeded to the Russian Federation.
The Slovak payer issued an invoice for the amount of 683 thousand Euros for customers in the Russian Federation, which it did not state in the submitted DAP.
The tax administrator carries out a tax inspection of the tax entity.
The difference between the acquisition data listed in the Slovak payer's DAP for the 3rd quarter of 2004 to the 1st quarter of 2005 and the delivery data reported by payers from EU member countries in each quarter was in the total amount of 4,800 thousand Sk.
The tax office found that the tax entity purchased goods from suppliers from the Czech Republic and Belgium and subsequently sold these goods to Ukraine.
The invoices were accompanied by export uniform customs declarations.
The acquisition of goods in the DAP was not mentioned by the tax entity, according to the statement of the company's manager, the goods in transit were transported directly from the Czech Republic to Ukraine.
The tax entity did not submit any VAT registration during the local investigation.
A tax inspection was initiated for the payer.
5.2 International exchange of information level L3
The exchange of information at level L3 is initiated by the locally competent tax administrators, who send their requests for information (hereinafter referred to as "RUI") or spontaneous information (hereinafter referred to as "SPI") relating to a particular tax entity or transaction through the MF CLO, respectively.
DR CLO to another EU member country. The objective of the RU is e.g. to prove the execution of a given transaction in the framework of intra-community transactions, to verify a certain TIN, etc.
In the case of SPI, it is the communication of information important for the tax administrator in another EU member country.
Cooperation in the field of exchange of information is regulated by Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003.
The maximum time limit for replying to the RU was set in Article 8 of this Regulation at 3 months.
The conditions for admissibility of requests are regulated by the Decision of the Commission of the European Communities of 15 November 2004, which stipulates that, unless the participating states agree otherwise, the STI must relate to commercial transactions with a value of at least EUR 1 500 excluding VAT.
If a STI relates to a commercial transaction with a value of less than EUR 15 000 excluding VAT, the requested authority may, in view of its workload, refuse to reply.
The procedure for processing received STIs by the tax administration of the Czech Republic, including an indication of the internal time limits set for processing at each organizational level, is illustrated in the following diagram.
In the SR, the time limit for processing STIs by the tax authorities was set internally at 2 months, so that the three-month deadline under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 could be met.
The MF CLO received a total of 29 STIs and 3 STIs from the SR between 1 May 2004 and 30 June 2005.
Of the 29 received STIs, 26 (i.e. 89.7%) were discharged within the stipulated time limit of 3 months and 3 (i.e. 10.3%) were discharged after this time limit.
In the same period, the DR CLO from the Czech Republic received a total of 71 STIs and 7 STIs.
Of the 71 RUs received, 64 (i.e. 90.1%) were processed within the stipulated period of 3 months, 5 (i.e. 7.0%) were processed after this period (for the remaining 2 cases it was not possible to determine the period of processing from the submitted materials).
More detailed data on the time of processing of RUs received by the MF CLO and DR CLO are contained in the following chart.
The reasons for sending RUs, stated on the SCAC forms, are contained in the following table.
Conclusion
On the basis of international cooperation, compliance with Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 on administrative cooperation in the field of VAT was verified as well as the use of the VIES system for the exchange of information between EU Member States, especially when controlling the application of the right to VAT exemption.
International cooperation made it possible to verify selected intra-community transactions carried out between VAT payers from the Czech Republic and Slovakia.
The examination of selected transactions revealed that on the basis of international information exchange, tax administrations of both countries detected cases of companies that carried out fictitious intra-community business transactions in order to obtain excessive VAT deductions, as well as cases where the acquirers did not declare VAT on the received supplies of goods in the correct amount.
The audit also found differences in the processing and use of VIES data by tax administrations of both countries.
The audit also pointed to problems caused by different reporting of data on intra-community supplies and acquisitions of goods in individual EU Member States.
The unification of the conditions for reporting these data within the EU would lead to more effective control activities of tax administrations of individual Member States.
The examination of the procedure of financial or tax authorities in the administration of VAT and the use of the VIES system revealed that the financial or tax authorities did not make sufficient use of all VIES possibilities and the relevant legal authorizations.
It was also found that the VIES system did not provide up-to-date information on deliveries of goods and on the validity of the VAT registration of tax entities in all cases.
The SAO SR compared the data on occurrence of erroneous data in the SH, processed before the start of the audit, with the data processed after the completion of the audit.
From the comparison of these data it was clear that the SAO SR's audit had an impact not only on the reduction of the number of SH with erroneously stated VAT numbers, but also on the reduction of the number of uncorrected errors in the SH.
In case of discrepancies in the reported data, the SAO SR asked the tax authorities to carry out local investigations, or to carry out tax audits.
The SAO, the Czech Republic, did not have such an option within the framework of the applicable legislation in the Czech Republic.
From the findings of the audit operation it was found that the VIES system provided the tax administrators with basic information necessary for the control of the correct application of VAT in intra-community transactions.
As there is still room for tax evasion in this area, it is necessary to pay increased attention to intra-community transactions in the administration of VAT.
Communiqué
This report was prepared in Czech, English and Slovak languages and signed by the President of the Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic and the Chairman of the Najvyššie Audit Office of the Slovak Republic.
Parallel Control of Value Added Tax and Excise Tax Administration between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic
Introductory word
This information material gives an overview of the progress and results of parallel control actions carried out by the Supreme Audit Office and the Supreme Audit Office of the Slovak Republic, which were focused on the area of value added tax and excise tax administration.
The cooperation between the supreme audit offices of both countries was realized on the basis of a contract on cooperation in control activities concluded in February 2004.
The topic of parallel control actions was chosen in view of the fact that indirect taxes significantly contribute to the revenues of the state budgets of both countries.
The design of the value added tax, allowing the refund of the excess deduction, provides a space for tax fraud or evasion.
High rates of excise taxes, especially on tobacco and tobacco products, alcohol and mineral oils, mean a high profit for those who escape taxation by illegally selling these goods.
Tax fraud is a problem not only in the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic, but also in other countries of the European Union.
Due to the need to address this issue comprehensively within the whole European Union, a working group of the VAT Working Group has been created by the supreme audit institutions of the European Union Member States, in whose activities the supreme audit offices of both countries are actively involved.
The greatest benefit of the audits carried out can be seen not only in the exchange of experience, but especially in the joint effort to identify problem areas of indirect tax administration with the aim of limiting the scope for tax evasion.
The gained experience and knowledge will be used in the framework of the planned audits of indirect taxes, focused mainly on the involvement of the tax administrators of both states in the VIES system, which allows to control the movement of goods between the Member States of the European Union.
Report on the results of the audits of the administration of value added tax and excise taxes for the years 2002 and 2003
1. Introduction
Audit number: (CZ) 04/07 (SK) 18/2004
Audit subject:
(CZ) Value added tax and excise taxes
(SK) Audit of the tax administrator's procedure for administration, control and enforcement of value added tax and excise taxes
On February 11, 2004, the Agreement on cooperation in the audit activities between the Supreme Audit Office (SAO) and the Supreme Audit Office of the Slovak Republic (SAO SR) was concluded. The subject of the Agreement was cooperation in the parallel auditing operations "Value added tax and excise taxes", included in the SAO Audit Plan for 2004 under No. 04/07 and "Audit of the procedure of the tax administration, control and enforcement of value added tax and excise taxes", included in the SAO Audit Plan under No. 18/2004.
The cooperation consisted in the exchange of information to the extent stipulated by the concluded Agreement and in the preparation of a joint final report on the outcome of the audits.
Both parties undertook in the contract to provide each other with information from public sources, from the database of the customs administration and from the files of tax entities maintained by the tax authorities in the Czech Republic and the tax authorities in the Slovak Republic, which the contracting parties could not obtain during the audit of the application of value added tax and excise taxes on imports and exports from sources in the territory of the respective state.
The audits were carried out in parallel in the period from January to August 2004.
In the territory of the Czech Republic (hereinafter referred to as the "CR"), the audit was carried out by the State Budget Department and the territorial departments of South Bohemia, North East Bohemia, South Moravia, Central Moravia and North Moravia.
The audited bodies were the General Directorate of Customs and 12 selected financial offices: the Financial Office for Prague 1, the Financial Office for Prague 3, the Financial Office in České Budějovice, the Financial Office in Frýdek-Místek, the Financial Office in Hodonín, the Financial Office in Jihlava, the Financial Office in Kostelec nad Orlicí, the Financial Office in Kroměříž, the Financial Office in Písek, the Financial Office in Rožnov pod Radhoštěm, the Financial Office in Ústí nad Orlicí, the Financial Office in Velký Meziříčí.
The auditing operation on the territory of the Slovak Republic (hereinafter referred to as "the Slovak Republic") was carried out by the Tax and Customs Administration Section of the SAO of the Slovak Republic in cooperation with the Expoziturami of the SAO of the Slovak Republic Banská Bystrica and Košice at 10 selected tax offices:
The Tax Office Bratislava for selected tax entities, the Tax Office of Bratislava III, the Tax Office of Trnava, the Tax Office of Pu-chov, the Tax Office of Banská Bystrica I, the Tax Office of Liptovský Mikuláš, the Tax Office of Žilina I, the Tax Office of Žilina II, the Tax Office of Košice I and the Tax Office of Košice IV.
Objective of the auditing operation
The aim of the audit was to verify the fulfilment of obligations of financial and tax authorities and customs offices in the administration of value added tax and excise taxes with a focus on the collection of these taxes on imports and exports of goods and services.
The aim of the international cooperation was to verify imports and exports of selected commodities between the Czech Republic and Slovakia in the customs database of the Czech Republic and the customs database of the Slovak Republic and their subsequent verification in tax returns at the respective financial and tax offices.
The audited period covered the years 2002 and 2003.
2. Recapitulation of the audit results
2.1. General evaluation of the audit activity
Within the framework of the international cooperation of the SAO, the SAO SR transmitted 22 206 items of uniform customs declarations (hereinafter referred to as "JCD") from the customs database of the Czech Republic on imports and exports of goods between the Czech Republic and Slovakia and vice versa, the SAO SR transmitted 30 221 items of JCD to the SAO from the customs database of the Slovak Republic.
A comparison of the selected JCD items from the customs database of the Czech Republic and the customs database of the Slovak Republic was performed.
Of the 5 883 selected items of the JCD from the customs database of the Czech Republic, a total of 43% of the related items of the JCD were assigned.
Of the 12 343 selected items of the JCD from the customs database of the Slovak Republic, a total of 26% of the related items of the JCD were assigned.
Based on the unassigned items of the JCD, a selection of the files of tax entities was carried out at the financial or tax offices, where the declared imports and exports were further verified in cooperation with the customs administrations of the Czech Republic and Slovakia.
Based on the exchange of information from the customs administrations of the Czech Republic and Slovakia and the financial or tax authorities, the realisation of the declared imports and exports between the Czech Republic and Slovakia was verified on the territory of the second state.
The SAO and the SAO carried out a joint pilot audit at the border customs crossing Starý Hrozenkov - Drietoma, during which both parties closely cooperated in verifying the accuracy of data on the movement of goods between the Czech Republic and Slovakia.
The audit did not find any deficiencies in the registration of selected cases of imports and exports of goods carried out in 2002.
International cooperation enabled the verification of commercial transactions carried out between business partners from both countries and pointed out deficiencies in the registration of imports and exports.
2.2. Summary of the audit results
In the area of international cooperation, the SAO and the SAO of the Slovak Republic focused on imports and exports of alcohol and spirits, tobacco and tobacco products, computers and computer components, mobile phones and their parts, as well as other types of goods.
On the basis of the audit of files of tax subjects at selected financial and tax offices, the SAO requested verification of the realisation of exports of goods declared on 40 JCD with a total statistical value of CZK 15,301,093 and the SAO of the Slovak Republic requested verification of exports with a statistical value of CZK 56,989.
The SAO and the SAO of the Slovak Republic found the following facts among others:
- commercial transactions were not declared in the same way on both sides, which made it difficult to identify the corresponding imports and exports in the customs database of the Czech Republic and the customs database of the Slovak Republic;
- errors in entering data into customs databases made it impossible to identify certain imports or exports,
- for some exports from the Czech Republic, corresponding imports into the Slovak Republic were not proved.
In these cases, there is a reasonable suspicion of fictitious exports of goods for the purpose of improper application of value added tax deductions,
- tax subjects did not fulfil certain statutory obligations when reporting imports and exports in value added tax returns,
- deficiencies were found in the activities of financial or tax authorities in the administration of value added tax and excise taxes and in their cooperation with customs authorities.
In the area of value added tax and excise taxes, attention will continue to be paid to international trade with the aim of effectively minimising tax evasion.
In particular, it is important to improve the work of tax authorities in the performance of the administration of value added tax.
Effective control of excise duties is based on control of document circulation, systematic physical control of goods and mutual exchange of information on import and export of goods.
3. Description of the situation regarding value added tax and excise duties
Value added tax
Value added tax (hereinafter referred to as "VAT") was levied by the tax or tax authorities on taxable transactions carried out within the territory of the country and by the customs authorities on importation of goods.
The tax revenue was determined by the tax authorities by the difference between the collected own tax liability and the refunded excess VAT deductions.
VAT revenue at customs offices was determined by the amount of tax collected by them.
In accordance with the basic principles of the VAT mechanism, the tax collected by the customs authorities was reflected in the tax deductions applied at the tax or tax authorities.
For most tax and tax authorities, excess VAT deductions exceeded tax liability.
VAT is one of the key taxes in terms of state budget revenues, as it accounted for about 31% of the tax revenues of the state budget of the Czech Republic in 2003 and for about 42% of the tax revenues of the state budget of the Slovak Republic.
The total VAT collection in the Czech Republic amounted to CZK 162.9 billion in 2003.
The financial and customs authorities collected a total of CZK 394.3 billion in VAT in 2003 and the excess VAT deductions returned amounted to a total of CZK 231.4 billion.
The total VAT collection in the Slovak Republic amounted to CZK 83.8 billion in 2003.
The tax and customs authorities collected a total of CZK 187.0 billion in VAT in 2003 and the excess VAT deductions returned amounted to a total of CZK 103.2 billion.
Excise taxes
