The collection of excise taxes (hereinafter referred to as the "CND") was carried out by the respective financial or tax authorities and the customs authorities when importing products subject to the CND.
The share of the CND in the tax revenues of the state budget in the Czech Republic amounted to about 16% in 2003 and about 19% in the Slovak Republic.
The total CND collection collected by the financial and customs authorities in the Czech Republic amounted to CZK 85.6 billion in 2003 and CZK 38.0 billion in the Slovak Republic.
4. Progress of the audit operation
The cooperation between the SAO and the SAO took place in two stages.
In the first stage, the comparison of imports and exports of selected commodities from the customs databases of the Czech Republic and Slovakia was carried out, in the second stage, the results of this comparison were used for mutual verification of the implementation of selected commercial transactions between the Czech Republic and Slovakia and for audits carried out on the territory of both countries.
4.1.
Preparation of the audit operation
The first proposal for cooperation in parallel audits of VAT and DTC was presented at a working meeting of representatives of the SAO and the SAO of the Slovak Republic in April 2003.
In November 2003, a coordination meeting was held at which, among other things, the selection of commodities - types of goods that represented a significant risk in compliance with customs and tax regulations was agreed on: - alcohol and spirits, tariff headings No 2207 and 2208, - tobacco and tobacco products, tariff headings No 2401, 2402 and 2403, - computers and computer components, tariff headings No 8471 and 8473 30, - mobile phones and their accessories, tariff headings No 8525 20 91, 8525 20 99, 8529 90 40.
Both parties agreed that the selection of tax subjects to be checked would be carried out: (a) from unassigned items determined by comparison of exports and imports of selected commodities between the Czech Republic and Slovakia, (b) from entities carrying out imports and exports regularly or in one-off large volumes, (c) on the basis of findings from inspections carried out by selected financial and tax authorities.
4.2. Comparison of the customs databases of the Czech Republic and Slovakia
In the first stage, the mechanism for the cross-referencing of JCD items registered in customs databases of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic was tested on a sample of imports and exports of selected commodities for the month of October 2002.
Subsequently, part of exports from the Czech Republic was compared with imports into the Slovak Republic for the year 2002 and vice versa for selected commodities according to the customs tariff:
- 2207 Undenatured ethyl alcohol of an alcoholic strength by volume of 80% vol or more; ethyl alcohol and other spirits denatured, of any strength,
- 2208 Undenatured ethyl alcohol of an alcoholic strength by volume of less than 80% vol; spirits, liqueurs and other spirituous beverages,
- 2401 Unmanufactured tobacco; tobacco refuse,
- 2402 Cigars (with or without ends cut off), cigarillos and cigarettes, of tobacco or of tobacco substitutes,
- 2403 Other tobacco products and tobacco substitutes; homogenised or reconstituted tobacco; tobacco extracts and essences;
- 8525 20 91 Transmission apparatus incorporating reception apparatus: For cellular networks (mobile phones),
- 8525 20 99 Transmission apparatus incorporating reception apparatus: Other;
- 8529 90 40 Parts suitable for use solely or principally with apparatus of headings 8525 to 8528.
Other: Parts of apparatus falling in subheadings 8525 10 50, 8525 20 91, 8525 20 99, 8525 40 11 and 8527 90 92.
JCD items from the customs databases of the Czech Republic and Slovakia were cross-referenced on the basis of the agreement of individual paragraphs of the JCD (e.g. invoiced price, quantity, weight, registration number of the vehicle transporting the load, date of crossing the national border, tariff heading, etc.).
The results of the comparison are given in the following tables and graphs.
The cross-referencing of individual imports and exports was made more difficult by the fact, among other things, that commercial transactions were not declared in the same way on both sides.
For example, exports from the Czech Republic declared on one export JCD were declared on more import JCDs in the territory of the Slovak Republic, or the export JCD had a different number of items from the import JCD.
Other factors that influenced the success of the attribution were the different composition of data in the customs databases of the Czech Republic and Slovakia, as well as the time shift between the registration of exports in the customs database of one country and the registration of corresponding imports in the customs database of the other country.
The results of the comparison were used in the selection of control samples at the audited financial or tax offices.
Priority was given to certain tax entities that carried out imports or exports between the Czech Republic and Slovakia, which could not be identified in both databases.
Furthermore, some tax entities were selected for the verification of commercial transactions reported in the VAT returns, for which data on imports or exports between the Czech Republic and Slovakia were found in both databases.
4.3. Pilot control at the border customs crossing Starý Hrozenkov-Drietoma
The border customs crossing point for the execution of the pilot control was selected on the basis of a joint analysis of unassigned JCD items in the customs databases of the Czech Republic and Slovakia.
Based on a bilateral agreement between the customs authorities of the Czech Republic and Slovakia, the use of control sheets was introduced at the border customs crossings between the Czech Republic and Slovakia from 1.6.1998.
The aim of this measure was to eliminate customs and tax evasion as much as possible, to ensure an overview of the movement of means of transport transporting commercial goods in the customs area and to create conditions for mutual comparison of customs records.
The joint pilot control was carried out from 8.3.2004 to 26.3.2004 and was aimed at examining this system of customs control.
Procedure for the use of control sheets at the border customs crossing Starý Hrozenkov-Drietoma:
1) Weighing the vehicle, issuing the control sheet and handing it over to the driver.
2) Unloading the vehicle in the designated sector in the parking area.
Customs processing in the clearance hall of the Police of the Czech Republic, Police of the Slovak Republic, Customs Administration of the Czech Republic, Customs Administration of the Slovak Republic.
The individual components confirmed the execution of the clearance by stamping in the control sheet.
3) Bringing the vehicle to the physical inspection area.
Presentation of the control sheet, JCD, or other documents to the customs administration employee - check the execution of all prescribed operations and documents.
Performance of the physical inspection by the respective components.
Release of the vehicle from the customs area.
Note: When importing goods into the Czech Republic, the weighing of the vehicle was carried out directly by the employees of the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic.
When importing goods into the Slovak Republic, the weighing of the vehicle was carried out by the employees of an authorized legal entity.
The vehicles were recorded in the computer register after weighing.

Exports from the Czech Republic to the Slovak Republic

4.3.2. Inspection sheets and their registration Exports from the Czech Republic to the Slovak Republic
When exporting from the Czech Republic to the Slovak Republic, the Customs Administration of the Slovak Republic issued and registered the inspection sheets.
The Customs Administration of the Czech Republic recorded the registration numbers of these inspection sheets in the electronic database of exports.
From the number of 453 JCD items, the SAO found 256 cases of imports into the Slovak Republic according to data from the customs database of the Czech Republic and Slovakia. The remaining 197 JCD items were identified by the SAO SR in cooperation with the staff of the Drietoma border crossing point.
Exports from Slovakia to the Czech Republic
When exporting from the Slovak Republic to the Czech Republic, the control sheets were issued and registered by the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic.
From the total number of 339 JCD items of the selected control sample, the SAO in cooperation with border customs crossing staff assigned the corresponding registration numbers of the control sheets to the 295 JCD items.
The remaining 44 cases were identified in the register by the employees of the border customs crossing Drietoma and the export of goods from the Slovak Republic to the Czech Republic was confirmed.
The SAO and SAO audit did not find any deficiencies in the registration of selected cases of imports and exports of goods in 2002 at the border customs crossing Starý Hrozenkov-Drietoma.
4.4. Selected audit findings when verifying commercial transactions
Within the framework of international cooperation, the implementation of imports and exports between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic was verified from documents of customs administrations and tax authorities in the territory of the other country.
The selected tax subjects were verified:
- whether the submitted JCD were registered in the customs databases of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic,
- fulfilment of legal conditions for application of VAT deduction on import, refund of excess VAT deduction and application of VAT exemption on export.
The verification of commercial transactions revealed:
1. The SAO of the Slovak Republic requested verification of the realization of export of alcohol in the statistical value of 56 989 CZK.
The SAO identified in the customs database of the Czech Republic the corresponding import in the statistical value of 42 624 CZK.
2. The company dealing with import and export of photographic devices and accessories applied an excess VAT deduction in the amount of 3 740 664 CZK in the VAT declaration for the month of December 2002.
In order to check the reported exports from the Czech Republic, the SAO selected 3 JCD (16 items) in the statistical value of 1 274 822 CZK.
The SAO identified 3 corresponding import JCD (17 items) at a statistical value of CZK 1,724,321.
The VAT was paid to the competent customs office in the Slovak Republic.
3. The company, whose business was mainly trading with optical devices, applied a total excess VAT deduction of CZK 4,1,36,000 higher than the tax liability in 2002.
In order to verify the reported trade activity, the SAO selected the export JCD (32 items) at a statistical value of CZK 7,154,124.
The SAO found that the import JCD (12 items) corresponded to this JCD with a statistical value of CZK 9,653,827.
The VAT was paid to the competent customs office in the Slovak Republic.
4. The company dealing with, among other things, the purchase of goods for resale and sales, did not report any export of goods in the submitted VAT returns in 2002 and 2003.
According to the customs database of the Czech Republic, the statistical value of the export of goods in 2002 amounted to CZK 3,439,888.
Based on these facts, the SAO selected for verification 5 export JCDs (5 items) at a total statistical value of CZK 669,839.
The SAO SR identified 5 corresponding import JCDs (5 items) with a statistical value of CZK 1,012,656.
The SAO SR audit at the relevant tax office proved the realisation of the declared imports and payment of VAT.
5. The company, whose business included the purchase of goods for resale and sale, production, installation and repair of electrical machinery and devices, reported in the tax returns of VAT in the year 2002 the export of goods with a value of CZK 12,966,706.
According to the customs database of the Czech Republic, the total value of exports in the year 2002 was CZK 14,474,381.
The SAO submitted 17 export JCDs (59 items) with a total statistical value of CZK 2,975,122.
The SAO SR identified 13 JCDs (50 items) with a statistical value of CZK 3,621,370 in the customs database of the Slovak Republic.
The Slovak customs database failed to identify the corresponding import JCDs to 4 export JCDs (9 items) with a total statistical value of CZK 399,776.
The relevant tax office in the Slovak Republic verified these imports with the tax entity.
The tax entity listed on the JCD as an importer to the SR expressed in the minutes of the local investigation that the imports declared on the Czech export JCDs had not been realized.
The SAO SR therefore asked the local tax office to carry out a tax audit of VAT and corporate income tax for the tax years 2002 and 2003.
6. The company engaged in the import and sale of cigarettes exported tobacco stickers with a statistical value of CZK 7,338,199 in 2002 and CZK 12,228,545 in 2003, according to the Czech customs database.
The company did not report any exports in the tax returns for VAT in 2002 and 2003.
The SAO selected for verification 5 export JCDs (5 items) with a total statistical value of CZK 2,471,598.
The SAO SR identified 7 JCDs (7 items) with a statistical value of CZK 2,919,514 in the Slovak customs database.
The corresponding imports could not be assigned to the export JCD (1 item) with a statistical value of CZK 224,738 in the Slovak customs database.
7. The software company did not report exports of goods in the VAT returns for 2002 and 2003.
According to the Czech customs database, the statistical value of exports of goods in 2002 and 2003 amounted to CZK 1,630,198 in total.
The SAO selected for verification in the SR 9 JCDs (9 items) with a total statistical value of CZK 755,588.
For the Slovak customs database, the SAO SR identified 8 JCDs (8 items) with a statistical value of CZK 915,601.
For the export JCD (1 item) with a statistical value of CZK 68,286, the corresponding import could not be assigned in the SR customs database.
In the above cases, the corresponding imports could not be identified in the SR customs database for 6 JCDs with a statistical value of CZK 692,800.
Of which:
- for 2 export JCDs from the Czech customs database with a statistical value of CZK 293,024, the corresponding import JCDs could not be identified in the SR customs database (see points 6 and 7).
Due to a certain error rate in entering data in the customs database, it was not possible to identify certain registered imports, e.g. in cases where the importer's name was missing or there was an error in the tax identification number (TIN).
Therefore, it cannot be concluded with certainty that these exports did not take place.
- to 4 export JCDs from the customs database of the Czech Republic, imports corresponding to exports from the Czech Republic to the Slovak Republic in the statistical value of CZK 399,776 were not proven (see point 5).
In such cases, there are reasonable grounds for suspecting that goods have been fictitiously exported for the purpose of wrongfully claiming a VAT deduction.
5. Control of imports and exports of goods and services within the scope of control of selected financial and tax authorities
5.1. Control sample
In order to verify the fulfilment of the obligations of tax entities in the import and export of goods and services and to evaluate the level of cooperation between the tax and customs authorities, the files of tax entities were selected at the audited financial and tax offices according to the following criteria:
1. tax subjects were selected from the customs databases of the Czech Republic and Slovakia: (a) with the highest volume of imports, (b) with the highest amount of VAT charged, (c) with the highest volume of exports,
2. tax entities were selected from the register of the tax or tax authorities according to the amount of: (a) VAT deductions applied on importation, (b) excess VAT deductions applied, (c) VAT refund entitlement, (d) VAT exemption applied on exportation,
3. tax entities that have been subject to a tax audit.
The sampling was carried out irrespective of the country of destination, with a focus on risky commodities.
5.2. Inspection findings in the Czech Republic
An overview of imports into the Czech Republic and exports from the Czech Republic for risky commodities in 2002 and 2003 is given in the following table:
5.2.1. Inspection of selected sample at financial offices
The SAO focused on:
- the procedure of the tax authorities in verifying the correctness of reported VAT,
- cooperation between the tax authorities and the customs administration,
- comparison of data from the customs database with the JCD database at financial offices with a focus on comparison of declared value, application of the correct VAT rate in connection with the customs classification of goods or services, or comparison of data on the JCD and attached invoices with data in the customs database,
- comparison of data from VAT tax returns on performed and received transactions from abroad with data in the JCD database at financial offices or in the customs database,
- method of verification of the right to exemption from VAT when exporting goods or providing services abroad,
- comparison of the volume of exports of goods or services declared in VAT tax returns with data from the customs database.
The JCD database at financial offices contained only records of those imports and exports where tax subjects were obliged to include imports or exports in their tax returns.
At the audited financial offices, the files of tax subjects were examined, which declared imports totalling CZK 60 396 379 thousand in the VAT returns in 2002 and 2003 and the corresponding VAT totalling CZK 12 644 052 thousand.
Furthermore, the files of tax subjects were checked, which reported exports totalling CZK 47 323 111 thousand in the tax returns for 2002 and 2003.
According to the customs database of the Czech Republic, the tax subjects for which the imports and exports between the Czech Republic and Slovakia were examined carried out imports into the Czech Republic from the Slovak Republic in 2002 and 2003 with a total VAT base of CZK 3 759 352 thousand, VAT of CZK 767 607 thousand and exports from the Czech Republic to the Slovak Republic with a total statistical value of CZK 1 989 090 thousand.
The detected differences between the records in the database of JCD at the financial offices and in the customs database of the Czech Republic were examined as follows:
- the items of JCD that were missing in the customs database of the Czech Republic were requested directly at the General Directorate of Customs of the Czech Republic,
- the JCD items that were missing in the database of the tax offices were verified as canceled documents,
- the JCD items that were found to have different values between the customs database of the Czech Republic and the database of the tax offices were requested at the General Directorate of Customs of the Czech Republic in written form, including the attached invoices.
The verification revealed that the JCD database at the tax offices did not contain, for example, records on import JCDs with a total value of VAT of CZK 3,622,000 and records on export JCDs with a total statistical value of CZK 9,359,000.
5.2.1.1. Detected differences
Comparing the JCD database at the tax offices and the cumulative tax obligations for 2002 and 2003 in the VAT returns for a selected sample of tax subjects, the following differences were found:
The differences in values were mainly due to:
- The time shift between the realisation of the imports and the exercise of the right to deduct the VAT charged on the importation of the goods.
The tax subject was able to exercise the right to deduct on the importation of goods within 3 years from the end of the tax period in which the goods were placed under the relevant scheme or, in the case of the temporary importation scheme, within 3 years from the end of the tax period in which the scheme was terminated.
- The time shift between the realisation of the exports and the moment when the tax subject received the JCD.
The tax subject was obliged to include data on realised exports exempt from the obligation to apply output tax in the VAT return at the earliest for the tax period in which the goods left the country if he also had a tax document, which was the JCD.
- The failure of tax subjects to fulfil their obligations when reporting imports and exports in the VAT returns.
In some cases, tax subjects did not include correct data on imports and exports in the VAT returns.
As tax subjects did not have to attach JCD lists to the VAT returns submitted, the control of the right to deduct or exemption from VAT by the tax authorities was made more difficult.
5.2.2. Cooperation of the financial and customs authorities
During the audited period, the customs authorities decided to refund or remit import or export duties and VAT.
Tax subjects were obliged by law to reduce the previously exercised right to deduct VAT by the amount of tax returned by the customs office in the tax return for the period in which the tax was refunded.
No legal regulation provided for the sending of information about changes in the amount of duties and VAT from the customs authorities to the tax authorities.
Some audited tax authorities received this information, but irregularly or with a considerable time delay and only from some customs authorities.
One audited tax office did not receive this information at all.
If the tax office did not receive information about changes in the amount of customs duties and VAT directly from the customs office, it did not have the necessary data for checking the fulfilment of the legal obligation of tax subjects.
In 2002, the customs offices returned VAT in the amount of more than CZK 319 million and in 2003 in the amount of more than CZK 398 million.
The results of the audit pointed to persistent deficiencies in the activities of tax administrators, some systemic errors in the cooperation of the tax authorities with the customs administration authorities and the non-fulfilment of certain obligations of tax payers filing VAT returns and the Income Tax Act.
During the administration of VAT and Income Tax Act, deficiencies were found in the following areas in particular:
a) at the cancellation of VAT registrations, the fulfilment of the obligation of tax payers to pay VAT on commercial assets registered or which should have been registered at the date of the cancellation of the registration, where the payer claimed a tax deduction, was verified only rarely,
b) the tax authorities did not consistently use the possibility to carry out a tax inspection or a local investigation.
This resulted in insufficient verification of the validity of the right to a VAT deduction in some cases,
c) the official records and minutes of oral proceedings did not contain all the necessary data proving the validity of claimed excess VAT deductions,
d) the tax authorities did not sufficiently verify imports and exports declared in VAT tax returns.
5.3. Inspection findings in the Slovak Republic
5.3.1. Inspection of the selected sample at tax offices
In the selected sample, the SAO audited or the tax office carried out a tax inspection for the tax years 2002 and 2003.
After analysing the submitted tax returns and requests for tax refunds at selected tax subjects, the SAO asked the tax office to secure the relevant JCDs documenting imports and exports, invoices and proof of payment of tax.
Subsequently, the SAO SR audited whether the submitted JCDs were registered in the customs database of imports and exports and whether the decisive facts and legal conditions were fulfilled in the application of the input tax deduction for imports, in the refund of excess VAT deduction, in the application of the tax exemption for exports and in the refund of the CAS.
At 10 audited tax offices, the SAO SR audited selected cases of imports and exports of goods between the Slovak Republic and the Czech Republic in the structure according to the number of JCD items and the sum of statistical values given in the following table.
In total, imports were audited at a statistical value of 856.2 mil. Sk, which represents 5.11% of the total value of imports of selected commodities from the Czech Republic into the CAS.
Exports of selected commodities were audited at a total statistical value of 176 mil. Sk, which represents 6.87% of the total value of exports of selected commodities from the Slovak Republic to the Czech Republic.
Furthermore, 618 cases of imports of other goods and services (mainly white goods, packaging technology and software) from the EU countries to the Slovak Republic were audited in the statistical value of SKK 532.8 million.
5.3.2. Cooperation of tax and customs authorities
The SAO scrutinized tax authorities and found discrepancies between data recorded in the Slovak Republic customs database and data recorded in specific VAT returns, e.g.:
- 2 tax subjects (natural persons) declared in their tax returns imports of goods in the total value of SKK 1 589 261, on the basis of which they claimed a claim for refund of excess VAT deductions.
In local investigations carried out at the instigation of the SAO of the Slovak Republic, tax subjects failed to prove to the tax office the legitimacy of applying the input tax with relevant documents on realisation of imports and payment of VAT,
- the tax subject (s. r. o.) declared in the tax return for the tax period January 2003 the received taxable performance in the value of 77 167 576 Sk, the export of goods in the value of 18 006 041 Sk and claimed the excess VAT deduction in the amount of 17 157 101 Sk.
The tax returns filed for the year 2003 show that the difference between the volume of purchase and export in the value of 59 161 535 Sk, which arose in January 2003, was not equalized during the whole year 2003.
In the above cases, the SAO SR asked the relevant tax authorities to carry out a tax inspection of the applied excess VAT deductions.
- in another case, the tax subject (s. r. o.) declared in the tax returns for the tax period January to June 2002 the export of goods in the total value of 87 199 Sk.
A verification in the customs database of the SR revealed that the tax subject made exports in the statistical value of 296 747 Sk in the indicated period.
The tax office carried out several local investigations at the registered office of the company, which found that the company's manager (a citizen of Great Britain) had travelled and the company had left the leased premises without terminating the lease agreement in August 2002.
At the time of the audit, the SAO SR filed a report with the law enforcement authorities on the suspicion of committing a crime of non-payment of tax.
Based on the results of the audit at selected tax authorities, the SAO SR finds that the biggest problems in the performance of the administration and control of VAT and VAT were found mainly in the following areas:
- failure to use the possibility to carry out the tax audit of VAT on problematic tax entities, especially in cases of application of a high value of excessive VAT deductions,
- the tax audit reports did not contain an inventory of audited documents
- JCD on import and export of goods,
- insufficient verification of declared import and export of goods in the tax returns,
- lengthy proceedings of tax administrators when issuing decisions, especially in the context of the assessment procedure, with the consequence of the extinction of the right to assess sanctions,
- failure to comply with legal conditions when granting deferments of payment of taxes,
- failure to compensate VAT arrears within the deadline for the refund of excessive VAT deductions,
- insufficient use of all forms of security and recovery of tax arrears.
Based on the audited shortcomings, the SAO asked the relevant tax authorities to perform VAT tax audits focusing on the justification of applied excessive VAT deductions for 14 tax subjects.
At all audited tax offices, measures were taken to eliminate the audited shortcomings, whose compliance will be monitored and audited by the SAO.
6. Conclusion
International cooperation enabled the verification of commercial transactions carried out between business partners from both countries and pointed out shortcomings in the registration of imports and exports.
The inspections also revealed persistent deficiencies in the fulfilment of the obligations of VAT and VAT payers, in the activities of the financial and tax authorities, in the system of cooperation and exchange of information between tax and customs administrations, which ultimately reduced the effectiveness and efficiency of tax inspections.
The findings also showed that the tax authorities in the Czech Republic have at their disposal within the tax information system basic data on imports and exports from the customs database of the Czech Republic. In SR, there is no similar system for transmitting information on imports and exports of goods between customs and tax administrations.
The procedure for verifying the performance of the VAT and VAT administration was not the same due to the different legislation and conditions in the two countries.
The SAO verified the necessary data from information obtained at the Czech Customs Administration and from documents available at audited financial offices. The SAO verified the execution of commercial transactions from documents of tax entities requested through tax authorities.
In case of detection of irregularities, it asked tax authorities to perform tax audits.
The performed parallel audits in the area of VAT and the VAT administration evaluated the state of administration of these taxes in the period before the accession to the European Union and pointed out the necessity of further cooperation in this area.
Mutual cooperation will be further deepened in the auditing of the activities of financial and tax authorities in connection with the adoption of the new VAT Act.
One of the new obligations related to the delivery of goods to other Member States of the European Union is the submission of the so-called summary report.
This report must be submitted by all VAT payers who carried out the delivery of goods to another Member State to a person registered for VAT in another Member State.
Tax administrators are obliged to enter the data from the summary reports into the VIES (VAT Information Exchange System) system, which is accessible to tax administrators from the Member States of the European Union.
The financial or tax authorities then have the possibility to compare these data with the data provided in the submitted VAT returns.
This system is further used to verify the validity of the VAT numbers of persons registered for VAT, to verify the validity of the applied VAT exemption in the case of a supply of goods to another Member State and to check the proper taxation of goods.
The implementation of parallel audits showed the possibilities of cooperation between the SAO and the SAO of Slovakia.
The results of these audits will be confronted with the outcomes of the upcoming audits, which will focus, among other things, on the verification of the VIES system, which is supposed to prevent tax evasion in so-called "intra-community supplies".
Due to the importance of VAT and the Internal Revenue Act for budgetary revenues, it is necessary to focus the auditing activities mainly on monitoring and identification of risk areas in order to limit the scope for tax evasion in indirect taxes.
Communiqué
This report was prepared in Czech, English and Slovak and signed by the Vice-President of the Supreme Audit Office and the Chairman of the Najvyššie Audit Office of the Slovak Republic.
Report on the Results of the Control in Asylum Facilities in the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic
State Property and Funds Intended for Securing the Activities of the Refugee Facilities Administration of the Ministry of the Interior
Control Action No. 04/23 "State Property and Funds Intended for Securing the Activities of the Refugee Facilities Administration of the Ministry of the Interior"
Control Action No. 15/2004 "Control of hospodárenia with state property and financial prostriedkami Intended for Providanie of Asylum and Temporary Refugee Cudzincom in the Slovak Republic"
1. Introduction
Population migration is one of the phenomena of a global nature and has become an inseparable part of the current development phase of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic.
Its cause is mainly the flight of citizens from their country of origin or last permanent residence from persecution, especially for reasons of race, religion, nationality, politics, as well as the consequences of military conflicts and ethnic cleansing.
Their aim is to obtain asylum and integration into society, especially in one of the advanced democratic countries of Europe.
A large group also consists of foreigners whose reason for migration is unfavourable economic and living conditions.
Migration is not a new phenomenon.
The adoption of the Geneva Agreement of 1951 and the New York Protocol of 1967 on the legal status of refugees, by accepting them, the governments of the signatory countries undertook to apply them in their foreign-policy orientation, already brought about the establishment of specific principles of assistance to refugees.
The Czech and Slovak Federative Republics ratified the New York Protocol in 1991 and the Geneva Agreement in 1992.
After the split in 1993, both the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic declared their position on the refugee issue by continuing to comply with the adopted international documents and confirmed their binding force within the framework of national legislation by a legal act.
Both Republics also enshrined the granting of asylum in their constitutional laws.
Parallel checks carried out by the Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic and the Supreme Audit Office of the Slovak Republic focused on the asylum process and related issues, the results of which are contained in a joint final report.
The cooperation between the supreme audit offices of both countries was implemented on the basis of the "Agreement on Cooperation in Control Activities" (hereinafter referred to as "the Agreement") concluded in April 2004.
In the Agreement, both parties undertook to provide each other with information on the legislation governing the asylum procedure in the other Contracting Party's State, selected statistical data concerning the number of asylum seekers and the results of the asylum process, as well as information on asylum facilities.
The parallel control action sought to identify the same problem areas and to point out the consequences arising from this for the area of population migration.
The cooperation consisted in the unification of the programme of control actions, in the exchange of information within the scope of the Treaty and in the preparation of a joint final report on the outcome of the controls.
At the first joint meeting, which took place from 5.4. to 7.4.2004, the same audit areas and control procedures were established in the preparation of the control actions.
At the second meeting, which took place from 28.6. to 30.6. 2004, the common points for the programme of the control action were specified.
At the third joint meeting, which took place during the control action from 8.11. to 10.11.2004, the experience of the ongoing controls was exchanged.
The forms of the outcomes of the controls were specified and the structure and content of the joint final report, which was prepared from 14.2. to 17.2. 2005 at the last joint meeting, were provisionally established.
The controls were carried out in parallel between September 2004 and January 2005.
In the Czech Republic, the control was carried out by the inspectors of the Department of Defence and Security and selected territorial departments.
The auditees were the Ministry of the Interior (hereinafter referred to as the "MoI") and the Administration of Refugee Facilities of the Ministry of the Interior (hereinafter referred to as the "SUZ").
In the Slovak Republic, the audits were carried out by the Section of Defence, vnútra and štátnych úradov.
The auditee was the Migračný úrad of the Ministry of the Interior of the Slovak Republic (hereinafter referred to as the "MoI").
The audited period covered the years 2001, 2002 and 2003 (hereinafter referred to as the audited period).
In some cases, statistical data for a longer period are also used in the joint report.
2. Recapitulation of the results of the audits
2.1. Evaluation of the auditing activities
The subject of the audits carried out in parallel were: - the asylum process, - asylum facilities, - the management of state funds and property, - the internal control system.
The mutual exchange of gained experience between the Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic and the Supreme Audit Office of the Slovak Republic took place at the stage of preparation and implementation of the auditing operations.
This exchange made it possible to evaluate the submitted documents more thoroughly, to analyse the causes of the detected differences in the security of the asylum process.
In this way, it was possible to concentrate on the decisive problems affecting the activity of asylum facilities.
In the end, this had a positive effect on the quality of the implementation of control activities.
2.2 Summary of control results
The harmonisation of the asylum law of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic with European Union (EU) documents has been the subject of evaluation reports by the European Commission on the readiness of both countries to join the EU.
The adoption of legislation regulating this area continues after the accession of both countries to the EU, with the aim of further harmonisation with EU law.
The number of asylum seekers in the Czech Republic increased significantly in 2001.
In the Slovak Republic, the number of applicants has been steadily increasing, with a significant increase in applicants occurring in 2001.
The Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic provide financial and material security for asylum seekers in the sense of international agreements.
The state budget of both countries allocates the necessary financial resources for this purpose.
The amount of expenditure drawn from the state budget of both countries is influenced in particular by the number of applicants, the duration of the asylum procedure until asylum is granted or not granted, as well as by the state of health of the applicants.
The amount of some of the benefits collected is comparable in both countries.
The Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic have established asylum facilities in which they have gradually created suitable conditions for the stay of asylum seekers.
The asylum facilities provide accommodation, meals, health care and basic material equipment and sanitary needs for the duration of the stay of asylum seekers.
At the same time, leisure courses are organised and the conditions for cultural and sporting activities are created for applicants.
The asylum facilities include reception centres and residential centres, and in the Czech Republic, integration centres.
The costs per stay day depend on the occupancy and equipment of the centre and are comparable in both countries.
In the Czech Republic, the capacity of asylum facilities is basically stabilised.
In the Slovak Republic, it is expected to increase by almost 1 000 places in the next two years.
The aim is to create the conditions for applicants, whose increasing number is expected to continue in the following years in connection with the application of the Dublin Convention.
In the Czech Republic, the largest part of the approved budget expenditure was spent on the provision of services. The decisive expenditure of this item was expenditure on accommodation and catering for applicants in asylum facilities operated on the basis of a contract, expenditure on health care provided to asylum seekers and the cost of a permanent security service providing protection of asylum facilities.
Expenditure on salaries, payments for work carried out and insurance premiums also contributed significantly to the total expenditure.
In the Slovak Republic, the budgetary management of the security of the migration policy and asylum process was marked by many budgetary measures that addressed the legitimate requirements related to the increase in the number of asylum seekers.
Expenditure on wages, salaries and insurance premiums, expenditure on materials and services and expenditure on security services contributed to a decisive extent to the drawdown of current expenses.
The results of the audit in the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic drew attention to some similar deficiencies that did not have a major impact on the financial management and management of state property.
These were deficiencies in particular in the area of the use of state budget funds contrary to the purpose for which they were determined by the Act on the State Budget, when ordinary expenses paid for actions having the character of technical evaluation of long-term tangible property.
The Act on Accounting in the area of inventory was also violated and in the failure to comply with the chart of accounts.
In the Czech Republic, minor deficiencies were also found in the management of State property when it was handed over to another person without a contract.
The Act on the Land Register was violated by failure to comply with the deadline for reporting changes in the Land Register data and the Act on Waste was violated by handing over waste for disposal to a person who was not a person authorised for waste management.
In the Slovak Republic, deficiencies were also found in the provision of unreasonably high advances for electricity and natural gas consumption, deficiencies in public procurement and in the management of State property when its registration was not sufficiently ensured and the method of disposing of unneeded assets was not demonstrated.
The internal control system was ensured in the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic in the sense of the generally binding legal regulations that govern the way financial control is carried out.
The submitted written documentation did not reveal any deficiencies.
The Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic and the Najvyšší Audit Office of the Slovak Republic, despite some deficiencies found, evaluate positively the procedure of SUZ and MU in providing services for asylum seekers.
Based on the findings gained during the audit, the Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic and the Najvyšší Audit Office of the Slovak Republic note that despite a significant increase in the number of asylum seekers in recent years, the respective organisational units of both countries have managed the tasks related to the care of asylum seekers to an adequate level.
The evaluation shows that the system is functional and stable.
The results of the audit were discussed with interested statutory representatives of the respective organisational units of the state on both the Czech and Slovak sides.
Based on the results of the audit, we recommend that positive methodological experience from the audit be used in other joint control actions within the framework of international cooperation of supreme audit institutions.
3. Legislative framework
In both the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic, asylum law is based on the 1951 Geneva Convention (the Convention Relating to the Status of Refugees and the subsequent New York Protocol of 1967).
The first legislation was implemented by Act No. 498/1990 Coll., on Refugees.
In the Czech Republic, Act No. 325/1999 Coll., on Asylum and on the Amendment of Act No. 83/1991 Coll., on the Police of the Czech Republic, has been effective since 1 January 2000.
This Act has been amended five times (Act No. 2/2002 Coll., Act No. 217/2002 Coll., Act No. 320/2002 Coll., Act No. 519/2002 Coll. and Act No. 222/2003 Coll.).
Two other amendments to Act No. 325/1999 Coll., on Asylum, are currently in the legislative process and the adoption of further amendments will be linked to European legislation.
At the time of the creation of Act No. 325/1999 Coll., on Asylum, the field of asylum was part of the 3rd pillar of the EU and asylum documents were political documents in terms of binding force.
Already within the framework of the adoption of this Act, efforts were made to make it as compatible as possible with EU law.
A significant change for asylum policy within the EU was the transfer of the issue of asylum from the 3rd to the 1st pillar, when the right of asylum became part of Community law from 1.5.1999 on the basis of the Treaty of Amsterdam.
This shift triggered the need to create appropriate legislation, i.e. to create legal instruments in appropriate legal binding force.
The compatibility of Czech asylum law with EU documents was the subject of regular evaluation reports by the European Commission.
Key Community regulations in the area of asylum were adopted shortly before or after the Czech Republic's accession to the EU and their transposition deadline had not yet expired at the time of the Supreme Audit Office's audit, the Czech Republic.
After their implementation into the Czech legal order, the Czech Republic will be obliged to notify the European Commission of how it has implemented the transposition.
In the Slovak Republic, the procedure of the state authorities in the procedure for granting refugee status and determining the obligations of foreigners who have applied for refugee status or who have been granted temporary refuge in the territory of the Slovak Republic was established with effect from 1.1.1996 by the Act of the National Council of the Slovak Republic No.283/1995 Z. z., o utečencoch.
Since 2003, the Act on Refugees has been replaced by the Act No.480/2002 Z. z. on Asylum and on Amendments to Certain Acts, in which the harmonisation of the legislation of the Slovak Republic with the Council of Europe Directive 2001/55/EC of 20.7.2001 on minimum standards for providing temporary protection in the event of a mass influx of displaced persons and on measures to promote the balance of efforts between member countries in receiving such persons and bearing the resulting consequences has been incorporated.
After two amendments to Act No. 480/2002 Coll., on Asylum, in 2003 and 2004, a third amendment was approved at the beginning of 2005, which entails further harmonisation of the Slovak Republic's law with the EU legislation in the area of migration and asylum.
Its important elements are, for example, the establishment of an obligation for asylum seekers to attend a course on the basics of the Slovak language during their stay in an integration centre, the designation of a guardian by the courts for foreign minors if they reside in the territory of the Slovak Republic without a legal representative, the possibility for applicants to enter into an employment relationship under certain circumstances specified in the amendment to the Act.
The harmonisation of the Slovak Republic's law with the EU law in the area of migration and the asylum process was evaluated in the regular reports of the European Commission on the preparedness for the Slovak Republic's accession to the EU.
In 2002, the report drew attention to the lack of staffing capacity of the Ministry of Interior, which did not correspond to the increased number of asylum seekers.
4. Asylum process
In the Czech Republic, since 1990, refugee matters have been the responsibility of the Ministry.
With effect from 1 January 1996, the Ministry established the organisational component of the State of SUZ. This was due to the separation of the performance of the state administration in the field of asylum procedure, which is carried out through the Department of Asylum and Migration Policy of the Ministry, from the provision of services to asylum seekers.
The task of the SUZ is to provide accommodation, catering, health and other services for the Ministry of Interior to participants in asylum procedures and asylum seekers.
In the Slovak Republic, the Ministry of Interior performs crucial tasks in the field of the asylum process, especially in terms of the financial and material-technical provision of the asylum process, to the extent defined by special regulations.
Priority tasks are issues related to the decision-making of asylum applications by foreigners at the first stage of the administrative procedure and the complex operation of asylum facilities in the field of accommodation, catering, health, financial and material provision of asylum seekers.
In addition, it prepares concepts on the migration policy of the state.
The results achieved in the field of asylum system development in the Slovak Republic in recent years were significantly influenced by the cooperation and support of the Office of the United Nations High Commissioner for Refugees (UNHCR).
A particular benefit was its financial contribution to the reconstruction of the housing stock for asylum seekers.
The UNHCR also co-financed social, cultural and sports activities for asylum seekers.
4.1 Development of the number of asylum seekers and the results of the asylum process
The development of the number of asylum seekers in the Czech Republic is shown in the chart.
A significant increase occurred in 2001 due to the Kosovo crisis and an increase in the number of refugees from Chechnya manifested itself in 2003.
An overview of the results of the asylum procedure in the Czech Republic is given in Table 1.
In the audited period, asylum was granted in a total of 394 cases, of which 83 in 2001, 103 in 2002 and 208 in 2003.
In the audited period, asylum was not granted in total in 22 731 cases and in 22 636 cases the asylum procedure was stopped.
The number of participants in the procedure as of 1.1. includes both persons who have not yet been issued with a decision and those who have not been handed a decision.
Also included here are persons who have been forgiven for missing the deadline for lodging an appeal, or who have had a previous decision revoked and have not yet been issued with a new one.
In the Slovak Republic, the number of asylum seekers is on a steadily increasing trend.
While 96 applicants were registered in 1993, in 2003 it was already 10 358 persons.
There was a significant increase in the number of applicants in 2001, when 8 131 applicants were registered, which represented an increase of 423% compared to 2000, in which 1 556 persons applied for asylum.
The data on the results of the asylum procedure in the Slovak Republic in the audited period are given in Table 2.
In the audited period, a total of 49 asylum seekers were granted and their number did not exceed 0.22% of the registered number of applicants in individual years.
Asylum was not granted in 860 cases.
The asylum procedure was stopped in a total of 23 088 cases.
The majority of applicants voluntarily left the asylum procedure before its completion by staying away from the asylum facility without permission.
In 2002 it was more than 82% of the total number of registered applicants and in 2003 it was already more than 94% of persons.
The length of stay of one applicant in one of the asylum facilities, converted to an average number of days, was 13 days in 2001, 18 days in 2002 and 19 days in 2003.
The findings of the Ministry also show that for most applicants entering the asylum process in the Slovak Republic it is a search for better living conditions, i.e. so-called economic migration, which is not supported by documents adopted by the international community, to which the Slovak Republic has also signed up.
In these cases the asylum system is used by applicants for a purpose.
An application for asylum based on economic reasons, such as seeking employment or better living conditions, is not a reason for granting asylum.
Such an application should be assessed as manifestly unfounded under the provisions of § 12(1)(a) of Act No 480/2002 Coll., on Asylum, and should be decided within 30 days.
Internationally recognized principles for identification of economic migrants, which would distinguish them from applicants persecuted in the country of origin and which would make it possible to speed up the asylum process, have not yet been established.
In view of the above, it can be concluded that the Slovak Republic is a transit country from the point of view of international migration, and the destination countries of migration have been and remain Western European states.
Upon accession to the EU, the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic acceded to the Agreement determining the state responsible for examining asylum applications lodged in one of the Member States of the European Communities (Dublin Convention).
The Convention prevents the submission of multiple targeted asylum applications in more than one EU country.
After positive identification in the EURODAC system, applicants return to the country of first registration.
The Slovak Republic is part of the external borders of the EU countries, therefore the application of the Dublin Convention may result in an increase in the number of applicants in the following period, who will need to create conditions for their stay in the Slovak Republic until a decision is taken on whether or not to grant asylum.
4.2 Drawing on funds
The Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic are obliged to provide financial and material security for asylum seekers in accordance with international agreements and the national legislative regulations based on them.
The state budget of both countries allocates the necessary funds for this purpose.
The amount of expenditure drawn from the state budget is mainly influenced by the number of applicants, the duration of the asylum procedure until the final decision on granting asylum, as well as their state of health.
The increasing number of people entering the asylum process has a direct impact on the higher uptake of statutory benefits for applicants, such as food expenses, pocket money, expenses for basic material equipment, other material equipment and other social contributions.
The amount of some selected benefits is comparable in both countries.
In the Czech Republic, during the audited period, meals were CZK 58 per person per day, pocket money was CZK 12 per person per day and CZK 6 per child up to 15 years of age.
The costs per asylum seeker per stay day were on average CZK 351 in 2001, CZK 383 in 2002 and CZK 345 in 2003.
In addition to pocket money, asylum seekers accommodated in residential centres with independent cooking and applicants accommodated privately outside asylum facilities can be granted a contribution up to the minimum subsistence level.
Act No. 325/1999 Coll., on Asylum, as amended, among other things grants municipalities the right to a contribution to reimburse costs incurred in connection with asylum facilities on their territory in Section 84.
The amount of the allowance was set annually by government resolutions and in the audited period was CZK 7 per person per day of stay.
At the same time, municipalities are granted a contribution to reimburse the non-investment costs of primary schools attended by asylum seekers.
The amount of the allowance was CZK 120 per pupil per month in the audited period, provided that in the given month the person attended school for a minimum of 10 days.
In the Slovak Republic, in the audited period, the meal allowance was SKK 70 per person per day, pocket money was SKK 12 per person per day and SKK 8 per child up to 15 years of age.
The cost per asylum seeker per day of stay was on average SKK 442 in 2001, SKK 447 in 2002 and SKK 445 in 2003.
Municipalities on whose territory an asylum facility is located are granted a contribution to partially reimburse the expenses incurred by the municipality in connection with the establishment and activities of the asylum facility, in accordance with Act No 480/2002 Coll., on Asylum.
Municipalities have so far only partially used the possibility to apply for the contribution, which is set at 1 500 Sk per bed per calendar year.
National legislation in both countries provides for a 90-day period from the start of the asylum procedure for issuing an asylum decision, while allowing for an extension of this period in justified cases.
The most common reason for extending the asylum procedure, which affects the level of state budget expenditure, is the lodging of appeals against the decision not to grant asylum.
In the Czech Republic, the highest number of final decisions was issued between 90 and 180 days (31.54%).
The second highest number was within 90 days from the date of lodging the asylum application (17.61%).
In total, 73% of asylum procedures initiated in 2001-2003 were finally decided within one year from their start.
Within two years from the start of the asylum procedure, 92% of asylum applications were finally decided.
In the Slovak Republic, according to the Ministry of Agriculture, up to 90% of applicants who were not granted asylum use the legal possibility of extending the deadline by lodging an appeal with the court.
In some cases, this was an extension of more than one year and the proceedings were not completed at the time of the inspection.
Some benefit in shortening the asylum procedure is expected from the establishment of joint offices of the Ministry of Agriculture and the Úrad hraničnej a cudzineckej polície Policajného zboru in reception centres in Adamova-Gbeloch, Opatovskej Novej Vsi and Liptovské Vlachoch, which was joined at the time of the inspection from 1.10.2004.
This is supposed to simplify the procedures and shorten the time limits of the proceedings between the two parts of the asylum process.
5. Asylum facilities
The Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic established asylum facilities in which they gradually created suitable conditions for providing services to participants in the asylum procedure.
The asylum facilities provide asylum seekers with accommodation, meals, health care, pocket money and basic material equipment and sanitary needs during their stay.
At the same time, courses are organized as part of leisure activities and the applicants are created conditions for cultural and sports activities.
5.1 Asylum facilities in the Czech Republic
SUZ manages and operates asylum facilities and is responsible for managing the state's property in the premises of the reception centre Vyšní Lhota, the reception and residence centre Červený Újezd, the residential centres Bělá-Jezová, Zastávka u Brna, Kostelec nad Orlicí, Havířov and in the premises of the integration asylum centres Jaroměř and Zastávka u Brna.
At the beginning of 2002, a reception centre was established in the transit area of Prague-Ruzyně airport.
SUZ also operates asylum facilities in Stráž pod Ralskem, Seč, Bruntál, Zbýšov and Kašava, which are operated by a legal entity on the basis of § 80 paragraph 3 of Act No 325/1999 Coll. on Asylum.
The total accommodation capacity of the reception centres is 747 places and the total accommodation capacity of the accommodation centres is 1 977 places.
Reception centres are closed facilities that asylum seekers are not allowed to leave until the prescribed medical examinations and basic reception operations referred to in Act No 325/1999 Coll., on Asylum have been carried out.
Infringement of the obligation to stay in the reception centre is classified as an offence.
The accommodation centres to which asylum seekers come from reception centres are used for housing asylum seekers until the decision on their application to grant or not to grant asylum becomes final.
Under certain conditions, asylum seekers have the possibility to leave the accommodation centres or to stay in private.
Asylum seekers have the right to free accommodation, provision of meals, other services and pocket money in the reception and accommodation centres in which they are reported to be staying, provided that they have suffered the acts necessary to establish their financial and financial circumstances, and these conditions are such that even partial reimbursement of the said services cannot be fairly claimed from them.
Integration asylum centres are used for the temporary accommodation of persons who have been granted asylum.
Clients are accommodated in the centre on the basis of an accommodation contract, which is usually concluded for 6 months, with the possibility of extension until adequate housing can be provided for them, or they can provide it themselves within the framework of the state integration programme.
In the integration centre, clients cover all the costs of accommodation and eat individually.
Persons with recognised refugee status have the same rights and obligations as Czech citizens and have the same access to social security.
5.1.1 Costs of asylum facilities
For the comparison of asylum facilities, the cost per physical stay day was chosen as the best indicator.
It is based on the actual number of persons who were actually provided with services provided by the asylum facility each day.
In Table 3 and in the graph, the facilities operated by SUZ are marked as own and those operated by legal persons on the basis of Section 80 of Act No 325/1999 Coll., on Asylum, as contract.
The cost per stay day in the own asylum facility operated by SUZ decreases with the increasing load capacity of these facilities. This is due to the fact that the fixed costs of running the facilities are allocated to more asylum seekers.
The total cost of providing services for asylum seekers increases proportionately with their increasing number.
In 2001 and 2003, the own asylum facilities accommodated applicants in crisis capacity.
In part of 2003, extra accommodation capacity in residential containers (320 beds in total) was even used to address the capacity crisis of asylum facilities caused by the mass arrival of asylum seekers of Chechen nationality from Poland.
This capacity was provided by renting 80 residential and 6 sanitary containers.
Expenditure per applicant per stay day was lower in these years.
However, long-term maintenance of high filling capacity of these facilities is not possible.
The risks of an unexpected influx of refugees and the associated demand for higher accommodation capacity must be taken into account.
At the same time, it is not possible to carry out some repairs, maintenance and investments when the accommodation capacity is fully occupied.
The form of asylum facilities operated under contract allows the adoption of operational solutions in the area of asylum facilities capacities if necessary.
5.2 Asylum facilities in the Slovak Republic
Asylum facilities are reception centres and residential centres.
The Ministry has in its administration the reception centres Adamov-Gbely, Rohovce, Opatovská Nová Ves and the Brezová pod Bradlom residential centre.
The total capacity of reception centres is 470 places and the residential centre 100 places.
The increasing number of asylum seekers was solved by the Ministry by setting up a residential centre in Gabčíkov in the rented premises of the Slovak Technical University of Bratislava with a flexible available capacity of 250 to 940 places.
According to the concluded contract, the renter also provides services related to the operation of the centre.
In this form, the Ministry solved the lack of its own staff.
The residential centre was also temporarily set up in 2002 and 2003 in the rented premises in Jazierciach with a capacity of 160 places.
The reception centres had an average occupancy rate of 57% to 62% during the audited period, while the residential centres had an average occupancy rate of 33% to 50%.
The occupancy rate varied according to the time of year and was highest in the last months of the year when a much larger number of asylum seekers applied for asylum compared to other months of the year.
A further increase in accommodation capacities of about 450 places will be possible after the reconstruction of the centres in Opatovskej Novej Vsi and Vlachoch.
After the completion of the centre in Humennom in 2006, the number of places will increase by another 550 persons.
5.2.1 Costs of asylum facilities
Data on the costs of running asylum facilities are given in Table 4.
Their analysis shows that the operation of an asylum facility by another entity, which will provide premises and ensure the running of the facility, including related activities, is one of the options to ensure the tasks arising from the stay of asylum seekers in the Slovak Republic at a reasonable cost.
6. Management of State Funds and Property
6.1 Analysis of Management
In the Czech Republic, in 2001, the approved budgetary expenditure of SUZ was increased by thirteen budgetary measures by CZK 103 077 thousand.
Of this, CZK 89,979 thousand (87.29%) were earmarked funds. The bulk was intended to deal with the consequences of the Kosovo crisis (CZK 44,538 thousand) and to provide health care provided to asylum seekers (CZK 38,870 thousand).
In 2002, the expenditures of SUZ were increased by 20 budgetary measures by CZK 88,362 thousand.
Of this, CZK 62,282 thousand (70.48%) were earmarked funds, of which the bulk (CZK 53,200 thousand) was intended for health care provided to asylum seekers.
In 2003, the expenditures of SUZ were increased by 14 budgetary measures by a total of CZK 88,078 thousand.
Of this, CZK 82,000 thousand (93.09%) were earmarked funds released from the General Treasury Administration.
The amount of CZK 51,000 thousand was intended for health care provided to asylum seekers, CZK 24,000 thousand for dealing with the influx of Chechen refugees and CZK 7,000 thousand for the humanitarian evacuation program of disabled residents of the Republic of Iraq.
An overview of the use of selected expenditures of SUZ in the audited period is given in Table 5.
From the above overview it is clear that the largest part of the expenses was spent on providing services.
The amount of expenses incurred on the purchase of services ranged from 37.07% to 38.23% of the total expenses.
The outrageous expenses in this item were expenses for accommodation and meals of asylum seekers in asylum facilities operated on the basis of a contract, expenses for medical care provided to asylum seekers and costs of permanent security service providing security in individual asylum facilities.
Expenditure on salaries, payments for work done and insurance premiums (23.99% - 24.97%) accounted for a significant share of the total SUZ expenses.
Last but not least, purchases of materials (approximately 14%) accounted for a significant share of the total SUZ expenses, with the largest share of these expenses having been the purchase of food (7.61% ? 9.83% of the total expenses).
In the Slovak Republic, the budget management of the Ministry of Interior for securing migration policy and the asylum process was marked by more budgetary measures that addressed legitimate requirements related to the increase in the number of asylum seekers.
The draft and breakdown of the budget in the expenditure part was characterised, especially in 2001 and 2002, by an imbalance between the requirements of the Ministry of Interior, which were based on the increase in the number of asylum seekers and on the need to finance their legal entitlements, and the resources provided, especially in the main category of current expenditure.
The administrator of the budget chapter addressed the disproportion during the year with several budgetary measures, increasing the limit of current expenditure by 41.8% in 2001 and by as much as 71.7% in 2002.
An overview of the execution of selected expenses of the Ministry of Interior in the audited period is given in Table 6.
Expenditure on wages, salaries and insurance premiums in the range of 24.47% to 30.51% and expenditure on materials and services in the range of 21.04% to 38.82% of total expenditure accounted for a significant share of current expenditure.
More than 10% were expenditures on security services and from 3.92% to 7.20% were expenditures on food purchases.
Another significant part was expenditures on accommodation and catering services ranging from 10.82% to 26.96%.
A relatively low share in the range from 1.03% to 6.25% were capital expenditures.
6.2 Detected deficiencies
The results of the audit in the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic pointed to some similar deficiencies that did not have a major impact on the management of state funds and property.
These were deficiencies in particular in the following areas: (a) the use of state budget funds contrary to the purpose for which they were determined by the Act on the State Budget, when current expenditures were paid for actions having the character of technical evaluation of long-term tangible assets; (b) violations of the Act on Accounting in the area of inventories and in non-compliance with the indicative chart of accounts.
Furthermore, in the Czech Republic, minor deficiencies were found in the management of State property, when it was left for use by another person without a proper contract; failure to comply with the deadline for reporting changes to the Land Register data violated the Act on the Land Register; failure to leave waste for disposal to a person who was not a person authorised to handle waste violated the Act on Waste.
Furthermore, in the Slovak Republic, deficiencies were found in the provision of unreasonably high advances for the collection of electricity and natural gas, deficiencies in public procurement and in the management of State property, when its records were not sufficiently secured and a method of liquidation of unneeded assets was not demonstrated.
7. Internal control system
In the Czech Republic, an internal control system within the meaning of the provisions of Act No 320/2001 Coll., on financial control, determining the competences of individual employees responsible for carrying out preliminary, continuous and subsequent control, was introduced at SUZ on 1 July 2002.
At the same time, an internal audit system was introduced and an internal auditor of SUZ was appointed.
Every year, SUZ is issued a plan of financial, social and operational technical controls aimed at comprehensive verification of the management of state funds and property in individual asylum facilities managed by SUZ.
In 2002, 42 management controls were carried out and in 2003, 54 were carried out.
In the Slovak Republic, the direct performance of control activities in the departments and organisations of the Ministry of Interior of the Slovak Republic with regard to compliance with generally binding legal regulations and internal regulations is ensured by the Office of Control of the Minister.
During the audited period, the performance of tasks in the field of asylum policy was not audited.
The internal control system of the Ministry of Interior is focused mainly on carrying out preliminary and interim financial control according to Act No 502/2001 Coll., on financial control and internal audit.
The performance of financial control is also regulated by the internal regulations of the Director of the Ministry of Interior.
The substantive focus of the control activities as part of the management of individual departments was determined in the framework of the annual plan of the Ministry of Interior.
The directors of departments were designated as responsible for the performance of the control in this area.
According to the submitted written documentation, no deficiencies were found.
Since the date of the Regulation of the Ministry of Interior of the Slovak Republic No. 28 of April 23, 2004, the Ministry of Interior is obliged to handle and investigate complaints under the Complaints Act.
The organisational security of this task will need to be solved in the near future.
Communiqué
This report was prepared in Czech, English and Slovak languages and signed by the Vice-President of the Supreme Audit Office and the Chairman of the Najvyšší Audit Office of the Slovak Republic.
Joint Report on Parallel Controls of Expenditure on the Prague – Dresden Motorway Construction
Introductory statement
Without the existence of trans-European transport networks, it would be difficult to imagine a modern, dynamic and, above all, united Europe.
High-quality transport networks are a prerequisite for maintaining and increasing the standard of living of Europeans.
Creating the conditions for fast, safe, reliable and cheap transport of people and goods is an important task for the state administration.
It is a very demanding task, both organisationally and technically, as well as financially.
European efforts at sustainable mobility often find it difficult to compromise with Europe's interest in maintaining a healthy and human-friendly environment.
Transport infrastructure construction, thanks to the necessary measures for the benefit of the environment, is financially demanding.
Considerate procedures and decisions by the state administration in preparing and acquiring transport constructions can bring significant savings of public financial resources, which can be used in other ways for the benefit of citizens.
One of the tasks of audit institutions is to actively search for deficiencies that led to lower-than-achievable economy, efficiency and effectiveness of expenditures on transport infrastructure constructions.
Audit institutions should not only alert the state administration to the detected deficiencies, but recommend measures that will lead to improvement of the situation, for the benefit of citizens, for the benefit of Europe.
Short summary
The two supreme audit institutions of the Federal Republic of Germany and the Czech Republic (hereinafter referred to as the Federal Republic of Germany and the Czech Republic) the Bundesrechnungshof (hereinafter referred to as the BRH) and the Supreme Audit Office (hereinafter referred to as the Supreme Audit Office (SAO) carried out parallel audits of expenditures on the construction of the Prague – Dresden motorway (the D8 motorway in the Czech Republic and the A17 motorway in the Federal Republic of Germany) in 2005 and 2006.
The motorways are connected by a border bridge, which is co-financed by both countries.
Thanks to cooperation with the SAO, the BRH was able to carry out a thorough audit of the effectiveness of the funds spent on the construction of the border bridge.
Based on the close cooperation with the SAO, the SAO obtained the necessary data on the level of German costs of bridges and tunnels for comparative purposes.
In 2000, the Czech Republic and the Federal Republic of Germany concluded a contract for the construction of the border bridge.
According to the construction process, the deadline for completion was finally scheduled for the end of 2006.
However, during the award procedure, the Road and Motorway Directorate of the Czech Republic (RMD) made errors, which led to an extension of the competition period and a shorter construction period.
The contract with the contractor was thus signed later than expected.
The contractor agreed to build the bridge in a shorter time and ensure its completion in 2006.
As a result, the RMD had to accept a significant increase in the price of the bridge.
In the framework of the joint audits, the prices of bridges on the D8 and A17 motorways were compared, based on the calculation of the square metre area of the bridge structure.
Statistical analysis of the prices allowed to identify bridges with high costs per square metre of area.
The analysis revealed that the border bridge was the most expensive bridge in the group of large bridges with a length of over 100 meters.
The price increase could also be attributed to the delay that occurred during the tender procedure.
In the analysis of the tunnel construction costs, the auditors found that the tunnel prices on the D8 motorway were significantly higher than the prices of comparable tunnels in Germany.
BRH and the SAO now have a database of the prices of bridges and tunnels on which they will be able to rely in future checks of the efficiency of the means used for transport infrastructure purposes.
For the construction of bridges, the two auditing institutions recommend: standardization of the bridge construction and the use of combined steel-concrete and special structures only in cases where prestressed reinforced concrete bridges are not adequate.
The main features of the cooperation included its team spirit and informality.
During the parallel inspection, the auditors shared their specific knowledge and skills.
Introduction
This report reports on the progress and results of the parallel audits of funds spent on the construction of the motorway connecting Dresden and Prague (D 8 in the Czech Republic and A 17 in Germany).
The audits focused on the economy, efficiency and effectiveness of the expenses incurred.
Parallel audits were carried out by BRH in Germany and by the SAO in the Czech Republic.
Parallel audits were carried out in 2005 and 2006.
The SAO audited the economy, efficiency and effectiveness of expenditures amounting to approximately CZK 20 billion including VAT (approximately EUR 690 million) on the border section of the D 8 motorway, which is numbered 0807.
Of this amount, EUR 64 million from European funds (ISPA) were planned to be used.
In addition to the parallel audits carried out jointly with the SAO, BRH audited the preparation and construction of the A 17 motorway in 2003 and 2005.
The funds spent on the construction of all three sections of the A 17 motorway amounted to approximately EUR 670 million, of which EUR 277 million will be co-financed by European funds (EFRE).
The motorway from Prague to Dresden is part of the Trans-European Transport Corridor IV. Dresden – Central and Southern parts of Eastern Europe – Istanbul.
The D 8 motorway runs from Prague through Ústí nad Labem to the state border.
The A 17 motorway runs from the state border of the Czech Republic/Germany to Dresden.
At the time of the audits, the border sections of the two motorways were under construction.
These sections were put into operation on 21 December 2006.
On the German side, the motorway is completed as far as Dresden, while on the Czech side of the D 8 motorway it is not completed because the section No 0805, which is 16.4 km long across the Bohemian Central Mountains between Řehlovice and Lovosice, is still in the preparatory phase.
According to the plan, the section No 0805 between Prague and Ústí nad Labem is to pass through the protected landscape area of the Bohemian Central Mountains.
According to forecasts carried out in the Czech Republic in 2001, the traffic intensity on the border section No 0807 of the D 8 motorway should be 22,940 vehicles per day in 2008.
According to German forecasts, the traffic intensity on the Czech border will total about 25,000 vehicles per day in 2010.
In 2000, Germany and the Czech Republic concluded the Contract between the Federal Republic of Germany and the Czech Republic for the interconnection of the German A 17 motorway and the Czech D 8 motorway on the common state border by the construction of a border bridge.
Both states are involved in the construction of the bridge, therefore the control of the construction of this bridge was an important aspect of the parallel controls carried out by the two audit institutions.
Cooperation between BRH and the SAO
