JOINT FINAL REPORT on the results of parallel audits of the administration of excise duties in the Slovak Republic and the Czech Republic
Joint Final Report
May 2017
Supreme Audit Office of the Slovak Republic
Supreme Audit Office of the Czech Republic
Introductory word
The submitted joint report informs on the progress and outcome of international cooperation in parallel audits carried out by the Supreme Audit Office of the Slovak Republic and the Supreme Audit Office of the Czech Republic, focusing on the administration of excise duties in 2012-2015.
The cooperation between supreme audit institutions of both countries was realized on the basis of a cooperation agreement between the Supreme Audit Office of the Slovak Republic and the Supreme Audit Office of the Czech Republic in the performance of parallel audits focused on the administration of excise duties, which was concluded in August 2015.
The topic of parallel audits was selected on the basis of the fact that both EU Member States are based on common European legislation in order to find out how it is applied at the national level, how the system of administration of excise duties is set up and in what way the systems in the Slovak Republic and the Czech Republic are different.
The greatest benefits of the control actions carried out were the exchange of experience, the identification of differences and the identification of good practice.
Last but not least, it was beneficial to find that the international comparability of data on the performance and efficiency of excise duty administration is very limited without the implementation of parallel controls.
Miloslav Kala,
Karol Mitrik,
President
President
Supreme Audit Office of the Czech Republic
Supreme Audit Office of the Slovak Republic
on the results of parallel controls of the administration of the SPD in the Slovak Republic and the Czech Republic
Summary and evaluation
The legislation on excise duties in the Czech Republic and Slovakia and their administration complies with EU legislation and significantly exceeds EU requirements.
Differences have been found between the excise duty adjustment in the Slovak Republic and the Czech Republic; in the Czech Republic, it contributes to the effective administration of excise duties by verifying the economic stability of applicants for a permit and mandatory marking and dyeing of selected mineral oils and certain other oils; In Slovakia, the distribution of control stamps is simpler than in the Czech Republic and less burdensome for tax administrators.
In the fight against evasion of excise taxes, monitoring of movements of raw tobacco or tobacco raw material, implementation of the fuel distributor institute and registration of sellers of consumer packaging of alcohol have proved good practice in both countries.
Revenues from excise taxes in the Slovak Republic and the Czech Republic have been growing more slowly than other tax revenues.
The EU objectives of reducing labour taxation, introducing eco-saving measures and reducing dependence on tobacco and alcohol have not been met in the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic so far, among other reasons, because the indexation of excise tax rates is not implemented in both countries.
This has the effect of reducing the importance of excise taxes on total tax revenues and, as a result of increasing purchasing power, a real reduction in the tax burden by excise taxes.
The introduction of eco-measures has been financially supported by the state for a long time, but these measures have a negative impact on excise tax revenues, which will have to be replaced by other revenues or by a reduction in state expenditures in the future.
Administrative expenditures spent on the administration of excise taxes in the Czech Republic and Slovakia have been growing for a long time, mainly due to wage increases, and their efficiency has been decreasing.
In the Slovak Republic, this efficiency has also been negatively affected by expenditures on the computerisation of excise tax administration (IT expenditures) and by expenditures on wages of employees performing permanent tax supervision in tax warehouses on alcohol.
The computerisation of excise tax administration in the Slovak Republic has not significantly affected the reduction of the number of tax administrators.
The SAO of the Czech Republic and the SAO of the Slovak Republic recommend that the Ministry of the Slovak Republic reconsider the validity of the performance of permanent tax supervision in tax warehouses on alcohol.
In the Czech Republic, the efficiency of administrative expenditures was influenced by the fact that the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic did not apply procedures during the audited period that would lead to a reduction in the personnel intensity of excise tax administration.
The number of comparable administrative acts of tax administrators was similar in the Slovak Republic and the Czech Republic in the individual years of the audited period, while the number of comparable tax subjects is approximately one third lower in the Slovak Republic than in the Czech Republic.
Tax administrators in the Slovak Republic perform administrative tasks mainly in the form of physical performance of tax supervision, while tax administrators in the Czech Republic emphasize remote supervision and risk analysis.
Administration of excise taxes in the Slovak Republic is administratively more demanding than in the Czech Republic and due to the ratio of the number of tax operations to the number of subjects it is also more costly.
The electronization of excise tax administration in the Slovak Republic and the Czech Republic took place in different areas.
Administration of excise tax returns is fully electronized in the Slovak Republic, documents proving taxation of selected products in free tax circulation are electronically transmitted in the Czech Republic.
Both methods of electronization support effective administration of excise taxes, and therefore the SAO of the Czech Republic and the SAO of the Slovak Republic recommend applying them not only in both countries.
The total expenditures for implementation of the EMCS system could not be compared, as the Slovak Ministry of Finance provided data on expenditures only for the upgrade of the system in the period 2011–2015, but expenditures were incurred even before this period.
Expenditures incurred in the period only for the upgrade of EMCS were in the Slovak Republic about 20% higher than expenses incurred in the Czech Republic both for the implementation of EMCS and for the upgrade of the system in more than ten years.
The administrators of excise taxes in the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic did not reach comparable values of qualitative indicators when spending comparable expenses.
The level of supervision is comparable in both countries, but in the Slovak Republic the administration of excise taxes is significantly more resource intensive.
The introduction of the electronic system for monitoring the movement of products subject to excise tax (EMCS) made the administration of excise taxes more efficient, but in the Slovak Republic to a lesser extent as significantly higher expenses were spent on the implementation of the system and its modernisation than in the Czech Republic.
Basic information
The cooperation of the two audit institutions took place on the basis of the Agreement on Cooperation in the execution of parallel audits focused on the administration of excise taxes dated 18 August 2015.
The SAO of the Czech Republic and the SAO of the Slovak Republic agreed to perform parallel audits, which will primarily focus on the issue of excise tax administration and whose results will allow analysis, mutual comparison and evaluation of the findings.
Joint audit questions were agreed on which the parallel audits were based.
Characteristics of the subject and objectives of the parallel audits:
The aim of the parallel audits was to compare the performance of excise tax administrators taking into account qualitative and quantitative indicators and to identify weaknesses in the excise tax administration process.
The following main audit questions were to be answered in particular:
Did the excise tax administrators in the Czech Republic and Slovakia achieve comparable values of qualitative indicators when incurring comparable expenses?
Did the introduction of the Excise Movement and Control System (EMCS) make the excise tax administration more effective and was the expenditure spent on its implementation effective?
Parallel audits were carried out to identify the causes of significant differences affecting the efficiency and effectiveness of the tax administration in the Czech Republic and Slovakia, especially in the area of legal regulation and in the setting of the organizational structure.
THISsegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
The General Directorate of Customs (DG) and the Financial Directorate of the Slovak Republic (FR SR) joined the joint declaration on mutual cooperation of the Visegrad Four countries, the objectives of this declaration include the fight against fraud, the examination of the possibility of harmonizing legislation and searching for harmonised interpretations on the rules of selected problems, the examination of the possibility of joint activities to increase the efficiency in detecting fraud and the sharing of experience and best practices.
1 The EMCS is operated according to the Decision No 1152/2003/EC of the European Parliament and of the Council of 16 June 2003 on the introduction of an electronic system for the transport and monitoring of products subject to excise duty.
Identification of the audit carried out by the SAO of the Czech Republic
Audit number: 15/33
Audit subject: Administration of excise duties
Audit objective: The objective of the SAO of the Czech Republic was to examine the procedure of the customs authorities in the administration of excise duties, in particular in the monitoring of transport under the system of conditional exemption from excise duties and in securing the tax (customs debts); to examine whether the system of administration of excise duties is set up in such a way as to ensure the efficiency of the collection of state budget revenues.
Audit period: years 2012–2015 and in case of factual connections the period before and after
Audit person: General Directorate of Customs
Audit identification of the audit carried out by the SAO of the Slovak Republic
Audit number: KA-023/2016/1050
Audit subject: Administration of excise duties
Audit objective: The objective of the audit was to examine independently and objectively whether the General Directorate of the Slovak Republic and the Customs Authorities (CA) in the administration of excise duties operate economically, efficiently and effectively in accordance with generally binding legal regulations.
Audit period: years 2012–2015
Audit person: Financial Directorate of the Slovak Republic
Legislation on excise duties in the Czech Republic and Slovakia
Legislation on excise duties administration is divided into the level of EU legislation (see Annex 1) and the level of national legislation (see Annex 2).
Council Directive 2008/118/EC, concerning the general regulation of excise duties and repealing Directive 92/12/EEC, defines excise duty and lays down the basic rules for the administration of taxes and the treatment of energy products and electricity, tobacco products, alcohol and alcoholic beverages.
This directive allows for the imposition of consumption taxes on other products.
EU legislation regulates in particular the minimum conditions for: the level of tax rates for each type of selected products, the production, storage, processing and holding of products subject to tax, the incurrence of tax liability, exemption from tax and refund of tax, supervision of transport of selected products between EU Member States, international cooperation and keeping of registers on economic operators and tax warehouses.
EU legislation allows for the establishment of control procedures and institutes at national level, provided that they do not distort competition.
Excise tax legislation in the Czech Republic
Definition of legislation in the Czech Republic
In the Czech Republic, the legislation on excise taxes is concentrated in the Excise Tax Act (Act No 353/2003 Coll.), which regulates the administration of the mineral oil tax, the alcohol tax, the tobacco products tax, the beer tax, the wine and intermediate products tax and the raw tobacco tax.
This Act defines the forms of disposal of products subject to excise taxes, the taxpayer, the authorisation procedure, the conditions for transport of products, the tax declaration and penalties for infringements of legislation.
The Act and subsequent decrees further regulate certain other conditions for handling mineral oils (marking of mineral oils), restrictions on the sale of spirits and tobacco products, the monitoring of the handling of special mineral oils and the storage of raw tobacco for a purpose other than the production of tobacco products.
Taxes on other energy products (i.e. natural gas and certain other gases, solid fuels and electricity) are regulated in parts 45 to 47 of Act No 261/2007 Coll., on the Stabilisation of Public Budgets.
In the Czech Republic, a number of provisions related to the administration of excise duties are also contained in special legislation. Act No 311/2006 Coll. on Fuel and an implementing regulation regulate the conditions for the sale, supply, distribution of fuel and keeping of records of fuel put into free tax circulation.
Act No 61/1997 Coll., on Alcohol, and its implementing regulations define the conditions for the production, storage, registration and control of the production and circulation of alcohol.
Act No 307/2013 Coll., on obligatory marking of alcohol, and the relevant implementing regulations stipulate the obligatory marking of alcohol in consumer packaging, the conditions for the handling of control tapes and the conditions for the handling of alcohol (i.e. for the production, processing, sale or other transfer, transport, transport, storage, taking over, use, possession, import or export of alcohol).
Tax procedures not specified in the special regulations are governed by Act No 280/2009 Coll., the Tax Code.
Penalties are imposed by procedures pursuant to Act No 500/2004 Coll., the Administrative Code.
The conditions for issuing a trade licence (concession) for the operation of the trade "production and processing of fuels and lubricants and distribution of fuel" and "production, treatment and sale of fermentation alcohol, potable alcohol and spirits" are governed by Act No 455/1991 Coll., on the trade business (Trade Licensing Act).
The Czech Republic has used the authorisation to introduce control procedures and institutes to control the transport of selected products in free tax circulation and to supervise compliance with legal regulations when handling selected products for which excise duty has not been paid, as well as when handling selected products for which tax has already been paid.
These include monitoring the handling of special mineral oils and raw tobacco, marking of certain other mineral oils, marking of tobacco products and alcohol in consumer packaging.
The Czech Republic has used the authorisation to apply excise duty to other products as well and has introduced excise duty on raw tobacco as one of the measures against tax fraud.
Structure of changes in legislation for individual types of excise taxes in relation to the subject of control in the Czech Republic
Based on the Government of the Czech Republic's resolution of 3 October 2012 no. 735, the implementation of the "zero tolerance plan for the black market in spirits" resulted in major legislative changes in the Czech Republic in 2012-2015, which introduced a number of measures against tax fraud on excise duty on alcohol.
During the same period, there were also major changes in the legislation on mineral oil tax, tax on tobacco products and the criminality of preparation of tax reduction.
Criminal law protection of tax revenues
With effect from 1 July 2016, the preparation of the crime of "tax reduction, fee and similar obligatory payment" is criminalised. The implemented regulation should enable police authorities to take more effective and timely measures to reduce tax fraud, e.g. the deployment of operatively searched means.
General provisions of excise tax administration
With effect from 1 January 2015, the issuance of a permit to dispose of products subject to excise duty under the Excise Tax Act is subject to: reliability; indebtedness; economic stability; authorisation to operate a trade enabling the pursuit of the activity related to the permit; situations where the applicant is not in liquidation or bankruptcy.
The aim of the legislation was in particular to address the issue of the creation of tax arrears by reducing entities authorised to dispose of products subject to excise tax.
The condition of economic stability newly allows the tax administration to take into account the financial situation of tax entities both in the authorisation procedure and after the authorisation.
The purpose of this measure is to prevent entities without sufficient financial income to properly fulfil tax obligations from disposing of selected products.
To assess the economic stability of the applicant, indicators (profitability, liquidity, financial stability, activity, labour productivity) have been established on the basis of which the financial analysis is carried out.
In addition to these indicators, the tax administrator's administrative discretion with regard to the individual conditions of the given procedure also depends.
The law stipulates the periodicity of the verification of compliance with the condition of economic stability due to the timeliness of the data – the verification takes place once a year in connection with the deadline for filing the income tax return.
The tax administrator has the possibility to determine other conditions needed for the tax administration.
If the permit holder does not fulfil the conditions, the tax administrator is entitled to cancel the permit or cancel it with a delay.
Out of the total number of 2,609 entities for which the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic examined the condition of economic stability, 18.6% were found to be economically unstable with a high risk of creating arrears in case the tax obligation exceeds the amount of the tax security (e.g. repeated recipient).
The permit was revoked for 10 entities, other applicants increased the tax security, capitalized their contribution to the company or provided up-to-date accounting data according to which they already fulfilled all the conditions for issuing the permit.
In addition to the applicant, the conditions of reliability and indebtedness must also be fulfilled by a natural person who is a statutory body or a member thereof, or by a natural person who, although not a statutory body of the applicant or a member thereof, carries out this activity (chaining of legal persons in the capacity of a statutory body or its member, so-called connected entities).
By the end of 2016, more than 30,000 connected entities were examined.
The records kept under the Excise Tax Act (Sections 37 to 40 and Section 60 of Act No 353/2003 Coll.) contain data on:
the type, name, code and quantity of goods produced, received, issued or dispatched, broken down by type of tax treatment regime (conditional exemption regime, import, retrospective entry into conditional exemption regime, export, free tax circulation, own consumption, loss);
the identifier (SEED ID) of the recipient or supplier of the selected products, the declarant, the date of the event and the entry in the register;
the transport of selected products (e.g. means of transport, carrier, transport number);
the registration numbers of the related documents;
the notification of the release into free tax circulation of the alcohol in consumer packaging marked with a control tape and the data of its distribution.
The record of receipt after transport must be made immediately after its termination.
In the case of registers kept electronically, the record must be kept or enable the output in the format xls, xlsx, ods.
Ethyl alcohol
After 2012, the Czech Republic introduced a complex of measures aimed at ensuring a detailed overview of the activities of entities (see Annex 3, Figure A) from the production of raw alcohol through the marking with a control tape to its distribution to the final seller or authorised user of the exempt alcohol.
In the Czech Republic, the production equipment for the production of alcohol which is not in operation is also subject to supervision by customs authorities.
The aim of the new legislation was to increase the overview of the processing of alcohol and the production of spirits and to identify persons handling alcohol in consumer packaging, to reduce the handling of alcohol to financially stable and reliable persons and to ensure constant supervision of the production and labelling of spirits.
The most important measures are: The records of the production, receipt, stocks and delivery of alcohol contain information on the quantity of alcohol according to the various stages of the production and processing of alcohol with the identification numbers of documents.
To limit the volume of consumer packaging, the material of packaging and to limit the number of packages with broken control tape at the point of final sale or delivery to the consumer.
Consumer packaging means a container or other packaging with a capacity of max. one litre, or three litres if it is a container made of glass.
Spirits in larger packaging are regarded as unmarked, which are prohibited from being handled.
At the point of final sale to a natural person for his or her personal consumption, there may be max. one consumer packaging with broken control tape, or three if they are fitted with a one-way valve.
Mandatory registration of a person who places alcohol in products in consumer packaging having at least 15% vol. of alcohol into free tax circulation and is: an importer of alcohol, a producer of alcohol in the Czech Republic or an operator of a tax warehouse under conditional tax exemption, provided that personal and technical conditions are fulfilled.
Personal conditions – reliability, integrity and non-pronouncement of disqualification – must be fulfilled by the applicant and a person in the capacity of a statutory body or a responsible representative.
The applicant must provide a security of CZK 100,000 to CZK 5,000,000 (i.e. approximately €3,700 to €185,000) depending on the anticipated quantity of control tapes collected.
Technical conditions for registration are an appropriate place for marking alcohol and equipping the place of marking or tax warehouse with a camera tracking device with continuous operation and remote access of the tax administration.
The control tape registration marks are introduced for marking spirits with a volume of more than 0.06 litre.
When control tapes are transported, the control tape registration mark must be stated in the transport documents or customs declaration at export.
The control tape until 30.11.2013 contained a ten-digit registration code, which included a four-digit registration number, the code of the application for allocation of control tapes and the code of classification according to the level of the volume concentration of ethanol.
Since 1 December 2013, the control tape newly contains two types of identifiers and the quantity of ethyl alcohol in consumer packaging, expressed in millilitres of ethanol at 20 °C, rounded down to whole millilitres.
The register of control tapes for marking spirits contains daily records of individual ways of handling control tapes according to the registration codes, as well as the documents on the basis of which the registration was made.
When specific control tapes are destroyed, lost or stolen, the holder is obliged to electronically notify the tax administrator of the registration code of the control tapes concerned and their number on the following working day after the decisive event.
Introduction of new facts of the offences and adjustment of the amount of penalties imposed for infringements of legislation when handling control tapes.
Penalties may be imposed up to the amount of excise duty or up to ten times higher (e.g. in case of destruction or loss of control tapes in the number exceeding 0.1% of the total quantity of the individual order of control tapes made, in case of failure to return control tapes within the statutory deadline).
Limitation of the handling of control tapes only to registered holders, who may not pass them on to another person, with the exception of their provision to a foreign supplier for the purpose of marking spirits in consumer packaging manufactured outside the Czech Republic.
Exported control tapes must be placed on consumer packaging and imported back no later than nine months after receipt from the tax administrator.
Compulsory registration of the distributor of spirits in consumer packaging provided that similar personal conditions are fulfilled as for the person obliged to mark spirits and with the obligation to deposit up to CZK 5,000,000 (i.e. approx. €185,000).
Definition of persons for the sale or purchase of spirits in consumer packaging.
Eligible persons are obliged to sell alcohol in consumer packaging to other registered persons or to final sellers, or they may sell it as a final seller.
They may acquire alcohol from other registered persons, the insolvency administrator, the administrative authority, organisational units of the state or unregistered persons in the execution of tax execution.
Notifications of the introduction of alcohol or sale in consumer packaging into free tax circulation are required to be sent by the holders and distributors of alcohol to the tax administrator via the information system maintained by the tax administrator (ORO web client) or in compliance with the content in xml format, immediately following the decisive event.
The notification includes the number of control tapes used, the volume and type of consumer packaging, the volume percentage of alcohol, the European commodity code (EAN), the identification of the distributor or final seller, as well as the name of the product and the batch of production.
Tax entities sent approx. 10.5 million notifications in 2014 and 2015.
Mandatory concession (a specific form of trade licence) not only for the production and modification of alcohol, but also for the sale of alcohol in consumer packaging by an entrepreneur to a natural person for his personal use or to another legal or entrepreneurial natural person for his own internal use.
Licensed trades can be carried out only after a decision has been issued by the trade licence office, subject to professional competence and other conditions.
No prescribed professional competence is required for the sale of alcohol.
The benefit for the tax administrator is an overview of sellers and their establishments and the restriction of
trading to reliable entities.
In the Czech Republic, for the branch including the production, modification of fermentation alcohol, potable alcohol, spirits and other alcoholic beverages and sales, there were registered in 2014 about 94 thousand and in 2015 about 104 thousand concessions.
Checks on compliance with legislation in the area of handling products subject to excise duties in the Czech Republic are also ensured in their activities outside the tax administrator: trade offices, the State Agricultural and Food Inspection, the authorities of the Financial Administration of the Czech Republic, the authorities of the Czech Trade Inspection.
If they find that there has been a breach of duty or a violation of the prohibition, they will immediately inform the excise tax administrator.
Mineral oils
The Czech Republic has introduced a comprehensive system of supervision (see Annex No. 3, diagram B) to which mineral oils subject to excise duty but also selected mineral oils not subject to excise duty, which have been misused for tax evasion.
The system includes supervision from the production of mineral oil through the storage, transport, marking and colouring of selected mineral oils, marking of certain other mineral oils up to delivery to the final consumer or user and in some cases the consumption of mineral oils.
The monitoring by the customs authorities includes the production of marking agents for the marking and handling of mineral oils.
The marking and colouring of selected mineral oils are subject to the mineral oils listed under Combined Nomenclature codes 2710 19 25 (kerosene others), 2710 19 29 (other medium oils not elsewhere specified) and heavy gas oils 2710 19 41, 2710 19 45 and 2710 19 49, where their marking is not prohibited.
For example, benzole, toluene, xylol and lubricating oils and other oils intended for purposes other than engine propulsion are subject to the marking and colouring of selected mineral oils.
The marking and colouring of selected mineral oils and certain other mineral oils is possible only with the permission of the tax authorities.

The most significant new measures since 2012:
Monitoring the handling of special mineral oils, which are a group of mineral oils under Combined Nomenclature codes 2710 19 71 to 2710 19 99 (i.e. lubricating oils and other oils intended for purposes other than engine propulsion), whose kinematic viscosity at 40 °C is less than 12 mm2. s-1 inclusive and have at least one of the following characteristics: a flash point of less than 150 °C, at the distillation test at least 20 % of the volume, including losses, is distilled up to 350 °C.
These mineral oils have been misused as an additive in finished fuel, in particular diesel fuel, or have been directly used or sold for engine propulsion because the physical characteristics are very similar.
The entities handling monitored mineral oils in bulk or in packages exceeding 220 litres must register with the tax authority.
The personal conditions of the applicant, the statutory body and the responsible representative must be fulfilled for the issuing of the registration, which is valid for the whole period 2 With the exception of beer, fruit wines, other wines and mead and fruit spirits obtained by firing.
3 Council Regulation (EEC) No 2658/87 of 23 July 1987 on the tariff and statistical nomenclature and on the Common Customs Tariff.
4 For example, when mineral oil is used as fuel (except for navigation on waters if it is not a private pleasure craft) or as a component for the production of fuel if the marking is defective in its use.
registration.
As of 30 November 2016, the register of persons handling special mineral oils contained 54 valid registrations, four registrations were cancelled at the proposal of the holder of the registration.
The electronic register shall contain detailed information on receipt, own consumption and sale or transfer of mineral oil including document numbers, notification numbers of acquisition to the tax authorities, places of storage and consumption, purpose of consumption, place of storage and consumption or, on sale, place of delivery and customer registration number.
Notification of any acquisition of special mineral oil shall be made to the tax authorities between 24 and 72 hours before receipt.
The identification of trading partners, the name and nomenclature of the special mineral oil, quantity, purpose of consumption or information on sale or transfer shall be notified.
Notification of the anticipated quantity of mineral oil acquired, sold or consumed in the relevant year shall be submitted by the entity together with the registration application or by the end of January of the relevant calendar year.
Notifications of the purpose of use and marking, the place of storage or consumption, the identification details of the person to whom the specific mineral oil is resold or transferred shall be transmitted before each change.
Notifications shall be submitted electronically by means of smart forms or a data box in PDFa format.
In 2015, persons handling specific mineral oils submitted 630 notifications.
The seizure and confiscation of specific mineral oils or means of transport, as the case may be, must be declared by the tax administrator in cases where he finds the handling of specific mineral oils without registration or where the registered person fails to fulfil his reporting obligation.
As in the case of non-compliance with obligations in the transport of products subject to excise duty, these deficiencies cannot be remedied subsequently.
Registration of a fuel distributor is compulsory for persons who sell or are authorised to sell fuel.
Registered fuel distributors may only be persons meeting the following criteria:
Compulsory concession of the Trade Licensing Office (a specific form of trade licence).
An opinion on the application for a concession, or on the appointment of a responsible representative, is given by the Customs Office, which examines whether the applicant for a concession, the statutory body or members of the statutory body of the applicant – legal persons and the appointed responsible representative meet the condition of reliability.
If these persons meet the condition of reliability, the Customs Office issues an affirmative opinion.
A reliable person means a person of impeccable character from the point of view of criminal property, customs and tax law.
A condition for the issue of a concession is professional competence.
Debt-free status of the same group of persons as in the case of reliability.
A person who provides sufficient guarantees that he will fulfil his payment obligations to the State in a proper and timely manner, i.e. he has no arrears to the State budget and general health insurance, is a debtor.
A fuel distributor may not be prohibited by a court or an administrative authority from carrying out his activity.
A fuel distributor may not be in liquidation or bankruptcy.
Deposit (or bank guarantee) of CZK 20,000,000 (i.e. approx. €740,000), which may be reduced to CZK 10,000,000 (i.e. approx. €370,000) after three years of registration of the fuel distributor and fulfilment of other conditions.
The distributor is obliged to submit a notification of the fuel distribution to the customs office within 20 days after the end of the calendar month.
The electronic notification must contain data on the individual purchase and sale of fuel.
The notified data are data on business partners, document numbers, selected product, quantity, price, carrier and transport, place of loading and unloading.
The claim for refund of the tax on mineral oils consumed in primary agricultural production was reintroduced at the end of 2014.
Claims for refund of excise duty on mineral oils can only be made for activities that are obviously related to activities carried out on land.
In 2015, there were about 64,000 claims for refund of tax totalling CZK 1,172,844,680 (i.e. €43,401,720).
Since 2017, the government of the Czech Republic has also introduced refund of excise duty on fuel to farmers with livestock production.
Farmers or breeders who, for example, are engaged in cattle, pigs, poultry, sheep and goats will be newly able to claim this right.
Tobacco products
Restrictions on the sale of tobacco products with the old tax rate
In response to the long-term under-achievement of budgeted revenues from excise duty on tobacco products, the Czech Republic introduced restrictions on the sale of tobacco products with the old tax rate in case of change of the tax rate with effect from 1 December 2014.
Excise duty on tobacco products is paid by the use of tobacco stickers.
The use of a tobacco sticker means its placement on a unit packet (Section 116 of the Excise Tax Act).
For the application of the rate of excise duty, the decisive factor is the production of the tobacco product in the condition intended for the final consumer, without its removal from stock, delivery, dispatch or sale, or sale to the final consumer.
The letter of the alphabet characterizing the rate of excise duty is shown on the tobacco sticker together with the price for the final consumer of cigarettes, the sticker indicates the number of items in the packet, or the quantity of tobacco to be smoked in kilograms.
The tobacco sticker has no identifier.
The length of the transitional period for the sale of unit packets of cigarettes intended for direct consumption and bearing a tobacco sticker with the previous (old) rate of duty has been fixed until the end of the last day of the second calendar month after the new rate of excise duty took effect.
The evolution of the removal of tobacco stickers in 2014 and the comparison with the evolution in previous years show that tobacco manufacturers significantly stockpiled each year with tobacco products bearing the ‘old’ rate of duty, thus effectively shifting the effectiveness of the ‘new’ rate of duty by about one year.
Raw tobacco tax
Due to the misuse of raw tobacco for the manufacture of tobacco products without the permission of the tax authority and the non-payment of excise duty, a tax on raw tobacco and the monitoring of the handling of raw tobacco were introduced as measures against tax fraud.
With effect from 1 July 2015, raw tobacco which has not been used or supplied for the manufacture of tobacco products, supplied to another Member State or a third country, or for which the origin, purpose of use or the person to whom the raw tobacco has been or is to be supplied has not been proved, is subject to excise duty.
Restrictions on the handling of raw tobacco
Measures such as the supervision of the transport and manufacture of tobacco products, the marking of unit packets with surveillance tape and restrictions on sales at specified locations have been supplemented by restrictions on the handling of raw tobacco.
The manufacturing facilities for the processing of tobacco raw materials and the manufacture of tobacco products are not subject to customs supervision.
Only a registered person may store raw tobacco for a purpose other than the manufacture of tobacco products, but such tobacco may not be further processed or treated.
Only a person meeting the personal conditions of the applicant, the statutory body and the responsible representative may be a registered person, which applies throughout the registration period.
The conditions for registration are: (a) the right to operate a trade enabling the activity of the person storing the raw tobacco to be carried out, (b) reliability, (c) debt-free status, (d) the fact that the person storing the raw tobacco has not been prohibited from carrying out its activity, (e) the fact that the person storing the raw tobacco is not in liquidation or bankruptcy, (f) the provision of a security of 20 000 000 CZK (i.e. approx. 740 000 €).
The electronic register must include the date of receipt or issue of the raw tobacco, the document number, the identification of the business partner, the quantity and type of raw tobacco.
The notification of any acquisition of raw tobacco by the registered person storing the raw tobacco must be made to the tax administrator between 24 and 72 hours before receipt or dispatch.
The details of the business partner, the quantity of the raw tobacco, the storage address, the purpose of the use and the details of the carrier are reported.
Notification of the estimated quantity in the relevant year of receipt or dispatch of raw tobacco is submitted by the entity together with the application for registration or by the end of January of the relevant calendar year.
Notifications are submitted electronically through a data box in PDFa format.
The transport of raw tobacco must be accompanied by a document with the prescribed particulars.
Excise tax legislation in the Slovak Republic
The legal framework regulating the excise tax area in the Slovak Republic is based on EU legislation and thus co-creates its single tax system.
The individual types of excise tax are exhaustively determined by the legislation of the Slovak Republic, which is similar to the legislation of neighbouring countries.
Definition of legislation in the Slovak Republic
The legislative regulation of excise taxes is ensured by four laws according to the individual subject of tax.
Harmonisation has been achieved by the adoption of the following laws on excise duties: Act No 98/2004 Coll., on excise duty on mineral oils, Act No 106/2004 Coll., on excise duty on tobacco products, Act No 530/2011 Coll., on excise duty on alcoholic beverages, Act No 609/2007 Coll., on excise duty on electricity, coal and natural gas.
All laws on excise duties are substantive law regulations and deal with the taxation of the subject of excise duties in the tax territory.
Act No 563/2009 Coll., on administration of taxes (Tax Code), is a regulation of procedural law, regulating the administration of taxes, rights and obligations of tax subjects and other persons.
This legal framework transposed individual provisions of Council Directive 2008/118/EC of 16 December 2008, concerning the general regulation of excise duties and repealing Directive 92/12/EEC, and also transposed provisions of other European Community directives and legislation.
Structure of changes in legislation for individual types of excise duties in relation to the subject matter of control in the SR
Since 2011, legislation concerning the administration of excise duties has undergone several fundamental changes according to the structure of individual excise duties.
In the EMCS system, the monitoring of the transport of selected products subject to excise duties under the suspension regime has been changed from a paper accompanying administrative document to an exclusively electronic system, where these transports are monitored in real time.
Within the EMCS electronic system, the institute of suspension of access for tax subjects to EMCS was introduced in 2015.
THISsegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
The customs office has the possibility to suspend access precisely when there is a justified fear of unpaid or undetermined tax from previous tax periods and its unenforceability.
This concerns the tax due, since the transport of excise goods requires the composition of a security, which is released by the termination of the transport.
Excise duty on mineral oils
A fundamental change in the administration of excise duty on mineral oils occurred in 2011, when the option to use so-called red diesel was abolished.
The labelled gas oil, commonly also called red diesel, belonged to mineral oils.
In the past, red diesel was used for specific legally defined purposes, e.g. in agriculture, and its use was favoured by a lower rate of excise duty.
This change had a positive impact on the revenue part of the state budget.
The aim of abolishing red diesel was to reduce the public deficit, simplify the system of taxation of mineral oils and reduce the administrative burden on the businesses concerned.
In 2012, a new type of tax entity was created, namely the fuel seller.
The purpose of this legal change was to introduce the obligation to keep a register for all petrol stations.
The clarification of the movement of taxed petrol and diesel is linked to the obligation to buy petrol and diesel from the fuel distributor.
In 2014, new institutes of tax entities were introduced, namely a fuel distributor and a fuel consumer.
This change contributed to the elimination of tax evasion for petrol and diesel and made the movement of these fuels more transparent (see Annex 4, Diagram A).
As part of the fight against tax evasion, the legal provisions on the registration of tax entities trading in lubricating and base oils were extended.
However, in the Slovak Republic, these mineral oils are not subject to the obligation to label with an indicator substance.
Excise duty on tobacco products
As part of the fight against tax evasion and monitoring of tobacco raw materials, the scope of the Tobacco Raw Material Act was extended and a new tax entity – a trader of tobacco raw material – was introduced.
Tobacco raw material is not a harmonised tobacco product and its movement is not monitored within the EU.
Furthermore, the obligation to register technological equipment for the production of tobacco products was introduced.
The legislation introduced a new system for ordering, assessing, printing, distributing and using control marks intended for the labelling of consumer packages of tobacco products.
The control mark is used to identify cigarettes, cigars, cigarillos and tobacco.
Under the new system, the purchaser of control marks must apply to the customs office for the issue of control marks electronically, via the information system for the collection of control marks.
This step introduced electronic communication between the tax entity and the tax administrator.
One state printing house of control marks was established – in Mincovna Kremnice.
The exercise of tax supervision over the printing of control marks was also introduced.
The changes contributed significantly to the elimination of tax evasion.
The new system for printing control marks strengthens the system for the control of goods, as a unique identification number is generated on the control mark to easily verify whether the goods originate from legal sources.
A unique 12-digit identification number (1st-2nd place is the control sum; 3rd place determines whether the code belongs to the control stamp or to a group of packages; 4th place is the series identifier; 5th-8th place is the alphanumeric part of the sequence; 9th-12th place is the decimal part of the sequence) can also be applied in the form of a two-dimensional barcode.
The control stamp intended for labelling cigarettes must also indicate the price of the cigarettes, the character for the validity of the excise duty rate, the number of cigarettes in consumer packaging and the length of the cigarettes.
Excise duty on alcoholic beverages
Alcohol, wine and beer were affected by the biggest legislative change as the original three substantive laws were repealed and one common law on excise duty on alcoholic beverages was created.
The law was drafted mainly because of the need for a comprehensive solution of the taxation of alcoholic beverages, solution of their production, monitoring of movement, securing the tax, as well as the need to improve the business environment in the area, to streamline the administration of the tax, to reduce the administrative burden for small and medium-sized entrepreneurs.
A new way of dealing with the taxation of different types of alcoholic beverages introduced the use of a uniform rate of excise duty on an alcoholic beverage and took into account the volume percentage of the actual alcohol content.
For still wine, sparkling wine and fermented beverages, the volume percentage of the actual alcohol content of the final product is taken into account.
The concentration of beer is also expressed in the volume percentage of the actual alcohol content of the final product.
A category of small-scale producer of fermented beverages has been introduced, the essence of which is to exempt from excise duty a natural person who produces a sparkling fermented beverage for his own consumption and for the consumption of his household up to a maximum of 1 000 litres per marketing year.
The legislation has introduced a new system of ordering, assessing, printing, distribution and use of control stamps intended for the labelling of consumer packaging of alcohol.
Under the new system, the purchaser of control stamps must apply to the customs office for the issue of control stamps electronically by means of an information system for the collection of control stamps.
This step has introduced electronic communication between the tax entity and the tax administrator.
One state printer of control stamps has been established – in Mincovna Kremnice.
The exercise of tax supervision over the printing of control stamps has also been introduced.
The changes have significantly contributed to the elimination of tax evasion (see Annex 4, Diagram B) and the elimination of counterfeiting of control stamps.
The new system of printing control stamps strengthens the system of control of goods because a unique identification number is generated on the control stamp, which can be used to easily verify whether the goods come from legal sources.
The unique 12-digit identification number (1st-2nd place forms the control sum; 3rd place determines whether the code belongs to the control stamp or to a group of packages; 4th place is the series identifier; 5th-8th place is the alphanumeric part of the sequence; 9th-12th place is the decimal part of the sequence) can also be applied in the form of a two-dimensional bar code.
Comparison and evaluation
Comparison
Excise duties on alcohol, mineral oils, tobacco products, beer, wine and intermediate products are regulated in the Czech Republic by one common law no. 353/2003 Coll.
Tax on solid fuels, tax on natural gas and certain other gases and tax on electricity are part of the law no. 261/2007 Coll.
In the Slovak Republic, on the other hand, every excise duty is regulated by a special law, except the law on excise duty on alcoholic beverages, which contains the tax on alcohol, beer, wine and intermediate products.
A special law regulates excise duty on electricity, coal and natural gas.
In the Czech Republic, since 1 January 2015, the issuance of the permit to dispose of products subject to excise duty under the Excise Tax Act is subject, among other things, to proof of the economic stability of the applicants, which is verified by the customs authorities each year by carrying out a financial analysis.
In the Slovak Republic, a similar form of analysis is carried out only when deciding to waive or reduce the securing of the tax.
The FR SR carries out tax supervision in the form of the presence of an employee of the Financial Directorate over the handling of control stamps for marking alcohol and tobacco products, their disposal in the printing works and their sale to individual customers.
The law stipulates that the production of control stamps is ensured by the state enterprise Mincovna Kremnica.
The production of tobacco stickers and control strips in the Czech Republic is not supervised by customs authorities in the printer.
Tobacco stickers and control strips are taken over from the printer by the authorized territorial office of the customs office in Kutná Hora.
Tobacco stickers are taken over by their customers in this territorial office, control strips for marking alcohol are further distributed to individual locally competent tax administrators according to the place of marking.
The legislation of the Czech Republic does not define the manufacturers of tobacco stickers and control strips.
In the Slovak Republic there is an obligation to register technological equipment for the production of tobacco products or its part, in the Czech Republic there is no such obligation.
In the Czech Republic, the tobacco sticker bears the excise duty on tobacco products, which is paid when the tobacco stickers are collected at the authorized customs office.
In the Slovak Republic, on the other hand, the control mark does not contain the excise duty on tobacco products.
In the Czech Republic, a refund of excise duty on mineral oils in case of their use for agricultural plant primary production, so-called green diesel, was introduced during the audited period.
Since 2017, this refund has been extended to animal production.
In the Slovak Republic, such support for farmers is not introduced (it existed until 31 December 2010 as so-called red diesel).
In order to strengthen the fight against tax fraud, a deposit of 20 million CZK (i.e. 740 thousand €) was introduced for fuel distributors in the Czech Republic.
As a result of the introduction of this measure, the number of fuel distributors decreased from 1 891 subjects in 2013 to 174 in 2014 (i.e. a decrease of 1 717 tax subjects).
In the Slovak Republic, a similar institute of fuel distributor is introduced, but without the deposit required to secure the excise duty on mineral oils.
In the Slovak Republic, 303 distributors were registered in 2014 and in 2015, 407 distributors were registered.
In the Slovak Republic, an institute of a fuel seller and a fuel consumer is introduced, which is issued with a permit by the locally competent customs office.
In the Czech Republic, such an institute is not introduced.
In the Czech Republic, selected mineral oils and also some other mineral oils are subject to labelling, while in the Slovak Republic, following the abolition of the so-called red diesel, mineral oil labelling is not applied.
In the Czech Republic, the alcohol labelling control tape contains an eight-digit individual code used to verify the origin of the alcohol and a 12-digit registration code indicating the spirit quality of the spirit according to which the control tape is kept.
The destruction, loss and return of the control tape are recorded in the register on the following working day.
The tape holder is obliged to notify their use within the same period.
In the Slovak Republic, the control mark intended to mark the alcohol in consumer packaging contains a unique 12-digit identification number, which is communicated to the tax administrator once a month in case of its use, and serves to verify the authenticity of the control mark.
The register contains the number of control marks collected, used and claimed.
Both the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic have introduced the institute of compulsory registration or registration of the distributor of alcohol.
In the Slovak Republic, the registration is subject to the fulfilment of conditions related to, among other things, the storage area exceeding 200 m2; annual turnover from the sale of the consumer packaging of alcohol at least 100 000 € or the paid-up basic assets at least 100 000 €; a minimum number of 10 employees.
In the Czech Republic, obtaining the registration is subject, among other things, to the lodging of a deposit in the amount of 5 000 000 CZK (i.e. 185 000 €) in favour of the tax administrator for the whole period of validity of the registration.
THISsegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
In the Slovak Republic, the permanent presence of the tax administrator is required for the production of alcohol not only in consumer packaging.
In the Czech Republic, the production of alcohol in consumer packaging requires a special form of registration of the person obliged to mark alcohol, with the condition of a deposit in favour of the tax administrator ranging from CZK 100,000 (i.e. €3,700) up to CZK 5,000,000 (i.e. €185,000) depending on the amount of control tapes collected and the installation of a monitoring device with continuous access of the tax administrator.
Assessment
The legislation of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic goes far beyond the minimum EU requirements for the subject matter and administration of excise duties and responds to the identified risks from other Member States as well as to those identified in tax territories.
The legislative changes adopted during the audited period enable tax administrators to prevent possible tax evasion to a greater extent.
In the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic, in order to combat tax evasion in the form of misuse of tobacco raw materials (e.g. leaves), an excise duty on raw tobacco or tobacco raw materials was introduced in addition to the EU legislation.
Although raw tobacco and tobacco raw materials are not a harmonised tobacco product, the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic monitor their movements.
The SAO of the Czech Republic and the SAO of the Slovak Republic can recommend that this measure be applied also in other EU Member States.
In the Czech Republic, good practice has shown that the verification of economic stability of applicants for the issuance of a permit under the Excise Tax Act has been successful because it reduces the risks of tax arrears.
For this reason, both audit institutions recommend applying such verifications also in the Slovak Republic.
Distribution of control stamps is more efficient in the Slovak Republic than in the Czech Republic because it does not burden customs authorities with costs related to transport between the printer and the purchaser of control tapes and tobacco stickers.
The financial administration of the Slovak Republic has a better overview of the existence and location of technological facilities for the production of tobacco products.
In the Czech Republic, however, the collection of tax on tobacco products is more efficient because the actual order of a tobacco sticker is a tax declaration with subsequent payment of tax.
The financial administration in the Slovak Republic has a better overview of the places of sale of fuel thanks to the introduction of the institutes of “fuel seller” and “fuel consumer”.
The introduction of compulsory marking of mineral oils in the Czech Republic allows easier control of misuse of mineral oils with reduced tax rate or tax exempted.
In the Czech Republic (2013) and the Slovak Republic (2014) a new control tape or a stamp containing an identification code has been introduced.
The control tape in the Czech Republic also contains an identification code, while in the Slovak Republic the new legislation has abandoned its introduction.
The impacts cannot yet be evaluated due to the short effectiveness of the legislative changes.
The introduction of effective marking of consumer packaging of alcohol with a control mark or tape is an effective measure in the fight against tax evasion.
The SAO of the Slovak Republic and the SAO of the Czech Republic can recommend the introduction of this control measure in other Member States as well.
The attitude of the Slovak Republic to the conditions for the distribution of alcohol is characterized by a pro-ient approach, which does not block the funds of tax subjects.
On the other hand, the Czech Republic's approach is rather restrictive, as it introduces a deposit on the cash flow of tax entities, but reduces the risk of tax arrears.
Development of excise tax revenues
Excise tax is an indirect tax introduced by the state in order to increase the revenues of the state budget and also to regulate the amount of goods sold, the consumption of which is considered to be harmful to individuals and/or society (the tax's regulatory function).
According to the Commission's communication: EUROPE 2020 – A strategy for smart, sustainable and inclusive growth of 3 March 2010, within the framework of the flagship initiative "Resource-efficient Europe", the European Commission intends to improve the framework for the use of instruments on the basis of the market, including in the form of a revision of energy taxation with a focus on reducing energy and resource consumption.
In order to fulfil the EC's intention, Member States should try to shift the tax burden from labour to energy and environmental taxation, among other things, within the framework of a greater "greening" of tax systems.
The collection of excise tax revenues in the Czech Republic and Slovakia includes the collection of excise tax on mineral oils, tobacco products, alcohol, beer, wine and intermediate products, as well as natural gas, solid fuels and electricity.
The share of excise taxes in total tax revenues and the share in GDP is monitored by the Organisation for Economic Cooperation and Development (OECD), among others.
The two supreme audit institutions used the following selection criteria to enter a query on the OECD website.
Collection of excise taxes in relation to macroeconomic indicators in the Czech Republic
In the Czech Republic, the share of excise taxes in total tax revenues and the share in GDP decreased slightly, according to OECD data.
The ECB's rate of the European Central Bank was used to convert amounts in CZK into € on 31 December of the relevant year.
The nominal exchange rate of CZK against € in 2013 depreciated by 9.1% year-on-year compared to 2012 (from 25.140 to 27.425).
This was mainly due to the CNB Bank Board's monetary policy decision of 7 November 20136.
The resulting values of the collection of excise duties, rates of excise duties and income per capita in € decreased significantly due to the exchange rate difference.
The significant decrease in the share of excise duties in 2014 was caused by a one-off shortfall in excise tax revenues from tobacco products due to the impact of new legislation restricting the sale of tobacco products with the old tax rate.
The share of excise duties is also influenced by the increase in the collection of income taxes, which increased significantly due to the improved overall economic situation of the Czech Republic.
Excise duty on mineral oils accounts for the largest share of the total collection of excise duties (in 2015 about 55.7%), but it decreased despite the significant growth of the economy compared to 2012.
The collection of excise duty on mineral oils in 2013 and 2014 was significantly lower than in 2012 and 2015, even though the registration of fuel distributors was introduced in 2013 as a measure against tax fraud.
The trend of eco-efficient vehicles and the promotion of biofuels are negatively reflected in the tax revenue.
A negligible share is accounted for by the natural gas tax, the solid fuel tax and the electricity tax, which is due to the low tax rate, which is close to the minimum rates set by the EU, compared to neighbouring countries.
If there is no increase in rates, their share will decrease in the future in view of the ever decreasing energy intensity of buildings and production processes.
The collection of excise duty on alcohol in 2013 and 2014 was negatively affected by the repercussions of a large-scale case of tax fraud consisting in putting untaxed alcohol, alcohol containing methanol or underdenatured alcohol into circulation in the form of spirits.
In 2015, after the adoption of a number of measures against such behaviour and after the revival of the spirits market, the collection of excise duty on alcohol exceeded the collection of 2012 by €4 million.
The proportion of tax on tobacco products increased due to increasing rates.
The standard rates of excise duties changed between 2012 and 2015 for the tax on tobacco products, with an increase in the rate mainly due to compliance with Council Directive 2011/64/EU on the structure and rates of excise duty on tobacco products.
As a result of the CNB's monetary intervention, the real rate of excise duties in €, excluding the tax on tobacco products, fell significantly. It has risen only slightly for tobacco products.
In relation to price growth, GDP or the standard of living, there is no indexation of the rate of excise duties, so the function of excise duties to regulate socially problematic activities may not be fulfilled.
With economic growth in the Czech Republic and rising living standards, real rates of excise duties are decreasing.
7 Indexation – automatic adjustment of a certain economic quantity for inflation, this adjustment is made on the basis of a law or a contract (in the case of pensions paid by the state it is called indexation).
Collection of excise duties in relation to macroeconomic indicators in the Slovak Republic
In the current legislation on excise duties in the Slovak Republic, the indexation of the rates of excise duties to the development of consumer prices is not addressed, because they are fixed.
THISsegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
THISsegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
THISsegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
THISsegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
Of all excise duties introduced in Slovakia, excise duty on mineral oils has the largest share of the state budget's annual tax revenue, while its share did not fall below 52% in the whole audited period.
The second largest share is reported by excise duty on tobacco products.
This tax represents on average about 32% share of the total excise tax collection.
Between 2012 and 2015, the collection of excise duty per capita of the Slovak Republic increased.
This development is caused by the growth of excise duty rates on tobacco products, higher purchasing power and higher consumption of the population in a given year.
The increase in excise duty collection per capita of the Slovak Republic is constant and corresponds to the development of rates of excise duties on tobacco products, higher purchasing power and higher consumption of the population in a given year.
In the Czech Republic, the decrease in income in € per capita is influenced by the CNB's intervention regarding the exchange rate of the crown against the euro.
The difference between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic in total SPD collection is mainly due to the collection of excise duties on mineral oils and tobacco products, which in the Czech Republic are approximately 2.7 and 2.8 times higher, respectively, but per capita of the Czech Republic the collection on these selected products is only about 1/3 higher.
This is due to the lower price of these selected products in the Czech Republic due to lower rates of excise duties in the Czech Republic and the exchange rate of CZK against € for foreign consumers.
In the case of the mineral oil tax, it is also due to greater transit through the Czech Republic and cross-border purchases.
In the case of the tax on tobacco products, increasing foreign tourism to the Czech Republic and cross-border purchases have a non-negligible influence.
Evaluation Real rates of excise duties in the Czech Republic have been declining as a result of the CNB's interventions.
The share of energy taxes in the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic in total tax revenues is not rising and there is no shift from taxation of labour to taxation of consumption of selected products subject to excise duties, which is not in line with EU strategies.
However, the achieved values of the share of excise duties are consistently above the average of the OECD.
The overall collection of excise duties is influenced mainly by the change in excise duty rates, the development of the economic condition and the behaviour of the population.
Future shortfalls in the collection of excise duties due to environmental measures subsidised by the state in various forms will have to be replaced by other revenues or by a reduction in state expenditure.
The fact that the indexation of excise duty rates is not introduced in the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic reduces their regulatory function and is insufficiently supported by the EU's objectives of making Europe less dependent on environmentally unfriendly sources and reducing dependence on alcohol and tobacco.
The higher collection of excise duty per capita in the Czech Republic is reflected in higher consumption of selected products by foreign consumers, which is influenced by the lower total price of selected products in €.
Administrative expenditure of excise duties
The efficiency of administrative costs reflects the mutual relationship between expenditure and revenue related to the administration of excise duties, i.e. it expresses the amount of expenditure per 100 units of revenue (CZK, €).
The higher the resulting value, the worse the efficiency of administrative costs.
The efficiency of the tax administration influences the competence and organisational arrangement of the tax administration, the management of the organization, the legal environment and the level of computerisation of individual activities.
The determination of the efficiency of administrative costs of the tax administration by the conversion rate method is based on the number of employees involved in the administration of excise duties in a line-managed structure.
In the Czech Republic, the administration of excise duties is performed, among other activities, by the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic, which is a separate organisational unit of the state and an accounting unit.
In the Slovak Republic, the tax administration is provided by the Financial Administration of the Slovak Republic, while the customs administration bodies are an internal organisational unit, costs and revenues are included in aggregate for the whole organisational unit.
Therefore, with regard to the possibility to compare the efficiency of the administration of excise duties, expenses and revenues of the Financial Administration of the Czech Republic have been included in the calculation of the efficiency of administrative costs.
Administrative costs of the administration of excise duties in the Czech Republic
The administration of excise duties is a complex of administrative tasks performed mainly by the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic.
Some partial control tasks are performed by other public administration bodies, but their importance is negligible.
The administration of excise duties is performed mainly by the following departments:
General Directorate of Customs
Department 23 TAXATION
Department 231 – Tax methodologies monitors and proposes legislative measures, ensures the interpretation of legislation, methodically manages and coordinates: the execution of tax administration agendas and related regulations, in particular tax administration and related control and supervisory activities, the administration of transport of selected products;
Department 232 – ELO and Search performs search and methodically manages transport controls of selected products and ensures international cooperation of ELO and EMCS;
Department 233 – Tax Control methodically manages and coordinates the execution of tax inspection agendas at customs offices;
Department 30 LEGAL
Department 301 – Legal performs methodological activities in the areas of administrative punishment, administrative management, tax inspection process, registration procedure, discovery procedure, payment of taxes, fines for delayed tax claims, penalties and interest;
Division 302 – Administrative activities performs decision-making activities in cases where the legislation determines the competence of the DG, e.g. deciding on the delegation of the territorial jurisdiction of the subject to another competent tax administrator, deciding on the attraction, i.e. taking over the case by the superior tax administrator, appeals against decisions of the customs offices and examines the incentives for inaction in tax and administrative proceedings;
Division 303 – Revenue Administration and Recovery methodically manages, coordinates and performs the execution of tasks within the framework of international cooperation in the recovery of tax arrears and the execution of tasks in the area of insolvency proceedings;
Division 60 ANALYSIS AND INFORMATION SUPPORTS
Division 601 – Risk and Criminal Analyses provides and performs risk analyses and participates in the management of executive risks and planning of control activities and control actions;
Division 604 – Financial Analyses performs financial analysis in the customs administration, especially in the framework of the authorization procedure.
Customs offices carry out activities within the agenda in various places in the region and even agendas are dispersed in several places:
Department 02 – Analyses and Information Support, which performs risk analyses, management of risk profiles and collection and evaluation of information from all available information sources;
Department 1 LEGAL
Department 11 – Legal and Administrative Activities, which processes documents, opinions and submission reports for the Appellate Body, issues authorization decisions in connection with the administration of excise and environmental taxes, the Act on Compulsory Alcohol Labelling and the Act on Alcohol, decides in the matter of ensuring payment for a tax not yet due or not yet determined;
Department 3 – TAX
Department 31 – Tax, which performs the following tasks: tax supervision at tax entities, e.g. checking compliance with the conditions laid down in the issued authorizations, supervising the functionality and correctness of the production equipment for the production of alcohol and ascertaining the quantity and concentration of the alcohol produced, professional supervision at the denaturation of alcohol, physical checks in the area of administration of excise taxes; non-tax controls in the area of controls on the basis of laws indirectly related to excise taxes, in particular control of mandatory labelling and colouring of selected mineral oils, control of taxation of selected products, control of labelling of tobacco products, control of whether sellers or buyers violate the Act on Prices and other price regulations, performs acts in connection with the Act on Fuel, performs acts in connection with the Act on Compulsory Alcohol Labelling and the Act on Alcohol, performs acts in connection with compliance with the obligation of a minimum quantity of biofuels for free tax circulation for transport purposes; registration of economic entities for taxes, registration of persons obliged to label alcohol and distributors of alcohol and registration of distributors of fuel; tax administration, in particular conducting tax proceedings regarding the assessment and prescription or refund of tax, monitoring of securing tax and its use for payment of tax, conducting searches;
department 39 – Tobacco stickers and control strips – is the organisational unit of the Customs Office for the Central Bohemian Region and carries out activities in the area of ordering, production and distribution and disposal of tobacco stickers and control strips.
For the disposal of returned/damaged tobacco stickers, representatives of the Customs Office as well as representatives of the DG are present, who supervise the disposal process and draw up a record of the disposal.
For control strips for alcohol marking, the director of the Customs Office appoints a three-member committee for the disposal of discarded uncollected/returned control strips by shredding.
After the physical shredding of control strips has been carried out, the chairman of the liquidation committee ensures the recording of data on destroyed control strips;
department 5 – CONTROL,
department 52 – Tax controls carries out tax controls;
department 6 – SUPERVISION
department 61 – Supervision of entities carries out supervision of entities at points of sale, e.g. control of sales of spirits and tobacco products;
Unit 62 – Mobile Surveillance carries out traffic checks on selected products en route.
Administrative costs of excise administration in Slovakia
Since 1 January 2012, the Financial Directorate of the Slovak Republic has undergone a demanding transformation process in accordance with the approved UNITAS programme.
The creation of DG SR was also reflected in the staff composition of the newly created departments of the merged customs and tax administration.
In the context of the excise administration, the excise administration activities within the organisational structure of DG SR have been integrated into a larger number of different sections and related departments.
Financial Directorate of the Slovak Republic Customs and Tax Section DG SR Excise Tax Department (Slovak-wide competence):
excise duty department – directs and coordinates activities in the field of excise duty administration; draws up expert opinions; submits proposals and comments on legislative changes; issues decisions on the delegation of territorial jurisdiction to tax entities; assigns and cancels registration sampling numbers;
tax supervision department – directs and coordinates activities in the field of tax supervision and control; performs tax supervision;
ELO and SPD systems department – directs and coordinates mutual administrative cooperation activities in the field of excise duties, including the exchange of information through the SEED and ISA systems; ensures administration and updates in the SysNeD and EMCS application equipment;
inspection marks department – directs activities in the field of printing and handling of control marks; performs tax supervision over the loading and disposal of printing sheets and control marks in the printing works.
Department of the Vice-President of the Financial Administration
Department of Appeals for Excise Duties and Customs (Slovak-wide competence):
Department of Appeals for Excise Duties – reviews decisions of customs offices on the basis of applied ordinary and extraordinary appeals; appeal procedure at the second stage of the decision-making process.
The section of customs offices was created during 2012; it directly included individual customs offices (9 customs offices) which have territorial competence determined by higher territorial units, with the exception of one customs office which was established, inter alia, to carry out tasks related to the external border of the Community.
Customs offices:
Excise department – performance of methodological activities in relation to the branches of Customs Offices and Customs Offices stations; for selected entities performs the direct acts of the tax administrator, which decides on the registration (tax warehouse, authorised receiver, registered sender), the amount of the tax security, determines and refunds the tax, performs the tax supervision and tax control; decides on the waiving of the deposit of the tax security; decides on the waiving of the obligation to ensure the presence of a Customs Office employee in the alcohol tax warehouse;
Legal department – decision-making activities in relation to tax violations; activities related to ordinary and extraordinary remedies; tax execution proceedings;
Customs office branch – decides on the registration (except tax warehouse, authorised receiver for repeated receipt, registered sender), the amount of the tax security; prescribes and refunds the tax; performs the tax supervision and tax control; decides on the security and forfeiture of goods;
Customs office station – performs tax supervision over the holding and movement of goods subject to excise taxes; ensures the performance of permanent tax supervision in tax warehouse for alcohol; decides on security and on forfeiture of goods.
Expenditure of the financial administration of the Slovak Republic on administration of excise taxes is constantly increasing, as with the exception of wage growth investments for effective administration of taxes and computerisation of the financial administration are increasing.
Although revenue from excise taxes was increasing, expenditure due to IT adjustments related to the UNITAS project was growing faster.
Wage expenditure in the Slovak Republic is significantly influenced by the performance of permanent tax supervision in tax warehouses for alcohol, which the Czech Republic does not apply.
Expenditure of the Customs administration of excise taxes increased more significantly in 2015 between 2012 and 2015, this growth was caused mainly by growth of wage expenditure and expenditure on technical support.
In the Czech Republic, revenue from excise taxes also grew at approximately the same pace.
Wage expenditure in the Czech Republic is positively influenced by the broader competences of the customs administration, e.g. weighing of trucks, monitoring of compliance with obligations in connection with tolls.
The efficiency of administrative costs in the Slovak Republic shows a slightly worsening trend year-on-year.
