The number of employees did not change significantly, but expenditure per employee grew.
Also in the Czech Republic, the number of employees did not change significantly, but expenditure per employee grew more slowly compared to the Slovak Republic.
Evaluation
In the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic, a significant factor of the worsened efficiency of administrative expenditure is the growth of wages, which can be evaluated as a natural development.
In both countries, maintaining a significant administrative burden in the administration of excise taxes appears to be a negative factor, which is confirmed by the non-decreasing number of employees in the area of administration of excise taxes.
In the Slovak Republic, however, the administration of excise taxes with lower revenues is significantly more demanding in terms of personnel capacity.
Performance indicators of administration of excise taxes
The administration of excise taxes is a set of activities aimed at correctly finding, determining and securing the payment of the tax.
The main processes in the administration of excise taxes are the assessment of taxes, authorisation and registration for activities, supervision of transport, control and searching of tax entities.
The numbers of administrative acts and entities managed are indicators of the performance of the tax administrator.
The mutual relationship between the monitored indicator and the number of tax administrators expresses the effectiveness of the activity of the tax administrator and defines the cost of a specific activity.
Authorisation and registration for activities are the basic prerequisite for the handling of selected products for commercial purposes and their transport under the regime of conditional exemption from tax.
The tax administrator is obliged to perform systematic administration for entities with authorisation or registration with a focus on supervision of compliance with legal regulations and conditions set by the tax administrator, to which adequate staffing resources must be allocated.
The monitored indicator was the number of valid permits or registrations for the activity as of 31 December of each year.
The number of issued permits or registrations is not the same as the number of tax entities.
Administrative acts are specific administrative acts in a matter.
The monitored administrative acts are the frequency of the most important acts of the tax administrator (tax claims, transport administration in EMCS), or activities that are a sequence of acts ending with a report or a decision.
Performance indicators in the Czech Republic
Authorisation and registration for the activity in the Czech Republic
Tax warehouse:
Selected products can be produced, processed, stored, received or dispatched on the basis of the permission of the tax administrator to operate a tax warehouse.
If the tax warehouse operator has more than one warehouse, the permission for each is issued separately, including tax security.
Tax security is not required in the case of distilleries under the permanent tax supervision of the tax administrator (i.e. the physical presence of a public official and the securing of the facility by the conclusions of the tax administrator).
In the Czech Republic, the permanent tax supervision is not applied.
The tax warehouse operator is also registered for tax pursuant to Section 125 of Act No 280/2009 Coll.
The permit to operate a tax warehouse is a condition for the transport of selected products conditionally exempt from tax from the point of import to a tax warehouse, to an authorised consignee in another Member State, to the point of export in another Member State or to a consignee in another Member State (it replaces the status of a registered consignor pursuant to Article 4(10) of Council Directive 2008/118/EC).
Tax warehouse statistics do not include permits for the acquisition of electricity, natural gas and solid fuels without tax, which are analogous to tax warehouse permits.
The distiller produces ethyl alcohol with a reduced 50% tax rate (14 300 CZK/hl ethanol) – fruit distillates for growers. It is not a tax warehouse and the permit to operate is issued by the Ministry of Agriculture.
The reduced tax rate can be applied to 30 litres of pure alcohol per household of a grower destined for personal consumption for the production period (July-June).
The register of crop burning kept by the distiller's operators and made available to the tax authorities must contain data on the grower, the basic raw material, the distillate issued, the origin of the fruit and the production of the distillate.
The authorised recipient for repeated receipt of selected products and the authorised recipient for one-off receipt of selected products is entitled, under the tax authorities' permission and the conditions laid down, to receive or repeatedly receive selected products in a conditional system transported from another Member State.
The authorised recipient is not a tax warehouse operator and may not store or dispatch selected products under the conditional exemption regime.
The user of selected products exempt from tax is a legal or natural person who receives and uses, or under § 52a or § 53 of Act No 353/2003 Coll. sells to another user selected products exempt from tax; users have the status of tax subjects without the obligation to register for tax.
Selected products exempt from tax may be received and used only on the basis of a final authorization, and only from a supplier specified in the authorization.
On the basis of the authorization, exempt mineral oils may be sold to another holder of the authorization for use or to a user who is authorized to use mineral oils without authorization.
Mineral oils exempt from tax may be sold without authorization in cases stipulated by law, such as:
waste oils in quantities of less than 10,000 liters per calendar year if the user himself produced them or arose in the course of his activity;
selected mineral oils exempt from tax in unit packs with a capacity of not more than 20 liters intended for purposes other than engine propulsion or heat production, and at the same time intended for sale to the final consumer.
Selected products exempt from tax may be transported with proof of exemption.
The distributor of alcohol in consumer packs is authorized to sell or otherwise transfer alcohol released for free tax circulation after compulsory registration with the tax administration.
The storer of raw tobacco is entitled to store raw tobacco for a purpose other than the production of tobacco products, based on registration with the tax authority and the conditions laid down.
A person handling special mineral oils is entitled to acquire, sell or otherwise transfer special mineral oils that are in bulk or placed in packaging exceeding 220 litres, based on registration with the tax authority and the conditions laid down.
The fuel distributor is entitled to sell fuel in the Czech Republic, with the exception of the sale of fuel from a petrol station, based on the issued concession and registration with the tax authority under the conditions laid down.
Transport of fuel must be accompanied by a tax document, a proof of sale or a proof of transport, or by a distribution plan and bottling tickets.
These documents may be replaced by electronic documents sent to the tax authority before the transport begins.
The operator of the petrol station is the owner of the fuel sold at the petrol station.
Petrol stations are places where the sale or issue of fuel, usually in the fuel tank, is permitted on the basis of a permit from the building authority.
The Ministry of Industry and Trade records petrol stations and their operators in the following breakdown: registered – normal sale or issue of fuel, usually in the fuel tanks of vehicles; with a defined approach – operation usually in various company premises (e.g. quarries, sawmills, agricultural farms, transport organisations, construction yards), sales are made here for the other party limited on the basis of specific contractual relations; non-public – fuel dispensing points only for the operators' own consumption.
A petrol station is not a construction or installation in the form of an operational tank placed in operation (e.g. on a chassis) if the fuel is dispensed only for own use.
Operating tanks are not subject to a permit from the tax administrator and are not registered.
Natural and legal persons may purchase, receive and sell liquefied petroleum gases put into free tax circulation for resale on the basis of the permission of the tax administrator.
They must also have permission if they purchase or acquire liquefied petroleum gases for own consumption that exceeds 20 tonnes per calendar year.
Administrative acts in the Czech Republic
Tax control is a set of acts. The subject of tax control is tax obligations, statements of a tax entity or other circumstances relevant for the correct determination and determination of the tax related to one tax procedure.
Tax control may be carried out jointly for more than one tax procedure of a tax entity.
Repeated tax control may be carried out only under the conditions laid down by law and justified when the control is initiated.
The tax inspection is carried out within the time limit for determining the tax, which is three years, with the time limit being extended by one year under the conditions laid down by law (e.g. the filing of additional tax proceedings, the initiation of criminal proceedings in connection with the tax in question) or suspended (judicial proceedings, international cooperation).
The time limit for determining the tax expires at the latest ten years after the expiry of the time limit for filing a proper tax claim.
The tax administrator is not obliged to carry out a tax inspection for each tax entity.
The initiation of a tax inspection suspends the time limits for the possibility of filing an additional tax return or additional statement by the tax entity (Section 141 of Act No 280/2009 Coll.) and restarts the time limit for determining the tax (Section 148 of Act No 280/2009 Coll.).
Based on its result, an ex officio assessment of the tax can be made.
A local investigation is an individual time-limited act (one day) during which the tax administrator searches for evidence and carries out an inspection of premises, goods, documents, records, means of transport and transport packaging at tax entities and other persons involved in the tax administration, on the spot outside the tax administrator's premises (e.g. at the tax entity, at a sales point, on the way during transport).
The tax administrator is entitled to borrow documents and items, take samples, or secure them.
Based on the result of a local investigation, the tax cannot be separately assessed, but the tax entity may be invited to file an additional tax return (Section 145(2) of Act No 280/2009 Coll.).
The inspection of traffic data in the EMCS system is not a local investigation.
The order of control tapes for alcohol marking may be submitted to the tax administrator to the locally appropriate place of marking only by a registered person obliged to mark alcohol and is carried out through intelligent forms that are automatically imported into the application of the register of alcohol signers.
The tax administrator processes the order, evaluates the adequacy of the ordered quantity of control strips and orders the production.
He does not supervise the production of control strips.
The production is provided by the State Printing House, a state enterprise.
The customer of control strips receives control strips from the tax administrator of the locally appropriate place of labeling.
The order for tobacco stickers for the labelling of cigarettes, cigarillos, cigars and smoking tobacco fulfils the function of a tax return.
The value of the tobacco stickers corresponds to the amount of the tax liability, while the purchaser of the tobacco stickers is obliged to pay their value within 60 days from the date of their withdrawal from the tax administrator.
The purchaser is obliged to calculate in the order himself the value corresponding to the amount of the tax liability of the tobacco stickers ordered.
This period applies only if the value of the tobacco stickers is ensured.
The order for tobacco stickers is submitted on a form specified by the Ministry of Finance in writing or through a data box with the possibility of using smart forms.
The production of tobacco stickers is ensured by the State Printing House of Valuables, a state enterprise.
The authorized tax administrator, which is the Customs Office for the Central Bohemian Region (territorial workplace Kutná Hora), ensures the purchase and transport of tobacco stickers to the tax administrator, who distributes them and further checks their transport, storage and use at the purchasers.
Tax claims include proper tax returns, additional and corrective tax returns, including orders for tobacco stickers, filed by tax entities.
Tax returns in the framework of customs proceedings based on customs declarations and claims for refund of tax on: mineral oils used for heat production, other gasolines used in the course of business activities other than for heat production or engine propulsion, mineral oils used for agricultural primary production are not included.
The fines imposed include administrative proceedings to deal with established violations of legislation, involving a set of consecutive administrative actions. The international exchange of information on tax entities (ELO) within the meaning of Council Regulation (EU) No 389/2012 takes place in the form of: a request for administrative cooperation, a response to a request for administrative cooperation, spontaneous information, an event report, an inspection report.
Transport under the conditional tax exemption regime between the Czech Republic and the EU Member States – the Czech customs office is the tax administrator of the receiving or sending tax warehouse or authorised recipient.
Performance indicators in the Slovak Republic
Authorisation and registration to operate in the Slovak Republic
The administration of excise taxes in the Slovak Republic is mainly ensured by the customs offices and the excise tax department of the Customs and Tax Division of the Slovak Republic, whose procedure for the administration of excise taxes is regulated by the individual laws on excise taxes and the Tax Code.
These laws stipulate not only the scope of authorisation for the CA and the Slovak Tax Administration in the administration of excise taxes, but also the rights and obligations of tax subjects in connection with the registration or payment of excise tax.
The largest year-on-year increase of tax subjects (by 234%) was recorded in 2012 and 2013, which was caused by an increase in issued permits within tax warehouses, an increase in registrations of authorised recipients for repeated receipt and registration of a large number of user enterprises.
The legislation clarified the transport of certain bulk mineral oils, as well as the obligation to notify if they are transported in bulk or in packaging with a capacity of more than 150 litres and 230 litres respectively, and also extended the list of mineral oils subject to inspection and the procedure during transport to other goods, e.g. anti-knock preparations, oxidation inhibitors, bitumen inhibitors, viscosity enhancement preparations, anti-corrosion preparations.
A mandatory indication of the kinematic viscosity of lubricating oils has been introduced.
An approximation of the registration process with selected tax entities in the sense of national legislation in the Slovak Republic is given in the following parts of the document.
Tax warehouse operator
Under the national legislation of the Slovak Republic, when registering a tax warehouse operator in all objects of excise duties, a person who wishes to operate a tax warehouse must simultaneously apply for registration and issue of a permit to operate a tax warehouse.
The resulting decision in the registration process is the certificate of registration for the relevant excise duty, by which the tax warehouse operator acquires legal personality for all tax warehouses.
At the same time, the CA issues a tax warehouse operating permit which entitles the tax warehouse operator to produce, process, store, receive or dispatch selected products under the duty suspension arrangement.
In the event that the tax warehouse operator has tax warehouses in more than one location, the tax administrator issues a separate tax warehouse operating permit for each tax warehouse.
The movement of excise goods under suspension of duty is monitored electronically through the EMCS.
A unique reference code is generated for each shipment, the so-called
The ARC code under which the traffic can be monitored online and therefore in real time.
If the tax warehouse operator is also the person authorised to distribute the spirit, he shall notify electronically to the CA the commercial name of the consumer packaging of the spirit, the volume and volume concentration of the spirit in the consumer packaging of the spirit and the EAN barcode for each new type of consumer packaging which he puts into free circulation, at the latest on the date of its release.
Registered Sender
A registered consignor is a special type of tax entity which cannot be simultaneously registered also as a tax warehouse operator, even if he sends the excise object under the duty suspension regime after its release for free circulation.
Under the national legislation of the Slovak Republic, when registering a registered consignor under all excise objects, a person who wishes to send the excise object under the duty suspension regime after its release for the customs “free circulation” regime must simultaneously apply to the CA to register and issue an authorisation to send the excise object under this regime.
The CA issues a certificate of registration for the relevant excise duty and also an authorisation to send the excise object under the duty suspension regime after its release for the customs “free circulation” regime.
Grower's distillery
The basic act for the operation of a grower's distillery is to obtain an authorisation for the production of alcohol in a distillery plant from the Ministry of Agriculture and Rural Development of the Slovak Republic.
However, the authorisation itself from the Ministry does not authorise the holder of the authorisation to operate a grower's distillery.
In order to operate a grower's distillery, a person must submit an application to the CA for registration and issue of a certificate of registration of the operator of the grower's distillery.
The CA issues a certificate of registration for the relevant excise duty, which at the same time authorises the operator of the grower's distillery to produce alcohol in a grower's distillery.
The purpose of a grower's distillery is to provide services to growers.
A grower's distillery cannot be a tax warehouse.
The legislature allows a reduced rate of tax to be applied to alcohol produced in a grower's distillery at a rate of 50% of the basic rate of tax, i.e. 540 €/hl a.
The reduced rate of tax applies to alcohol produced in the distillery, at a rate of no more than 43 l a. per grower and his household per production period in the tax territory.
The production period runs from 1 July of the current year to 30 June of the following year.
The production period is not the same as the calendar year, and therefore a reduced rate of tax may be applied to the alcohol produced more than once in the same calendar year, as the alcohol in question is produced in two production periods.
This is the production of alcohol outside the suspensive regime, which in practice means that the alcohol produced is in free tax circulation.
The grower pays not only the excise duty and value added tax but also the price of the services provided to the distillery for the alcohol produced.
The distillery issues the grower with an exit certificate, which serves not only as proof of proof of the origin and method of acquisition of the alcohol, but also of payment of the excise duty.
The transport of the alcohol thus produced is not subject to monitoring by the tax authorities.
Consumer packet importer
National legislation allows persons intending to import, in the course of their business, consumer packets of alcohol or cigarettes from the territory of a third country and to place them in free tax circulation in the tax territory to apply to the CA for inclusion in the register of importers of consumer packets.
The importer of consumer packets does not register for the excise duty in question, but the CA issues him a certificate of inclusion in the register of importers of consumer packets.
This certificate entitles the importer to import consumer packets of alcohol or consumer packets of cigarettes from the territory of a third country.
At the same time, he must lodge a tax security for the amount of tax on the quantity of alcohol or cigarettes he wishes to place in free tax circulation before the issue of the control stamps.
The importer of consumer packets must put into free tax circulation only consumer packets marked with a control stamp.
For this reason, he must present to the customs office of export the number and identification number of the control stamps exported to the territory of a third country.
On importation, the importer is obliged to have the customs office of importation confirm the number of control marks imported back from the territory of the third country.
On importation of the consumer packaging, the importer proceeds in the sense of the customs regulations, where the amount of excise duty is also part of the customs debt.
In the case of release of the consumer packaging into free tax circulation, the tax security lodged is returned to the importer or can be used to pay the customs debt.
The importer of the consumer packaging is not a tax warehouse.
If the importer of the consumer packaging of alcohol is also the person authorised to distribute the alcohol, he is obliged to notify electronically to the CA the commercial name of the consumer packaging of the alcohol, the volume and volume concentration of the alcohol in the consumer packaging of the alcohol and the EAN bar code for each new type of consumer packaging which he puts into free tax circulation, at the latest on the day of its introduction.
Seller of the consumer packaging of the alcohol in free tax circulation
In order to monitor the movement of the alcohol in free tax circulation and to eliminate tax evasion, the legislator has introduced a new tax institute of the seller of the consumer packaging of the alcohol.
A person wishing to hold a permit for sale must apply to the CA for a permit and fulfil the legal conditions (trade licence for a commercial activity; integrity in relation to intentional economic offences; he/she has not had his/her permit for sale withdrawn for a period of ten years; he/she is not in liquidation or bankruptcy).
As it is a consumer packaging of the alcohol in free tax circulation, an accompanying document is not required for the transport of these goods.
For example, an invoice, which also contains the number of the holder of the distribution licence, is sufficient to prove how the consumer packaging of the alcohol was acquired.
The holder of the authorisation is required to keep a record for each establishment in respect of the calendar month of the number of units of consumer packaging of alcohol received, the number of units of consumer packaging of alcohol issued, the stock of alcohol in consumer packaging of alcohol as at the last day of the month and a record of shortages or surpluses in the number of units of consumer packaging of alcohol received and issued.
The holder of the authorisation is obliged to purchase the alcohol in consumer packaging or otherwise take it in the course of business only from the person authorised to distribute.
Distributor of consumer packaging of alcohol
In order to monitor the movement of alcohol in free tax circulation and to eliminate tax evasion, the legislator has introduced a new tax institute, the distributor of consumer packaging of alcohol.
A person wishing to hold a distribution authorisation must apply to the CA for a distribution authorisation.
The applicant must comply with the legal conditions (trade licence for a commercial trade; storage area exceeding 200 m2; annual turnover from the sale of consumer packaging of alcohol of at least €100,000 or paid-up capital of at least €100,000; minimum number of 10 employees; no arrears to the customs office; no arrears of compulsory levies; integrity in relation to intentional economic offences; no authorisation to sell has been withdrawn for 10 years; he is not in liquidation or bankruptcy).
As this is a consumer packaging of alcohol in free tax circulation, no accompanying document is required for the transport of these goods.
For example, an invoice, which also contains the number of the holder of the distribution licence, is sufficient to prove how the consumer packaging of alcohol was acquired.
The holder of the distribution authorisation is obliged to keep a record for each establishment for the calendar month of the number of units of consumer packaging of ethyl alcohol received, the number of units of consumer packaging of ethyl alcohol issued, the stock of ethyl alcohol in consumer packaging on the last day of the month and a record of shortages or surpluses in the number of consumer packaging of ethyl alcohol received and issued.
The holder of the distribution authorisation is obliged to purchase ethyl alcohol in consumer packaging only from another person authorised to distribute.
The person authorised to distribute notifies the data for each calendar month electronically by the 25th day of the following calendar month.
Fuel seller
In order to monitor fuel in free tax circulation as well as to eliminate tax evasion, a new type of tax entity, namely the fuel seller, has been introduced.
There is no specific regulation regulating petrol stations in the territory of the Slovak Republic.
Therefore, petrol stations are incorporated as fuel sellers in the national legislation of the Slovak Republic.
A person who wants to sell petrol, diesel or LPG for final consumption in free tax circulation in the tax territory is obliged to ask the CA for a permit for the sale before the sale begins and to submit a document proving that the storage facility is verified and equipped with a suitable verified measuring device enabling the quantity of mineral oil to be measured on receipt and dispensing, and the tank must comply with technical standards.
If the fuel seller is a tax warehouse operator, authorised consignee or registered consignor, the CA will also automatically issue a permit for the sale of fuel to registered persons.
The fuel seller is obliged, among other legal obligations, to keep a record of petrol, diesel or LPG bought and sold in a calendar month and is also obliged to notify the CA of a new supplier (distributor) of fuel.
The fuel seller is legally obliged to purchase or otherwise purchase fuel only from the fuel distributor or from a registered person.
As the fuel is in free tax circulation, no accompanying document is required for the transport of the goods.
However, when the fuel is delivered by car tanker, the distributor prints a so-called bottler from a measuring device built into the car tanker when the fuel is pumped to the seller.
In addition to the quantity data, the document also contains the date and time of delivery and the registration number of the car assigned by the Transport Inspectorate.
For example, an invoice is sufficient to prove the method of acquisition of the fuel, which also contains the number of the fuel distributor assigned by the Tax Inspectorate.
The Tax Inspector in the territory of the Slovak Republic records tax evasion related to the transport of this type of goods when exercising tax supervision over mineral oils.
In particular, it is an effort to avoid roadside checks during transport, so hauliers use secondary road roads, bypassing the toll collection system due to the more difficult monitoring of actual transports.
Also, transports of mineral oils are carried out in converted double-bottomed tankers.
Many times, illegal transports are accompanied by a vehicle which reports to the haulier possible mobile patrols in order to change the route and avoid roadside checks.
Also, fuel is mixed with light fuel oils or waste oils.
Fuel distributor
In order to monitor fuel in free tax circulation as well as to eliminate tax evasion, a new type of tax entity has been introduced, namely the fuel distributor.
A person who intends to distribute petrol, diesel or LPG in free circulation in the tax territory as part of a business is required to apply to the customs office for a distribution permit before the distribution begins and to produce a document proving that the storage facility is verified and equipped with a suitable verified measuring device, as well as a list of suppliers and customers.
The fuel distributor is required, among other legal obligations, to keep a record of petrol, diesel or LPG purchased and sold for a calendar month separately for each establishment.
The fuel distributor is legally obliged to purchase or otherwise purchase fuel only from the fuel distributor or from a registered person.
The fuel distributor may sell in the tax territory only to the fuel distributor, a registered person or a fuel consumer.
However, when the fuel is delivered by car tanker, the distributor prints out a so-called bottler from the measuring device installed in the car tanker when the fuel is pumped to the fuel seller or the fuel consumer.
In addition to the data relating to the quantity, the said document also contains the date and time of delivery and the vehicle registration number assigned by the transport inspectorate.
As the fuel is in free tax circulation, no accompanying document is required when transporting the goods.
For example, an invoice is sufficient to prove the method of acquisition of the fuel, which also contains the number of the fuel distributor or the registered person assigned by the tax administrator.
Fuel consumer
The fuel consumer has a special position in national legislation.
A person who purchases petrol, diesel or LPG in free tax circulation for his own consumption in the tax territory and stores this mineral oil in a storage facility with a capacity of 15 000 litres or more is obliged to notify the customs office no later than before the first placing in the storage facility.
The fuel consumer is recorded by the customs office.
The customs office is obliged, in addition to the legal facts, to indicate the location of the storage facility.
In practice, these are large transport companies, cooperatives, bus companies, road construction companies and other entities.
The storage facility must be verified and equipped with a measuring device enabling the quantity of fuel to be measured at reception and delivery (gauge, measuring rod).
The tank must comply with technical standards.
The fuel consumer must purchase fuel only from the fuel distributor or from a registered person.
As the fuel is in free tax circulation, no accompanying document is required for the transport.
However, when the fuel is delivered by car tanker, the distributor prints out a so-called bottling device from the measuring device incorporated in the car tanker when the fuel is pumped to the consumer.
The said document contains, in addition to the data concerning the quantity, the date and time of delivery and the registration number of the car allocated by the Transport Inspectorate.
For example, an invoice is sufficient to prove the method of acquisition of the fuel, which also contains the number of the fuel distributor allocated by the Tax Inspectorate.
The Tax Inspectorate in the territory of the Slovak Republic, when exercising tax supervision over mineral oils, records tax evasion related to the transport of this type of goods.
Small independent brewery
The operator of a small independent brewery is a person who, in the course of his business, produces beer and fulfils the legal conditions.
Provided that the legal conditions are fulfilled, a small independent brewery can apply a reduced tax rate, i.e. 2,652 € per hl/percent of the volume of the actual alcohol content.
The annual production of beer is limited to a quantity of up to 200 000 hl of beer.
As it is a production of beer outside the conditional exemption regime, the transport does not require an accompanying document as it is in free tax circulation.
A small independent brewery cannot be a tax warehouse.
In practice, it is a small family business which also operates restaurants or saloons in which they offer their own production of beer for sale.
Administrative operations in the Slovak Republic
This sub-chapter approximates the exercise of tax supervision of the administration of excise duties for selected tax entities within the meaning of national legislation in the Slovak Republic.
The largest year-on-year increase in administrative operations (5,3 %) was recorded between 2012 and 2013, which was caused by the realisation of more transport operations in the EMCS system.
By contrast, the largest decrease was recorded year-on-year in 2014, by up to 4.3%, which was due to a smaller number of completed tax inspections and fewer tax returns submitted.
This decrease related to legislative changes.
Tax inspections
Through the performance of the tax inspection, the CA detects or verifies facts decisive for the correct determination of the tax.
In the performance of the tax inspection, the employees of the CA are shown a mandate to perform the tax inspection, which includes, among other things, the purpose and subject of the inspection and the extent of the audited tax periods.
In practice, this means that the audited tax period can be one month, but also more tax periods.
The extent of the audited tax periods is determined by the CA.
The tax inspection starts with the writing of the report on the commencement of the tax inspection.
The receipt of documents is confirmed by the CA.
The borrowed documents are required to be returned by the CA within 30 days of the completion of the tax inspection.
The CA employee draws up a report from the tax inspection.
If the tax audit reveals a difference in the total that the audited tax entity should have paid, reported or claimed a tax refund for, the CA, together with the report, also sends the audited tax entity an invitation to comment on the findings in the report.
The tax audit is completed on the date of receipt of the report.
The deadline for carrying out the tax audit is a maximum of one year from the date of its commencement.
The tax audit of registered persons and selected registered persons is carried out as necessary, but at least once before the date of the expiry of the right to determine the tax, which is 5 years.
The FR SR issued an internal management act which modified the above mentioned deadlines due to the uniform procedure of the tax administrator in the territory of the SR.
Local investigation
Local investigation is the activity of the tax administrator, in which it searches for evidence, examines and ascertains facts that are needed for the purposes of the tax administration.
The CA employee draws up a report on the local investigation and submits a copy thereof to the tax entity.
In carrying out the local investigation, the employee of the CA has the right to unlimited access to the land, to the operational buildings, to the rooms and to places including means of transport, transport packaging and to accounting documents.
The accounting of the quantity of alcohol produced is ascertained in the form of a local investigation.
The ascertained facts are the basis for carrying out the tax inspection.
Also in carrying out the local investigation, the CA is entitled to take samples as well as to secure the matter.
FŘ SR issued an internal management act, which regulated the carrying out of the tax supervision and local investigation for individual objects of excise taxes in order to unify the procedures of the tax administrator.
Permanent tax supervision in tax warehouses for alcohol
With the accession of the Slovak Republic to the European Union on 1.5.2004, a change also occurred in the area of excise tax administration.
The need for more efficient spending of state budget funds in the administration of excise duty on alcohol, improvement of the business environment in the given area and introduction of legislative instruments for more effective suppression of the grey economy in the given area resulted in the adoption of new laws in 2004 in connection with the administration of excise taxes.
One of the measures brought about by the new legislative change was not only the transfer of the tax administration in the area of excise tax administration from tax offices to customs offices, but also the introduction of the need for the tax administration to be present in the tax warehouse for alcohol.
In the territory of the Slovak Republic, national legislation defines exhaustively that it is only possible to receive, issue, produce or process alcohol in the tax warehouse in the presence of an employee of the CA.
This does not apply to the tax warehouse that receives, stores or dispatches alcohol only in consumer packaging of alcohol.
At the same time, the CA is obliged to secure employees in the tax warehouse in order not to limit the receipt, issue, production or processing of alcohol.
The tax warehouse operator is obliged to safeguard the working environment conditions for the employees of the CA.
On the basis of a contract concluded with the FD SR for the premises provided, the CA pays the tax warehouse operator monthly for the rental costs.
In a tax warehouse during the production, processing or storage of the alcohol, the production facility for storing the alcohol must be adapted so that the quantity of alcohol produced, processed alcohol, stored alcohol including the stocks of the alcohol and the alcohol contained therein can be ascertained at any time.
THISintentionallyLEFTblank
If the alcohol in the tax warehouse is not accepted, issued, produced or processed, the customs office may waive the obligation to secure the presence of the customs office employee, while it is obliged to secure this area by sealing the customs office.
In practice, however, this possibility is too often not used, as tax warehouse operators use the continuous presence of the customs office employee for their benefit.
Some tax warehouse operators use a legal option within the meaning of Act No 467/2002 Coll., on the production and marketing of ethyl alcohol, and use the production equipment for the production of ethyl alcohol in a distillery for cultivation burning and also for the purposes of a distillery for distillates, which must be a tax warehouse.
Around 250 customs officers ensure the exercise of permanent tax supervision in tax warehouses for ethyl alcohol.
Issuing vouchers for the collection of control stamps for ethyl alcohol
The basic act for the collection of control stamps is to send an application to the customs office for the allocation of a registration sampling number and to issue a voucher for the collection of control stamps for ethyl alcohol.
An alcoholic beverage, which is ethyl alcohol, means goods of the Combined Nomenclature 2207 and 2208 with an actual alcoholic strength exceeding 1,2 % vol.
The control mark is intended for the labelling of the consumer packaging of ethyl alcohol.
Consumer packaging of ethyl alcohol is considered to be a closed consumer packaging filled with ethyl alcohol intended for direct human consumption.
Consumer packaging falling within Combined Nomenclature codes 2207 and 2208 may be put into free tax circulation in the tax territory only if it is marked with a control mark.
Only the tax warehouse operator, the authorised consignee and the importer of the immediate packaging may mark the immediate packaging of ethyl alcohol with a control mark and place it in free tax circulation.
The control mark contains, among other things, an identification number consisting of a 14-digit numerical digit. The identification number contains the registration withdrawal number (1st-6th digit), the volume of ethyl alcohol (7th-11th digit) and the volume concentration of ethyl alcohol in the immediate packaging (12th-14th digit).
Original model of the control mark for ethyl alcohol:
The registration withdrawal number is assigned separately by the CA to each purchaser of the control mark.
Only the control mark whose identification number corresponds to the volume of the consumer packaging, the volume concentration of ethyl alcohol in consumer packaging and the purchaser's control mark may be used to indicate the consumer packaging of ethyl alcohol.
National legislation introduced a new information system for control marks towards the end of 2014.
The new information system for control marks aimed at simplifying and computerising the system for ordering, assessing, printing, distributing and using control marks intended for the labelling of consumer packaging of ethyl alcohol.
Only the tax warehouse operator, the authorised consignee, the importer of consumer packaging and the consignee (purchaser) of ethyl alcohol may mark the consumer packaging of ethyl alcohol.
The purchaser of control marks who wishes to take control marks under the "new system" must apply to the customs office for the issue of control marks electronically.
Through the electronic system, the buyer of control marks is obliged to apply for their issue, to notify the data resulting from the national legislation of the Slovak Republic and to keep a register of control marks.
The number of ordered pieces of control marks must not be less than 500 pieces or their multiple.
The tax administrator also communicates with buyers of control marks through the electronic system of control marks, especially when notifying the number of control marks that the buyer of control marks can take away or when determining the date of receipt of control marks by the buyer of control marks at the printing works.
The buyer of control marks is obliged to deposit on the tax administrator's account the funds corresponding to the price of control marks that he can take away and the quantity of which is notified by the customs office.
The price of the control mark takes into account the amount of refunds to the printing works. However, it does not take into account the amount of excise duty.
The control marks are authorised to be printed by the state enterprise Mincovna Kremnice.
The FR SR carries out tax supervision over the handling of the control stamps and their disposal at the printer.
The FR SR is obliged to ensure the presence of an employee of the financial directorate at the printer when handling the control stamps.
The FR SR ensures the sale of the control stamps to the purchaser of the control stamps at the printer.
The withdrawal of control stamps is possible only at the printer from an employee of the financial directorate.
Issuing of vouchers for the collection of control stamps for tobacco products
The purchaser of the control stamp must ask the CA to assign a registration collection number and issue a voucher for the collection of the control stamp.
Consumer packs of cigarettes can only be put into free tax circulation if they are marked with a control stamp.
It is only possible to mark consumer packs of cigarettes with a control stamp in a company that produces cigarettes.
The purchaser of control marks can only be a tax warehouse operator, an authorised consignee or an importer of tobacco products who wants to put tobacco products into free tax circulation in the tax territory.
Only a control mark can be used to mark a consumer pack of cigarettes, the data of which correspond to the relevant price of cigarettes, the number of cigarettes in the pack, the length of cigarettes, the tax rate validity sign and the registration withdrawal number.
A consumer pack of cigarettes can only be sold for final consumption at the price indicated on the control mark.
National legislation introduced a new information system for control marks at the end of 2014.
The aim of the new information system for control marks was to simplify and computerise the system for ordering, assessing, printing, distributing and using control marks intended for the marking of consumer packs of tobacco, cigars, cigarillos and cigarettes.
A purchaser of control stamps who wants to take control stamps under the "new system" must apply to the customs office for the issue of control stamps electronically.
Through the electronic system, the purchaser of control stamps is obliged to apply for their issuance, to notify data resulting from the national legislation of the Slovak Republic and to keep a register of control stamps.
Control stamps are authorised to be printed by the state enterprise Mincovna Kremnice.
The FR SR carries out tax supervision over the handling of control stamps and their disposal at the printing works.
The FR SR is obliged to ensure the presence of an employee of the financial directorate at the printing works when handling control stamps.
The FR SR ensures the sale of control stamps to a purchaser of control stamps at the printing works.
Control stamps can only be taken at the printing works from an employee of the financial directorate.
The operator of a tax warehouse or an importer of tobacco products may mark consumer packages of tobacco or cigarillos with a control stamp.
The operator of the tax warehouse, the importer of tobacco products or an authorised consignee may mark consumer tobacco packaging or cigarillos with a control mark.
Only the control mark, the data of which correspond to the character for the validity of the rate of excise duty, shall be used to mark consumer tobacco packaging with a control mark.
Only in the company that produced them may mark consumer cigarette packaging with a control mark.
The number of ordered pieces of control stamps may not be less than 500 pieces or their multiple.
The CA shall electronically notify the purchaser of control stamps within three working days at the latest of the number of control stamps which it can withdraw, the price of control stamps and the account number of the FR SR.
The CA may reduce the number of ordered pieces of control stamps if circumstances have arisen on the basis of which it is reasonable to assume that a violation of tax regulations may occur.
The FR SR shall determine the date of receipt of control stamps by the purchaser of control stamps, but not later than 10 days.
The date of receipt of control stamps is announced by the FD SR via the electronic system of control stamps to the purchaser of control stamps.
Control stamps are issued by the Financial Directorate exclusively at the printing works, but only after the receipt of the funds corresponding to their price to the respective account indicated in the electronic notification of the Customs Office.
The purchaser of control stamps is obliged to keep the registration of control stamps separately in the electronic system of control stamps for cigarettes, cigars, cigarillos and tobacco.
Administrative cooperation between EU Member States (ELO)
Pursuant to Council Regulation (EU) No 389/2012, the Department of ELO and SPD systems of the Excise Tax Department of the FD SR is responsible for ensuring the exchange of information on the basis of a request for administrative cooperation between EU Member States and the competent financial administration authorities.
These include, in particular, requests for verification of entities within the excise tax administration, requests for information concerning the excise tax administration and also requests for confirmation of information from the SEED database.
The exchange of requests takes place in electronic form within the EMCS system.
The following acts are included in the administrative cooperation between EU Member States: requests for administrative cooperation (request for verification, request for information on the excise tax administration, request for confirmation of registration in the SEED); response to a request for administrative cooperation; spontaneous information; event report; inspection report.
Comparison and evaluation
Comparison
Permission and registration
In the SR, tax warehouses are subject to permanent tax supervision for alcohol, in the Czech Republic this supervision is replaced by continuous supervision by the tax administration through a monitoring device.
In the Czech Republic, small independent breweries are tax warehouses, in the SR they are only registered by the tax administration.
In the SR, the registered consignor institute is introduced, which is included among tax warehouses in the Czech Republic.
In the Slovak Republic it is possible to burn 43 l a at a reduced rate of excise duty on alcohol in case of cultivation burning.
In the Czech Republic, on the other hand, the reduced rate of tax on alcohol can be applied only for 30 l a.
Growing brandy in the Slovak Republic must have authorisation not only from the Ministry of Agriculture and Rural Development of the Slovak Republic, but also from the tax administrator.
In the Czech Republic, growing brandy is only authorised by the Ministry of Agriculture.
In the Slovak Republic, import of consumer packaging of alcohol is carried out by the importer of consumer packaging of alcohol in addition to the tax warehouse operator.
Authorisation of the importer is conditional on registration of the applicant with the excise tax administrator.
In the Czech Republic, no special authorisation by the tax administrator is required for import of consumer packaging of alcohol.
In the Slovak Republic, the sale of consumer packaging of alcohol is conditional on the issuance of authorisation by the tax administrator for the seller.
The seller of consumer packaging of alcohol has a legal obligation to keep a record of, among other things, the purchase and sale.
In the Czech Republic, the tax administrator does not issue any permit for final sellers of consumer packaging of alcohol, the issuance of a concession for the sale of alcohol by the trade office is sufficient; the final seller does not keep any special record.
In the Slovak Republic, the seller of fuel must have a permit from the tax administrator to sell it.
National legislation in the Slovak Republic does not regulate petrol stations by any special regulation, all activities related to petrol stations are regulated only by the Excise Tax Act on Mineral Oils.
In the Czech Republic, petrol stations are regulated by the Special Fuel Act, however, the tax administrator does not issue any permit for the sale of fuel.
Petrol stations are registered and a list of them is published by the Ministry of Industry and Trade.
In the Slovak Republic, it is technically not possible to obtain a list of petrol stations from the financial administration system.
In the Slovak Republic, the number of selected permits or registrations of tax entities has increased significantly since 2012.
This increase was caused by a legislative change in that period.
In the Czech Republic, on the other hand, the number of selected permits decreased significantly in 2013 due to the introduction of a deposit for fuel distributors.
Administrative acts
In the Slovak Republic, substantive legislation stipulates the obligation to carry out tax inspections of selected tax entities.
This issue is further specified by an internal management act issued by the Slovak Ministry of Finance due to the application of a uniform procedure of tax administrators in the territory of the Slovak Republic.
In the Czech Republic, substantive legislation does not regulate the obligation to carry out tax inspections, the procedural regulation only stipulates the possibility to carry out inspections at the latest by the deadline for tax assessment.
The reason for the large differences in the number of tax inspections carried out and local inspections in the Slovak Republic is the fact that the internal management act of the Slovak Ministry of Finance stipulates in which cases and within which deadlines the tax administrator must carry out a tax inspection, while in the Czech Republic the correctness of the declared amount of excise duty or its refund is verified mainly by a local investigation.
The number of comparable administrative operations in the Czech Republic has increased since 2012 due to the increase in the number of EMCS traffic and at the same time due to the increase in the number of tax returns filed.
In the Slovak Republic the number of administrative operations had a slightly increasing trend between 2012 and 2015, which was influenced by the increasing number of EMCS traffic and at the same time by the decrease in the number of tax returns.
Evaluation
The large differences between the numbers of comparable permits and tax entity registrations were reflected in the different legislative arrangements.
The number of comparable administrative operations of tax administrators was similar in the Slovak Republic and the Czech Republic in the individual years of the audited period.
In the Slovak Republic the total number of comparable tax entities, which is about two-thirds compared to the number of tax entities in the Czech Republic, accounts for approximately the same amount of administrative operations.
From the above it can be stated that the Slovak Republic focuses more on carrying out administrative operations by tax administrators, e.g. the performance of physical tax supervision.
In the Czech Republic, emphasis is placed more on remote supervision, e.g. monitoring equipment, immediate sending of data via a web interface and risk analysis.
Electronicization of administrative acts
Electronicization of administrative acts in the Czech Republic
Tax returns can be filed via a data box.
The Czech Customs Administration has introduced so-called interactive forms of tax returns, which however cannot be further processed automatically.
The data must be further transcribed into the personal tax account of the tax entity.
The benefit is a reduction in the error rate of filed tax returns (DAPs), which saves the tax administrator's actions related to the management of corrections of erroneously filed DAPs.
The DG is working on a new application for electronic processing of DAPs.
Through intelligent forms, it is also possible to: file tax applications or registration for activities and notifications of data changes, file claims for tax refunds, fulfill reporting obligations when handling special mineral oils, handling raw tobacco and fulfilling obligations in the field of biofuels.
The handling of control tapes is recorded by tax subjects in the ORO WebClient information system, which is available for registered entities for registration by the tax administrator of specified data.
Transport of selected products in the Czech Republic under the regime of conditional exemption from tax must be realized in the Czech Republic on the basis of an electronic accompanying document, which is implemented in the Czech Republic as a national functionality in the electronic system for monitoring the transport of selected products (EMCS).
Transport of selected products in free tax circulation in the tax territory of the Czech Republic can always be realized with a document proving their taxation, a proof of exemption from excise tax, a decision of the customs office to release selected products into the customs procedure, a simplified accompanying document or another decision to assess excise tax.
The required content of data is determined by legal regulations.
To facilitate the fulfilment of these obligations, the Czech Republic has introduced a voluntary electronic system for issuing alternative documents (Sections 5 and 6 of Act No 353/2003 Coll.).
This allows the paper form of documents to be replaced or supplemented by electronically issued documents, which are sent via the web interface of the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic to a data warehouse, where each such document is assigned a unique 12-digit identification code (JIK).
JIK serves for the purposes of control by customs authorities on the way and makes repeated transport on the same document impossible.
For the largest operator of a tax warehouse of fuel in the Czech Republic, which puts about half of the volume of fuel into free tax circulation, CS CR has online access to an electronic registration system, into which the entity automatically stores issued tax documents.
CS CR is considering the introduction of e-VDO, i.e. an electronic system for recording and monitoring the transport of selected products carried out in free tax circulation.
This system should use 70% of the existing functional specification of EMCS.
The advantage will be a user-familiar environment for declarants and customs officers.
It will also be connected to the system of global guarantees, to the register of tax entities or to the system of risk analysis.
The system should allow an overview of transport in free circulation between Member States, which so far operates on the basis of written documents without registration and sharing of reference numbers through simplified accompanying documents.
The risks of the existing procedure for the registration of transport of selected products in free tax circulation can be seen mainly in the misuse of a simplified accompanying document, repeated use of one document or illegal transport without any document.
Electronicization of administrative operations in the Slovak Republic
In the administration of excise taxes, the Slovak Republic Financial Administration uses electronic communication for monitoring the movement of goods in the EMCS system under the regime of conditional exemption, control marks, filing of tax returns and also for registering and registering tax subjects.
In 2014, one-way electronic communication of tax subjects with the tax administrator was also introduced, which was extended to two-way communication in 2016.
Within the electronic communication, the tax subject has access to a personal Internet zone, the so-called electronic personal mailbox, which is intended for communication with the financial administration.
Within this zone, the tax subject has access to an electronic mailroom, through which he/she submits applications, notifications, tax returns and other documents related to the administration of excise taxes.
However, electronic communication through the personal Internet zone does not concern all tax subjects.
National legislation defines tax entities that are obliged to communicate with the tax administrator electronically.
These are mainly VAT payers, tax advisors representing the tax entity and attorneys representing the tax entity.
During the audit, the SAO SR also dealt with the issue of the scope of computerisation of the administration of excise taxes.
These were only fully electronic acts, namely tax returns and electronic communication within ELO.
If transport carried out in the EMCS system is not included, there has been an increase in computerisation of selected comparable administrative acts, which is also a requirement for modern tax administration.
Comparison and evaluation
Comparison
In the SR, fully computerised processing of tax returns is already in place, from its submission to the registration of tax obligations.
In the Czech Republic, the electronic processing of tax returns is not set up.
In the Czech Republic, the possibility for tax entities to insert on the website obligatory documents for individual transport in free tax circulation is set up.
In the future, the reporting of transport operations in free tax circulation is being prepared in the form and on the basis of the EMCS system.
Evaluation
The system of reporting transport operations in free tax circulation in the Czech Republic contributes to tax supervision, thus eliminating the transport of selected products for which excise tax was not paid in violation of the legislation.
This can be recommended as good practice.
THISsegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
Due to good practice in the Slovak Republic in the area of computerisation of tax returns, the SAO of the Slovak Republic and the SAO of the Czech Republic recommend to complete computerisation of tax return processing in the Czech Republic.
Analysis of changes in organisational structure and personnel security in the area of excise taxes
The organisational structure of the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic and the Financial Administration of the Slovak Republic has undergone fundamental changes.
Organisational structure of the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic
The Customs Administration of the Czech Republic since 1 January 2013 consists of the General Directorate of Customs and Customs Offices, which are administrative offices and organisational units of the state.
The DG is the accounting unit for the whole customs administration.
The Customs Administration of the Czech Republic has been carrying out the comprehensive administration of excise duties since 2004 as one of the many competences it provides.
The CS of the Czech Republic also carries out:
(a) control:
ശശ in the area of road transport (weighing of trucks, payment of fees for the use of roads, fulfilment of conditions for the transport of dangerous goods, professional supervision of the work of vehicle crews in international road freight transport and in matters of international passenger transport),
ശശ management of waste and packaging material,
ശശ safety of imported food,
ശശ in the area of consumer protection and protection of intellectual property rights,
ശശ employment of foreigners,
(b) customs administration – it is a complex application of customs regulations, commercial policy measures and formalities in the import and export of goods,
(c) collection and recovery of cash payments imposed by other public administration bodies within the framework of the divided administration,
d) activities of the police authority (authorized customs authorities) in proceedings on offences committed in breach of customs and related regulations and tax regulations, if the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic is the tax administrator.
The scope of competences (concurrent control activities) increases the overall cost of the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic, but there are cost savings of scale, as the public administration does not have to incur the expenses for the position of the control group for each subject of the inspection separately.
At the same time, the administrative burden of the audited persons is reduced by repeated inspection.
10 The Customs Administration of the Czech Republic furthermore exercises competence to verify compliance with obligations in the registration of sales from 1.12.2016 (§ 2 paragraph 2 of Act No. 112/2016 Coll., on the registration of sales) and from 1.1.2017 to supervise compliance with the law and conditions of operation of gambling including the imposition of sanctions (section 116 of Act No. 186/2016 Coll., on gambling).
As part of the Modernization of the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic, the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic changed the three-tier structure to a two-tier structure with effect from 1 January 2013, with the elimination of the central part of proceedings (Customs Directorates).
The DG has spent about CZK 51 million (i.e. about €2,031,000) on the project.
EN The Czech Republic since 1 January 2013 consists of the DG and regional customs offices, which are administrative offices and organisational units of the state.
Customs offices and their competences are determined by law, the administration of excise duties is carried out by all customs offices through departments and territorial offices.
Territorial offices are internal organisational units of customs offices.
The Ministry of Finance is entitled to establish and abolish territorial offices and to determine their material competences by decree.
The legislation does not stipulate any competences for territorial offices; territorial offices carry out the competences of the customs office on its behalf.
Organisational structure until 31 December 2012
Organisational structure since 1 January 2013
The excise tax administration until 31.12.2012 was carried out by the DG, eight DCs and 58 departments of the CA (including branches), i.e. a total of 67 departments and departments.
As of 1.1.2016, the excise tax administration was carried out by the DG and 51 departments at the CA and their territorial workplaces, as well as eight workplaces of the legal department of the DG and the CA departments providing mobile supervision, i.e. about 60 posts.
The costs of the CA most significantly affect the wage expenditure.
There were no savings in personnel resources as a result of the reorganisation of the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic.
The main processes are carried out by customs officers in service under the Act on the service relationship of members of the security forces.
The possibility to reduce the numbers of these members is very limited in the Czech Republic, as according to the provisions of § 42 paragraph 1 of Act No 361/2003 Coll., on the service relationship of members of the security forces, they can be dismissed from service only in cases exhaustively defined.
Reduction of service posts due to organizational changes in the security forces is not a reason for dismissal and the employer is obliged to ensure that the members of the corresponding service posts within the force are assigned, or to secure service posts with other security forces (e.g. Police of the Czech Republic, Prison Service of the Czech Republic), otherwise it will transfer them to the reserve for the temporarily non-attached, in which members of the security forces are entitled to 80% of the average service income according to the Act.

Organizational organization of the administration of excise taxes in the Slovak Republic
The Government of the Slovak Republic, within the framework of the program statement for the years 2012 to 2016, has set as one of the priorities the completion of the reform of the tax administration through the UNITAS program, which will secure additional budgetary resources by unification of the collection of taxes, duties and levies and suppression of tax evasion.
In this context, the tax reform was implemented at the central level, which resulted in the merger of the Tax Directorate of the Slovak Republic and the Customs Directorate into the Slovak Republic's Financial Directorate and the creation of the financial administration.
The Slovak Tax Directorate was established on 1 January 2012 by Act No 333/2011 Coll., on state administration bodies in the field of taxes, fees and customs, as amended, as a budgetary organization, which has its seat in Banská Bystrica and is connected to the state budget through the budget chapter of the Ministry of Finance of the Slovak Republic.
The Slovak Tax Directorate, the CA and the Criminal Office of the Financial Administration within the meaning of Act No 199/2004 Coll., the Customs Act and on the amendment and supplementation of certain laws, as amended, are customs authorities if they perform tasks according to customs regulations.
Within the meaning of Act No 333/2011 Coll., on state administration bodies in the field of taxes, fees and customs, as amended, they together with the tax authorities form the financial administration.
The new organisational structure of the financial administration as of 1 January 2012 consists of the Financial Directorate of the Slovak Republic, the Criminal Office of the Financial Administration, the Competent Centre for Financial Operations, the tax authorities, the Tax Office for selected tax entities, tax office branches, tax office contact points, customs offices, branches of customs offices (branch of the Czech Tax Office, branch of the Czech Tax Office combined, branch of the Czech Customs Office) and customs office stations.
The main mission of the Slovak Ministry of Finance is the effective collection and administration of taxes and duties, i.e. also excise duties, to fulfil the revenue part of the state budget and to protect the economic interests of the state.
The statutory body of the Slovak Ministry of Finance is the President of the Financial Administration, who is appointed and dismissed by the Minister of Finance of the Slovak Republic.
The president of the financial administration is responsible to him for the activities of the entire financial administration and therefore also for the activities of the Slovak Ministry of Finance, which he manages and represents in full.
Organizational Structure of the Slovak Ministry since 1. 1. 2012 in abbreviated form
Within all customs offices in the territory of the SR, activities and processes in the field of administration of excise taxes are ensured in addition to the branches of customs offices (38 branches) and customs office stations (18 stations) also by the excise tax department (9 departments) and the legal department (9 departments).
