Comparison and evaluation
Comparison
Comparison
Within the organizational structure of the financial administration of the SR, in 2015 in addition to the FR SR, 74 organizational departments with a total number of 1,300 employees dealt with administration of excise taxes; these departments administer nearly 48,000 tax entities.
Within the organizational structure of the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic, in 2015, approximately 60 organizational departments with a total number of 1,011 employees dealt with administration of excise taxes, administering approximately 114,000 tax entities.
In the Czech Republic, the performance of individual activities of administration of excise taxes is divided among several personnel-independent departments.
Their mutual coordination and cooperation is dealt with through middle and top management.
In the Slovak Republic, the performance of individual activities (registration, tax return, tax inspection) in the area of administration of excise taxes is divided between the department of excise taxes and the branch of the customs office, within which the agenda is often dealt with by the same employees of the tax administration.
Evaluation
In the Slovak Republic, approximately one third of the number of tax entities per the total number of employees in the area of administration of excise taxes is compared to the situation in the Czech Republic; the impact of the higher number of employees on the efficiency of the administration of excise taxes is not obvious.
EMCS system
According to the preamble of Decision No 1152/2003/EC of the European Parliament and of the Council of 16 June 2003 on the introduction of an electronic system for the transport and monitoring of excise products, the aim of the introduction of an electronic system for monitoring the transport of selected products was to enable real-time information on the transport and to carry out the prescribed checks, to simplify the movement of goods within the Community under suspension of excise duty.
When introducing the system, Member States should have allowed economic operators, especially small and medium-sized enterprises active in this sector, to use these national elements at the lowest possible cost.
Article 3 of the aforementioned EP and Council Decision allows the inclusion in the EMCS of a national specification, a national database forming part of the system and such technical or software as a Member State considers necessary to ensure the full use of the system within its administration.
EMCS in the Czech Republic
Development and functionalities of the EMCS system
In the Czech Republic, EMCS was preceded by a system of registration of selected products (EVV), which operated from May 2004 until the end of March 2010.
EMCS has been fully operational in the Czech Republic since 1.4.2010 and is continuously supplemented with European and national functionalities (see Annex 5).
In the Czech Republic, the so-called customs module and the declarant module have been introduced.
The customs module contains a number of national functionalities.
Beyond the Community system, in the Czech Republic, EMCS monitors shipments under the conditional tax exemption regime both started and ended in the Czech Republic.
The system provides for automatic transmission of information to the register of tax entities after approval of the notification of the receipt of a shipment intended for the authorised recipient for a one-off receipt, followed by the invalidation of the permit.
The system provides for the administration of received and sent requests for international cooperation and spontaneous information from ELO, including the sending of replies with an attachment in any format and the provision of translations.
It is also possible to receive a manual export termination message in the ECS (in the EU, only the forwarding of the automatically created message is implemented).
The risk profiles for outgoing or incoming shipments are set according to the currently required criteria.
The EMCS system does not allow approval of e-AD or a notification of receipt without a response of the competent customs authority to the risk profile (the risk profile cannot be ignored).
The declarant module is available free of charge for tax subjects, it takes the form of a web application into which the user logs in with a user name and password (coordinates), which are assigned to him after registration with the CS CR.
Every action against the EMCS customs module must be provided with a valid electronic signature in the EMCS declarant module.
The declarant module allows tax subjects to directly enter data on started and finished shipments under the suspension regime, and thus tax subjects do not have to spend money on acquiring the system.
The national functionalities of the declarant module allow data to be retrieved and stored off-line (saving time on frequently used data), to fill in data on the recipient based on the SEED ID check and to require the mandatory completion of data that are optional at EU level (maximum data for risk analysis).
The system also allows for the real-time blocking of excise duty security for each shipment sent from the Czech Republic up to the time of the termination of the transport.
The amount of security is calculated automatically by the EMCS system.
Without a sufficient amount of security, it is not possible from the EMCS declarant module to send the e-AD proposal for approval to the CA of dispatch.
Each guarantee has a unique number and contains the ARC of the transport (including the amount of the blocked security) for which it was used.
The tax entity can administer its guarantees directly in the EMCS declarant module, where it can see the current amount of the blocked and unblocked excise duty guarantee.
Expenditure on the implementation and use of the EMCS system
The development of the EMCS was carried out on the basis of eight contracts with performance from 2006 to 2017 for a total amount of CZK 46,791,924.60 (i.e. €1,761,412.56) excluding VAT.
In accordance with the concluded contracts, the contractor issued invoices for a total amount of CZK 43,577,255.19 (i.e. €1,640,401.10) excluding VAT from 2006 to the end of 2015.
During the audited period, expenditure amounting to CZK 14,545,454 excluding VAT (i.e. €547,438.99) was spent on the upgrade of the EMCS system.
The amount spent on the upgrade of the EMCS during the audited period and converted into one transport entered into the EMCS is on average CZK 16.49 (i.e. €0.62), excluding national transport, this expenditure amounts to CZK 24.40 (i.e. €0.92) when converted into one transport between the Czech Republic and the EU Member States.
The technical support of the EMCS was carried out on the basis of four contracts with performance from 2011 to 2017.
By the end of 2015, the total amount of technical support was invoiced in the amount of CZK 7,499,675 (i.e. €281,389.77) including value added tax.
The average amount of technical support spent since 2011 per transport entered into the EMCS since 2010 is 6.18 CZK (i.e. 0.23 €).
The invoices for both development and technical support related to the national solution and led to the development of the EVV application, which was already operated by the DG before EMCS itself.
The invoices were paid under the programme financing from national sources.
Technical support is invoiced as part of deliveries of services to other applications provided by the supplier for the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic.
EMCS in SR
The EMCS is an electronic system operated by EU Member States to monitor movements of excise goods between Member States under a duty suspension arrangement.
It replaced the accompanying administrative document – SAD, which was used before the system took effect, thus ensuring better control and management of traffic.
It has been introduced in the Slovak Republic since 1 April 2010 and is continuously supplemented by requirements arising from EU legislation.
A unique reference code is generated for each transport, the so-called ‘reference code’.
The ARC code under which the traffic can be monitored online, i.e. in real time.
Development and functionality of EMCS
The EMCS provides for the receipt and dispatch of excise goods only by those taxable persons who are authorised to use the EMCS, thereby greatly reducing the risk of tax evasion.
The greatest development of functionalities occurred in 2011, when EMCS was fully operational (see Annex 6).
Expenditure on the implementation and use of EMCS
The introduction of EMCS was implemented as an additional SysNeD application equipment module and therefore it is not possible to determine the exact cost of its initial application on the Slovak side.
Comparison and evaluation
Comparison
The aim of the EMCS was to replace a system based on paper-based transport administration.
The benefit of the EMCS system is a comprehensive overview of transport between individual Member States within the EU from the notification of the start of transport to its termination – a significant reduction of administrative costs for tax administrators and tax subjects for processing, transmission and archiving of documents.
In the Czech Republic and Slovakia, the EMCS system was introduced with a national functionality allowing monitoring of transport in a conditional system between two places in the Czech Republic and Slovakia respectively.
In the Czech Republic, the automatic functionality of on-line monitoring and guaranteeing of the excise tax guarantee is also applied.
The national functionality is also introduced, which monitors the risk of the tax entity or transport, followed by the obligatory reaction of the tax administrator.
The Slovak Republic and the Czech Republic record a comparable number of transport within the EU in the EMCS system.
Expenditure spent in the Slovak Republic on the upgrade of this system was however 744 310.01 € higher than in the Czech Republic between 2012 and 2015.
The SAO SR obtained data on the upgrade of the EMCS system from the Slovak Republic only for the period from 2011, despite the fact that the system had been implemented and operated earlier.
Despite this, the expenditure spent on the upgrade of the EMCS system in the Slovak Republic was by 188,134.44 € higher than the expenditure on the introduction and upgrade of the EMCS system for approximately ten years of its operation in the Czech Republic.
Evaluation
During the audited period, the amount of expenditure related to the upgrade of the EMCS system in the Slovak Republic in terms of one transport was 2.3 times higher than the expenditure of the same type in the Czech Republic.
Conclusion
The cooperation of the SAO of the Czech Republic and the SAO of the Slovak Republic fulfilled the objectives.
Both audit institutions gained a deeper knowledge of the excise tax administration system in the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic.
It was found that despite the common basic legal framework, there are significant differences in both tax systems that affect the efficiency of the excise tax administration.
During parallel audits, examples of good practice were found that could contribute to the reduction of tax fraud, their importance will increase with increasing tax rates.
Procedures reducing the costs of the excise tax administration were also identified.
Mutual cooperation has revealed differences that significantly affect the efficiency of tax administration and limit international comparisons, unless mutually coordinated due diligence checks are carried out with the tax administration.
In this, the role of supreme audit institutions is irreplaceable.
Report on the results of the parallel control of the value added tax administration carried out in the Czech Republic and the Federal Republic of Germany
Introductory word
The Lima Declaration of 1977 stresses that supreme audit institutions (SAIs) have the power to audit all public financial operations.
The Declaration asks that tax revenues be audited to the greatest extent possible.
The European Organisation of Supreme Audit Institutions (EUROSAI) considers taxes to be one of the most important components of public revenue.
The VIth EUROSAI Congress held in Bonn in 2005 dealt with the audit of public revenue carried out by the SAIs.
An important step on the way to optimise the control activities of the SAIs is the development of a specific strategy for the audit of public revenue.
This applies in particular to taxes as the most voluminous source of public revenue, which is most susceptible to large losses.
As national economies become increasingly interconnected and dependent, the SAIs may to some extent be unable to carry out control activities without the cooperation of the SAIs of another state.
An example is the audit of internationally organised fraud, which causes substantial losses in the revenues of many countries.
To combat this crime, the responsible authorities need to cooperate with each other.
The SAIs carrying out control in this area must be willing to establish closer cooperation with each other.
It was at the 6th EUROSAI Congress in Bonn that the idea of carrying out a control of the administration of value added tax (hereinafter "VAT") and the VIES system was developed within the framework of the cooperation of the Supreme Audit Office and the Federal Court of Auditors, the Bundesrechnungshof.
This was followed by careful preparation, where both parties first had to get acquainted with the legal environment and procedures for the administration of VAT in the Czech Republic and the Federal Republic of Germany.
Based on the analysis of this information, a selection of audit topics was made, which were included in the audit programme.
Achieving an effective and efficient administration of VAT is a long-term problem and individual states (especially the Member States of the European Union) are looking for solutions to improve the system, simplify and make the collection of this tax more transparent.
We are convinced that the results of our audit can serve not only to improve the work of tax administrators, but also as a basis for a proposal to improve the system of international exchange of information.
Report on the results of parallel audits of the administration of value added tax carried out in the Czech Republic and the Federal Republic of Germany
Introduction
Audit number: (CZ) 06/27 (D) VIII 2 – 2005 – 1215
Audit subject:
(CZ) Value added tax administration after the accession of the Czech Republic to the European Union
(D) Examination of administrative cooperation in the field of value added tax pursuant to Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 and Commission Regulation (EC) No 1925/2004
Audit objective:
(CZ) The aim of the audit operation in the Czech Republic was to examine the procedure of the financial authorities in the administration of value added tax after the Czech Republic's integration into the single internal market of the European Union (hereinafter referred to as the EU) connected with the free movement of goods and services and to examine the use of the VIES system, in particular when checking the application of the right to exemption from value added tax for intra-Community supplies.
(D) The aim of the audit was to examine the system of control of intra-Community value added tax with a special focus on administrative cooperation in the field of value added tax pursuant to the aforementioned regulations.
The result should be a report on weaknesses and recommendations for their elimination.
System of exchange of information on value added tax The audited operations were carried out by the Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic (hereinafter referred to as the SAO) and the German Bundesrechnungshof (hereinafter referred to as the BRH) in mutual cooperation on the basis of a contract concluded between the two auditing institutions on 8 June 2006.
The cooperation focused mainly on the examination of selected commercial transactions carried out between payers from the Czech Republic (hereinafter referred to as “the Czech Republic”) and the Federal Republic of Germany (hereinafter referred to as “Germany”), the use of information obtained through international cooperation between tax administrations and the comparison of the VAT administration systems of both countries.
The joint final report on the results of the auditing operations was prepared in the sense of European Directive No. 31 for the implementation of the INTOSAI auditing standards.
The audited period covered the period from 1 May 2004 to 31 December 2005.
Summary of results and evaluation of parallel auditing operations
The parallel audit in the field of VAT administration in the Czech Republic and Germany was carried out on the basis of a contract between the two SAIs.
Apart from the main point – the exchange of information on the basis of Council Regulation (EC) No. 1798/2003 and Commission Regulation (EC) No. 1925/2004 – the audit covered other topics, such as the registration of payers, VAT returns and summary reports, which are closely connected with the main point.
In addition, the control included the legal situation in the field of international bus passenger transport and a comparison of some statistical data.
Comparison of the VAT administration systems of the two countries revealed differences in the following areas:
1) VAT registration.
While in Germany entrepreneurs are registered irrespective of their turnover, in the Czech Republic the primary criterion (among others) for registration is exceeding the limit set in the VAT Act.
In the Czech Republic, payers are assigned only one tax identification number, which they also use in intra-community transactions.
In Germany, payers are assigned a tax number when registering for VAT, serving only for commercial transactions in the territory of Germany.
If a German payer intends to carry out intra-community transactions, he must apply for a special identification number, the so-called VAT ID.
As different methods of registration cause problems, conditions should be balanced across the EU (see 4.1).
2) International bus passenger transport.
In the Czech Republic, international bus passenger transport is exempt from VAT with the right to deduct VAT.
In Germany, part of the transport that takes place on German territory is subject to VAT.
At EU level, efforts should be made to harmonise the situation in the sense of Article 393 of Council Directive 2006/112/EC on the common system of VAT (see 4.2).
3) VAT returns.
While in the Czech Republic, tax payers file VAT returns only for individual tax periods (month or quarter), in Germany, tax payers are obliged to file so-called preliminary VAT returns (monthly or quarterly) and after the end of the calendar year, they have to file annual VAT returns.
Unlike in the Czech Republic, tax payers in Germany are obliged to file preliminary tax returns electronically.
The introduction of an obligation to file VAT returns electronically in the Czech Republic would increase the efficiency of the Czech tax administration (see 4.3).
4) Summary reports.
While in the Czech Republic, tax payers file summary reports at the tax offices, in the Czech Republic, tax payers file summary reports at the Customs Office.
The tax authorities in the Czech Republic therefore have the data from the summary reports available immediately after they have been submitted.
The German tax authorities have the information from the summary reports available only after they have been processed into the CLO.
Combating VAT fraud requires that updated information on intra-community transactions is available as soon as possible.
Monthly submission of the summary reports would shorten the time lag between the date of the transaction and the updating of the data in the VIES.
This would in turn allow for a timely verification of taxation in the acquirer's Member State (see 4.4).
This would, however, require all Member States to adopt the same deadline for submission of the summary report.
5) International exchange of information in the field of VAT.
The Czech CLO monitors compliance with the three-month deadline for received requests for information.
The German CLO does not monitor the elapsed time.
As a result, the German tax administration handled a significantly lower percentage of received requests within the deadline.
Due to these problems, the BRH recommended that the German CLO carry out a permanent alert (see 4.6).
6) Risk management system.
Each of the two Member States develops its own risk management system (RMS), which has both strengths and weaknesses.
The SAO and the BRH point out that an effective RMS cannot be developed by just one Member State.
Successful criteria, components and approaches of RMS must be exchanged and implemented in each EU Member State, otherwise fraudsters choose the Member State with the weakest RMS (see 5.).
As part of the cooperation, the two SAIs examined selected cases of intra-community transactions, carried out between tax entities from the Czech Republic and Germany.
Together, thirty-one cases of commercial transactions where there were doubts about their completion or suspicion of VAT evasion were examined using the legislation for the Customs Office.
It was found that:
In some cases, the tax authorities used the information obtained through international cooperation to assess the VAT liability of the payers.
In these cases, the payers either improperly claimed the VAT exemption of the supply or failed to declare the acquisition of the goods in the VAT return.
In some cases, the tax authorities could not use the information obtained because the information was either incomplete or incomprehensible.
In other cases, the information could not be used because of different legal provisions in both Member States.
In some cases, the tax administration of another Member State refused to respond to a request for information.
Cases have been identified where payers have erroneously reported commercial transactions in recapitulative statements.
As a result, the data in the VIES were incorrect and the tax administrations had to check these cases (see 6.).
Progress of control action
Progress of the audit operation in the Czech Republic
The audit was carried out between June 2006 and March 2007 by the State Budget Revenue Department and the territorial departments of Central Bohemia, Northwest Bohemia, Southern Bohemia, Southern Moravia, Central Moravia and Northern Moravia.
The audited bodies were: the Ministry of Finance (hereinafter referred to as the “MoF”) and 10 financial offices – the Financial Office in Humpolec, the Financial Office in Jihlava, the Financial Office in Kadani, the Financial Office in Liberec, the Financial Office in Nymburk, the Financial Office in Otrokovice, the Financial Office for Prague 1, the Financial Office for Prague 4, the Financial Office in Sokolov and the Financial Office in Třinec.
The audit conclusion from this audit operation was approved by the SAO College on 23 April 2007.
Audit operation in Germany
The audit was carried out between June 2006 and February 2007 by the Indirect Tax Audit Group and by the staff of the designated regional audit offices in Berlin, Frankfurt am Main and Munich.
The audit was part of the 2006 audit plan and was therefore reported to the Federal MoF in 2006.
After the testing phase, the audit was launched in the fourth quarter of 2006.
According to the cases selected by the BRH and later selected by the SAO, the BRH had to notify a number of federal states of the audit.
In addition to the interviews at the Federal Ministry of Finance and at the CLO, the auditing operation was carried out in the following federal states:
Baden-Württemberg, Bavaria, Hamburg, Lower Saxony, North Rhine-Westphalia, Rhineland-Palatinate and Saxony.
Tax files of the following tax authorities were included:
Bruchsal, Ettlingen, Freudenstadt, Karlsruhe-Stadt, Leonberg, Mühlacker, Singen, Tuttlingen, Cham, Fürstenfeldbruck, Munich - FÚ for corporations/legal entities (München-Körperschaften), Munich II, IV and Munich V, Starnberg, Hamburg-Altona, Hamburg-Hansa, Hamburg-Centre (Hamburg-Mitte), Hamburg-North (Hamburg-Nord) and Hamburg for large enterprises (Hamburg für Großunternehmen), Hannover-Nord (Hannover-North), Winsen-Luhe, Bonn Centre (Bonn-Innenstadt), Cologne Centre (Köln-Mitte), Cologne-Porz (Köln-Porz), Cologne South (Köln-Süd), Sankt Augustin, Pirmasens, Bautzen (Bautzen), Chemnitz South (Chemnitz-Süd), Dresden II (Dresden II), Freiberg, Leipzig I (Leipzig I) and Zschopau.
In addition, discussions were held with the Tax Office Augsburg-City (Augsburg-Stadt), Aurich, Düsseldorf-Old Town (Düsseldorf-Altstadt), Eisleben, Kelheim and Verden.
A report on the audit findings was submitted to the Ministry of Finance in May 2007.

4. Value added tax administration in the Czech Republic and Germany
Registration of payers in the Czech Republic
A) Taxpayers having their registered office, place of business or establishment in the Czech Republic
According to Act No. 337/1992 Coll., on the Administration of Taxes and Fees (hereinafter “Act No. 337/1992 Coll.”), a taxpayer, taxpayer and legal successor of a natural or legal person, which is defined as a tax entity by law.
As of 31 December 2004, a total of 421,865 tax subjects were registered for VAT in the Czech Republic.
As of 1 December 2005, the number of tax subjects registered for VAT increased to 457,590.
A taxable person having his registered office, place of business or establishment in the Czech Republic, whose turnover exceeds CZK 1,000,000 (EUR 33,575) for the next 12 preceding consecutive calendar months, becomes a taxpayer from the 1st day of the third month following the month in which he exceeded the registration limit (Section 94, subsection 1 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll., on Value Added Tax; hereinafter “Act No. 235/2004 Coll.”).
This person is obliged to submit an application for registration within 15 days after the end of the month in which he exceeded the registration limit.
The current legislation does not allow to register a taxable person so-called retrospectively in cases where the reason for registration is exceeding the legal limit for registration.
A taxable person with a registered office, place of business or establishment in the Czech Republic who carries out taxable transactions or transactions exempt from VAT with the right to deduct may become a taxable person even if he does not exceed the turnover of CZK 1,000,000 (EUR 33,575) if he fulfils any of the other conditions set out in Act No. 235/2004 Coll.
A taxable person with a registered office, place of business or establishment in the Czech Republic who does not fulfil any of the conditions set out by the Act may apply for VAT registration voluntarily.
By delivery of the application for registration to the locally competent tax administrator, the registration procedure pursuant to Act No. 337/1992 Coll. is initiated.
A voluntary VAT payer shall also indicate on the application for VAT registration the date on which he or she applies for registration as a VAT payer.
The tax administrator shall check the data communicated by the tax entity, i.e. the completed application for registration with all annexes.
If he or she has doubts about the stated data, he or she shall ask the tax entity to explain, complete or substantiate the data.
After the tax administrator has verified that the tax entity fulfils the conditions for registration, he or she shall issue a decision in the form of a certificate stating that the tax entity is registered and has been assigned a tax identification number (hereinafter referred to as the Tax Identification Number).
On the certificate, the tax administrator shall indicate the effective date of the registration for VAT and the periodicity of the tax period for VAT.
The tax period shall be the calendar quarter if the turnover of the payer for the previous calendar year has not reached CZK 10,000,000 (EUR 335,750).
If the turnover of the payer for the previous calendar year has reached CZK 10,000,000 (EUR 335,750), the tax period shall be the calendar month.
A payer whose turnover for the previous calendar year has reached CZK 2,000,000 (EUR 67,150) shall be entitled to choose a calendar month for the tax period and shall notify the tax administrator of this change.
THISsegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
The allocation of the TIN in the registration certificate is always constitutive and the tax entity is obliged to state it in all cases of communication (including payments) with the tax administrator and in cases where a special law so provides (e.g. Act No. 235/2004 Coll. when issuing tax documents).
The TIN contains the code "CZ" and the ordinary part, which consists of a general identifier.
The general identifier is the birth number for a natural person, or another general identifier if a special law so provides, and the identification number for a legal person (Section 33, subsection 12 of Act No. 337/1992 Coll.).
If a tax entity has not fulfilled its registration obligation even at the request of the tax administrator, the locally competent tax administrator registers it automatically.
The result of the registration procedure is the issuance of the Certificate of Registration ex officio, which is delivered to the tax entity.
In the Czech Republic, a tax entity that has obtained a business license is allocated the TIN at the moment of its first registration for any tax.
The same TIN is used by the taxpayer even if it is registered as a VAT payer.
According to the wording of Act No. 235/2004 Coll., which is effective from 1 January 2005, in case of failure to comply with the registration obligation for VAT, the tax administrator may impose compensation of up to 10% of the total revenue or income for taxable transactions, which this person carried out without tax, for the period from the date on which he should have been a registered payer by law to the date on which he became a registered payer by decision of the tax administrator (provision § 98 paragraph 1 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll.).
Payment of the amount thus determined is considered as a tax payment (section 98 paragraph 3 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll.), i.e. it is not a penalty.
The cancellation of the registration of a VAT payer when fulfilling the conditions laid down by law is possible for two reasons:
1)
The cancellation of the registration at the request of the payer, mainly due to the amount of turnover, which does not reach the registration limit (section 106 paragraph 1 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll.).
The payer is entitled to apply for the cancellation of the registration at the earliest after the expiration of 1 year from the effective date stated on the registration certificate.
2) The cancellation of the registration "ex officio" (Section106(7) of Act No. 235/2004 Coll.) if: a) the payer has not performed the performance for 12 consecutive months without notifying the tax administrator of the reason, b) the payer has not fulfilled his obligations under Act No. 235/2004 Coll., c) the payer ceases to be a taxable person.
B) Taxpayers who do not have a registered office, place of business or establishment in the Czech Republic A person registered for tax in another Member State who does not have a registered office, place of business or establishment in the Czech Republic, or a foreign taxable person who carries out a performance with a place of performance in the Czech Republic and is a person obliged to declare and pay tax on this performance pursuant to Section 108 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll. (the so-called "non-established payer"), becomes a payer on the day of the performance.
This person is obliged to submit the application for registration to the Financial Office for Prague 1 no later than the date of the performance.
In the application for registration, he is obliged to state all the VAT numbers allocated to him in other Member States or in a third country.
If a "non-established" taxpayer submits an application for registration later than the date of the first taxable performance in the Czech Republic, the Financial Office for Prague 1 registers him retroactively, because according to Act No. 235/2004 Coll., the taxpayer became a VAT payer on the date of the first taxable performance in the Czech Republic.
In the case of retroactive registration, the Financial Office for Prague 1 requires from tax entities proof that the performance has been performed (invoices, or explanatory letters).
If a "non-established" taxpayer applies for registration in the Czech Republic before the first taxable performance takes place, the Financial Office for Prague 1 requests the submission of contracts that the performance will take place.
At the Financial Office for Prague 1, 473 "non-established" taxpayers were registered as of 31 December 2004, of which 124 were from Germany, and as of 31 December 2005, 951 "non-established" taxpayers were registered, of which 233 were from Germany.
Pursuant to the provisions of Section 106(9) of Act No 235/2004, the tax administrator is entitled to cancel the registration of a "non-established" taxpayer as of 31 January of the following calendar year if the tax payer did not incur any obligation to declare and pay the tax during the current calendar year.
The SAO audit found that if a "non-established" taxpayer submits a tax return abroad for postal transport on 25 January, i.e. in accordance with the statutory regulation at the deadline for filing the tax return, the tax office often does not have it available yet on 31 January.
In cases where the facts relevant for the possibility of cancellation of the registration are known to the tax office later than 31 January, it is not possible to cancel the VAT registration of a "non-established" taxpayer in the Czech Republic in the given calendar year.
Registration of taxpayers in Germany
Due to the legal provisions of the German Tax Code (§§ 137, 138 Abgabenordnung, hereinafter referred to as "AO"), anyone who carries out business activities is obliged to inform the city/municipal office or the relevant tax office.
The deadline for submitting information is one month after the start of the business.
This information is processed by the municipal/municipal authority for the tax authority.
If the tax authority identifies an enterprise that has started the business but has not registered, the relevant tax authority can register this payer ex officio – and retroactively.
Taxpayers who are both tax residents and non-residents in Germany are obliged by law to register for VAT if they meet the criteria set out in Section 2 of the German VAT Act (hereinafter "UStG").
This obligation does not depend on the volume of turnover they realise.
There is no voluntary VAT registration in Germany.
There are special tax authorities for entrepreneurs permanently resident abroad.
For example, for those who have their registered office in the Czech Republic, the relevant tax authority is Chemnitz-Süd.
As of 30 April 2004, a total of 295 Czech entrepreneurs were registered at the Chemnitz-Süd tax authority; as of 1 March 2006, a total of 1050 Czech entrepreneurs were registered.
The BRH found that these special tax offices often refused to register so-called semi-dependent independent workers based in the new eastern EU Member States.
Since the work permits of employees from the ten new EU Member States are limited after their accession to the EU, these independent workers tried to avoid these restrictions by starting a business.
These businesses do not meet the criteria for entrepreneurs set out in Section 2 of the UStG, as they are usually dependent on a single employer who determines their working hours and the way in which they carry out their work.
In order to register, the entrepreneur must fill in a questionnaire from the relevant tax office, in which he must provide information about the company and the activities he carries out.
The questionnaire is a standard form that is binding for all tax offices in Germany.
It is processed either by special departments of the tax offices or by departments with a general focus, which are responsible for assessing taxpayers.
The risk assessment of individual taxpayers is carried out through this form before the tax office issues a tax number.
The structure of the tax number for domestic transactions is governed by certain rules:
The first three digits provide information about the relevant tax office, the next three (or four) provide information about the relevant department at the tax office, the next five (or four) are for distinguishing the payers, with the last always being a check digit.
If the entrepreneur intends to participate in intra-community trade, he needs a VAT identification number (VAT ID) in order to receive an exempt intra-community supply.
The CLO assigns a VAT ID at the entrepreneur's request, if the entrepreneur is registered in Germany and if he has a VAT number.
The CLO assigns a VAT ID automatically to the entrepreneur when the payers include an intra-community supply in their VAT return.
The structure of the VAT ID is the country code (DE) followed by a series of nine digits.
The trader's registration can be cancelled: 1. at his request (for example, if he has ceased his business activity), after all administrative work has been carried out (assessment for all business years), and 2. if the tax administration realises that he is no longer engaged in business activity.
The validity of the VAT identification number is usually linked to the validity of the VAT tax number.
In such cases, the tax authorities are obliged to inform the CLO of the cancellation of the tax number so that the CLO can terminate the validity of the VAT identification number.
Under the German VAT Act (§ 19 (1) UStG), tax residents in Germany are not obliged to pay VAT if 1. the turnover plus the relevant VAT of the previous calendar year does not exceed EUR 17 500 and 2. the following year is not likely to exceed EUR 50 000.
The so-called small traders ("Kleinunternehmer") are not entitled to invoice other traders for VAT and are not entitled to deduct input tax.
Although they are not liable to pay VAT, small entrepreneurs must be registered with the tax office and must submit an annual VAT return.
A small entrepreneur can declare that he will not apply the provisions of § 19 (1) UStG.
This return is binding on him for the next five years.
The entrepreneur can then invoice VAT and deduct input tax.
For non-residents, there is the possibility to appoint tax representatives (§ 22a UStG).
A prerequisite is that they carry out exclusively tax-exempt business operations and are not entitled to deduct input tax.
The function of a tax representative is to fulfil the tax obligations of a foreign entrepreneur, who is thus not required to register for VAT.
The invoices must include information on representation for tax purposes.
Comparison and evaluation
The situation is different in both countries.
While in Germany entrepreneurs are registered irrespective of the amount of their turnover, in the Czech Republic the primary criterion (among others) for registration is exceeding the limit set in the VAT Act.
If a tax subject in the Czech Republic does not exceed the limit set, he or she has the possibility to apply for VAT registration on a voluntary basis.
The registration procedure is standardized in Germany, but differences may occur due to different organizational models in federal states.
In the Czech Republic, the tax payer is assigned a VAT number at the moment of his or her first registration for any tax.
If the payer registers for VAT, he or she uses the same VAT number for intra-community transactions as well.
In Germany, the tax payer is assigned a tax number when registering for VAT, serving only for business transactions in the territory of Germany.
If a German payer intends to carry out intra-community transactions, he or she must apply for a special identification number, the so-called VAT ID.
As the SAO and BRH have found, the German two-tier registration system can cause many misunderstandings in other Member States, such as in the Czech Republic, which assigns a single identification number for national VAT registration and registration for intra-community transactions.
On the other hand, the two-tier system allows for retroactive (national) registration in cases where payers refuse to inform the municipality or the relevant tax office about their business.
This retroactive registration allows for a correct assessment of VAT for the previous tax period, especially an accurate estimation of VAT liability.
As different registration methods cause problems, the conditions should be balanced across the EU.
The German Parliament recently decided to introduce a tax identification number (hereinafter the Tax Identification Number).
The Federal Tax Office will assign the Tax Identification Number at the birth of a natural person.
This Tax Identification Number will be valid for the whole life of a natural person who is a German resident.
If a natural person starts a business, the relevant tax office will apply for an economic Tax Identification Number, which will be used as the VAT ID.
In the future, there should be no delay between the national registration of the payer and the assignment of the VAT ID.
Work on the introduction of the IT means to administer the Tax Identification Number has not yet been completed.
International Bus Transport of Persons
Legislation in the Czech Republic
Pursuant to the provisions of Section 70 of Act No 235/2004 Coll., with effect from 1 May 2004, the transport of passengers between individual Member States and also between Member States and third countries in the Czech Republic is exempt from VAT with the right to deduct VAT.
This transport is exempt from VAT even if it is carried out by entrepreneurs who are registered for tax in other Member States or by a foreign taxable person.
The return transport is considered to be a separate transport.
If "non-established" tax entities in the Czech Republic do not carry out any other economic activity apart from international bus transport of passengers, they are not obliged to register as VAT payers in the Czech Republic.
International passenger transport has been exempt from VAT in the Czech Republic pursuant to the Act of Accession of the Czech Republic, Annex V, Chapter 5, paragraph 1 (b), which states:
"For the purposes of Article 28(3)(b) of Directive 77/388/EEC, the Czech Republic may continue to exempt from value added tax international passenger transport pursuant to point 17 of Annex F to the Directive until the condition set out in Article 28(4) of the Directive is fulfilled or the same exemption is applied by an existing Member State, whichever is the earlier."
Description of the legislation in Germany
According to Article 46 of Council Directive 2006/112/EC of 28 November 2006, implemented in Article 3b(1) of the German VAT Act, the place of provision of passenger transport (i.e. transport services) is the route (i.e. the place) where the transport takes place.
The German tax system therefore does not distinguish between domestic and international cross-border passenger transport.
Only the part of the route that takes place in Germany constitutes the taxable supply of transport in Germany.
The German tax system also does not distinguish between tax residents and non-residents.
If a non-resident transports passengers through Germany, the part of the route that takes place in Germany also constitutes a taxable supply of transport.
A non-resident must declare his intention to provide passenger transport to the relevant tax office before carrying out his services in Germany.
The tax office registers this non-resident for tax purposes (cf. 4.1.2) and issues a special certificate for any bus or coach that is mentioned in the taxpayer's notification.
The taxpayer is obliged to declare his taxable transport services in the German VAT return.
As of 1 March 2006, the Chemnitz-Süd tax office registered 741 Czech taxpayers who carried out passenger transport.
If passenger transport is provided to a resident taxpayer who is subject to VAT, the non-resident taxpayer does not have to pay the VAT to the tax office himself.
Instead, the entity liable to pay the VAT to the tax office and the invoiced net amount to the non-resident taxpayer is the resident taxpayer who receives the services; this process is known as the reverse charge and is in accordance with Article 196 of Council Directive 2006/112/EC.
In addition to the notification of the non-resident taxpayer and his VAT return, the German tax administration has several means to assess the correctness of the declared taxable passenger transport supplies.
The customs office's mobile control groups audit the certificates of buses licensed (licensed) for foreign transport, which are used to transport passengers through Germany.
After each audit, the mobile control groups send a control report to the relevant tax office.
If the bus driver does not have a valid certificate, the mobile control group is entitled to claim the payment of VAT from the bus driver before continuing with the next transport.
The non-resident may deduct the VAT thus paid from the tax calculated in his VAT return.
If the tax office has doubts about the accuracy of the VAT return, it may declare its intention to carry out an audit, which must be carried out in the office of the tax office, or it may use the means of administrative cooperation referred to in Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 (see 4.6).
Even if the non-resident refuses to pay the amount of VAT assessed in accordance with its statutory rate, the tax office may request administrative cooperation under Council Directive 76/308/EEC.
If a review of the VAT return or the non-resident's compliance is to be carried out, the BRH considers all these means of administrative cooperation to be too labour intensive compared to the small amounts of VAT to be paid for taxable passenger transport services.
In particular, the audit of the non-resident's accounts entails disproportionate costs for both the taxpayer and the tax administration.
The tax administration has to carry out an audit of foreign accounts, which means not only the need for knowledge of a foreign language, but also familiarity with foreign accounting standards.
An audit of this type is also likely to require more time than an audit of a resident taxpayer, but this audit is limited to those passenger transport services carried out in Germany.
On the other hand, a non-resident taxpayer may not only accept the right to carry out an audit, which is the responsibility of his national tax administration, but also the right to have an audit carried out by other Member States in which he transports passengers.
Moreover, in any Member State in which only one passenger transport service is carried out, the taxpayer is obliged to fulfil all tax obligations applicable to him in those Member States, in all languages and on all tax forms of those Member States.
The actual taxation of cross-border passenger transport therefore entails disproportionate bureaucratic costs.
Comparison and evaluation
The legal situation in both countries is different.
In the Czech Republic, passenger transport between individual EU Member States, or between Member States and third countries, is exempt from VAT with the right to deduct tax under the Act of Accession of the Czech Republic.
In Germany, the part of the transport which takes place on German territory constitutes a taxable transaction.
If this transport is provided in Germany for the first time by an non-established taxpayer, he is obliged to give prior notification of the provision of the transport to the relevant tax office.
The tax office registers this taxpayer and the taxpayer is obliged to declare in Germany the taxable provision of part of the transport in the tax return.
The implementation of the Act is very time-consuming in Germany.
At least three out of four Czech taxpayers registered at the Chemnitz-Süd Tax Office operate in passenger transport.
Compared to the given effort, the tax revenue, if realised, is rather low.
Member States that collect VAT in accordance with Article 46 of Council Directive 2006/112/EC of 28 November 2006 on the common system of VAT are burdened with time consuming obligations without a financially sensitive result.
In order to avoid disproportionate costs for charging VAT, the provision of cross-border passenger transport should be taxed only in one Member State.
This could be the state where the transport begins or where the provider resides.
Such taxation would require modification of Council Directive 2006/112/EC.
VAT returns
Submission and processing of VAT returns in the Czech Republic
The payer is obliged to submit a VAT return on the form prescribed by the Ministry of Finance within 25 days after the end of the tax period, even if he has not incurred any tax liability, unless the law provides otherwise.
The actual tax liability is due within the deadline for filing a VAT return, with the exception of the tax charged in connection with the importation of goods pursuant to Section 20 of Act No 235/2004 Coll., where the tax due is determined by customs regulations.
If a refundable overpayment arises as a result of the assessment of the excess deduction, it shall be returned to the payer without request within 30 days of the assessment of the excess deduction.
The deadline is not applied in cases where the tax administrator initiates tax proceedings concerning the payer's tax liability.
In accordance with the provisions of Section 73, subsection 11 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll., the right to deduct tax can be exercised in the regular VAT return at the latest for the last tax period of the calendar year in which the right to deduct tax could be exercised.
After the expiry of this deadline, the right to deduct tax can be further exercised within 3 years from the end of the tax period in which the right to deduct tax could be exercised at the earliest.
However, this is only possible in the form of filing a supplementary VAT return.
The amendment to Act No. 235/2004 Coll., effective from 1 January 2005, allows filing a supplementary VAT return only for the period in which the right to deduct tax could be exercised for the first time.
The taxpayer is obliged to submit a supplementary VAT return if (a) the summary of corrections increases the tax liability, (b) the correction does not change the last known tax liability, but only data previously claimed by the taxpayer, (c) the correction of the rate and amount of tax pursuant to Section 49 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll.
The taxpayer may submit a supplementary VAT return if the summary of corrections reduces the tax liability.
The taxpayer is obliged to submit a supplementary VAT return by the end of the month following the discovery of these facts.
The filing of a VAT return in electronic form can be done either via the Internet or on a technical data carrier.
The filing over the Internet can be done as a filing with a data message accompanied by a guaranteed electronic signature or as a filing with a data message not accompanied by a guaranteed electronic signature.
In the case of a submission with a data message not bearing an advanced electronic signature, the submission in written form, i.e. delivery of the computer set to the tax administrator (e-form) is still required.
The VAT return contains separate lines relating to the values of intra-Community supplies/acquisitions of goods.
The values of acquisitions of services are reported on separate lines of the VAT return.
Some lines are used for the purpose of the initial automated check under the ADIS system.
The values of supplies of goods to persons registered for tax in other Member States are compared with the data provided in the recapitulative statements submitted by Czech taxpayers.
The values of acquisitions of goods from other Member States from persons registered for tax in other Member States are compared with the values obtained through the VIES system from the recapitulative statements of taxpayers from other EU Member States.
A credibility test of VAT returns is carried out at the tax office under the ADIS system.
This test is carried out automatically, since without the test the VAT returns cannot be assessed.
The credibility test involves the calculation of the credibility criteria and the evaluation of the risk types of VAT returns.
According to the provisions of Section 37 (1) of Act No 337/1992, the tax office may repeatedly impose a fine of up to CZK 2,000,000 (EUR 67,150) on a person who fails to comply within the prescribed period with an obligation of a non-monetary nature arising from this or a special tax law or imposed by a decision under this law.
An automated tax information system, which is used by the tax offices to provide technical support to the tax administration.
The audit revealed that the tax authorities did not generally use the possibility to impose a fine on taxpayers for failing to file a VAT return.
Submission and processing of VAT returns in Germany
In Germany, we distinguish between a preliminary monthly or quarterly VAT return and an annual VAT return.
Those taxpayers who are required to submit preliminary VAT returns still have to submit an annual VAT return.
Even small entrepreneurs who are not required to pay VAT must submit an annual VAT return.
Generally, taxpayers are required to submit a quarterly VAT return by the 10th day of the month following the quarter in which the VAT is incurred (§18(2) UStG).
However, if the VAT liability exceeds EUR 6 136 in the previous calendar year, or if it is a newly established business, the relevant entrepreneur is required to submit a monthly VAT return by the 10th day of the following month.
The taxpayer may also decide to submit a monthly VAT return if a tax refund exceeding EUR 6 136 was made in the previous year (§18(2a) UStG).
VAT returns do not have to be submitted if the annual VAT amount does not exceed EUR 512.
The relevant amount of VAT liability must be paid by the 10th day of the month following the tax period in which the VAT was incurred.
The refund may lead to an even more detailed investigation by the Tax Office.
There are no time limits (according to the law) for processing tax returns and refunding excess VAT.
In order to obtain a timely refund, it is possible to offer security for the amount to be refunded.
The basic principle is to prepare VAT returns and return the tax quickly.
The German VAT Act provides for the possibility of extending this time limit (section 18(6) of the UStG).
Such an extension must be requested separately.
It allows the VAT return to be submitted and the relevant VAT liability to be paid a month later, provided that a special advance is paid in the case of the monthly VAT return.
This advance payment will be offset against the December VAT liability.
Whenever an error is detected, the trader must file a corrected VAT return.
There is no additional VAT return.
Once the annual VAT return, which must be submitted by 31 May of the following calendar year, is registered at the tax office, the entrepreneur cannot correct the incorrect preliminary VAT return, but only the annual VAT return.
The correction of the annual VAT return to the benefit or disadvantage of the payer is possible during the next 4 years after the year in which the first annual VAT return was filed.
After these four years, the annual VAT return can normally be corrected only in cases of tax fraud or evasion.
The payers are obliged to submit preliminary VAT returns electronically.
The tax authorities may apply exceptions to this rule to avoid excessive hardship.
The submission of the annual VAT return is possible in paper form or via the Internet, either with or without certification.
If it is made without certification, the payer must submit the return once more on paper with personal signatures.
In case the payer fails to submit the VAT return, the tax administration is entitled to make a rough estimate of the taxpayer's turnover.
In case of late submission, a penalty payment (a maximum of 10% of the tax to be paid or EUR 25,000) may be imposed on the payer.
During the previous inspection, the BRH found that the tax authorities often do not assess this standard penalty.
In other cases where the tax authorities have imposed a penalty, the amount has been assessed inconsistently and arbitrarily.
The standard penalty therefore fails to meet its objective of shortening the average delay, especially when filing the annual VAT return.
The VAT return contains separate lines relating to the values of intra-community supplies/acquisitions of goods.
The values of acquisitions of services are reported on separate lines of the VAT return.
Non-taxable transactions must be reported on a separate line of the VAT return.
In the case of VAT returns that are submitted in paper form, a copy must be made either via a scanner or by staff specifically authorised to do so.
Data from the VAT returns submitted electronically is immediately available to the tax office staff.
Once all the data are entered into the system, the RMS staff goes through them and makes a selection of cases that meet certain criteria.
Selected VAT returns must be rechecked by the tax office staff on the basis of a control report prepared by the system.
(see section 5.2).
Although the tax administration has to make a rough estimate of the amount of VAT that the taxpayer has to pay, the estimated tax must be as accurate as possible.
Comparison and evaluation
In the Czech Republic, taxpayers submit VAT returns within 25 days of the end of the tax period.
The tax period is either a calendar quarter or a calendar month, depending on the amount of the payer's turnover.
In Germany, taxpayers file their preliminary VAT returns, depending on their tax liability in the previous year, either within 10 days of the end of the calendar quarter or the month.
By 31 May of the following year, payers are obliged to file their annual tax returns.
The obligation to file their annual VAT returns has its pros and cons:
+ at the end of the calendar year, the payer is able to correct errors in the (monthly preliminary) tax returns by filing a single annual VAT return;
– if the payer corrects the declared intra-community transactions, the correction cannot be related to the period for which the recapitulative report is filed;
– federal states usually do not compare VIES data on intra-community acquisitions of German payers before the annual VAT return is processed.
According to the registration (see section 4.1.3), German payers are obliged to file their annual VAT returns independently of their turnover.
This obligation allows the German tax authority to verify the maximum turnover limit for small businesses.
In addition, the responsible tax office is able to compare the annual VAT returns with the direct tax returns and with the final accounts.
In the Czech Republic, tax authorities are able to determine the amount of the payer's turnover only from the submitted income tax returns.
Unlike in the Czech Republic, taxpayers in Germany are obliged to submit VAT returns in electronic form.
The introduction of an obligation to submit tax returns electronically in the Czech Republic would contribute to increasing the efficiency of the Czech tax administration.
Summary reports
Submission and processing of summary reports in the Czech Republic
The summary report (hereinafter referred to as "SH") is submitted pursuant to the provisions of Section 102 of Act No 235/2004 Coll. by a payer who has made a supply of goods to another Member State to a person registered for tax in another Member State.
Data on the value of the goods supplied are always presented in Czech currency, broken down by individual tax subjects, indicating their VAT ID under which they are registered in their country.
Data on services provided are not included in the SH.
The SH is submitted by payers with monthly and quarterly tax periods for each calendar quarter within 25 days after the end of the calendar quarter to the locally competent tax authority.
Correction of erroneous data is carried out in the subsequent SH within 15 days from the date of detection of errors.
The erroneous data stated in the SH are always replaced by the data stated in the subsequent SH.
In the same way as tax returns, payers can file the SH in electronic form.
In case the payer does not file the SH or the subsequent SH and should have filed it according to Act No.235/2004 Coll., the tax administrator will invite him to file it and at the same time inform him about the consequences in case of non-filing of the SH or the subsequent SH, i.e. that the tax administrator is entitled to repeatedly impose a fine of up to CZK 2,000,000 (EUR 67,150) for non-pecuniary failures.
The audit of the SAO found that the tax authorities did not usually use the possibility to impose a fine on payers for non-compliance with their legal obligations.
In particular, in the case of filing the SH, tax subjects are not sufficiently motivated to comply with their obligations, because the non-filing of the SH does not affect the VAT tax liability.
The tax administrator is obliged under Section 102(5) of Act No. 235/2004 Coll. to verify the data in the SH, or in the subsequent SH, to remove any ambiguities and to use the data for determining the tax liability.
In case of non-compliance of the data in the SH and the data in the relevant (payer with a monthly tax period) or the relevant (payer with a quarterly tax period) VAT return, the tax administrator should verify the correctness of the declared tax liability stated in the VAT return.
The tax entity removes the erroneous data in the SH by filing the subsequent SH itself, or it may be requested to do so.
The tax administrator corrects the data on the delivery of goods to other Member States in the ADIS system in case:
– the payer does not prove the data stated in the SH (or the subsequent SH) and corrects them by filing the subsequent SH,
– the tax administrator proves that the data stated by the payer in the SH or the subsequent SH are not true.
The tax administrator, by inserting a correction without filing a subsequent SH by the payer, does not replace the submission of the tax entity, only modifies the data in the VIES database so that they are up-to-date, complete and accurate.
The data from the SH are sent to the respective Member States.
It can be sent and received only by a national financial administration authority designated for cooperation with other Member States in the field of VAT; this is the CLO (in the Czech Republic this function is fulfilled by the Ministry of Finance, Department of International Cooperation in the Administration of VAT (CLO).
The O_MCTL is an automatic message that the CLO receives from other Member States.
It contains all the erroneous VAT IDs listed in the dispatched lines of the SH.
If the erroneous VAT ID is used in any of the transmitted normal lines of the SH or a subsequent SH, an entry is made in the table of erroneous VAT IDs.
The table contains the so-called "Doubt Notice on the VAT ID".
The tax administrator checks the data and records the result of the verification in the system.
When acquiring goods from another Member State, the payer is obliged to declare the VAT and indicate the acquisition values on separate lines of the VAT return.
Selected cases of irregularities in the value of the acquired goods declared by the Czech payer in his VAT return and in the value of the delivered goods as declared by the payers from other Member States in their SH are sent from the Customs Office to the tax office for verification.
The tax administrators are obliged to investigate the irregularities.
Three situations can occur:
a) The value declared by the Czech payer in the relevant lines of the VAT return is lower than the value of the delivery declared by the EU payers.
In this case, the tax administrator checks the accuracy of the data.
b) The amount of the difference is 0.
This situation can occur either by changing the data in the EU (the foreign supplier corrects his SH) or by changing the data in the VAT return (the Czech tax entity itself files an additional VAT return in the meantime).
In this case, it is up to the tax administrator to verify the accuracy of the data in the VAT return despite this fact.
c) The value of acquisitions of goods from other Member States, which the Czech taxpayer stated in the relevant rows of the VAT return, is higher than the value of supplied goods declared to the EU taxpayer.
Here too, it is at the discretion of the administration whether it will verify the accuracy of the data.
After verifying the difference and explaining the causes of its occurrence, the tax administration will enter the result of the verification in the ADIS.
The results of the verification are transmitted back to the CLO.
The numbers of cases sent from the CLO to the tax authorities for verification for each quarter of 2005 are shown in Chart 1 (NB: source: MF).
The above chart 1 shows that the number of cases transmitted from the CLO to the tax authorities for each quarter of 2005 was decreasing.
The number significantly decreased for the fourth quarter of 2005. The CLO increased the minimum financial limit, including with regard to the possibility of sending requests for information to other EU Member States.
The discrepancy between the data from the VAT returns and the data from the EU may not always be caused by an error on the part of the domestic taxpayer.
It may also be an error on the part of EU payers or an error due to the fact that in individual EU Member States certain types of transactions may be reported in the SH in a different way.
The most common reasons for discrepancies in the values of reported transactions found at audited financial offices are shown in Table 1.
Submission and processing of recapitulative statements in Germany
Entrepreneurs who make intra-Community deliveries from Germany to other EU Member States or are involved in triangular transactions are obliged to submit quarterly SHs listing intra-Community deliveries by recipients (Section 18a(1) UStG).
The SH must be submitted by the 10th day of the month following the relevant calendar quarter.
If an extension of this deadline is allowed in the case of preliminary VAT returns, this also applies to the SH.
The SH must be delivered to the CLO.
From 1 January 2007, they must be submitted electronically.
Exceptions may be granted by the competent tax authorities to certain taxpayers in order to avoid undue hardship.
In cases where taxpayers realise that the SH contains incorrect data, they are required to submit a corrective report within one month.
In the event that taxpayers fail to submit the SH, the CLO will initiate proceedings to compel the submission of this report.
This procedure includes: – a first reminder – a second reminder linked to the threat of a fine/periodic penalty payment, and – the assessment of periodic penalty payments.
Although the German Tax Code allows fines of up to EUR 25 000 to be imposed (Section 329 AO), the CLO assesses fines in three steps, in the amounts of EUR 125, 250 and 500.
In addition, Paragraph 26a(1) No 5 UStG provides that payers act unlawfully if they intentionally or negligently fail to file the SH properly, file it incomplete, file it on time or if they fail to correct or correct the SH at all.
This offence can be punished by a fine of up to EUR 5 000.
Data on intra-Community deliveries cannot be entered into VIES by the tax office, as the processing of the SH is the sole task of the CLO.
The SH data are only stored in the CLO system.
The SH data are therefore only visually available to the tax office after they have been processed into the CLO.
The deadlines for the processing of the SH are laid down in Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003.
Data from the SH must be stored within three months following the calendar quarter in question.
If incorrect VAT IDs are entered in the SH of German payers, the CLO receives O_MCTL codes from another Member State.
The CLO contacts a particular trader and asks him for the correct data.
If the CLO fails to obtain the correct information, the case is forwarded to the relevant tax offices.
It is then up to these tax offices to request the correct data.
During the inspection, the BRH found that most traders had corrected the VAT ID at the request of the CLO.
However, the challenge, the threat and the imposition of three additional fines take up too much time in cases where the payer may be involved in cross-border carousel fraud.
These cases, which were eventually reported to the relevant tax authorities, were usually completed within one or two months.
The tax authority rejected the exemption of declared intra-community supplies in 73% of these cases.
When the payer provided the correct VAT ID, the tax authority asked him to submit the corrected SH to the CLO, as the tax authorities cannot correct the VIES data themselves.
The BRH found that neither the tax authorities nor the CLO checked the filing of the corrected SH, so often the payers did not comply with the request.
Due to the fact that the CLO does not have access to the VAT return data, a comparison of the delivery data declared in the VAT return and in the SH does not take place before the submission of these data to the CLO of the other Member States.
This control can only be carried out by the tax authorities and is usually applied when preparing the VAT control.
Data obtained from other Member States are processed into the CLO.
Incorrect VAT IDs are selected and then submitted to the relevant Member States.
These data are used for the purpose of the control of acquisition by the tax authorities.
Once entered into the system, the CLO checks them on the basis of a comparison with data from previous calendar quarters.
In case they meet certain criteria (see 5.2), the control information is created and sent to the respective tax authorities.
This procedure is applied on a permanent basis, while the compilation of data on the acquisition of goods or services for all VAT payers is created later and submitted to the tax authorities.
The RMS installed for the purpose of the assessment procedure subsequently checks these data with data on intra-community acquisitions.
This system completely covers those entrepreneurs who do not have a full right to deduct VAT.
Comparison and evaluation
In the Czech Republic, payers who have made a supply of goods to another Member State to a person registered for tax in another Member State submit the SH within 25 days after the end of the calendar quarter to the locally competent tax authority.
The tax authorities process the SH and transmit the data to the CLO.
The values of the supply of goods to another Member State, indicated by the payers in the SH, are compared at the tax authorities with the values of the supply of goods to another Member State, indicated by these payers in their VAT returns.
The results of the comparison are used in the assessment procedure.
In Germany, payers who have made intra-Community supplies are obliged to submit the SH quarterly by the 10th day of the following calendar quarter.
The SH is submitted by the payers to the CLO, since 1 January 2007 in electronic form.
The tax authorities have the information from the SH only after it has been processed into the CLO.
The payers from both the Czech Republic and Germany list only the supply of goods in the SH, the provision of services is not mentioned in the SH.
Unlike the Czech tax authorities, the German tax authorities are not able to correct the wrong lines submitted by the SH themselves.
As a result of this limited access to the German VIES data, the wrong VAT ID was not corrected, even though the payer provided the correct VAT ID to the FÚ.
The German tax administration does not compare the data on intra-Community supplies that are included in the VAT return of the German payer and his SH.
Differences between the data of these two statements are usually not detected before the German CLO provides the data from VIES to other Member States.
Given the BRH's findings, it is clear that a comparison would increase the reliability of the transmitted data in VIES.
Data on supplies of goods to Czech payers, delivered from other Member States, are compared in the Czech Republic with the data on acquisitions of goods from other Member States declared by the Czech payers in their VAT returns.
The comparison is carried out by the CLO separately for each calendar quarter.
The most significant cases of irregularities are transmitted to the tax authorities as a warning of possible errors in the tax returns of payers.
Unlike the Czech tax administration, the German tax administration does not usually check the taxation of intra-Community acquisitions.
Such a general check is processed only for payers who do not have a full right to deduct VAT.
In addition, the German tax administration only checks the taxation of intra-community acquisitions of other taxpayers if the RMS produces a control notice or if the payer is designated for the check anyway.
This procedure relieves the tax authorities from having to clarify the reasons for each difference.
On the other hand, the detection of VAT fraud depends on the quality of the RMS.
Combating carousel fraud requires continuously updated information on intra-community acquisitions as soon as possible.
The current SH system, specifically VIES, provides financial authorities with information that can be up to six months old.
This delay can be reduced by up to four months if payers file the SH monthly.
Monthly filing would not be a significant increase in bureaucratic costs as most payers in the Czech Republic and Germany are required to file VAT tax returns monthly – and the SH does not require any additional information compared to the tax return.
To avoid bureaucratic costs, filing the SH monthly may be associated with filing a VAT tax return.
However, the obligation to file the SH on a monthly basis would cause more time mismatches between the reporting of intra-Community delivery and intra-Community acquisition and could increase the flow of data between the various CLOs.
The German federal government considered the general provision of the monthly SH in 2006.
Its implementation failed due to doubts of the federal states.
They feared that the monthly submission of data from VIES to the CLOs of other Member States could lead to misunderstandings and confusion.
In fact, if the monthly reporting obligation of the SH and the monthly data transmission were to be effective, the monthly update of the VIES system would require a European monthly SH standard.
Statistical data on delivery and acquisition of goods between the Czech Republic and Germany
In the context of foreign trade, the SRN represents the most important trading partner for the Czech Republic.
The total volumes of intra-Community transactions in goods, carried out between the Czech Republic and Germany, are shown in Table 2.
Both SAIs requested data on the number of erroneous TINs or VAT IDs contained in the O_MCTL reports transmitted between the Czech Republic and Germany for each quarter of the audited period.
These data are contained in the following tables.
The data show substantial differences.
The reason for these differences may be a different basis for determining the number of O_MCTL reports.
While the Czech CLO refers their numbers to the calendar quarter for which the SH was submitted, the German CLO refers their numbers to the calendar quarter in which the O_MCTL report was received.
International exchange of information level 3
Implementation of the international exchange of information in the Czech Republic
The international exchange of information allows tax administrators to obtain information from other Member States concerning intra-Community commercial transactions and the payers who carried out these transactions.
Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003, on administrative cooperation in the field of value added tax and repealing Regulation (EEC) No 218/92, distinguishes between two basic categories of information exchange, namely the exchange of information upon request and the exchange of information without prior request.
The international exchange of information upon request takes the form of so-called requests for information (hereinafter referred to as "RUs"), using the SCAC standardized forms.
Tax authorities from the Czech Republic send their RUs or replies to the received RUs through the Financial Directorates to the Customs Office, which ensures the translation of the information provided on the SCAC standardized forms into a foreign language and their dispatch to other Member States.
The Customs Office also ensures the receipt of RUs from other Member States and replies to the dispatched RUs, their translation into Czech and their distribution to the locally competent tax authorities for processing.
Article 8 of Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 sets the maximum time limit for processing RUs at 3 months from the receipt of the request.
The SAO audited all the RUs submitted during the audited period between the Czech Republic and Germany.
Out of the total number of 94 RUs received in the Czech Republic from Germany, 70 cases (i.e. 74.5%) were processed within the stipulated three-month time limit, another 23 cases (i.e. 24.5%) were processed after this time limit and for the remaining 1 case no reply was sent to Germany by the time of the SAO audit.
Chart 2 contains more detailed information on the time limits within which replies to RUs received from Germany were sent from the Czech Republic.
Out of the total number of 335 RUs sent from the Czech Republic to Germany, 136 cases (i.e. 40.6%) received a reply within the stipulated three-month time limit, another 179 (i.e. 53.4%) received a reply after this time limit and 19 cases (i.e. 5.7%) did not receive a reply from Germany by the time of the SAO audit (in the remaining 1 case it was not possible to determine when the reply from Germany was received from Germany from the submitted data).
Chart 3 contains more detailed information on the time limits within which replies to RUs sent to Germany were received to the Czech Republic.
Figure 4 provides a percentage of the values of intra-community transactions reported in the RU transmitted between the Czech Republic and Germany.
As can be seen from the above chart, the value of commercial transactions examined through the RU was most often in the range above EUR 60 000.
International exchange of information without prior request takes place either in the form of automatic or structured automatic exchange of information or in the form of spontaneous exchange of information.
Tax administrators from other Member States are often forwarded information that may be relevant for them in the administration of VAT without prior request.
In the Czech Republic, all information is collected at the Customs Office.
Information is transmitted electronically between individual Member States.
"Automatic exchange" means the systematic communication of predetermined information to other Member States without prior request and at predetermined regular intervals, according to Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003.
"Structured automatic exchange" means the systematic communication of predetermined information to other Member States, without prior request and as soon as the information is available.
