The Czech Republic provides other Member States with information on the delivery of new means of transport in the form of automatic exchange.
This information is available to the tax authorities from the form Reporting on the delivery of a new means of transport pursuant to Section 19 of Act No 235/2004 Coll. and from a copy of the issued tax document.
The tax authorities fill in the necessary data in a specially created template during the processing of the aforementioned form and transmit it by return to a contact person at the Financial Directorate where the data are collected and within a specified period, i.e. no later than two months from the end of the quarter in which the information was available, transmitted to the CLO for subsequent processing and transmission to other Member States.
Furthermore, the Czech Republic provides other Member States with information on mail order sales which are exempt from VAT in the Member State of origin, information on intra-EU transactions which appear to be unauthorised and information on potential missing traders.
The information is sent to other Member States in the form of spontaneous exchange using the SCAC form.
Implementing the international exchange of information in Germany
In Germany, both requests for information and the processing of spontaneous information are initiated by the locally competent tax authority.
The tax authorities send the completed SCAC 2004 form by email directly to the German CLO, which forwards the SCAC forms to foreign CLOs.
The tax authorities have been instructed to write their requests for information or their own spontaneous information only in German; even the SCAC form used is not multilingual.
Half of the German requests for information, controlled by the BRH, have been sent in order to ensure that intra-Community acquisitions are taxed in another Member State, or to prove that intra-Community supplies from Germany to another Member State are exempt from tax.
If the German CLO receives a request for information from another Member State, it will check the value of the supplies of goods or services specified in the request for a minimum threshold of EUR 15 000.
If there is no reasonable reason for this request, the German CLO will reject any request containing an amount below this threshold.
In addition, the German CLO translates the free texts of the SCAC form [(B1-17) or (E)] if these texts are not in German or English.
To answer the request for information, the CLO sends the request to the relevant tax authority, referring to the three-month deadline.
There are no further deadlines for processing requests at specific organisational levels of the tax administration.
Although the German CLO has the technical conditions to monitor past deadlines, it lacks sufficient staffing capacities to alert the tax authorities to answering blank requests for information.
The tax authorities obtain the necessary information by sending a letter to the taxpayer or by carrying out an audit.
Auditors usually choose between two different types of audit: a special VAT audit, which covers any taxable process over a period of several months, or a so-called VAT inspection, which can only cover a single business transaction that has been carried out recently.
This short and ﬂexible type of audit requires no notification to the taxpayer and has proven its usefulness in investigating individual taxable business transactions.
In an automatic exchange without prior request, the FRG provides other Member States with information – on VAT IDs allocated to payers who are resident in other Member States, – on the refund of input tax to payers who are resident in other Member States.
In addition, the FRG has undertaken to provide other Member States with the following information through a structured automatic exchange:
a. Supply of new means of transport to entrepreneurs without using their VAT ID, b. dispatch or catalogue sale in other Member States which is not taxable in the FRG, c. significant differences between intra-Community acquisitions declared by the payer and VIES data provided by other Member States, d. intra-Community delivery of goods which the German payer did not declare in the SH because it treated the supplies as domestic transactions, e. potential "missing trader" who carried out intra-Community transactions independently of the validity of their VAT ID, f. entrepreneurs who supplied goods to potential "missing traders" or to those recipients who misused their VAT ID.
Comparison and evaluation
The dispatch of the RU or spontaneous information is initiated by the local tax authorities both in the Czech Republic and in the FRG, who send the completed SCAC form to the CLO.
While the Czech CLO uses the bilingual SCAC form (Czech – English) and translates the sent information into English or German, the German tax authorities follow the instruction to write RUs or spontaneous information only in German on the monolingual form.
The German CLO does not provide for the translation of German texts.
Examination of RUs submitted between 1.5.2004 and 31.12.2005 between the Czech Republic and Germany revealed that the Czech tax administration handled 74.5% of received applications within the three-month deadline, while RUs sent to Germany were handled by the German tax administration within the three-month deadline in only 40.6% of cases.
Although the German CLO alerts the tax authorities to the three-month deadline, it does not keep track of the elapsed time limits.
The result of the missing alerts is a large number of delayed replies to the RUs.
Because of these problems, the BRH recommended regular alerts to the CLO.
The situation has already improved.
According to the latest information, the German CLO now alerts the tax authorities to replies to the incomplete replies to the CLO.
VAT risk management
Risk management in the Czech Republic
In the Czech Republic, VAT risk management is dealt with by several departments at various organisational levels of the tax administration.
Within the Ministry of Finance, the following departments deal with the issues of risk management and the fight against VAT fraud:
The Methodology and VAT performance department and within it the VAT risk management department, which, among other things, manages the selection of risks of possible tax evasion and evaluates the trends of these risks at both the domestic and Community level.
It coordinates the functioning of the role of the Trust of VAT tax returns and the use of data from the VIES system nationwide in terms of the risks of tax evasion in the framework of intra-community transactions.
Based on data from the trade balance, the Czech Republic evaluates risky commodities, processes the conceptual VAT risk management and cooperates in this area with the relevant EU institutions and with other Member States.
The Department of International Cooperation in the Administration of VAT, which inter alia ensures the exchange of information in the field of VAT, participates in the creation and maintenance of information databases, analyses data from other Member States contained in the VIES system, provides information to the public and ensures other forms of international cooperation within the meaning of Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003.
Both SAIs requested data on the number of erroneous VAT IDs or VAT IDs contained in the O_MCTL reports transmitted between the Czech Republic and Germany for each quarter of the audited period.
These data are contained in the following tables.
The data show substantial differences.
The reason for these differences may be the different basis for determining the number of O_MCTL reports.
While the Czech CLO refers their numbers to the calendar quarter for which the SH was submitted, the German CLO refers their numbers to the calendar quarter in which the O_MCTL report was received.
The Tax Control and Search Methodology department, which, among other things, carries out risk analysis in the framework of the methodological management of tax controls and, in accordance with risk analysis, sets priorities for the targeting of tax controls in the plans of the financial directorates, processes risk analyses in the framework of the reduction of tax evasion, including the gathering of knowledge gained from the administration of taxes as well as from other sources, and proposes measures to reduce tax evasion.
Search departments are established in the financial directorates, which carry out, among other things, searches of tax entities and areas that are risky in terms of occurrence of tax fraud (e.g. internet shops, gold, pharmaceutical industry), searches of unregistered tax entities in terms of risks of tax evasion (e.g. in the field of internet services, job placement, radio and press services, etc.), analysis of links of chain fraud and transmission of information to the territorial financial authorities.
Specialised control departments are established in the selected 12 financial offices.
They have regional competence and carry out tax controls outside the territorial competence of the tax offices on the basis of mandates.
The need to set up specialised tax control units has emerged from the increasing findings of new and improved forms of tax evasion, which are mainly found in entities linked to chains.
These units focus on checking tax entities according to the requirements of search departments, tax entities with specific activities and multinational companies and tax entities with a large scale of activity in terms of turnover.
The following mechanisms have been integrated into the ADIS system to limit VAT risks: – role Credibility of VAT tax returns, used to evaluate the risk of tax returns submitted; – role Selection of tax entities for inspection, allowing the selection of the payer for inspection on the basis of selected criteria; – role of VIES, through which tax administrators have access to data provided from other EU Member States.
The role of VIES allows, among other things: – to check the validity of VAT IDs of payers from other Member States; – to obtain from other Member States the values of goods supplied to the Czech payer, declared in SH by all its suppliers from other Member States; – to generate a report of payers who did not submit SH; – to carry out a formal check of the data provided by payers from the Czech Republic in SH before sending these data to other Member States; – to generate a report of payers for whom the data on supplies of goods to other Member States stated in VAT returns do not match the data in SH; – to generate a report of payers for whom the value of acquisitions of goods from other Member States stated in VAT returns does not match the data declared in SH by all its suppliers from other Member States.
As part of their activity to limit the risk of tax evasion, tax authorities have access to registers of state government bodies such as the Commercial Register, the Real Estate Register, the Register of Motor Vehicles, the Register of Trade, etc.
More detailed information can be found in Chapter 4.4.1 Submission and processing of recapitulative statements in the Czech Republic.
Risk management in Germany
Due to the federal (federal) structure of Germany, the Federal Tax Administration (in particular the CLO) and the Tax Administrations of 16 federal states are involved in the development and operation of the RMS.
Although there are joint development working groups, neither the CLO nor the Tax Administrations of the federal states share a fully consistent database.
At the level of the CLO, the ST I 2 unit (hereinafter referred to as ‘KUSS’ – Coordination Unit for Special VAT Audits and Tax Investigations) collects audit findings concerning tax fraud in a special database called OPUS.
KUSS, in cooperation with the tax authorities, has introduced a new database called ZAUBER for the transfer of names of companies of tax fraudsters ‘missing traders’.
KUSS coordinates related cases of national and cross-border tax fraud.
The experience of KUSS is reflected in the development of the RMS in the working groups.
In addition, the specialists of several other CLO and MF departments are entrusted with the duties and powers associated with RMS.
At CLO level, a formal check of the composition of VAT IDs of other Member States in the SH filed by German payers is introduced.
This formal check is carried out before the data from the SH are provided to other Member States, to improve the clarity and use of the VIES data provided (see 4.4.2).
The verification of the validity of VAT IDs listed in the SH is carried out on the basis of O_MCTL codes provided by other Member States (for the procedure of correcting invalid VAT ID, see also 4.4.2).
In addition, the RMS on the CLO is based on VIES data transmitted by other Member States and creates several types of control reports based on several characteristics, which usually figure in so-called carousel trading operations, in order to identify potential ‘missing traders’.
The Federal Tax Authorities are instructed to process these control reports and, in some cases, to report on the results of their findings to the CLO.
The BRH audit findings confirmed that it is necessary to take into account all the available characteristics if a case of tax fraud is to be assumed with sufficient probability (instead of focusing solely on company turnover).
The BRH therefore suggested to the MF that different characteristics should be taken into account when processing the reports.
The RMS should also cover other elements, such as the payment behaviour (morality) of the taxpayer, the field (economic activities) or the shareholder structure.
The second level of the RMS is processed in the Federal Tax Administrations and focuses on the processing of VAT returns.
For example, the RMS generates a list of those payers who have declared intra-community supplies in their tax returns.
This list is sent to the CLO to monitor the full submission of the SH.
In addition, this type of RMS compares intra-community acquisitions reported in the payer's annual VAT return with data from the VIES system.
The tax administrations of the Länder try to avoid comparing quarterly data because this comparison would reveal too much disapproving data that is attributed to reasons other than tax evasion or tax fraud; for example:
– different execution times of the intra-community transaction in the opinion of the supplier on the one hand and the beneficiary on the other;
– different accounting for sales discounts and sales promotions (incentives) and their different reporting in the tax return.
In addition to comparing data from VAT returns and the VIES system, many Länder have introduced elements of the RMS that are based on data from VAT returns and some other elements (such as company name structure, shareholder age, number of employees and payment behaviour/morality of the taxpayer).
Bavaria has introduced a rule-based RMS which allows a team of tax fraud specialists (hereinafter risk managers) to programme their own rules for singling out potential tax fraud offenders.
This RMS is applied when the tax authorities process the monthly VAT returns.
The relevant tax authority therefore receives a recommendation made by the RMS before determining the VAT.
As this RMS is not able to reflect current findings in its activities, risk managers have to adjust the relevant rules based on feedback from the tax authorities.
The Mecklenburg-West Pomerania district has programmed an adaptive artificial neural network with data from tax files in which the inspection revealed tax evasion.
Based on this data, the RMS is able to identify the characteristics of tax evasion.
The RMS produces a monthly list of tax files suspected of tax evasion.
The relevant tax authorities use this list as a basis for deciding on the audit of proposed taxpayers.
After the audit, auditors have to report their findings so that the results of the list can be reflected in the RMS.
The administrative region of North Rhine-Westphalia uses an adaptive artificial neural network, which is combined with a rules-based fuzzy system.
Based on the large number of data of assessed VAT returns and some other facts, this neural-fuzzy system or data-mining system calculates the probability that a particular taxpayer has committed tax fraud.
It then compiles a monthly list of potential fraudsters.
The local tax authorities use this list as a basis for selecting the relevant taxpayers for the audit and report the findings of the audit to the data processing centre.
The implementation of any of these three RMS in the other Länder is still ongoing.
As none of these three RMS is based on the same approach, a combination of all systems seems to be useful for tackling tax fraud.
The question remains whether this system will lead to the expected results.
Comparison and evaluation
Although the specific criteria of RMS in the Czech Republic and Germany cannot be discussed in this report, the SAO and BRH found that each Member State has developed its own RMS.
As well as the different approaches in the three Länder of Germany, the RMS of each EU State has its strengths and weaknesses.
New trends and new models of cross-border VAT fraud are currently being discussed by the tax authorities of the EU Member States.
VAT fraud - especially carousel fraud - is not proving to be a national problem, but rather a European one.
Payers in fraudulent activities act simultaneously not only in one Member State, but in more than one.
An effective RMS cannot be developed by just one Member State.
Successful criteria, components and approaches of RMS must be exchanged and implemented in each EU Member State, otherwise fraudsters choose the Member State with the weakest RMS.
A VAT loss caused by fraud in the EU may not affect the Member State of the initiator of the fraud.
Any Member State that is involved in fraudulent activities may be affected.
Therefore, there should be a European exchange and discussion of RMS.
Selected audit findings during verification of commercial transactions
As part of the cooperation on the implementation of parallel audit actions, the SAO and BRH examined the quality and use of information on selected commercial transactions, which were the subject of an international exchange of information between the tax administrations of the Czech Republic and Germany.
Furthermore, the two audit institutions jointly examined the implementation of several commercial transactions, where there were doubts about their completion, or irregularities in the way the tax payers from both countries reported these commercial transactions in their VAT returns, respectively SH.
The SAO scrutinized a total of 8 cases, which related to commercial transactions between 8 Czech and 8 German tax entities, at BRH's request.
In addition, the SAO scrutinized in 43 cases, based on BRH's notification, the values of intra-community transactions with Germany, which the Czech payers reported in their tax returns and SH.
The BRH scrutinized a total of 23 cases, which related to commercial transactions between 23 German and 21 Czech tax entities, at the SAO's request.
Important information was exchanged on the basis of Council Regulation (EC) No. 1798/2003 through official communication with CLO.
Examination of the selected cases revealed, among other things, that the different way of registration in the EU member states leads to problems mentioned in chapter 4.1:
1.
According to the VIES data, the Czech payer should have purchased goods worth EUR 60,500 from the German payer in the third quarter of 2004.
As the Czech payer only reported the acquisition of goods worth EUR 29,869, the Czech tax administrator sent a request to the Federal Republic for verification of the value of the delivered goods.
In a reply to the RU received from Germany, the German side stated that the German payer had delivered goods worth EUR 27,381 to the Czech payer in the second quarter of 2004, EUR 31,997 in the third quarter and EUR 10,276 in the fourth quarter of 2004.
The reply also showed that the VAT ID of the German payer was valid only from 28 September 2004, but the German Customs in 2006 issued a VAT ID validity certificate retroactively from 1 May 2004 based on the additional request of the German payer for a VAT ID validity certificate.
The German payer made a correction to the SH.
The Czech payer based on this information was concerned with the acquisition of goods.
The SAO inquired with the local tax administrator in the Czech Republic and found that the Czech payer submitted additional VAT returns for individual tax periods of 2004, in which he increased the value of goods purchased from other Member States and at the same time exercised the right to deduct VAT on the acquisition of goods from other Member States.
However, from these additional VAT returns, the Czech tax authority could not clearly determine whether the values of supplies from the above-mentioned German supplier were included.
The BRH found out that the German supplier had been registered for VAT in September 2003, based on the SAO's request.
However, since he did not apply for a VAT ID when registering, he was allocated only an identification number for transactions within Germany.
Although it is usually not possible to allocate a VAT ID retroactively in Germany, in this case the German tax official in 2006 allocated a VAT ID retroactively as of 1 May 2004 to the above-mentioned German taxpayer.
The German Customs Office allocates a VAT ID retroactively if the German entrepreneur did not cause a delay in the allocation; for example, if the delay was caused by the Customs Office after the payer's application for a VAT ID.
In this case, the Customs Office allocates a VAT ID retroactively because the entrepreneur does not need his own valid VAT ID for intra-community supplies pursuant to Section 6 of the German VAT Act.
On the other hand, the German recipient does not need his supplier's valid VAT ID in order to declare intra-Community acquisitions.
Due to these different procedures between Member States, the German Customs Office allocated the VAT ID retroactively in this special case.
2.
The Czech tax administrator requested verification of the German payer's VAT registration as part of the international exchange of information.
The VIES indicated the date of registration as March 5, 2005, while the German payer's registration certificate issued by the competent German tax office indicated the date as October 1, 2004.
In the reply received from the German tax office, the German party stated that the German tax entity had been registered since October 1, 2004, but the VAT ID had not been provided to it in Germany until February 16, 2005, for organizational reasons.
The SAO, by enquiry with the local tax administrator, found that the Czech tax administrator had performed a VAT check on the Czech payer for the tax period from the 3rd quarter of 2004 to the 2nd quarter of 2005.
The audit revealed that the Czech taxpayer had included in the VAT return services worth CZK 9,897 (EUR 314) provided to the German taxpayer in the period before his VAT registration (i.e. before 1 October 2004).
For the tax period from the third quarter of 2004, the Tax Office assessed the taxpayer VAT amounting to CZK 1,880 (EUR 60).
The BRH found out, based on the SAO's request, that the German taxpayer had been allocated the VAT ID only on 16 February 2005 when it informed the Tax Office about its business, which it had started in 2004.
In addition, the Tax Office registered him for VAT retrospectively as of 1 October 200415 in order to monitor the submission of the annual VAT return for 2004.
In this tax return, the payer reported intra-community acquisition from the Czech Republic amounting to EUR 160 (approx. CZK 5,000).
3. The Czech taxpayer reported in the VAT return for September 2004 and in the SH for the third quarter of 2004 the delivery of goods amounting to CZK 114,615 (EUR 3,642) to the German taxpayer.
When verifying the registration of the German payer in the VIES system, the Czech tax administrator found that its registration was valid from 11 November 2004, i.e. only after the delivery of goods by the Czech payer to Germany.
The Czech payer submitted an additional VAT DAP, in which it declared the tax base of the effected transactions in the Czech Republic worth CZK 114,615 (EUR 3,642) and VAT in the amount of CZK 21,777 (EUR 692), which it paid.
The SAO found that the Czech payer subsequently filed an application for a renewal of the proceedings concerning the additional VAT return and as evidence submitted a confirmation by the German tax administration that the German payer had been taxed since 1 January 2000.
Therefore, the Czech tax administrator verified the validity of the registration of the German payer in the framework of the international exchange of information.
The reply received from the German tax administration showed that the German payer was allocated a VAT ID only on 11 November 2004, i.e. after the date of the delivery of goods.
For this reason, the tax administrator in the Czech Republic rejected the application for a renewal of the proceedings.
BRH found that the case did not involve an intra-Community acquisition of the goods, as the German payer only obtained a VAT ID on 11 November 2004.
However, the German payee declared the acquisition as an intra-Community acquisition and declared the VAT on this acquisition when he requested the refund of the input tax in the same amount.
However, since there would have been no changes in the value of the VAT that the German payer was obliged to pay, the tax administrator in Germany did not correct the data in his VAT return.
BRH also found that the name of the German payer, mentioned in the RU, was changed during the processing of the reply in Germany, resulting in confusion between two German tax entities.
This change in the name of the German payer also confused the Czech tax administrator.
4.
In the framework of the international exchange of information, the German tax administrator verified the acquisition of the goods by the Czech payer in the 1st quarter of 2005 in the value of EUR 22 686 from the German payer.
The SAO inquired with the locally competent tax administrator in the Czech Republic and found that the administrator had carried out a local investigation with the Czech payer, during which he verified that the delivery of goods had taken place and the Czech payer had accounted for and paid the invoice for the goods in question.
The Czech payer did not declare the acquisition of goods in the VAT return, because the German supplier did not state his VAT ID on the tax document, but only the tax number designated for domestic transactions in Germany.
In the VIES application, the Czech tax administrator found that the German payer had been registered for VAT for intra-community transactions only from 21.4.2005, i.e. after the delivery to the Czech payer.
At the same time, the Czech tax administrator asked the German tax administration to send a copy of the German payer's registration certificate, so that he could take steps to assess the tax if necessary.
The Czech tax office assessed the commercial transaction as the acquisition of goods from a non-payer in Germany, and therefore did not subsequently charge the Czech payer the tax on the commercial transaction.
The BRH found that under German law, a payer who supplies goods to other Member States does not need to have a VAT ID in order for the intra-Community supply of goods to be exempt from VAT.
The supplier only needs to have a VAT ID of the purchaser from another Member State and must be able to prove that the goods have been transported to another Member State.
According to the German VAT law, the transaction was therefore an intra-Community transaction and VAT should be charged in the Czech Republic.
In any case, it is important that the Czech tax administrator noticed the transaction because the delivery of the machine at the specified value was not the German supplier's core business.
As described in chapter 4.6.2, the German CLO refuses to answer the RUs, which relate to intra-Community transactions with a value of less than EUR 15 000: 5.
According to VIES data, the Czech payer should have purchased goods worth EUR 12 561 from the German payer in the third quarter of 2004.
The Czech tax administrator carried out a tax check on the tax entity for this tax period.
As part of the international administrative cooperation, it asked the German tax administration to verify the delivery of these goods using the SCAC form.
The Czech payer denied the acquisition of the goods, claiming that he had never traded with the German company and that the acquisition of these goods had not been accounted for in his accounts.
The German tax administration rejected the request to provide evidence – contracts, orders, invoices and transport documents, on the grounds that the turnover did not exceed EUR 15 000 and no other explanatory reasons were given.
As the Czech tax administration did not obtain evidence to assess the tax on the acquired goods, it terminated the tax audit without a finding and the tax liability remained assessed at the original amount.
BRH, based on the request of the SAO, found that the German payer acted as a so-called "fiscal representative" (§ 22 a – e UStG).
The German payer declared the mentioned supplies in its annual VAT return and in the SH.
He was entitled to the exemption of the supply.
Based on the BRH's warning, the German tax office sends to the Czech Republic the documents needed for the assessment of the tax on the acquired goods in the Czech Republic.
As stated in chapter 4.6.1, the replies to the RU sent from Germany to the Czech Republic exceeded the stipulated three-month deadline more often than the replies from the Czech Republic to Germany: 6.
The SAO found that the Czech tax administration sent a request for information to Germany on 5 October 2005 concerning the verification of the value of the delivered goods for the 4th quarter of 2004.
The German payer declared in the SH for this period the delivery of goods to the Czech payer amounting to EUR 86 307, but the Czech payer stated in the same period in the VAT return the acquisition of goods only amounting to EUR 35 314.
In the reply to the RU, delivered to the Czech Republic on 9 May 2006, i.e. after the expiry of the deadline for the processing stipulated in Article 8 of Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003, the German side stated that the request could not be processed as the German company's operations were terminated at the end of 2005.
As the German tax administration did not comply with the deadline for processing the RU, the Czech tax administration did not have the necessary documents for the tax proceedings in the Czech Republic.
7. In 2005, the Czech tax administration applied through the SCAC form for the verification of the deliveries of cars worth EUR 1 265 554 to the German tax payer, made in the 3rd and 4th quarters of 2004, which showed signs of carousel fraud.
The SAO found that no reply to the RU had been received from the Federal Republic of Germany by the time of the verification.
The SAO also found that the Czech tax payer had not included in the VAT return the deliveries of new means of transport for the German tax payer in the amount of CZK 11 816 103 (EUR 375 472).
The Czech tax administration corrected the data in the tax return and the Czech tax entity submitted the subsequent SH.
Based on the request of the SAO, the BRH found that the German customs office had not transmitted the aforementioned RU to the local tax office for verification due to technical reasons.
After the BRH was notified, an inspection was carried out at the German acquirer in Germany, during which it was found that the acquisition of all cars had been properly taxed and that the respective cars had been sold to another payer in Germany.
8. According to the VIES data, the Czech payer should have purchased a passenger car worth EUR 48,500 from the German payer in the fourth quarter of 2004.
The acquisition of these goods was not declared by the Czech payer.
When questioned by the locally competent tax administrator in the Czech Republic, the SAO found that the Czech payer had not filed VAT returns since August 2004.
The tax returns were not filed by the Czech payer even after the requests of the tax administrator, so on 23 May 2005 the tax office charged him VAT amounting to CZK 0 for the period October to December 2004.
On 2 June 2005 the Customs Office pointed out the aforementioned delivery from the German payer.
As the Czech payer did not cooperate with the tax administrator, the tax administrator sent the ŽOI to Germany regarding the aforementioned delivery.
As the response to the RU was not received in the Czech Republic until 7 February 2007, it was not known how the Czech tax administrator used the information obtained from the international exchange until the completion of the audit by the SAO.
The tax office cancelled the VAT registration of the Czech payer as of 23 August 2005 due to the failure to comply with the obligations arising from the VAT Act.
In some cases, only a partial reply was sent to the RU because the audit performed by the tax authorities on the payers was not completed at the time of the audit by the SAO and the BRH:
9.
In 2005, the Czech tax administrator applied through the SCAC form for the verification of the delivery of a car worth EUR 16,991 to the German payer, made in the third quarter of 2004, which showed signs of carousel fraud.
In the reply to the RU, the German tax administrator stated that he only had the invoice issued by the Czech payer for the delivery worth EUR 16,335.
The BRH, based on the request of the SAO, found that the audit performed by the German tax office at the acquirer from Germany had not yet been completed.
The German acquirer declared the acquisition of goods worth EUR 16 335 twice, in the tax returns for the months of August and September 2004.
10. The Czech tax administrator requested in 2005, through the SCAC form, the verification of the delivery of cars to the German payer worth EUR 198 167, carried out in the 4th quarter of 2004 and the 1st quarter of 2005, which showed signs of carousel fraud.
The German tax administration sent to the Czech Republic a partial reply to the IRS, in which it confirmed the acquisition of some cars by the German payer and further stated that the investigation in Germany had not been completed.
THISsegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
The SAO found that the locally competent tax office carried out several local investigations at the Czech supplier in order to verify the drawdown of excess VAT deductions, during which it did not detect their unjustified drawdown.
The BRH found that the German payer had declared in its VAT returns the acquisition of goods from other Member States for a total value of EUR 579 114 and that the control carried out by the German tax office at the acquirer from Germany had not been completed yet.
In chapter 4.4.1, the reasons for the differences between the values of the intra-Community acquisition of goods declared by the recipient in the tax return and the values stated by the supplier in its SH are described.
The audited cases showed that the most common reasons for the differences were not the time difference or the incorrect value of the intra-Community delivery of goods in the SH:
11.
The Czech payer should have purchased goods from the German payer for a value of EUR 35 716 in the first quarter of 2005 according to the VIES system, but the Czech payer did not declare this acquisition.
As the Czech payer did not cooperate with the tax administrator and did not carry out any activities at the company's registered office, the Czech tax administrator requested to verify how the German payer communicated with the Czech payer in the framework of the international exchange of information.
The response to the RU received from Germany revealed that according to the findings of the German tax administration, the Czech tax entity was unknown at the address communicated and that the goods had been taken over by the contracted carrier.
The order was for a total amount of EUR 155 000, but the German payer only delivered goods worth EUR 21 659.
The Czech payer sent the German payer a false confirmation of payment of EUR 155 153 in favour of the German payer.
After discovering fraudulent behaviour on the part of the Czech purchaser, the German payer, with the help of his other Czech customers, managed to recover the supplied material, with the exception of one item worth EUR 7 916.
The SAO inquired at the locally competent tax office in the Czech Republic and found that, based on the information obtained, the tax administrator assessed the Czech payer for VAT on the acquisition of goods from other Member States in the amount of CZK 388 522 (EUR 13 044).
Based on the request of the SAO, BRH confirmed that the German supplier declared the delivery of goods to the Czech payer after repairs only in the amount of EUR 7 916.
According to the German legal situation, the German taxpayer reported the corrected values of the goods and the reduction of the taxable amount in the quarter in which the repairs took place.
Thus, its SH included the following values of the delivery in relation to the Czech taxpayer:
12.
Within the framework of the international exchange of information, the German tax administrator asked the SCAC form to verify the delivery of goods and the provision of services carried out in the third quarter of 2005.
According to this RU, the Czech taxpayer should have delivered goods totalling EUR 396,126 to the German taxpayer during this period and provided services in the amount of EUR 11,885.
The SAO found that the Czech tax administrator carried out a local investigation in order to verify this delivery with the Czech taxpayer.
In reply to the RU, the Czech tax administrator stated that the Czech taxpayer had supplied the German taxpayer with a production line including assembly.
The individual parts of the production line were delivered by the Czech taxpayer before the Czech Republic entered the EU and after 1.5.2004 the line was assembled on the basis of the order.
The German taxpayer did not take over the assembled line because it claimed that it had defects.
In the third quarter of 2005 the Czech payer issued invoices to the German payer for the amounts of EUR 107 100 for assembly and EUR 11 885 for services.
The German payer took over the issued invoices, but did not recognise them and did not pay.
The SAO also found that all invoices were properly recorded in the accounts of the Czech payer by enquiring of the local tax administrator in the Czech Republic.
The VAT returns for the third quarter of 2005 only show the amounts that were evidenced by the Czech payer and which relate to invoicing after 1 May 2004.
The BRH found that on the basis of the reply from the Czech tax administration, the local tax office in Germany concluded that the transaction concerned the supply of goods from the Czech payer to the German payer including services for assembly.
In this special case, the place of the so-called performance of work is where the assembly of the production line took place.
According to the German VAT Act, the German recipient of the supplied service is obliged to pay VAT.
At the same time, the recipient can claim a VAT deduction on the same amount.
As there would be no changes in the value of the VAT that the German payer was obliged to pay, the corrections in the VAT tax return were neglected by the German tax office.
13. According to the VIES data, in February 2005, Czech payer A should have purchased a machine worth EUR 58 000 from German payer C.
The Czech tax administrator sent a request to Germany to verify this delivery.
In response to the RI, the German party stated that this machine had already been delivered by German payer C to Czech payer B in 2004, but that the machine should have been returned to German payer C in October 2004.
According to the information of the German tax administration, the machine was not transported back to Germany, but was transported to the organizational component of German payer C in the Czech Republic.
Further, the response to the request for information showed that German payer C sold the machine to Czech payer A in February 2005.
This payer took over the machine at the headquarters of the organizational component of German payer C in the Czech Republic.
As the delivery took place only within the Czech Republic, it was not an intra-community supply of goods.
The SAO inquired with the tax administrator of the locally competent payer B and found that according to VIES data, the German payer C had delivered goods (another machine) worth EUR 88 027 to the Czech payer B in the third quarter of 2004.
The payer B denied this acquisition of goods, so the locally competent tax administrator from the Czech Republic sent the RU to Germany.
According to the response to this request, the delivery of the machine took place.
Further investigation with the payer B revealed that the machine worth EUR 88 027 was not in the accounts of the payer B, and that it could be a machine of the same type as the one delivered by the organizational component of the German payer C to the Czech payer A in February 2005.
The SAO also found that the Czech tax administrator of the locally competent payer A had carried out a local investigation with this payer.
The tax administrator had an invoice from the German payer C dated 7 February 2005, on which the payer A was listed as the purchaser of the machine.
The Czech tax administrator found that the payer A did not have this invoice included in the accounts.
A payer A had a lease agreement with another Czech company, where the lease was for a machine of the same type.
The machine was handed over from the leasing company on February 9, 2005, and the transport of the machine was provided by the leasing company.
The information contained in the reply to the request for information was not used by the Czech tax office to determine the tax liability of payer A.
BRH found that the German payer C had not delivered the machine worth EUR 88 027 to the Czech Republic, but to another German payer D.
It was therefore not an intra-community supply of goods, but a taxable supply in Germany.
For these reasons, the German tax administrator did not recognize the German payer C's VAT exemption and corrected the data in his tax return.
The German payer D supplied the machine to the Czech payer B.
According to the German legislation, this supply was not taxable in Germany, but was subject to VAT in the Czech Republic.
BRH also found that the German payer C had indicated in his SH for the first quarter of 2005 the supply of the machine worth EUR 58 000 to the Czech payer A.
This supply was not checked during the tax audit carried out by the German tax office.
The following diagram shows the relations between the participants in the above-mentioned commercial transactions.
14.
The SAO found that the Czech tax administration received a request for information from the German tax administration on 4 October 2005, in which the German tax administrator asked for verification of the intra-community delivery from the German payer worth EUR 879 680 625 to the Czech payer.
According to the German tax administrator, there was a suspicion that this case was a fake intra-community delivery of goods.
The RU also stated that the German payer had not carried out any active commercial activity since 1999.
The SAO found that the Czech tax administrator carried out a local investigation with the Czech payer.
According to the statement of the manager of the Czech company, the above-mentioned case appeared to be a claim of the German payer against the German tax administration, which the Czech payer asserted as a partner of the German company at the German tax office.
According to the information provided by the SAO, the Czech tax administrator does not have any information that the German tax administration has solved the issue related to the Czech payer.
According to the available information, it was not a supply of goods, yet the mentioned value is still included in the VIES system as an intra-community supply of goods to the Czech payer from Germany.
The main reason for the following irregularities was that the recipients did not declare intra-community acquisitions of goods in their tax returns (see also chapter 4.4.1):
15. According to the VIES data, the German payer delivered goods totalling EUR 33 205 to the Czech payer in the third quarter of 2004 to the first quarter of 2005. The Czech payer did not declare this acquisition.
THISintentionallyLEFTblank
The Czech tax administrator requested verification of the delivery of goods from Germany as part of the international exchange of information.
In response to this request, the German tax administration stated that the German payer had sent part of the goods to the address of the Czech payer, the remaining goods were collected by the Czech payer personally.
By enquiring with the locally competent tax administrator in the Czech Republic, the SAO found that before receiving the response to the RU, the Czech payer had submitted additional VAT returns for the given periods.
Despite this submission, the differences in the acquisition values were not resolved, so the Czech tax administrator recommended a tax inspection of the Czech payer.
The inspection has not yet been carried out.
16. The German payer delivered goods worth EUR 46,854 to the Czech payer according to VIES data in the 3rd quarter of 2004.
The Czech payer granted intra-community acquisitions only in the amount corresponding to EUR 14,856 for the same period.
The Czech tax administrator requested verification within the international exchange of information on the value of the effected deliveries.
The response to the RU, delivered from Germany, was accompanied by 3 invoices with the total value of the delivery of goods of EUR 31,999, i.e. the value corresponding to the difference between the acquisition declared by the Czech payer and the VIES data.
The SAO inquired with the local tax administrator in the Czech Republic that after receiving the reply from the FRY, the Czech tax administrator contacted the accountant of the Czech payer and agreed with her to discuss with the owner of the company the submission of a supplementary VAT return for the 3rd quarter of 2004 after examining these invoices.
The supplementary VAT return has not yet been filed.
The Czech tax administrator told the SAO that it would proceed in order to comply with the stipulated deadlines for a possible supplementary VAT assessment for the relevant tax period.
17.
The German payer was supposed to deliver goods worth EUR 11,600 to the Czech payer in the 4th quarter of 2004.
The German tax administrator asked for confirmation within the international exchange of information whether the Czech payer actually existed because the alleged partner of the German payer had established several fictitious companies in the FRY.
During the examination of the business transaction, the Czech payer confirmed to the tax office the acquisition of the goods.
According to the Czech payer, however, the goods were not transported from the FRY to the CR and were resold during 2005 in the FRY.
The Czech payer submitted documents on the sale of the goods for January 2005.
The Czech payer was not registered as a VAT payer in Germany, did not declare or pay the tax on the sale of the goods in question in the Czech Republic or Germany.
All these facts indicated tax evasion in the territory of Germany and the Czech tax administrator communicated them to the German tax administration in reply to the IRS.
The SAO found out that the Czech payer submitted an additional VAT return for the 4th quarter of 2004, including the value of the acquisition of the goods from the German payer and at the same time claimed the right to deduct the tax on the acquisition of the goods from other Member States.
The VAT on the sale of the goods in Germany was not included in the Czech VAT return.
The Czech tax administrator assessed the additional VAT return after the local investigation without change.
According to the Czech legislation, the acquisition of the goods from other Member States was not involved, because the goods were not dispatched or transported from another Member State to the Czech Republic.
The Czech tax administrator therefore carried out an incorrect conclusion of the local investigation.
BRH found that the German tax administrator corrected the German payer's tax return immediately after receiving a reply to the RU stating that the goods had not left Germany and demanded from him VAT amounting to EUR 1 600.
In addition, the relevant tax office sent a warning to the tax office of the actual recipient of the goods in order to ensure that the resale of these goods would be correctly taxed.
In the following cases, the payers reported intra-community transactions which probably did not actually take place:
18.
The Czech tax administrator received a request from the German tax administration for information on whether the Czech payer had purchased a passenger car worth EUR 47 400 from the German payer in February 2005.
A copy of the certificate of registration of the Czech payer for VAT was attached to the request.
A copy of the passport of the person who was said to have carried out the transfer of the said car was also attached.
The Czech tax administrator discovered that the passport had been stolen, that the person mentioned in the passport had not imported any vehicle into the Czech Republic and denied all contacts with the German tax entity.
The certificate of registration for VAT, a copy of which was sent by the German party, was never issued by the Czech tax administrator.
The Czech tax administrator included this information in the reply to the RUC together with the communication that he could not confirm the acquisition of the goods – the car in question.
The SAO found that the Czech payer did not reside at the address given in the Commercial Register and that the manager of the company was not contactable.
The Czech tax administrator assessed the Czech payer for a tax liability of CZK 0 after the complaint procedure carried out for the tax period February 2005.
Further investigation, the Czech tax administrator found that the car in question had been sold to another Czech entity who had purchased it through an advertisement on the internet.
BRH found that the locally competent German tax administrator, based on the Czech response to the IRS, would not recognize the German tax payer's right to exemption from VAT for this supply.
19. During the inspection, the German tax office was not able to clarify the difference of EUR 3,000 between the value of the acquired goods declared in the tax return of the payer and the value provided from another Member State.
It was reported that the Czech payer was supposed to deliver goods worth EUR 89,424 to the German payer during the fourth quarter of 2004 to the first quarter of 2005.
Since the acquisition declared by the German payer did not correspond to the data in VIES, the German tax administrator requested verification of the supplies and their payment in the framework of the international exchange of information.
In response to the IRS, the Czech tax administrator stated that the sole agent of the Czech company had been deleted from the Commercial Register on 8 July 2005 and the new agent had not been registered.
The German recipient of the goods was apparently related to a partner of the Czech company.
The Czech payer filed VAT and SH tax returns, which were signed by an unauthorized person – the said partner of the company – after the manager had been deleted from the Commercial Register.
The accountant of the Czech payer confirmed to the tax administrator that the partner of the company had deposited the cash paid for the invoiced goods in EUR into the company's account.
Treasury documents were not issued.
The SAO in the Czech Republic, enquired with the local tax office, found that the tax administrator recognized the Czech payer for the fourth quarter of 2004 the right to be exempt from VAT on the supply of goods to another Member State in the amount of CZK 1,326,307 (EUR 42,145) and for the first quarter of 2005 in the amount of CZK 1,416,180 (EUR 47,548).
The BRH found that the tax administrator in Germany had not corrected the German payer's VAT return, because a German judge had in the meantime confirmed the German payer's insolvency.
As the earlier inspection did not reveal any signs of tax fraud, it will not be possible to enforce the assessed tax liability.
20. According to the VIES data, the German payer acquired goods from the Czech Republic in 2005 worth EUR 4 251 196, after acquiring goods worth EUR 43 274 in the previous year.
In the 2004 tax return and in the 2005 tax return, the German payer did not declare intra-community acquisitions.
In addition, he did not declare any reasonable supplies.
Because of these differences, the German tax office sent the RU relating to the 4th quarter of 2005 and the 1st quarter of 2006.
The Czech supplier reported intra-community supplies of goods to the German payer in the SH for these two quarters, totalling CZK 167 246 083 (EUR 5 615 299).
On 6 September 2006, the RU was delivered, in which the German party requested to check whether the Czech payer's declared intra-community supplies had been carried out.
In reply to this RU, the Czech tax administration stated that the request of the German party could not be complied with, because the Czech payer had no agent.
As the materials provided by the SAO by the relevant tax administrator show, on 30 March 2006, a protocol was drawn up with the Czech payer's manager to start the VAT audit for the 4th quarter of 2004 and January to December 2005.
The payer was also asked by the tax administrator to submit all accounting and tax documents for the above mentioned periods, but did not submit any documents.
According to the Commercial Register, the only manager of the Czech payer ceased to be in office on 16 May 2006, a new manager was not appointed.
From April 2006, the Czech payer stopped filing VAT returns.
As part of the audit, the SAO, in cooperation with BRH, examined, among other things, several cases of intra-community supplies made between the Czech Republic and Germany, which had not been the subject of a previous exchange of information between the tax administrations of both countries.
Information on the audited cases was exchanged between the two supreme audit institutions via the Customs Offices of both countries.
21. A Czech company (eCR), which is not resident in Germany, informed the relevant tax office (Chemnitz-Süd) that it intended to carry out a taxable transaction in Germany.
Because of this information, the company was registered since June 2005, but did not receive a German VAT ID.
(ECR) received an order from a Danish entrepreneur (eDK) for the production of several wind power plants and for the delivery of these wind power plants in the name, at the risk and on behalf of a Danish customer to Austria.
Due to a lack of own capacity, the Czech company handed over part of the order to a German taxpayer (eD), which is based in Germany.
The following diagram shows the contractual relations and the method of transportation of wind power plants:
According to the German legal situation, the place of execution of these transactions must be determined according to the following:
– A Danish entrepreneur (eDK) sent wind power plants for assembly under his name, at his risk and on his own account to Austria.
As the assembly of this supply took place in Austria, the supply of wind power plants is taxable in Austria.
– As the carrier was instructed by a Danish entrepreneur (eDK) and the transport took place under his name, at his own risk and on his own account, the supply of the German subcontractor (eD) took place where the transport began – in Germany.
Although the wind power plants were sent to another Member State and the recipient is a registered payer from another Member State, the supply of the German subcontractor (eD) could not obtain an exemption as the other Member State of destination is different from the other Member State of the seat of the Czech company.
This supply is therefore correctly taxed in Germany and the Czech company (eCZ) deducted the input tax in its tax returns.
The place of the supply of the Czech company (eCR) is also determined at the beginning of the transport.
The transport of some wind power plants started in the Czech Republic and others in Germany.
– The supply of those wind power plants that are produced in the Czech Republic took place in the Czech Republic.
– The supply of the other wind power plants that are produced in Germany took place in Germany.
So the Czech company (eCR) made both intra-community supplies from the Czech Republic to Austria and intra-community supplies from Germany to Austria.
BRH found that the Czech company (eCR) did not declare any intra-community acquisitions in its tax return for VAT in Germany nor did it file a SH with the German CLO.
So it is possible that the Czech company reported all intra-community supplies uniformly as intra-community supplies from the Czech Republic.
The SAO found that the (eCR) did not declare any intra-community supplies to Austria, but intra-community supplies to Denmark.
Examination of the taxation of intra-community acquisitions in Austria would require the cooperation of at least four tax administrations (Austrian, Czech, Danish and German), even though the case does not show any sign of tax fraud or evasion.
The SAO and BRH also examined the transactions to point out the differences between the tax return and the VIES data, which were caused by different VAT legislation in 2004.
The audited cases also demonstrate that the changes in the legislation need time for the application of the new legislation by both payers and tax authorities:
22. In the SH for the second to fourth quarters of 2004, the Czech payer reported intra-community delivery to the German payer for a total value of CZK 792,977,452 (EUR 25,197,885).
For the same period, another Czech payer in the SH reported intra-community delivery to another German payer for a total value of CZK 18,157,265 (EUR 576,970).
According to information provided by the SAO from BRH, both cases involved the supply of electricity.
Both Czech payers reported the above-mentioned supplies in the SH in accordance with the wording of Act No.235/2004 Coll., valid in 2004.
By further examining the above-mentioned transactions, the SAO auditing group found that in 2004 there were differences between the Czech Republic and Germany in the legal regulation of the supply or purchase of electricity.
While in the Czech Republic, payers reported the supply of electricity in accordance with the valid wording of Act No. 235/2004 Coll. as an intra-community supply of goods, from the point of view of the German statutory regulation valid in 2004 it was not an intra-community acquisition, but a taxable supply with the place of performance in the territory of Germany.
The difference in the statutory regulations was eliminated in the Czech Republic by the adoption of Act No. 635/2004 Coll., which amends certain laws in connection with the adoption of the Act on Administrative Fees, effective from 1 January 2005.
23. When examining selected intra-community transactions in cooperation with the BRH, it was also found that the Czech payer reported intra-community supplies to the German payer in the SH for the 1st to 4th quarter of 2005 in the total value of CZK 240,411,163 (EUR 8,071,823) and another Czech payer reported intra-community supplies to the German payer in the SH for the same period in the total value of CZK 263,470,776 (EUR 8,846,050).
According to the information provided by the SAO from the BRH, both cases involved the supply of electricity.
According to the wording of Act No.235/2004 Coll., effective from 1.1.2005, in the case of the supply of electricity, the place of supply is the place where the purchaser has its registered office, place of business or where it has an establishment for which the goods are supplied.
Therefore, Czech payers should not have reported the supply of electricity to SH in 2005.
By reporting intra-Community supplies of electricity in SH, both above-mentioned payers distorted the VIES data by a total of CZK 503,881,939 (EUR 16,917,873).
Conclusion
The cooperation fulfilled the objectives of BRH and the SAO.
Both SAIs gained a deeper knowledge of the VAT administration systems in the Czech Republic and Germany.
The cooperation revealed differences between the two systems and showed that the VAT administration legislation differs.
During parallel inspections, suspicious cases of intra-Community transactions were found.
Some of them make sense to be subsequently examined.
Based on the inspection findings, both SAIs made recommendations concerning the VAT administration.
The follow-up of these recommendations should also be part of the follow-up inspection.
New experience and knowledge gained through the cooperation of the two audit institutions are the basis for the successful implementation of the following VAT administration inspections.
Communiqué
The report was prepared in Czech, English and German and signed by the President of the Supreme Audit Office, Czech Republic and the President of the Bundesrechnungshof, Federal Republic of Germany.
Report on the outcome of international cooperation in the audits of the administration of excise duties between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic in 2006
Introductory word
The submitted joint report informs on the progress and outcome of international cooperation in the parallel audits carried out by the Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic and the Najvyšší Audit Office of the Slovak Republic, aimed at the administration of excise duties in the period after the accession of both countries to the European Union.
The cooperation was carried out on the basis of a contract on cooperation in the audit activity concluded in February 2006.
The topic of the parallel audits was chosen in view of the fundamental change in the system of collection of excise duties, which took place in connection with the integration of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic into the internal market of the European Union from 1 May 2004.
The functioning of the internal market of the European Union requires the free movement of goods, including goods subject to excise duty.
The basic principle is to allow the circulation of goods free of tax until the day of their delivery for final consumption.
In accordance with the above principle, the new legislation, adopted in both countries, allows goods to move under tax supervision under a conditional exemption regime.
The system places great demands on the tax administration and assumes close cooperation between the competent administrative authorities of the Member States in the fight against tax fraud in this area.
Report on the outcome of international cooperation in audits of excise tax administration for the period from 1 May 2004 to 31 December 2005 1.
Introduction
Audit number: (CR) 05/34 (SR) 48/11
Audit subject: (CR) Excise tax administration (SR) Procedure of the competent authorities in the administration of excise taxes
On 8 February 2006, the Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic (hereinafter referred to as “SAO-CR”) and the Supreme Audit Office of the Slovak Republic (hereinafter referred to as “SAO SR”) concluded the “Contract on Cooperation in Audit Activities”.
The subject of the contract was cooperation in the parallel audits "Administration of Excise Taxes", included in the SAO-CR Audit Plan for 2005 under No. 05/34, and "Control of the procedure of colných orgánov in the administration of excise taxes", included in the SAO-CR Audit Plan for 2006 under No. 48/11.
The parallel audits had the character of a coordinated audit.
The cooperation consisted in the exchange of information that the contracting parties could not obtain during the audit of the administration of excise taxes on the territory of their country, and in the preparation of a joint final report on the outcome of the audits within the meaning of the European implementing directives for the implementation of the INTOSAI auditing standards - Directive No. 31.
On the territory of the Czech Republic, the audit (hereinafter referred to as the "CR") was carried out by groups of auditors from the State Budget Department and from the territorial departments of central Bohemia, southern Bohemia, western Bohemia, northwestern Bohemia, northeastern Bohemia, northeastern Bohemia, southern Moravia, central Moravia and northern Moravia in the period from 7 February to 2 June 2006.
The auditing operation involved 27 auditors.
The audited bodies were the General Directorate of Customs (hereinafter referred to as "DG") and 11 financial offices.
Within the DG, 12 selected customs offices out of a total of 54 were audited.
The auditing operation on the territory of the Slovak Republic (hereinafter referred to as "the Slovak Republic") was carried out by the Financial and Tax Office of the Slovak Republic in cooperation with the SAO of the Slovak Republic Banská Bystrica and Košice at 5 customs offices out of a total of 9 in the period from 13 February to 2 June 2006.
The auditing operation involved 8 auditors.
The aim of the parallel audits was to examine the procedure of the customs authorities in the administration of excise duties and compliance with the relevant legislation in force in both countries and in the European Union.
The international cooperation was focused on the procedure of the tax administrators in the performance of supervision of the transport of goods subject to excise duties, in particular on the registration of started and finished transport under the suspension regime, and on the exchange of information within the framework of mutual administrative assistance between the excise tax administrators of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic.
2. Administration of excise duties
The administration of excise taxes in the Czech Republic was carried out by financial authorities until 31 December 2003.
Since 1 January 2004, this agenda has been taken over by customs authorities, which have so far only collected excise duty on imports.
Excise taxes in the Czech Republic are subject to mineral oils, ethyl alcohol, beer, wine and intermediate products and tobacco products.
The revenue of the state budget from excise taxes in the Czech Republic amounted to a total of 82.8 billion CZK in 2004 and 19.5% of the revenue of the state budget from taxes and fees amounted to 424.7 billion CZK.
In 2005, the revenue of the state budget from excise taxes amounted to 103.6 billion CZK and the share of the revenue of the state budget from taxes and fees amounted to 460.4 billion CZK was 22.5%.
In 2004, the revenue from excise duties on mineral oils to the state budget amounted to 80% of the total revenue from this tax and in 2005 it amounted to 90.9%.
The difference to 100% amounting to 13 billion CZK in 2004 and 6.9 billion CZK in 2005 was the revenue of the State Fund for Transport Infrastructure.
The administration of all excise taxes in the Slovak Republic has been carried out by the customs authorities since 1 May 2004, with the exception of excise tax on mineral oil, which they have been administering since 1 January 2002.
Until then, the administration of excise taxes was carried out by the tax authorities.
Excise tax in the Slovak Republic is subject to mineral oil, ethyl alcohol, beer, wine and tobacco products.
The revenue of the State Budget from excise taxes in the Slovak Republic was a total of SKK 43.4 billion in 2004 and excise taxes accounted for 20.7% of total tax revenue amounting to SKK 209.5 billion.
In 2005, the revenue of the State Budget from excise taxes was SKK 50 billion and excise taxes accounted for 22.5% of total tax revenue amounting to SKK 222.6 billion.
Graph 1 — Comparison of revenue of the State Budget of the Czech Republic from taxes and fees and tax revenue of the State Budget of the Slovak Republic with revenue from excise taxes
The legislation in both countries is based on the European Union rules governing this area, in particular: - Council Directive 92/12/EEC on the general arrangements for products subject to excise duty and on the holding, movement and monitoring of such products (hereinafter referred to as "Directive 92/12/EEC"), - Council Regulation (EC) No 2073/2004 on administrative cooperation in the field of excise duties (hereinafter referred to as "Regulation No 2073/2004"), - Commission Regulation (EEC) No 2719/92 on the accompanying official document for the movement of products subject to excise duty under suspension of excise duty (hereinafter referred to as "Regulation No 2719/92"), - Commission Regulation (EEC) No 3649/92 on the simplified accompanying document for the movement within the Community of products subject to excise duty which have been released for consumption in the Member State of dispatch (hereinafter referred to as "Regulation No 3649/92").
The basic legislation governing the issue of excise duties in the Czech Republic is Act No 353/2003 Coll., on excise duties, as amended (hereinafter referred to as Law No 353/2003 Coll.), which has been in force since 1 January 2004.
In administering excise duties in the Slovak Republic, the customs authorities are bound, inter alia, by the following generally binding legislation: - Act No 98/2004 Coll. on the spotrebnej tax on mineral oil, as amended by the non-statutory regulations (hereinafter referred to as Law No 98/2004 Coll.), - Act No 104/2004 Coll. on the spotrebnej tax on wine, as amended by the non-statutory regulations (hereinafter referred to as Law No 104/2004 Coll.), - Act No 105/2004 Coll. on the spotrebnej tax on lieh, as amended by the non-statutory regulations (hereinafter referred to as Law No 105/2004 Coll.), - Act No 106/2004 Coll. on the spotrebnej tax on tobacco products, as amended by the non-statutory regulations (hereinafter referred to as Law No 106/2004 Coll.), - Act No 107/2004 Coll. on the spotrebnej tax on beer, as amended by the non-statutory regulations (hereinafter referred to as Law No 107/2004 Coll.).
2.1 Movement of excise goods under suspension of excise duty between the Member States of the European Union
The conditions for movement of excise goods under suspension of excise duty are governed by Directive 92/12/EEC in Title III — Movement of goods Articles 15 to 20.
According to these provisions, the movement of such goods may be carried out only by an authorised warehousekeeper, who means a natural or legal person authorised by the competent authorities of a Member State to produce, process, store, receive and dispatch products subject to excise duty.
The consignee in another Member State may be an authorised warehousekeeper or an economic operator without the status of authorised warehousekeeper, but who may not store or dispatch such products under suspension of duty.
Authorised warehousekeeper in the Czech Republic and Slovakia means a tax warehouse operator, the economic operator is an authorised consignee for repeated or ad hoc receipt of products subject to excise duty.
Transport of products subject to excise duty under suspension of duty is possible under Directive 92/12/EEC only with an accompanying document.
The accompanying document is issued by the consignor in four copies before the transport begins, unless the competent authorities of the Member State of dispatch require further copies.
2.2 Procedure for the start and end of transport of goods under suspension of duty between the Czech Republic and Slovakia
Transport from the Czech Republic
The procedure for the start of transport is governed by the provisions of Section 25(3) of Act No 353/2003 Coll., which states, among other things:
‘The tax warehouse operator shall inform the customs office which is locally competent to the tax warehouse from which the transport is to start before the transport of the selected products begins;
transport of the selected products may start only with the consent of this customs office.
The customs office shall give its consent for the transport of the selected products without delay after the condition of securing the tax has been fulfilled...’
The consignor in the Czech Republic may start transport of all types of products subject to excise duty only with the consent of the locally competent customs office.
The customs office shall only give consent to the start of transport if the securing of the tax amounting to the tax attributable to the transported products is provided.
The consignor shall prepare an accompanying document in five copies before the start of the transport.
The customs office shall indicate on the accompanying document consent to the start of the transport.
Copy No 1 shall be kept by the consignor, copies No 2, 3, and 4 shall be handed over by the consignor to the carrier and copy No 5 shall be kept by the customs office authorising the transport.
According to Slovak legislation, the consignee in the Slovak Republic shall keep copy No 2 of the accompanying document. On copies No 3 and 4 he shall acknowledge receipt of the products and submit both copies to the locally competent customs office.
Copy No 3 certified by the customs office shall be sent to the consignor no later than the 15th day of the month following the calendar month in which he received the products.
Copy No 4 shall be kept by the customs office of the consignee.
The transport is terminated by receipt of the products by the consignee.
The release of the tax security is decided by the customs office in the Czech Republic, which authorised the start of the transport, within 5 working days after submission of copy No 3 of the accompanying document, which is certified by the consignee and by the Slovak customs office.
Graph No 2 — Circulation of the accompanying document for transport started in the Czech Republic and terminated in the Slovak Republic
Transport from the Slovak Republic
The procedure for the transport of alcohol and tobacco products from the Slovak Republic to another Member State of the European Union was amended as follows until 31 December 2005:
Pursuant to the provisions of Section 26(4) of Act No 105/2004 Z.
‘Pri preprave liehu from a tax warehouse in the tax territory to a tax warehouse or to an authorised consignee, or to a tax agent in inom členskom štáte je odosielatel’ (supplier’) obligatory in deň začatia prepravy to send a copy of the first diel sprievodného document electronically or by fax to Colné úradu Poprad; túto kópiu is obligatory to send aj colného úradu písomne do piatich working days odo dňa začatia prepravy.’
Pursuant to Article 22(4) of Law No 106/2004 Z. z.
‘When transporting tobacco products from a tax warehouse in the tax territory to a tax warehouse or to an authorised consignee, or to a tax plenipotentiary in the inom Member State, the odosielatel’ (supplier) is obliged, on the day of the start of the transport, to send a copy of the first diel of the sprievodné document electronically or by fax to the Colné úrad Poprad; it is obliged to send that copy to the colný úrad pisomne najor to those working days of the start of the transport. “
In respect of the transport of other products subject to excise duty (mineral oil, wine and beer) during the period from 1 May 2004 to 31 December 2005 (hereinafter referred to as the ‘audited period’), the taxpayer was not required to notify the Poprad Customs Office or the competent customs office of the start of the transport under the duty suspension arrangement.
The tax administrator became aware of the transport of these products only during a local investigation or tax inspection from the accompanying documents and accounting documents of the taxpayer.
The consignor in the Slovak Republic is obliged to prepare an accompanying document in four copies before the start of the transport.
Copy No 1 is retained by the consignor (when transporting alcohol and tobacco products, he sends a copy of Copy No 1 electronically or by fax to the Customs Office in Poprad and the relevant customs office).
Copy No 2, 3 and 4 accompany the goods being transported.
According to the Czech legislation, the consignee in the Czech Republic keeps Copy No 2 of the accompanying document issued by the consignor in the Slovak Republic and confirms receipt of the products on Copy No 3 and Copy No 4.
Confirmed Copy No 3 and Copy No 4 is sent to the locally competent customs office in the Czech Republic at the latest on the first working day after the end of the transport.
The customs office keeps Copy No 4 and Copy No 3, on which it verifies the accuracy and validity, is returned to the consignee.
The consignee sends the confirmed Copy No 3 to the consignor in the Slovak Republic at the latest on the following working day after its receipt.
Transport in the Slovak Republic is considered to have ended on the day of receipt of the products by the consignee.
Termination of transport shall be proved by the consignor submitting copy No 3 of the accompanying document certified by the consignee and the tax administrator in the Czech Republic.
Graph No 3 — Circulation of the accompanying document for transport (alcohol and tobacco products) started in the Slovak Republic and finished in the Czech Republic
In 2006, amendments to all excise tax laws were gradually adopted in the Slovak Republic, according to which the consignor of goods under suspension of tax is obliged to send a copy of copy No 1 of the accompanying document electronically or by fax to the customs office of the locally competent consignor before the start of transport.
The document proving the end of transport of alcohol and tobacco products shall be copy No 3 of the accompanying document certified by the consignee and his competent tax administrator.
The document proving the end of transport of mineral oils, wine and beer shall be copy No 3 certified by the consignee.
The confirmation of the receipt of the goods by the consignee by the tax authorities of another Member State shall be required if the latter are obliged to certify copy No 3 of the accompanying document according to the legislation of the respective Member State.
2.3 Registration of started and finished transport operations by customs authorities in the Czech Republic and Slovakia
There is no single electronic system for monitoring the transport of goods under suspension of tax between Member States of the European Union.
Decision 1152/2003/EC of the European Parliament and of the Council of 16 June 2003 on the introduction of an electronic system for the transport and monitoring of products subject to excise duty requires Member States and the European Commission to introduce an electronic system (Excise Movement and Control System) from 1 July 2009, which would allow excise tax authorities in individual Member States to obtain information on the transport of goods in real time.
