The system will enable the electronic transmission of accompanying documents, which are currently used only in paper form, and will contribute to the simplification of the movement of goods under the suspension regime and to ensuring more effective control of the movement of untaxed products within all Member States.
The system will include national databases of transport operations of individual Member States.
The Customs Administration of the Czech Republic records all transport operations commenced and terminated on the territory of the Czech Republic in the module of the Registration of Selected Products (hereinafter referred to as EVV).
All customs authorities in the Czech Republic have on-line access to the system.
In the case of transport operations carried out only on the territory of the Czech Republic, tax authorities can obtain information on the commencement or termination of the transport operation immediately after registration of the accompanying document by the customs office in EVV.
The customs office releases the tax security for the transported products provided by the consignor at the moment of registration of the termination of the transport by the customs office of the locally competent consignee.
Customs offices in the Slovak Republic use a database based on the application software SysNed, which provides automation of their activities in the administration of excise taxes and communication with the systems of the European Union.
By registering the tax warehouse, the operator of the tax warehouse or the authorised consignee in the application software SysNed, this data is automatically transferred to the database "System for Exchange of Excise Data" (hereinafter referred to as "SEED").
3. Preparation and course of cooperation
The first coordination meeting between representatives of the SAO-CR and representatives of the SAO of the Slovak Republic, at which the concrete process of cooperation in the implementation of parallel inspections in the field of excise taxes was discussed, took place in January 2006.
Both parties became acquainted with the legislation in the field of excise taxes and with the organization of the administration of excise taxes in both countries.
Special attention was paid to the procedure of the customs authorities of the CR and the Slovak Republic in authorizing, respectively, the beginning and ending of the transport of products subject to excise duty under the suspension regime and the exchange of information between the excise tax authorities of both countries.
At the meeting it was agreed that the Czech and Slovak sides: - will process the total data on the quantity of products subject to excise duty transported from the CR to the SR and vice versa, whose transport started during the audited period, - will compare the data on mineral oil transport - Combined Nomenclature code 2710 and 2711 and ethyl alcohol - Combined Nomenclature code 2207 and 2208 under the suspension regime initiated in the CR and terminated in the SR and vice versa in the months of November 2004 and September 2005.
During the audits, the audited periods were extended by the months of October and November 2005 and during the audits, the transport of tobacco products under the suspension regime was also subjected to the audits.
Tables 1 and 2 show the total quantity of products subject to excise duty which were transported under suspension of tax between Czech and Slovak tax subjects during the audited period.
4. Comparison of records of transport of goods under suspension of tax exemptions
The SAO-CR provided the Slovak side with a database of transport operations terminated in the Czech Republic, which contained a total of 5,876 items listed on accompanying documents, of which 5,738 items related to mineral oils, 134 items to ethyl alcohol and 4 items to tobacco products.
The SAO-CR provided the Czech side with a database of transport operations terminated in the Slovak Republic, which contained a total of 3,319 items listed on accompanying documents, of which 696 items related to mineral oil, 2,066 items to ethyl alcohol and 557 items to tobacco products.
The SAO-CR compared data on transport operations listed in the register of commenced transport operations in the Czech Republic with data on completed transport operations registered in the Slovak Republic.
The results of the comparison are shown in Table 3.
Data on transport operations in the months of November 2004 and September 2005 were compared by the SAO-CR with the Slovak Customs Administration database, which the SAO handed over to the SAO at the beginning of the audit.
The database did not contain data allowing reliable reconciliation of individual transport operations and therefore only 63 % of commenced transport operations were assigned.
Individual transport operations were assigned according to more data, e.g. consignor, consignee, date of transport, quantity of transported products.
Data on transport operations commenced in the Czech Republic and terminated in the Slovak Republic in the months of October and November 2005 were compared by the SAO-CR with the Slovak Customs Administration database, which contained all data according to accompanying documents, on the basis of which 93 % of commenced transport operations were unambiguously assigned.
In the database of the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic, data on the quantity of mineral oils were given in litres or in tonnes depending on the type of mineral oil.
The quantity of alcohol was given in litres in most cases, which could be converted into litres of absolute alcohol based on the database of the stated percentage of alcohol content.
The quantity of tobacco products was given in pieces, in thousands of pieces and in kilograms according to the type of tobacco products.
In the case of transport operations initiated in the Czech Republic, the completion of which could not be reliably verified in the Slovak database or where the data on the transported quantity of products did not match, the accompanying documents were checked.
The documents accompanying 487 transport operations of alcohol, mineral oils and tobacco products were checked.
The documents were checked at the customs offices, where the SAO-CR performed the check.
In the case of transport operations authorised by other customs offices, the accompanying documents were requested via the DG.
The Czech side asked the Slovak side to verify the realization of 141 shipments for which the customs offices in the CR did not prove the certified copies No.3 of the accompanying document, or the quantity of products indicated on the accompanying document did not correspond with the quantity of products indicated in the database.
In addition, the Slovak side was provided with data on the shipments registered in the Slovak database, which, however, did not contain the database of the Czech customs administration's shipments.
The SAO SR searched the Slovak customs administration's database for 95 shipments.
The verification of the remaining 46 shipments was requested by the locally competent customs offices, which proved their completion with copies of accompanying documents.
The Slovak side provided the Czech side with copies of accompanying documents, on the basis of which the shipments were identified also in the Czech database, with the exception of the shipments carried out by two Czech tax entities, which were not found in the Czech database of commenced shipments.
The audit of these cases found:
- in the Slovak database of transports, 11 transports of alcohol in the total amount of 276.7 litres of alcohol carried out by the Czech tax entity in 2004 and 20 transports of alcohol in the total amount of 404.66 litres of alcohol carried out in 2005 were registered.
The SAO-CR found that these were transports of taxed products, for which the consignor does not need the consent of the tax administrator.
The consignor informed the tax administrator in writing about the commencement of the transport. The transport was carried out on the basis of accompanying documents, which are used for the transport of products under the suspension of tax;
- in the Slovak database of transports, a total of 94 transports of mineral oils, Combined Nomenclature code 2710 11 21, were registered in the total amount of 173 thousand litres carried out by the Czech tax entity in the period from September 2004 to December 2005.
The SAO-CR found that in the period from May 2004 to June 2005 the tax entity carried out the transport of 102 thousand litres of untaxed mineral oils without the appropriate authorization.
The tax entity held a special authorization for receiving and using products exempt from tax, on the basis of which it could supply untaxed products only to the holder of the same authorization.
It did not notify the customs office in the CR of the start of the transport and did not provide a tax security of CZK 1,207,680 for the transported products.
In the period July 2005 to December 2005, the tax entity transported 71 thousand litres of taxed mineral oils to the territory of the SR. Even in these cases, it did not fulfil the legal obligation by failing to notify the customs office of the start of the transport.
The consignor in the CR can start the transport of products put into free tax circulation in the tax territory of the CR without the consent of the customs office, but he is obliged to inform the customs office of this fact in writing before the start of the transport.
The tax entity receiving products put into free tax circulation in another Member State is obliged to declare the quantity and ensure the tax before their withdrawal.
The products can be transported only with a simplified accompanying document, the particulars of which are regulated by Regulation No 3649/92.
This regulation also allows the use of an accompanying document for transport under suspension of tax, but it must be clearly indicated that it is a "simplified accompanying document for the purposes of tax control (products subject to excise duty)".
The same regulation of transport and acceptance of products placed into free tax circulation in another Member State applies in the Slovak Republic.
In these cases, the tax entities transported the products placed into free tax circulation with an accompanying document for transport under suspension of tax, the 3rd and 4th copies of which were submitted by the consignee to the tax administrator in the Slovak Republic for verification.
The customs authorities in the Slovak Republic registered these transportations in the database of transport under suspension of tax, as the accompanying documents did not state that it was a simplified accompanying document.
The SAO of the Slovak Republic compared the database of transport of the Czech customs administration with the Slovak customs administration's database of transport and found:
- in the databases, the quantity of transported products was stated inconsistently, e.g. mineral oil was given in litres, in hectolitres or in kilograms; alcohol was given in litres or litres of alcohol, making it difficult to compare the transported quantity of goods;
- the quantity of transported alcohol given in invoices did not match the quantity recorded in the databases;
- in the databases, not all related invoices were given;
- in the Slovak customs administration's database, two transports of alcohol from the Czech Republic to the Slovak Republic carried out in November 2004 in a total volume of 47 237 litres of alcohol were recorded, which were not found in the Czech customs administration's database.
The Slovak side handed over copies of the accompanying documents to the Czech side.
5. International exchange of information between the customs authorities of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic
Until 30 June 2005, the conditions of cooperation between the administrative authorities of the Member States responsible for the administration of excise duties were regulated by Council Directive 77/799/EEC, concerning mutual assistance between the competent authorities of the Member States in the field of direct taxes, certain excise duties and taxes on insurance premiums.
On 1 July 2005, Regulation No 2073/2004 entered into force, laying down rules and procedures allowing the competent authorities of the Member States of the European Union to cooperate and exchange the information necessary for the correct assessment of excise duties.
Each Member State shall designate a central liaison office, which shall ensure contacts with other Member States in the field of administration of excise duties and shall be responsible for the exchange of information on the movement of excise goods.
In the Czech Republic, in order to ensure the exchange of information in the field of excise duties between the Member States of the European Union, an “Excise Liaison Office” (hereinafter referred to as “ELO ČR”) has been established at the DG.
With effect from 1 May 2004, the ELO at the Poprad Customs Office was responsible for ensuring the management of the systems for controlling the movement of excise goods (SEED, MVS, EWSE) and the exchange of information in the framework of mutual administrative assistance between the Member States of the European Union and the Slovak Republic.
With effect from 1 July 2005, the tasks of ELO are carried out by the ELO Unit (based in Poprad) of the Excise Department of the Customs Directorate of the Slovak Republic (hereinafter referred to as ‘ELO SR’).
Under Article 3(3) of Regulation No 2073/2004, the central liaison office is responsible in particular for: - the exchange of data held in the electronic register of the SEED, - the Early Warning System Excise (EWSE), - requests for verification of movements of excise goods sent to or received from other Member States by the Movement Verification System (MVS).
The content, scope and functions of the SEED, EWSE and ISA systems are governed by Articles 22, 23 and 24 of Regulation No 2073/2004.
SEED - System for the exchange of information on tax subjects trading in excise goods.
The system is made up of national excise tax registers and allows tax authorities in the territory of the European Union to ascertain whether excise products are traded by a person authorised to do so.
Each national register is made available to the competent authorities of other Member States for excise purposes only.
The central liaison office of each Member State ensures that persons involved in the movement of excise goods in the territory of the European Union can obtain confirmation of the information held in this database.
In accordance with § 41 of Act No 98/2004 Z., with § 39 of Act No 104/2004 Z., with § 46 of Act No 105/2004 Z., with § 40 of Act No 106/2004 Z. and with § 39 of Act No 107/2004 Z. ELO SR maintains an electronic database containing a register of tax warehouse operators, authorised recipients and tax warehouses - the SEED database.
Customs offices in SR contribute to the SEED database by registering the tax warehouse, tax warehouse operator or authorised recipient in the SysNed application software, which is automatically connected to ELO SR.
For example, if a new tax warehouse operator, authorised recipient or tax warehouse is registered in the SysNed database, the related data are automatically transferred to the SEED database.
The SAO SR found that the exchange of SEED databases between the Slovak Customs Administration and the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic took place in the audited period usually once a month, exceptionally several times a month.
The Customs Administration of the Slovak Republic received 22 SEED files and sent 25 SEED files.
The data are transferred to the SEED database in the Czech Republic from the national register, in which all persons authorised to dispose of products subject to excise duty and issued authorisations to dispose of these products are recorded.
Individual customs offices in the Czech Republic do not have access to the international SEED database.
Requests from customs offices to provide information from the SEED database of other member countries are obtained only through ELO CR.
EWSE - an early warning system focused on controlling the transport of goods subject to excise duty, through which the transport of risky consignments is announced.
Transport of certain products subject to excise duty in quantities exceeding the limits set by a regulation of the European Commission is considered to be a risky consignment, and transport that is evaluated as a risk by the tax administrator.
The exchange of information takes two forms:
- information - is sent when the established limits are exceeded,
- a warning message - is sent when the transport of goods is evaluated as a risk.
When assessing the degree of risk of a consignment, ELO SR uses the SEED database for sending the warning message, on the basis of which it checks the data stated in the accompanying document.
If the data in the SEED database does not match the data in the accompanying document (for example, the registration number of the consignee of the goods or the registered office of the consignee does not match), ELO SR draws up a warning message, which it sends to the ELO office of the Member State of the consignee of the goods.
ELO follows the regulations of the Tax and Customs Commission CED 317 and CED 457 when drawing up the reports, which among other things determine the type and quantity of goods in the respective measurement units for drawing up informative and warning messages.
During the audited period, ELO SR sent one warning message to ELO ČR.
In the Czech Republic, information on initiated transport of products in quantities exceeding the specified limits is generated automatically when entering the data from the accompanying document into the database at the time of transport approval.
If the tax administrator in the Czech Republic evaluates a consignment as risky on the basis of its own analysis, it prepares a so-called warning message, which it sends to the respective Member State via ELO ČR.
In 2005, ELO ČR sent two warning messages to ELO SR.
The MVS - the system for controlling the movement of goods - allows through MVS requests to control individual transports of products subject to excise duty as well as the control of the specified transport route between the entities mentioned in the accompanying document.
The exchange of information takes place on the basis of a request in which ELO of the sending country specifies its requirements.
The system is used especially in cases where the consignor takes over the certified copy No.3 of the accompanying document and requests e.g. reimbursement of excise duty, and in cases where the data stated in the accompanying document cannot be verified in the international database SEED.
In the audited period ELO SR sent 33 requests to MVS.
ELO ČR sent 25 requests to MVS.
Customs offices in the Czech Republic most often examined the data stated in the accompanying documents, especially the quantity of received or dispatched products or whether the consignor of products mentioned in the accompanying document is entitled to dispose of products subject to excise duty, if this fact could not be verified in the international database SEED.
Received requests from MVS were in both countries forwarded to customs offices locally competent for the consignee or consignor of products subject to excise duty.
Customs offices verified the required data and notified the result of the investigation through ELO to the other member country.
6. Summary
Cooperation between the SAO and the SAO SR enabled to compare the basic legislation governing the area of excise duties in both countries, the procedure of the customs authorities of the Czech Republic and Slovakia when starting and ending the transport of products under the suspension regime between the two countries, the registration of these transports and to compare the exchange of information between customs authorities within the framework of international cooperation.
6.1 Comparison of legislation governing the area of excise duties in the Czech Republic and Slovakia revealed differences:
a) in the procedure of tax entities and tax administrators when starting the transport of products under the suspension regime.
The transport of products under suspension of tax exemption can be started by a tax subject in the Czech Republic only with the consent of the tax administrator, who will allow the transport to start on condition that the transported products have been provided with a guarantee of tax amounting to the amount of tax attributable to them.
The start of the transport of products under suspension of tax exemption in the Slovak Republic is not subject to the permission of the tax administrator.
During the audited period, the tax subject was obliged to notify the tax administrator of the start of the transport of alcohol and tobacco products.
The transport of mineral oils, beer and wine could start without informing the tax administrator.
In 2006, amendments to all excise tax laws were gradually adopted in the Slovak Republic, according to which the consignor of goods under suspension of tax is obliged to send a copy No. 1 of the accompanying document electronically or by fax to the customs office, which is competent locally, before the transport starts;
b) within the deadlines for sending copy No. 3 of the accompanying document.
The consignee in the Czech Republic is obliged to send copy No.3 and copy No.4 of the accompanying document to the tax administrator for verification no later than the following working day after the completion of the transport.
The certified copy No.3 is obliged to send to the consignor no later than the following working day after its receipt from the tax administrator.
The consignee in the Slovak Republic is obliged to send to the consignor of products copy No.3 confirmed by the tax administrator and the consignee of the products no later than the 15th day of the month following the month in which he received the goods.
6.2. Customs authorities in both the Slovak Republic and the Czech Republic keep electronic records of transport of products under suspension of excise duty.
The content and manner of keeping such records is not regulated by legislation in the Czech Republic or the Slovak Republic.
Customs authorities in both countries enter into the records all data from accompanying documents on the basis of which the transport is carried out.
For the monitoring of the transport of goods under suspension of tax between Member States of the European Union, there is currently no single electronic system that allows excise tax authorities in each Member State to obtain information on the transport of goods in real time.
According to Decision 1152/2003/EC of the European Parliament and of the Council of 16 June 2003, the introduction of an electronic system for the monitoring of the transport of products subject to excise tax is foreseen from 1 July 2009.
On the basis of a contract on cooperation in control activities, the Czech side transmitted to the Slovak side a database of transports of products under suspension of tax started in the Slovak Republic and finished in the Czech Republic.
The database contained 5 876 items relating to transported mineral oils, alcohol and tobacco products.
The Slovak side transmitted to the Czech side a database of transports of products under suspension of tax started in the Czech Republic and finished in the Slovak Republic.
The database contained 3 319 items relating to transported mineral oils, ethyl alcohol and tobacco products.
The Czech side compared the data on transport operations listed in the register of commenced transport operations in the Czech Republic with the register of transport operations terminated in the Slovak Republic.
The Slovak side compared the data on transport operations of goods under suspension of tax commenced in the Slovak Republic and terminated in the Czech Republic.
The comparison of the data was made more difficult by the fact that the quantity of transported goods was not reported uniformly in the databases.
In cases where it was not possible to unambiguously assign the data on individual transport operations in the two registers, a check of the accompanying documents was carried out and no violations of the suspension of tax or cases of tax evasion were detected.
Based on the findings from the parallel checks, it can be concluded that Member States can obtain valuable information from the transport registers to improve the administration of excise duties.
The establishment of an electronic system for the transport and control of excise goods within the meaning of Decision No 1152/2003/EC of the European Parliament and of the Council will allow the electronic transmission of the accompanying document and more efficient control of movements under the suspension arrangement in the territory of the European Union.
Communiqué
This report was prepared in Czech, English and Slovak languages.
The report was signed by the President of the Najvyššie Audit Office of the Slovak Republic and the President of the Supreme Audit Office of the Czech Republic.
Value Added Tax Administration in the Czech Republic and the Federal Republic of Germany
Report on the results of the ex-post audit
Introductory word
Taxes generally constitute a key source of public revenue.
It goes without saying that Supreme Audit Institutions (SAIs) should focus their attention on this area.
An example of this is value added tax (VAT) fraud.
In their case, a loss of EUR 100 billion is estimated every year in the European Union (EU).
Already in 2005, participants of the VI EUROSAI Congress in Bonn agreed on the need for very close cooperation.
As part of this cooperation, SAIs can exchange control procedures, find the best solutions, etc.
VAT is a very suitable area for audit cooperation, as it is the only tax harmonised within the EU.
The Supreme Audit Office of the Czech Republic (SAO) and the Federal Court of Auditors (Bundesrechnungshof, BRH) carried out the first parallel audit in the field of VAT in 2006.
The relevant report was published in 2008.
As VAT fraud is not limited to a single country, but is spread throughout the EU, close cooperation between SAIs is necessary to ensure a comprehensive evaluation of the steps taken to solve this problem.
Both SAIs therefore decided to further develop cooperation in this area and carried out the subsequent parallel auditing.
1. Introduction
Audit number: (CZ) 09/11 (D) VIII 2 - 2009 - 0892
Audit subject: (CZ) Value Added Tax Administration (D) Bilateral audit with the SAO (follow-up audit)
Audit objective:
(CZ) The aim of the auditing operation was to examine the procedure of the financial authorities in the administration of VAT, in particular to verify the procedure for resolving selected cases of commercial transactions between the Czech Republic and the Federal Republic of Germany (hereinafter referred to as Germany), and to examine the procedures of the tax administrations of both countries within the framework of international cooperation.
(D) The auditing operation was designed to evaluate the measures taken by the tax administration to implement the recommendations issued by the SAO and the BRH.
It was also intended to cover other areas related to VAT.
The resulting audit findings were intended for comparison with the established best practice (if any).
The audited period covered the years 2006 to 2008, in case of factual connections also the periods before and after, until the end of the audit.
2. Summary of the results and evaluation of parallel audit actions
The follow-up audit of the VAT administration in the Czech Republic and Germany was carried out on the basis of an agreement between the two SAIs.
During the previous parallel audits, suspicious cases of intra-community transactions were detected.
Some of them required further examination.
Based on the audit findings, both SAIs formulated recommendations concerning the VAT administration.
The follow-up audit action performed was used to evaluate the measures taken in response to these recommendations and to examine selected suspicious cases.
Furthermore, the audit focused on, for example, selected cases of high-risk intra-community transactions, mutual assistance in the recovery of claims and the implementation of VAT controls on large tax entities.
During the audit of the VAT administration in selected areas in both countries, the auditors arrived at the following audit findings:
1. Recommendations from the previous audit
• Recommendation 1: Conditions of registration of payers should be harmonised within the EU
In previous parallel controls, a comparison of the VAT registration systems in both countries revealed differences.
As the different registration methods cause problems, both SAIs recommended harmonising the conditions of registration of payers within the EU.
This recommendation was presented at EU level.
The proposal to amend Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 on administrative cooperation in the field of value added tax and repealing Regulation (EEC) No 218/92 (hereinafter "Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003") called for the extension of existing databases within the EU, including the VAT payers' tax identification numbers database.
It also modified common standards for the registration and deregistration of tax payers.
The SAIs expected EU Member States to agree on appropriate standards to support their decision to exclude unreliable traders from the VAT system as quickly as possible.
However, the latest version of this document, agreed by EU Member States in the framework of ECOFIN, no longer contains the mentioned issue.
Both SAIs regret that the idea of common minimum standards has been abandoned.
However, they continue to consider this intention as a relevant tool for prevention in the fight against VAT fraud.
• Recommendation 2: Monthly submission of recapitulative statements
In the framework of international cooperation, a previous control action recommended that all EU States introduce a monthly deadline for the submission of recapitulative statements to allow for a more timely verification of the values of intra-Community transactions.
Council Directive 2008/117/EC amending Directive 2006/112/EC on the common system of value added tax to combat tax evasion linked to intra-Community transactions reduces the period for the submission of recapitulative statements on intra-EU transactions to one month.
In the Czech Republic, this measure was implemented through the Value Added Tax Act with effect from 1 January 2010, in Germany it was implemented from 1 July 2010.
In Germany, the obligation to submit recapitulative statements monthly was not introduced by the deadline in accordance with the applicable EU rules, while in the Czech Republic it was.
• Recommendation 3: Comparison of data in VAT returns and recapitulative statements in Germany to achieve greater reliability of data in the VIES system and consideration of linking the two systems for VAT returns and recapitulative statements
The German tax administration accepted the BRH's recommendations and set up a working group to explore possible solutions.
Work is still ongoing and the BRH will closely monitor further developments.
• Recommendation 4: Sharing of successful criteria, components and approaches of the risk management system at EU level Based on the results of the previous audit, both SAIs agreed that an effective risk management system cannot be developed by only one Member State.
Successful criteria, components and approaches of the risk management system must be exchanged and implemented in individual EU Member States.
If this is not the case, the perpetrators of fraudulent activities will choose the Member State with the weakest risk management system.
The audit found that our two Member States use different risk management systems, which have their advantages and weaknesses.
In this area, the SAO carried out an audit of the EUROCANET system, which allows exchange of information within the EU, while the BRH focused on the German participation in the so-called risk management platform.
2. Follow-up of selected cases of intra-community transactions
During the previous audit operation, business transactions where there were doubts about their completion or irregularities in the reporting of business transactions in tax returns or summary reports by tax payers from both countries were examined together.
The two SAIs selected nine cases for the follow-up, which included intra-Community movement of goods between the Czech Republic and Germany.
The audits carried out by the tax authorities of the respective countries were not closed on the date of completion of our previous joint audit operation.
The follow-up operation verified that most of the tax procedures related to the selected cases of commercial transactions between tax payers from the Czech Republic and Germany were closed and that adequate measures were taken by the tax administration of the Czech Republic or Germany (e.g. additional VAT assessments or avoidance of input tax refunds).
3. Audit of selected cases of risky intra-Community transactions
High-risk cases of intra-community transactions carried out by EU payers, which were included in the EUROCANET system, were selected for the audit.
The EUROCANET system is a tool for detecting risky tax payers within the EU.
Participation of the Member States in the system is voluntary.
The Czech Republic is an active participant in the EUROCANET system, while Germany has a passive status.
It is unsatisfactory for an active participant in the system if some Member States refuse to participate actively.
Due to the fact that the German tax administration did not participate in the exchange of data in the EUROCANET system, it was not possible to obtain any information about which suppliers with the German VAT ID were assessed as risky.
The SAO found cases of common commercial transactions as well as cases of suspected involvement in carousel transactions or fraudulent behaviour related to VAT.
Tax administrators have limited possibilities of controlling risky transactions, especially when it comes to missing traders, and mere physical verification of documents can hardly prove any fraudulent behaviour to the taxpayer.
A similar situation arises for tax administrators when imports and exports to third countries are linked to intra-Community carousel trades.
In such cases, it would be advisable to ensure greater cooperation between customs and financial authorities in order to identify goods and irregularities in transport documentation as well as to monitor their physical movement within the EU towards the final consumer.
Germany, like some other countries, is hesitant to actively participate in EUROCANET due to the lack of a sufficient legal basis.
In Germany, other tools for detecting risky tax payers are being used, which until now have proved successful for the German tax administration.
In this area, there is a need to communicate and exchange experiences between EU Member States.
The Council of the EU reached a political agreement on a draft regulation amending Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003.
Its main innovation is the creation of the EUROFISC network.
The experience gained so far in using EUROCANET should be the basis for the creation of this new network for combating VAT fraud.
4. Mutual assistance for the recovery of claims
In the area of international assistance for the recovery of claims, all EU Member States are governed by the same European legislation.
Therefore, the way of handling requests for international assistance for the recovery of claims in the Czech Republic and Germany is the same.
The SAO and BRH compared the statistics submitted by both Member States to the European Commission for the years 2006-2008.
The data contained in these statistics were not the same.
Both SAIs consider it useful to renegotiate the statistics at EU level in order to find a way to avoid persistent discrepancies.
Without this, the statistics will not be reliable and comparable.
In addition, the SAIs agree that reliable statistics should contain more information on VAT.
It would probably be useful for the Commission to prepare an analysis based on more detailed statistics to help the Member States strengthen the effectiveness of the fight against VAT fraud.
In the opinion of both SAIs, this means helping Member States with a low recovery rate so that they can increase the recovery rate to at least the EU average.
If a Member State so wishes, the Commission should actively participate in this process.
5. Audit of large tax entities
The SAIs analysed the legal situation regarding VAT control of large tax entities (hereinafter referred to as "VDS") in both countries.
In addition, they gathered information from the tax authorities in the form of a questionnaire on the areas that the SAIs consider essential for managing this issue.
The responses received clearly show that the situation is developing differently in the two countries.
The Czech Republic has a system in place to guide the selection of risk-prone cases, which is based on a large volume of relevant data (e.g. information from the tax controls carried out, balance sheet and profit and loss statements, etc.).
This ensures effective management and analysis of VAT control in general.
In 2012, it is planned to set up a specialised tax office for the administration of VDS.
In Germany, a similar system does not yet exist, which makes it difficult to manage and analyse VAT control in general.
Germany has so far focused more on the selection of individual cases in question, mainly on the basis of data from the VAT return and the recapitulative statement.
The analysis of these data is based on various components of risk management, which will be strengthened.
3. Conduct of the control action
3.1 Conduct of the control action in the Czech Republic
The control was carried out between May 2009 and February 2010 by the Department II. - the State Budget Revenue Department and the Territorial Departments IX. Plzeň, X. České Budějovice, XIII. Brno and XV. Ostrava.
The audited bodies were: the Ministry of Finance of the Czech Republic (hereinafter also referred to as the “Czech Ministry of Finance”) and 25 financial authorities (hereinafter referred to as the “FÚ”): FÚ Brno II, FÚ Brno III, FÚ Brno IV, FÚ Břeclav, FÚ Domažlice, FÚ Hodonín, FÚ Hradec Králové, FÚ Cheb, FÚ Jablonec nad Nisou, FÚ Karlovy Vary, FÚ Kraslice, FÚ Ostrava I, FÚ Ostrava III, FÚ Písek, FÚ Plzeň, FÚ pro Prahu 1, FÚ pro Prahu 4, FÚ pro Prahu 8, FÚ Rakovník, FÚ v Sokolově, FÚ v Tábor, FÚ v Vysoké Mýt, FÚ Zlín and FÚ Žamberk.
The audit conclusion of this auditing operation was approved by the College of the Supreme Audit Office on 27 April 2010.
3.2 Conduct of the auditing operation in Germany
The auditing operation was carried out between February 2009 and February 2010 by the Indirect Taxation Audit Service and by the staff of the designated regional audit offices in Berlin, Frankfurt am Main and Munich.
After selecting a sample of cases, a number of Länder were notified of the mission of the auditing operation.
In addition to the interviews at the Federal Ministry of Finance, the audit operation was carried out in the following Länder: • Bavaria, • Hamburg, • Hesse, • North Rhine-Westphalia, • Saxony.
The tax files of the following financial offices were included: • Erlangen, Zentralfinanzamt München (Central Financial Office in Munich), Hof, Schwandorf, Regensburg, Weiden in der Oberpfalz, Grafenau; • Hamburg-Nord (Hamburg-North), Hamburg-Hansa, Hamburg für Großunternehmen (Hamburg-VDS);
In addition, discussions were held with the tax offices Mühlacker, Reutlingen, Starnberg, Verden, Erfurt, Leipzig, Halle-Süd (Halle-South) and with the financial directorates in Frankfurt am Main, Chemnitz and Münster.
The report on the audit findings was submitted to the Federal Ministry of Finance in April 2010.
3.3 Cooperation between the two audit institutions
In preparation of the parallel audit actions, a meeting of representatives of the two audit institutions was held in September 2008 to discuss and establish the audit topics.
Subsequently, in December 2008, the highest representatives of the two SAIs signed an agreement on cooperation in the implementation of the parallel audits.
At the meeting in Bonn in June 2009, the audit teams informed each other about the initial results achieved during the preparation of the audit, discussed possible audit approaches and agreed on the next steps.
The second meeting took place in Prague on 2-4 December 2009.
The audit teams exchanged the previously collected findings and agreed together on a timetable for the preparation of the joint report.
The two SAIs decided to focus on: • follow-up of the implementation of recommendations made in the previous report; • screening of selected cases of intra-Community transactions between tax payers from the Czech Republic and Germany that were not solved during the previous parallel audit; • screening of selected cases of intra-Community transactions between tax payers from the Czech Republic and Germany that were classified as high risk; • auditing of the tax administrations' progress in the area of international assistance in the recovery of VAT claims; • tax audits of large companies.
The report on the results of the parallel audits was prepared during a working meeting in June 2010.
4. Auditing of the VAT administration in selected areas
4.1 Evaluation of recommendations from the previous audit
4.1.1 Evaluation of recommendations in the Czech Republic
Recommendation 1
Conditions for registration of tax payers should be harmonised within the EU
Based on the results of the previous audit, the SAO recommended modification of the conditions for registration for VAT and introduction of a new rule for cancellation of registration in the Czech Republic.
The modified conditions should make it possible to reduce the risk of possible tax evasion in the collection of VAT more effectively.
In this context, it was found that in some cases the tax authorities did not make use of the right to cancel VAT registration for payers who did not comply with the obligations arising from Act No.235/2004 Coll., on Value Added Tax (hereinafter the "VAT Act").
The Czech Ministry of Finance has not yet proposed a change in the provision introducing an obligation for tax administrators to cancel VAT registration for payers in case of repeated failure to file a VAT return.
According to the VAT Act, the tax administrator can cancel a tax payer's registration "ex offo" in cases where: (a) the payer did not perform a performance for twelve consecutive months without notifying the tax administrator of the reason; (b) the payer does not comply with his obligations arising from this Act; (c) the payer ceases to be a taxable person.
In the previous auditing operation, it was found that the applicable legislation allowed the Tax Office for Prague 1 to cancel the VAT registration on 31 January of the following calendar year to so-called non-established payers who did not incur any obligation to declare and pay the tax during the current calendar year.
The Tax Office for Prague 1 often did not cancel the VAT registration of these payers because the relevant provision set an insufficient deadline for the cancellation of the registration.
This problem was remedied by an amendment to the VAT Act with effect from 1 January 2009.
The tax administrator is entitled to cancel the registration of a non-established tax payer in case the tax payer has not supplied any taxable goods or services or exempt goods or services with the right to deduct VAT in the previous calendar year.
Recommendation 2
Monthly submission of summary reports
In the framework of international cooperation, the previous auditing operation recommended that all EU states introduce a monthly deadline for the submission of summary reports.
The Council Directive reduces the period for the submission of recapitulative statements on intra-EU transactions to one month. This measure was implemented in the Czech Republic through the VAT Act with effect from 1 January 2010.
There is also a new obligation to submit recapitulative statements in electronic form.
The recapitulative statement must be submitted to the taxpayer even if the services for which the place of performance is determined in accordance with Section 9(1) of the VAT Act are provided to a person registered for tax in another Member State and if the recipient is obliged to declare and pay tax on these services.
This obligation is based on Council Directive 2008/8/EC amending Directive 2006/112/EC as regards the place of supply of services.
Recommendation 3
Comparison of data in VAT returns and recapitulative statements with a view to achieving greater reliability of data in the VIES system This recommendation concerned the German tax administration.
The Czech administration carries out a comparison of data on intra-Community transactions reported in VAT returns and recapitulative statements of Czech payers in an automated way in the ADIS system.
Recommendation 4
Sharing of successful criteria, components and approaches of the risk management system at EU level
Proper collection of VAT is one of the prerequisites for the proper functioning of the EU internal market.
The fight against VAT fraud is therefore one of the priority areas of interest and has received considerable attention in recent years.
The importance of this fight is evidenced by the conclusions of a study published by the European Commission in October 2009, in which an external evaluator attempted to determine the difference between the eligible and actually collected VAT levels in the 25 EU Member States (hereinafter referred to as the EU-25) during the period 2000-2006.
Based on the analysis of the available data, the author concluded that the estimated loss from uncollected VAT for this period is between EUR 90 and 113 billion, while on average 12% of the eligible VAT is not collected annually in the EU-25.
For the Czech Republic, the VAT loss for 2006 was even estimated at 18 %.
Within the framework of international cooperation, the previous audit operation stated that an effective risk management system cannot be developed by one Member State alone.
The successful criteria, components and approaches of this system must be shared and implemented in each EU Member State.
As regards the risk management system, the SAO carried out an audit of the EUROCANET system, which is used for information exchange in the EU.
Cases of risky intra-community transactions carried out by EU tax payers, included in the EUROCANET system, were selected for the audit (see chapter 4.3).
The objectives of improving administrative cooperation and increasing the effectiveness of the fight against VAT fraud should also be achieved by setting up the EUROFISC network, which should improve cooperation between the responsible authorities into a form that allows fraud to be detected in its bud.
The network should later also become an important source of information in the assessment of risks in intra-Community transactions.
The ECOFIN Council already approved the creation of the EUROFISC network on 7 October 200812 and at the same time laid down the basic principles that will guide the network.
The EUROFISC model is the already functioning system of rapid and selective exchange of information EUROCANET, developed by the Belgian tax administration in cooperation with other Member States and with the support of the European Commission and OLAF.
The aim of this system is to detect risky commercial transactions and entities involved in organised VAT fraud.
4.1.2 Evaluation of the recommendations in Germany
The evaluation of the recommendations of the first report produced the following findings:
Recommendation 1
Conditions for the registration of payers should be harmonised within the EU
The German tax administration has established a well-functioning system for the registration of tax payers, based on a detailed questionnaire.
The Federal Ministry of Finance drew the Commission's attention to this system in October 2007.
The system is being improved on an ongoing basis.
At present, the questionnaire data is electronically processed and will subsequently serve for the survey as part of risk management already during registration.
The Commission has presented a proposal to amend Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003, which included common standards for the registration and deregistration of taxpayers.
Member States have requested further clarification and detailed elaboration of this issue.
The BRH has asked the Federal Ministry of Finance to safeguard the already achieved level of standards in this area in Germany.
Recommendation 2
Monthly submission of recapitulative statements
On 8 April 2010, the Act transposing EU Directives into national law was adopted.
This Act contains provisions concerning the monthly submission of recapitulative statements on intra-Community supplies.
These provisions took effect on 1 July 2010.
Recommendation 3
Comparison of data in VAT returns and recapitulative statements to achieve greater reliability of data in VIES and consideration of linking the two systems for VAT returns and recapitulative statements
A joint working group composed of staff from the Länder and the Federal Ministry of Finance was established.
The group developed a strategy for automatic comparison of data from VAT returns and recapitulative statements.
This strategy is still being discussed in the Länder.
Furthermore, the working group looked at a tool designed to optimise the control procedure for transactions in the internal market.
Recommendation 4
Sharing of successful criteria, components and approaches of the risk management system at EU level The exchange of relevant information takes place at EU level.
Germany is a participant in this exchange within the framework of the so-called risk management platform.
The European Commission supported the idea of this platform and, following a written consultation on 18 October 2006, the establishment of the risk management platform was added to the Fiscalis 2006-2007 action plan.
The members of the platform are further divided into sub-groups dealing with individual topics such as: • risk management tools, • influencing negotiations, • evaluations, • updating the risk management guide.
Reports on the results of the activities of these sub-groups were published in early 2010.
4.1.3 Evaluation
Registration
The issue of the conditions for VAT registration and de-registration in different countries was addressed at EU level.
The draft amendment to Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 included an extension of existing databases within the EU, including the VAT payer tax identification number database.
It also regulated common minimum standards for the registration and deregistration of tax payers.
The issue of registration and de-registration was left for the time being to the national legislation of the EU Member States.
Member States requested further clarification and detailed elaboration of the issue.
The BRH asked the Federal Ministry of Finance to ensure that the level of standards already achieved in Germany did not fall.
On 8 June 2010, the ECOFIN Council reached a political agreement on the draft regulation.
The idea of common minimum standards was abandoned.
Member States have to implement national procedures and are only obliged to inform the Committee on Administrative Cooperation about these procedures.
Both SAIs regret that the Commission has not been able to convince Member States of the need for common standards for the registration and deregistration of payers, as both SAIs consider this measure to be an important element of prevention in the fight against VAT fraud.
They would therefore welcome further efforts by the Commission in this direction.
Monthly submission of recapitulative statements
In the framework of international cooperation, a previous control action recommended that all EU States introduce a monthly deadline for the submission of recapitulative statements, allowing for more timely verification of the values of intra-Community transactions.
Council Directive 2008/117/EC amending Directive 2006/112/EC on the common system of value added tax to combat tax evasion linked to intra-Community transactions reduces the period for the submission of recapitulative statements on intra-EU transactions to one month.
In the Czech Republic, this measure was implemented through the VAT Act with effect from 1 January 2010, in Germany it came into effect on 1 July 2010.
Germany did not introduce an obligation to submit recapitulative statements monthly according to a specified calendar, while the Czech Republic did (in line with EU directives).
Comparison of data in VAT returns and recapitulative statements in Germany to achieve higher reliability of data in the VIES system and consideration of linking the two systems for VAT returns and recapitulative statements
The German tax administration accepted the BRH's recommendations and set up a working group to find possible solutions.
Work is still ongoing and the BRH will closely monitor further developments.
Sharing of successful criteria, components and approaches of the risk management system at EU level
Germany and the Czech Republic apply different approaches to the risk management system for the purpose of detecting risk-prone traders.
The SAO performed an audit of the EUROCANET system used for the exchange of information in the EU (see chapter 4.3).
BRH focused on the German participation in the so-called risk management platform in this area.
4.2 Follow-up of selected intra-Community transactions
In the previous audit operation, the execution of commercial transactions where there were doubts about their execution, or inconsistencies in the way the tax payers from both countries reported these commercial transactions in their VAT returns or summary reports, was jointly examined.
The two audit institutions selected for the follow-up nine cases involving intra-Community movement of goods between the Czech Republic and Germany, whose control carried out by the tax administrations of both countries had not been completed during the previous joint audit operation.
1)
In the first quarter of 2005, a Czech payer purchased goods worth EUR 22 686 from a German payer.
This acquisition of goods was not declared by the Czech payer in his VAT return, because the German payer had not been allocated a VAT ID during that period, but only a tax number intended for domestic transactions in Germany.
On the basis of international administrative cooperation under Council Regulation (EC) No 798/2003, the Czech tax administrator received information that under the German VAT Act, a payer who supplies goods to other Member States does not have to be allocated a VAT ID in order for intra-Community delivery of goods to be exempt from VAT.
A follow-up audit by the SAO revealed that on the basis of the control carried out by the Czech tax administrator, the Czech payer filed an additional VAT return, in which he declared the acquisition of goods worth the stated value and at the same time claimed the right to deduct VAT in the same amount in this tax return.
2)
The Czech payer should have purchased goods worth EUR 12 561 from a German payer in the fourth quarter of 2004.
The acquisition of these goods was denied by the Czech payer and did not appear in his VAT return.
Upon request under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003, the German tax administration refused to cooperate as the turnover of the transactions did not exceed EUR 15 000.
As the Czech tax authority did not obtain evidence, it terminated the inspection without a finding and the tax liability remained assessed at the original amount.
Subsequent audit The SAO found that the Czech tax administrator received two spontaneous information from Germany pursuant to Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003, which showed that the German payer invoiced the goods to Slovakia.
The Czech payer purchased the goods from the Slovak payer and stated this acquisition in the regular VAT return for the month of October 2004.
3)
In the fourth quarter of 2004, the Czech payer was to purchase a passenger car worth EUR 48 500 from the German payer.
The acquisition of the goods in question was not declared by the Czech taxpayer.
Since August 2004, this payer has not filed VAT returns, so the tax administrator has charged VAT of CZK 0 for this quarter.
On the basis of information obtained in the framework of the international exchange of information pursuant to Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 from Germany, in March 2007, the tax administrator asked the taxpayer to file an additional VAT return, which the taxpayer did not file.
A subsequent inspection found that the tax administrator had carried out further acts in the tax proceedings in 2007, which showed that the passenger car in question had been sold by the Czech taxpayer to a used car dealership in the Czech Republic.
The Czech tax administrator issued a payment notice for the tax period in December 2004, which issued an additional VAT assessment for the acquisition of goods from another Member State and their subsequent sale amounting to CZK 295 379.
By order of the regional court, the Czech taxpayer was dissolved with liquidation and a liquidator was appointed.
In the absence of executions of the taxpayer's actionable assets, this arrears appears to be uncollectable.
(4)
The Czech taxpayer was supposed to make deliveries of new means of transport (passenger cars) to Germany during the 4th quarter of 2004 and the 1st quarter of 2005 in the total value of EUR 198 167.
The response to the request for information under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 showed that tax-criminal proceedings against the German entity were pending in Germany.
During the subsequent audit, BRH was informed that after the completion of the tax proceedings in Germany, it was demonstrably found that the German taxpayer had been included in fraudulent activities.
The intracommunal acquisition of goods was taxed in the value of EUR 182 424 (2004) and EUR 369 690 (2005).
The SAO found that the Czech taxpayer had been involved in carousel transactions with new means of transport.
Based on information from the German tax administration regarding the verification of the delivery of goods, a VAT audit for the tax periods of April, May and June 2005 was initiated with the Czech taxpayer.
Based on the audit findings and information obtained within the international exchange of information, the tax administrator additionally assessed VAT for the period of May 2005 in the amount of CZK 703 031 and for the period of June 2005 in the amount of CZK 726 551.
5)
In February 2005, the Czech payer A was supposed to purchase from the German payer a machine with a total value of EUR 58 000.
This German payer was supposed to deliver to the Czech payer B a machine with a value of EUR 88 027 in the 3rd quarter of 2004, but the payer B denied this acquisition of goods.
The SAO's subsequent audit found that the payer B purchased the machine from a German company that had an organizational component established in the Czech Republic.
The Czech payer A did not declare the acquisition of goods from the German payer in its VAT return.
The response from the German tax administrator to a request for information pursuant to Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 showed that the German payer did not make an intra-community delivery of the machine with a value of EUR 58 000, but a delivery of goods within the Czech Republic.
BRH's follow-up audit found that after the tax audit, the intra-Community supply of the machine was reclassified as a supply of the machine within the Czech Republic and the VAT exemption was abolished.
6)
The German tax payer was supposed to deliver goods worth EUR 11 600 to the Czech payer in the 3rd quarter of 2004.
The goods were purchased and subsequently sold in Germany in 2005.
The SAO's follow-up audit found that the Czech tax administrator assessed the submitted additional VAT return, where the acquisition of goods from another EU Member State was improperly stated, including the acquisition of goods worth the stated value.
BRH found that after receiving the response to a request for information under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003, the German tax administrator corrected the German payer's VAT return and additionally assessed VAT worth EUR 1 600.
The further movement of goods in Germany and the application of VAT in Germany are subject to the tax audit.
The summary report of the German payer has not yet been corrected, because only the payer who submitted the summary report can make corrections to the summary reports in Germany.
7)
The Czech tax administrator received a request for information from the German tax administration under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003, whether the Czech taxpayer had purchased a passenger car worth EUR 47 400 from the German payer in February 2005.
After the tax procedure carried out for the tax period February 2005, the Czech tax administrator assessed the Czech payer's tax liability at CZK 0 and informed the German tax administrator that it could not confirm the acquisition of the car by the Czech payer.
A subsequent audit by the SAO found that the registration of the Czech VAT payer had been cancelled in 2007 for non-compliance with obligations and the Czech tax administrator sent the documents to the Police of the Czech Republic.
A subsequent audit by the BRH found that the German payer had changed its registered office and the new local tax administrator had cancelled the VAT exemption for the supply of the car to the Czech payer based on the audit.
The German tax payer had not corrected the data in the summary report and filed an appeal against the tax administrator's decision.
8)
According to the VIES data, the German tax payer delivered goods totalling EUR 33,205 to the Czech tax payer between the 3rd quarter of 2004 and the 1st quarter of 2005.
The SAO's subsequent audit revealed that the Czech tax administrator had attempted to find out the causes of the differences created by the Czech tax payer in the acquisition of goods between the 3rd quarter of 2004 and the 1st quarter of 2005.
The Czech tax payer repeatedly submitted an additional VAT return for the 1st quarter of 2005.
The Czech tax administrator did not clarify the difference in the value of the acquired goods amounting to CZK 134,273 for the period between the 3rd quarter of 2004 and the 1st quarter of 2005, as according to the Czech tax administrator it was not possible to accurately capture the commercial transactions for the individual quarters and therefore the tax administrator accepted the submitted additional tax returns.
9)
The German tax payer delivered goods amounting to EUR 46,854 to the Czech tax payer in the 3rd quarter of 2004.
The Czech tax payer declared the intra-community acquisition of goods worth only EUR 14,856 for the same period.
The Czech tax administrator verified the amount of the effected supplies within the framework of the international exchange of information pursuant to Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003.
The reply to the request for information received from Germany was accompanied by 3 invoices with the total value of the delivery of goods stated at EUR 31,998, which is the value corresponding to the difference between the acquisition declared by the Czech tax payer in the VAT return and the data provided in the VIES system.
A subsequent audit by the SAO found that the Czech tax payer filed the additional VAT return for the tax period from July 2004 to January 2007 after many urges from the tax administrator.
In this tax return, the tax payer also claimed the right to deduct the VAT, thus the tax obligation for the given tax period remained unchanged.
The follow-up audit verified that for selected cases of commercial transactions between taxpayers from the Czech Republic and Germany, most of the tax procedures had been completed and that the tax administrators in both the Czech Republic and Germany had taken adequate measures (i.e. additionally assessed the VAT or prevented the refund of the input tax).
4.3 Control of selected cases of risky intra-community transactions
4.3.1 Results of the audit in the Czech Republic
EUROCANET can be an important source of information for detecting risky entities within the Member State where the goods were acquired.
In the Czech Republic, the signal information obtained from the EUROCANET system was compared with the data on acquirers by the relevant local tax authorities.
Starting from the first quarter of 2008, the Czech Republic sends data on risky transactions and on tax entities acting as suppliers to the EUROCANET system.
Within the framework of international cooperation, nine Czech tax entities included in the EUROCANET system were selected for the audit.
These entities acted either as suppliers or as purchasers of goods.
Relevant data from tax administrations from other Member States were captured in EUROCANET.
As the German tax administration did not participate in the EUROCANET data exchange, it was not possible to obtain any information that would help to determine whether suppliers with a German VAT ID were assessed as risky entities by the German tax administration.
The audit operation revealed cases of normal commercial transactions as well as cases of suspected involvement in carousel trades or VAT fraud.
Where relevant, tax administrations used the exchange of information under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003.
For example:
• Tax administrations did not detect any suspicions of involvement in risky transactions when verifying signal information.
Tax authorities continuously monitor such tax entities due to their inclusion in EUROCANET.
• Tax authorities did not show deviations from the rules applicable to the calculation of the tax base and VAT in the submitted accounting records during the verification of risky transactions, although they found irregularities in the area of transport and storage of goods or revealed business relationships with suspicious or non-contact companies from other Member States.
• The verification of commercial transactions was complicated as some tax payers did not cooperate with tax authorities and could not be contacted.
Locally competent tax authorities mostly examined risky tax entities and risky transactions listed in the EUROCANET signal information.
Tax authorities have limited possibilities in the verification of risky transactions, especially in relation to the verification of missing traders, and it is difficult to prove fraudulent behaviour to a tax entity only from the physical control of documents.
Stricter requirements for VAT registration of payers and more flexible cancellation of registrations would help reduce missing trader fraud.
In the case of tax entities involved in carousel fraud and other fraudulent activities, VAT registration takes place for the purpose of reporting fictitious deliveries of goods within the EU or for issuing formally correct tax documents to payers who, on the basis of these documents, unduly draw input VAT deductions.
In cases where the involvement of tax entities in carousel trade and other fraud is suspected and goods are imported and exported from third countries, it would be advisable to ensure greater cooperation between customs and financial authorities.
Closer cooperation between these authorities would help in identifying goods and irregularities in transport documentation, as well as in monitoring the physical movement of goods within the EU towards the end consumer.
Participation of EU Member States in EUROCANET is voluntary.
The fact that three large Member States (Germany, Italy and the United Kingdom) did not participate in EUROCANET was assessed by the European Parliament in late 2008 as a weakness of the system which should be eliminated by the establishment of a mandatory EUROFISC network.
4.3.2 Results of the control in Germany
The BRH analysed the information available at the Federal Central Tax Office, which contained data from EUROCANET.
This data was the criterion for selecting six files of German tax payers for control.
Germany, like some other countries, refused to participate actively in EUROCANET.
Thus, Germany has a passive status, which means that it does not send data to Brussels, but only receives data from EUROCANET.
The justification for this position is contained in the following statement:.in the view of the government, it is not legally permissible for state (public) institutions to provide data to EUROCANET.
Currently, there is no legal basis for violating the applicable rules on the confidentiality of tax information.
Moreover, the government has no reliable information on how such data is used in EUROCANET by other Member States."17 Since October 2007, the Federal Central Tax Office has been carrying out analyses of data from EUROCANET and forwarding them to the Länder tax authorities in accordance with the agreed procedure.
The German tax authorities receive control information on the direct business relationships of payers (registered with specific tax authorities) with traders from other Member States who have been included in EUROCANET.
However, the German tax authorities receive no information on whether such a trader from another Member State has any risky business relationships with traders from other Member States who also have business relations with the German trader in question.
4.3.3 Evaluation
The Czech Republic is an active participant in EUROCANET, while Germany has a passive status.
It is unsatisfactory for an active participant if some Member States refuse to participate actively.
As a result, the control in this area had to be carried out in different ways.
However, the results did not reveal major differences in terms of detecting VAT fraud cases, as EUROCANET is not the only systemic risk management tool.
The tax administrations of both countries have a number of other tools to detect fraudulent transactions, but it is necessary to establish a comprehensive risk management system within the EU.
The EU Council reached a political agreement on a draft regulation, the main contribution of which is the establishment of EUROFISC.
The experience gained from the use of EUROCANET data should also be part of the envisaged VAT fraud network.
Member States should therefore communicate their experience at European level.
On the other hand, cases brought before courts at both national and European level show that a discussion between Member States and the Commission on the conditions for tax exemptions in intra-Community transactions seems necessary.
4.4 Mutual assistance for the recovery of claims
4.4.1 International assistance for the recovery of claims in the Czech Republic
In particular, the following directives provide the basic framework for international cooperation for the recovery of certain financial claims within the EU:
• Council Directive 76/308/EEC on mutual assistance for the recovery of claims resulting from operations forming part of the system of financing the European Agricultural Guidance and Guarantee Fund, as well as agricultural levies and customs duties;
• Council Directive 2001/44/EC amending Directive 76/308/EEC on mutual assistance for the recovery of claims resulting from operations forming part of the system of financing the European Agricultural Guidance and Guarantee Fund, agricultural levies and customs duties, value added tax and certain excise duties;
• Commission Directive 2002/94/EC implementing certain provisions of Council Directive 76/308/EEC on mutual assistance for the recovery of claims relating to certain levies, duties, taxes and other measures.
In the Czech Republic, Council Directive 76/308/EEC was implemented by Act No 252/2000 Coll., on International Assistance for the Recovery of Certain Financial Claims.
After the adoption of Council Directive 2001/44/EC, it was necessary to implement this Directive into the Czech legal order and at the same time to amend the aforementioned Act No. 252/2000 Coll.
In this context, a new Act No. 191/2004 Coll., on International Assistance for the Recovery of Certain Financial Claims, was adopted.
Commission Regulation (EC) No 1179/2008 of 28.11.2008 is a new regulation in the system for regulating international cooperation in the recovery of certain financial claims within the EU.
The annex to the Regulation sets out new models of requests, which have been in use since 1 January 2009, newly stipulates the obligation of electronic communication and the obligation of the applicant authority to confirm the conformity of the documents sent with the original document.
The main principles for providing international cooperation in the recovery of claims:
1. reciprocity;
2. assistance is always provided only on the basis of a request containing the prescribed particulars;
3. assistance does not apply to financial claims that are of the nature of a criminal law sanction in the requested State;
4. the provision of international assistance for the recovery of claims is governed by the national law of the State which has been requested for assistance;
5. foreign claims do not have priority in the recovery;
6. assistance is provided only for the recovery of uncontested claims;
7. principle of exhaustion (the requesting State has, without success, used all applicable possibilities for the recovery of a claim provided for in its legal order).
Act No 191/2004 defines three forms by which the assistance takes place, namely the provision of information, the service of documents and the actual recovery of claims.
Procedure for sending requests for recovery to other EU Member States
The locally competent financial authority electronically sends the request for information, the request for delivery or the request for recovery of claims together with the relevant documents to the Czech Ministry of Finance via the financial directorates.
The Czech Ministry of Finance arranges a translation of the request into the relevant language, scans it including the annexes and sends it via the CCN/CSI network to the competent tax authority of the designated State.
There are two basic requirements for recovery: the claim must be higher than EUR 1 500 and must not be older than 5 years.
If these requirements are not met, the requested authority may refuse recovery.
Procedure for receiving requests for recovery from other EU Member States
On receiving a request from another Member State, the Czech Ministry of Finance must acknowledge receipt of the request as soon as possible, and no later than within seven days.
If the Czech Ministry of Finance decides not to comply with the request, it will inform the requesting authority of the reasons for the rejection of the request, indicating the specific provisions of the directive on which it relies.
This communication must be sent no later than three months from the date of the acknowledgement of receipt of the request.
Upon receipt of the request, the Czech Ministry of Finance will verify whether the request has all the requisites according to the law and should immediately forward the request through the Financial Directorate to the locally competent Financial Office for execution.
If the request for recovery is accepted, the tax administrator will, among other things, identify the debtor's assets, e.g. by taking extracts from the Real Estate Register, by checking accounts at banks, by verifying the registration of vehicles at the Transport Inspectorate, etc.
After six months have elapsed from the date on which the receipt of the request was confirmed, the Czech Ministry of Finance should inform the requesting authority of the outcome of the investigation that was carried out in order to obtain the requested information.
In the case of non-contact tax entities, when it is not possible to recover the claim, the requesting authority should also be informed of this fact.
Any amount recovered by the tax administrator will be transferred to the requesting authority in CZK within one month from the date on which the claim was recovered.
It is not excluded that the Czech tax administrator recovering foreign claims will allow it to wait to be paid or to be paid in instalments, if the state that requested the recovery gives its consent.
During the recovery period, the debtor is prescribed interest or a penalty payment in accordance with Act No 337/1992 Coll., on the Administration of Taxes and Fees.
This interest or penalty payment belongs to the state that requested the recovery.
In the case of received requests for recovery, the Czech Ministry of Finance did not send requests to the locally competent tax administrators for processing in a timely manner, especially in 2006 and 2007.
A similar situation was found in the context of international assistance for the recovery of claims as well as in the case of requests received from tax administrators from the Czech Republic.
The audit revealed that the Czech Ministry of Finance did not proceed in accordance with Act No 191/2004 Coll., because it did not inform the locally competent authority of the Member State of the progress made in the recovery within six months from the date when the request was confirmed.
This situation has been improving since 2008.
Statistical data
In accordance with the provisions of Section 13, paragraph 4 of Act No 191/2004 Coll., the Czech Ministry of Finance processes every year by 15 March statistical data for the European Commission, indicating the number of requests for information, delivery or recovery sent or received in the past year, indicating the amount of claims covered by the requests.
The European Commission processes a report on the state of recovery of claims, which it submits to the EU Council and the European Parliament, on the basis of documents provided by all EU Member States.
The audit found that the Czech Ministry of Finance undervalued the statistical data due to an error in the item of recovered claims in 2008 by EUR 5 250 000 by indicating the incorrect value of the recovered claim for VAT (this was a shift of the decimal point after the conversion of the claim from Czech crowns to the value in euros).
The error was subsequently reflected in the European Commission statistics.
Information on mutual assistance, including recovered amounts, is presented in the following table.
4.4.2 International assistance for recovery of claims in Germany
The legal mandate for international administrative assistance in tax matters is derived from European Community law, Council Directive 2008/55/EC of 26 May 2008 (EC Directive on recovery of claims) and Commission Regulation of 28 November 2008 (EC Implementing Directive).
In order to make the wording more accessible and easier to understand, the EC Recovery Directive codifies Council Directive 76/308/EEC of 15 March 197621, the provisions of which have already been substantially amended several times.
The provisions apply, inter alia, to the recovery of VAT, income tax and capital gains tax, including accessories.
The EC Recovery Directive was transposed into national German law by the (EC) Act on the collection of state taxes of 3 May 2003.
The recovery procedure in Germany is governed by the German Fiscal Code.
