Article 117.2 of the Code emphasises that tax authorities may provide international judicial and administrative assistance on the basis of international agreements and legal instruments of the European Communities which are in force in national jurisdiction and on the basis of the EC Act on Administrative Assistance.
Part Six of the German Fiscal Code (Articles 249-346) enshrines the statutory provisions governing the recovery procedure.
The administrative acts of the tax authorities are governed in particular by the instructions for execution and the instructions for recovery.
The Federal Ministry of Finance has reached an agreement with representatives of the highest tax authorities of the Länder regarding the principles of administrative assistance for the assessment of taxes and has transferred its own responsibility in this matter to the Federal Central Tax Office.
The general prerequisites for submitting recovery applications are as follows:
• Legal requirements must be fulfilled (Sections 251 and 254 of the German Fiscal Code [AO]).
• All available domestic means of recovery have already been exhausted.
• Claims which are the subject of requests for recovery assistance must be final.
• No more than 5 years must elapse between the issue of the recovery order or the date on which the claim becomes final (i.e. it is no longer subject to appeal) and the date on which the applications are submitted.
• The total amount of the claim must be more than EUR 1 500.
Procedure for sending recovery applications to other EU Member States
German requests for recovery of outstanding tax liabilities are sent from the implementing departments of the tax authorities to the relevant foreign office, such as the Czech Customs Office, via the Intermediation Office and the Federal Central Tax Office.
The closer procedure is governed by the Methodological Guideline on International Administrative Assistance in Tax Matters (Recovery of Claims) of 19 January 2004.25 Currently, a working group of the Federal and Land Governments is reviewing this Methodological Guideline in order to adapt it to the Recovery Directive.
The request, including the annexes, is submitted electronically by the Tax Office to the Intermediation Office.
The Tax Office checks the correctness of the request in terms of content and form.
If the request is not correct, it is returned to the relevant Tax Office.
If it fulfils all the requirements, it is referred to the Federal Central Tax Office.
The Federal Central Tax Office subsequently ensures the necessary communication with the relevant foreign office and also arranges the translation of the request.
Procedure for receiving recovery applications from other EU Member States
Recovery applications received from other Member States are registered by the Federal Central Tax Office and within 10 days it sends an acknowledgement of receipt.
In addition, the Federal Central Tax Office checks whether the formal requirements have been fulfilled.
The Federal Central Tax Office submits these applications to the intermediary office, which then forwards them to the relevant tax offices and monitors their execution.
The Federal Central Tax Office also sends preliminary or final reports.
If the application takes more than 6 months to process, it invites the intermediary office to submit a preliminary report, which must be submitted in accordance with Article 16 of Commission Directive 2002/94/DG.
After checking the formal and factual elements of the application, the implementing services notify the method of recovery.
All recovered amounts must be transferred to the bank account indicated in the application within one month of their receipt.
Statistical data

4.4.3 Enforcement control, case studies
In the framework of international cooperation, 21 applications for international assistance for recovery between the Czech Republic and Germany were selected for the verification.
Examination of the 10 selected cases revealed, among others:
1.
On 20 October 2006, the Czech Ministry of Finance received from Germany a request for recovery of VAT claims for the years 2004 and 2005 totalling EUR 3 883, i.e. CZK 109 820, from a Czech tax entity.
The Czech Ministry of Finance did not send a request for recovery to the tax administration until 26 February 2008.
In order to secure the enforced claim, the Czech tax administration established a lien on real estate owned by a Czech tax entity.
As even by mortgaging the real estate it was not possible to pay the entire enforced claim, a payment schedule with instalments of at least CZK 2,000 per month was agreed with the Czech tax entity.
On 31 August 2009, information on the status of the enforcement of the claim was sent to the German tax administration, with the claim being partially recovered in instalments of CZK 49,600 as of 25 August 2009.
This amount was sent to Germany and a further instalment of CZK 3,000 was sent to Germany on 28 August 2009.
2.
On 7 January 2008, the Czech Ministry of Finance received a request for the recovery of tax arrears of a Czech tax entity that owed in Germany the amount of EUR 180,869, i.e. CZK 4,434,915, on VAT and on income tax and accessories.
The Czech Ministry of Finance did not send the request to the tax administrator until 27 November 2008.
The tax administrator, by examining the ownership of accounts at banks, securities, real estate, motor vehicles and movables, found that the debtor did not own any enforceable assets.
Furthermore, a local investigation found that the debtor did not stay at his permanent residence address for almost a year.
His whereabouts in the Czech Republic are unknown.
This communication was received by the Czech Ministry of Finance on 6 April 2009 and on 16 April 2009 the tax administrator's reply was sent to the German tax administration.
3.
On 21 November 2007, the Czech Ministry of Finance received a request for recovery from Germany concerning the turnover tax arrears and accessories of the Czech tax entity amounting to EUR 3 139, i.e. CZK 84 846.
The Czech Ministry of Finance sent a request for recovery of this claim to the tax administrator on 6 August 2008, although already on 18 February 2008 the Czech Ministry of Finance received information from Germany that the Czech tax entity had paid the claim in Germany.
On 9 December 2008, the Czech Ministry of Finance notified the tax administrator that the request for recovery was settled by the payment of the claim by the Czech tax entity in Germany.
However, the claim in question was also paid in the framework of recovery in the Czech Republic and sent to Germany on 27 October 2008.
Due to the long time limits within which the Czech Ministry of Finance informed the authorised tax administrators, the claim was paid twice in this case - by the entity itself in Germany and by recovery of the claim by the Czech tax administrator.
In cooperation with BRH, it was found that the amount recovered from the Czech Republic should have been set off against the claim from another request for recovery of EUR 6 649, which should have been sent to the Czech Republic in September 2008.
The Czech Ministry of Finance records only the request for recovery of the claim amounting to EUR 3 139 with this company, the request for recovery of the claim amounting to EUR 6 649 does not appear in the records of the Czech Ministry of Finance with the company in question.
4.
On 15 September 2008, the Czech Ministry of Finance received a request from Germany for the recovery of tax arrears of a Czech taxpayer who owed EUR 39 957 in income tax and VAT and accessories in Germany, i.e. CZK 956 654.
On 19 December 2008, the Czech Ministry of Finance sent the request to the Czech tax administrator.
On 1 June 2009, the procedure for the recovery of the claim was initiated, execution was ordered for the attachment of the claim on accounts with banks in the Czech Republic and for the deduction on wages (the deduction amounted to CZK 7 000).
During negotiations with the tax administrator, the debtor stated that he did not agree with the amount of the claim and considered it questionable.
The Czech tax administrator found out that the taxpayer had been willing to pay EUR 250 per month in the past, which was not accepted by the German tax administrator.
The taxpayer promised to discuss the request with the German tax administrator in order to obtain a change in the amount of its claim.
The recovery of the claim continued during the auditing operation of the SAO.
5.
On 19 November 2007, the Czech Ministry of Finance received a request for recovery from Germany concerning a Czech tax entity that owed a total of EUR 113 444, i.e. CZK 3 116 304, in income tax for 2005 and in turnover tax for 2003-2007 and accessories.
The Czech Ministry of Finance did not send the request to the Prague 1 Tax Authority, which is responsible for administering the tax at non-established tax entities in the Czech Republic, until 14 November 2008, as it was not possible to determine the tax administrator with local jurisdiction based on the address of the tax entity.
During the auditing operation, the FÚ received information that the debtor had an income of EUR 4 704 on 19 September 2008; however, the FÚ was no longer able to issue an enforcement order for this amount, as the Czech Ministry of Finance forwarded the request for recovery of the claim only after that date.
On 26 January 2009, the Czech tax administrator initiated the enforcement of the claim and issued an enforcement order for attaching the claim to the debtor's funds in accounts held with banks and savings and credit cooperatives.
The enforcement of the claim continued during the auditing operation of the SAO.
6.
The Czech tax administrator requested international cooperation in the recovery of the VAT claim and the costs of the proceedings totalling CZK 146 223 742 on October 3, 2006.
The Czech Ministry of Finance did not send this request for recovery to the German tax administration until May 13, 2008.
On September 8, 2008, the German tax administrator transferred to the Czech authorities through the Federal Bank the amount obtained from the execution of the funds in the debtor's account amounting to EUR 17 700, i.e. CZK 439 226.
An error in the conversion of the recovered amount was found during the verification of the recovered amount.
The recovered amount of CZK 146 223 742 was converted at the rate of EUR 1 = CZK 25,065 erroneously to EUR 583 378.
The correct conversion of the recovered amount amounts to EUR 5 833 781.83.
The request for recovery was therefore sent to Germany, which was lower by EUR 5 250 404.
7.
On 1 March 2007, the Czech tax administrator sent the Czech Ministry of Finance a request for recovery of the tax arrears from a Czech tax entity which owed CZK 1 970 632, or EUR 79 847, in respect of VAT and accessories.
The Czech Ministry of Finance did not send the request to the German tax administration until 10 November 2008.
On 4 February 2009, the German tax administrator requested the debtor to pay the arrears.
In view of the significant decreases in the company's turnover in the second half of 2008 and in particular in the first half of 2009 and the related liquidation situation of the company, the following payments were made to pay the arrears: on 8 April 2009, EUR 4 600, on 6 May 2009, EUR 3 000 and on 16 June 2009, EUR 2 500.
These payments were sent to the tax administrator's account in the Czech Republic.
On 23 June 2009, the German tax administrator agreed with the debtor to pay a further instalment of EUR 2 500 until 30 June 2009.
8.
A request for recovery totalling EUR 398 653, i.e. CZK 9 832 779, including a claim for real estate transfer tax, was received from the Czech tax administrator to the Czech Ministry of Finance on 22.5.2008.
The Czech Ministry of Finance sent a request for recovery to the German tax administration on 2.10.2008.
On 3.4.2009 the Czech Ministry of Finance received a communication from the German tax administration that the request had been returned by the German tax administration.
The German tax administration justified the refund on the grounds that the real estate transfer tax is not a tax within the meaning of Article 2(e), (f), (g) or (h) of Council Directive 2008/55/EC.
The German tax administration further stated that Article 2(g) concerns claims related to income tax and wealth tax.
Similarly, Article 3 of Council Directive 2008/55/EC applies to income and wealth taxes, which are listed in Article 1(3) in conjunction with Article 1(4) of Council Directive 77/799/EEC.
The Czech Ministry of Finance proposed to draw up and submit a new request for recovery excluding arrears of real estate transfer tax amounting to CZK 61 759 and including arrears of VAT, corporate income tax and personal income tax, which will be re-sent to the German tax administration.
The Czech Ministry of Finance received a new request from the Czech tax administration for the recovery of tax arrears concerning the same tax entity that owes CZK 7 079 735 in income tax and VAT.
9.
On 6 February 2006, the Czech tax administration sent a request to the Czech Ministry of Finance concerning the recovery of tax arrears of a Czech tax entity that owed CZK 3 445 782 in personal income tax and VAT, i.e. EUR 123 328.
Of this amount, VAT amounted to CZK 1 133 967.
The Czech Ministry of Finance sent the request to the German tax administration only on 18 April 2007.
The Czech Ministry of Finance forwarded to the Czech tax authority the reply of the German tax authority dated 9 July 2007 until 11 November 2008.
The reply stated that the German tax authority had issued an execution order on 11 June 2007 for a bank account, which however stated that it had no business relations with the tax entity.
The German tax authority thus considered the request to be settled.
10.
On 26 September 2005, the Czech tax authority sent a request to the Czech Ministry of Finance concerning the recovery of VAT tax arrears totalling CZK 1,296,845, or EUR 43,591.
The request from the Czech tax authority was received by the Czech Ministry of Finance on 10 October 2005.
The Czech Ministry of Finance sent the request to the German tax authority on 15 December 2005.
Before sending the request for recovery, the Czech tax authority executed the debtor's funds on bank accounts and payroll deduction and established a lien on immovable property.
The request for recovery was preceded by a request for information sent to the German tax authority on 16 March 2005.
The response to the request for information received by the Czech tax administration on 16 September 2005 showed that the Czech tax entity was in Germany and had income of EUR 8 437 from non-business activities.
The Czech Ministry of Finance received the response to the request for recovery on 20 April 2006, but forwarded it to the Czech tax administration only on 12 February 2008.
The response stated that no enforcement proceedings could be initiated in Germany because of the debtor's insolvency - no assets were found and his non-business income was already subject to another enforcement procedure.
The German tax administration thus considered the request for recovery to be completed.
4.4.4 Comparison and evaluation
In the area of international assistance for recovery of claims, all EU Member States are governed by the same European legislation.
Therefore, the way in which requests for international assistance for recovery of claims are handled is the same in the Czech Republic and Germany.
The SAO and the BRH compared the statistics submitted by both Member States to the European Commission for the period 2006-2008.
The data contained in these statistics did not match.
In the 2006 report, the European Commission recommended that Member States pay increased attention to the management of their statistics.
In the 2009 report, the Commission concluded that the incidence of inconsistencies in the statistics has decreased, even though the number of requests has increased.
Both SAIs consider it important that statistical issues are discussed again at EU level.
This discussion should focus on how to avoid persistent inconsistencies, otherwise the data reported by individual EU States in the statistics will not be reliable and comparable.
In addition, both SAIs agree that reliable statistics should report the annual number of requests as well as the nature of the claims in question (i.e. whether the claims relate to VAT, income tax, etc.) as well as the amount of claims recovered by individual Member States.
Both SAIs consider it important for the Commission to provide more detailed analyses of the statistics submitted by the Member States, as this may assist Member States in assessing their own effectiveness in fighting VAT fraud.
The fact that the recovery rate can be calculated broken down by Member State, both SAIs consider it useful for Member States with lower recovery rates to step up their efforts and try to improve the recovery rate at least to the level of the EU average.
If a Member State so wishes, the Commission should actively participate in this process.
In particular, in 2006 and 2007, the Czech Ministry of Finance did not submit requests for recovery of claims on time to the local tax authorities.
A similar situation was found for requests for international assistance received from tax authorities in the Czech Republic.
The audit revealed that the Czech Ministry of Finance did not act in accordance with Act No. 191/2004 Coll., on International Assistance for the Recovery of Claims, because it did not inform the local competent authority of the Member State of the progress made in recovery within six months from the date when the receipt of the request was confirmed.
4.5 Control of large tax entities
4.5.1 Control of large tax entities in the Czech Republic
General information
The VAT audit of large tax entities is governed by the same rules as that of other tax entities.
The procedural procedure for the control of VDS is based on Act No. 337/1992 Coll., on the Administration of Taxes and Fees.
The Czech Ministry of Finance defined VDS as natural or legal persons that were established or established for the purpose of business and whose net turnover for the tax period stated in the personal/corporate income tax return amounted to CZK 2 billion or more.
The classification of a tax entity as a VDS took place after the submission of the income tax return for the relevant tax period, for the first time for 2003.
A tax entity ceased to be referred to as a VDS if, in three consecutive tax periods from the end of the period on which it submitted the tax return on the basis of which it was classified as a VDS, its net turnover for the tax period fell below the stated limit.
A tax entity was not allowed to be removed from the VDS register without carrying out a tax audit of at least one tax for one tax period.
All VDS were audited at least every five years until the end of 2009.
Since 2010, a written evaluation of the tax entity must be carried out at least every two years and the chosen subsequent procedure must eliminate the tax risks and their negative impact on the correct determination and collection of the tax.
The audit of the FÚ is focused on at least one type of tax; the tax administrator usually chooses several tax periods at once.
The VDS were audited by specialised audit departments, which are set up at 13 FUs in total, or by the staff of the audit departments of the locally competent FUs.
The specialised audit departments carry out tax audits within the remit set by the Director of the Financial Directorate.
In addition to large tax entity audits, it also examines
• tax entities operating in unusual and specific fields of business;
• entities where carrying out a tax audit is technically and extremely time-consuming;
• entities with a branched territorial and organisational structure;
• entities suspected of large-scale tax evasion;
• entities connected in chains and networks where there is a suspicion of large-scale tax evasion and unjustified enticement of excessive deductions.
The number of tax audits carried out by specialised audit departments of the FUs and the results of these audits are shown in Table 3.
The Czech Ministry of Finance has proposed an amendment to Act No 531/1990 Coll., on territorial financial authorities, which consists in the establishment of a specialised Tax Office with nationwide coverage for selected tax entities (i.a. for legal entities set up for the purpose of business which have a turnover of more than CZK 2 billion).
4.5.2 Inspection of large tax entities in Germany
General information
VAT inspections of large companies are governed by the same rules as tax inspections in general, i.e. the relevant provisions are enshrined in the following regulations: • the German Fiscal Code (AO), • the Fiscal Administration Act (FVG), • the regulations on tax inspections (BpO).
Other methodological documents are also in force.
The German Fiscal Code
The statutory control provisions are enshrined in sections 193-203 of the German Fiscal Code in Section IV - Tax Control on Site. These articles enshrine in particular the rules on the admissibility of tax control on site (i.e. on the premises of an undertaking), their scope in terms of subject matter, the rules on the allocation of responsibilities, the form and content of the control notice, the control principles, the obligations of the taxpayer to cooperate and the prerequisites for carrying out the final examination and communication of the control report.
Tax control on site is carried out by the responsible tax authorities (section 195 of the Code).
Fiscal Governance Act According to section 5.1, point 1, in conjunction with section 19 of the Act, participation in tax controls on site by the tax authorities is compulsory for the Federal Central Tax Office.
The authorities involved agree with each other on the spot the nature and extent of the Federal Central Tax Office's participation in tax controls.
In addition, the Federal Central Tax Office has the right to require that the specific undertakings it chooses be subject to an inspection at a time it determines.
In such a case, it may declare the rules for the conduct and content of the inspection at the premises of those companies.
Tax inspection regulations Under Article 108.7 of the German Constitution, the regulations on tax inspections (German abbreviation BpO 2000) have been approved by the Federal Council (Bundesrat, the upper house of the German Parliament in which the governments of the Länder are represented).
These administrative regulations apply to the on-the-spot check carried out by the tax authorities of the Länder and by the Federal Central Tax Office.
The undertakings are classified by size at regular intervals, in accordance with Article 3 of the BpO 2000.
Large undertakings are subject to subsequent inspection (Article 4.2 of the BpO).
Under Article 33.1 of the BpO 2000, each informed tax office must keep a register of groups of companies as defined in the BpO 2000.
Methodological guidelines
In addition to the above, the following guidelines set out an additional methodology for the tax administration:
• Uniform manual for special VAT controls in Germany ;
• USLO manual, which sets out the methodology for using data on intra-Community business relations kept in the VIES system;
• ZAUBER manual, which sets out the methodology for using the ZAUBER database;
• Work aids for various and special objects.
The classification of tax entities is based on criteria such as turnover and net profit, with different thresholds depending on the type of business.
The data is published by the Federal Ministry of Finance.
They are evaluated every three years and fixed for the following three years.
The number of companies to be inspected - not just large enterprises - must be determined at regular inspection intervals.
As a general rule, inspections of large enterprises are carried out on an ongoing basis.
Inspections are usually announced, including VAT inspections.
This means that during the inspection, inspections are carried out definitively mainly on income tax, excise tax and VAT - i.e. inspections of all types of relevant taxes.
VAT inspections can be carried out either by tax inspectors or by VAT inspectors.
Implementation varies and depends on the organisational arrangements of the Länder.
The number of tax periods covered by inspections usually varies between three and five years.
The BpO 2000 foresees a control period of three years.
All taxes of the company are subject to inspection.
4.5.3 Management of control of large tax entities
Both SAIs decided not to examine individual cases of VDS inspections carried out, but focused on management issues in order to obtain an overview of how the tax administrations manage the issue of VAT inspections at VDS.
In the form of a questionnaire, they gathered information from the tax administrations on the areas they consider essential for managing this issue.
• What statistical records and analyses are available to the management of the tax administrations regarding the VAT inspection at VDS?
In particular:
• Are there any statistics or records of the extent to which a distinction is made between the fight against VAT fraud and VAT control in general?
Czech Republic: No, the ADIS system does not allow such a distinction with the current data version.
Germany: The tax administration does not distinguish between control designed to fight VAT fraud and general VAT control.
• Are there any statistics or records of the timeliness of VAT controls (in relation to the time period of the audited transactions)?
Czech Republic: The records of the timeliness of the questioning with relevance for intra-community acquisitions of goods for selected VAT payers are reported in the ADIS system.
In addition, the information recorded in the ADIS system also includes data of the type of time the questioning took.
Germany: No, the uniform statistics at federal level for tax inspectors only contain information on the average time of the last inspection (information on the year).
This data does not provide an overview of the selected inspection periods with regard to individual entrepreneurs.
VAT inspectors focus on the most recent tax assessment period; they also have the right to carry out VDS checks.
However, the statistics produced at federal level for special VAT inspection units do not provide information on the classification of tax entities.
• There are any statistics or records on the nature of the tax revenues additionally generated, broken down e.g. according to the following criteria:
i. net increase in tax liability (e.g. in cases where a tax entity has unduly applied a reduced VAT rate instead of the standard tax rate);
ii. only nominal increase in tax liability (e.g. transfer of a fully qualified VAT case to another tax period);
iii. additional collection of tax revenue (payment of outstanding additional tax due).
Czech Republic:
The Czech tax administration monitors the number of tax verifications carried out, the amounts of additional tax assessed broken down by type of tax, by the number of tax entities audited and by the number of tax periods audited.
Other tax procedures (local investigations, complaints procedures) are monitored in the same way.
Time data and amounts of additional taxes paid are recorded as a separate task.
Statistics on general debts are also kept broken down by type of tax, but not by the declared tax or the tax determined by the tax administration.
Germany: No, the uniform statistics at federal level for tax inspectors and special VAT inspection units do not distinguish between the above criteria.
Moreover, the majority of tax administrations visited do not distinguish between these differences either.
• Are inspection areas registered which generate high additional revenues?
Czech Republic: Yes, the tax administration has the right to select tax payers for verification on the basis of criteria which can be linked to the selected indicators in the special sections of the ADIS.
Germany: There are no regulations at federal level.
It follows that the uniform statistics at federal level for tax inspectors and special VAT inspection units do not provide such data.
However, there is one coordinated approach by the finance ministers of the Länder and the federal government.
In the ZAUBER database, tax inspectors or tax investigators from the Länder must record their increased tax (VAT) liability if it exceeds a certain amount.
In such a case, they must specify, for example, the nature of the increased tax liability.
• What are the most common findings?
Czech Republic:
- The VDS claim an unjustified right to deduct input tax on supplies and services:
• which have not been used to carry out any economic activity pursuant to Section 72(1) of the VAT Act;
• which have been used for representation pursuant to Section 75(3) of the VAT Act;
• on the basis of tax documents which did not meet the requirements laid down in Section 73(1) of the VAT Act;
- The VDS did not declare output VAT pursuant to Section 21(1) of the VAT Act.
Germany: It has been established that there are no regulations at federal level.
It follows that the uniform statistics at federal level for tax inspectors and special VAT inspection units do not provide such data.
Findings relating to VAT are not separately registered by the Länder insofar as they result from the tax inspections of the VDS.
However, in the ZAUBER database, where tax inspectors or tax investigators from the Länder have to enter their increased tax (VAT) liability if it exceeds a certain amount, the Federal Central Tax Office is able to analyse this information.
• Does the tax administration carry out analyses of the control areas from which a high "return" results and draw the consequences for the management?
Czech Republic: Yes, for example, they launch nationwide audits focusing on risky commodities or the subject of economic activity.
Germany: There are no regulations at federal level.
The uniform statistics at federal level for tax inspectors and special VAT inspection units do not provide data on the audit areas from which a high "return" results.
There are different views on the process of analysis as well as on case management in terms of materiality.
Some regional tax offices provide special information, but its use is at the discretion of the tax authorities.
4.5.4 Comparison and evaluation
The differences in the replies of the two Member States show that the Czech Republic provides a system that collects a lot of data from the tax inspections carried out as well as data from the financial statements - balance sheet and profit and loss statements.
Based on a wide range of data, the Czech Republic is able to guide the selection of risk-prone cases.
The same is true of VAT control analysis and management in general.
In 2012, the establishment of a specialised tax office for the administration of VDS is planned in the Czech Republic.
In Germany, the tax administration does not collect this information.
This makes it more difficult to carry out these tasks in a similar way.
However, the philosophy of Germany places more emphasis on the selection of individual cases based on data from submitted tax returns.
Therefore, the risk management components will be strengthened and improved.
Based on adequate reference notes, expert auditors must be able to assess the exact amount of VAT.
Both SAIs agree that the Member States should be able to ensure adequate financial management as well as an adequate risk management system.
This will help to reduce the shortfall in VAT revenues.
As a result, the revenue from VAT collection will increase and the level of risk detection for unreliable entrepreneurs will also improve.
5. Conclusion
The cooperation of both SAIs on parallel controls of VAT administration met the objectives set by the SAO and the BRH.
Both SAIs got to know each other better the systems in place in the following areas: • intra-community transactions; • VAT risk management, especially with regard to the selection of transactions with a propensity to risk; • assistance in the recovery of VAT claims; and • VAT control of large tax entities.
Thanks to the mutual cooperation, differences in the strategies for detecting cases of VAT fraud as well as differences in the above mentioned areas of VAT administration were revealed in the Czech Republic and Germany.
Control findings have been compared and best practices have been identified on the basis of them.
In addition, both SAIs hope that the results achieved will provide an impetus for stakeholders to start a discussion on approaches and strategies within the Member States, among them at the level of the European Commission.
The extremely valuable experience and knowledge gained from the cooperation of both SAIs can serve as an encouragement for the implementation of future control actions in the field of VAT administration.
6. Communiqué
The report was prepared in Czech, English and German and signed by the President of the Supreme Audit Office of the Czech Republic and the President of the Federal Court of Auditors (Bundesrechnungshof) of the Federal Republic of Germany.
Edition closing date: June 2010.
